## THE BOOK OF SONG OF SOLOMON

INTRODUCTION

[In the ]{.class-0}[Authorized Version]{.class-2}[, the last of the poetical, wisdom books is The Song of Solomon. In a Hebrew Bible, the book follows the book of Job and precedes the book of Ruth; it is part of the section called the ]{.class-0}[Hagiographa]{.class-2}[ (Gk.--Holy Writings), known in Hebrew as the ]{.class-0}[Kethubim.]{.class-2}[ This is the section which Christ called ]{.class-0}["the psalms"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 24:44).]{.class-0}

[The title is taken from the very first verse: ]{.class-0}["The song of songs, which is Solomon's."]{.class-1}[ The Hebrew title is also taken from that verse: ]{.class-0}[The Song of Songs.]{.class-2}[ You will also hear it referred to as ]{.class-0}[Canticles,]{.class-2}[ the Latin word for "songs." The ]{.class-0}[Bishops' Bible]{.class-2}[ called it the "Ballet of Ballets" (the Dance of Dances).]{.class-0}

[The Song of Solomon is composed entirely of a series of lyric love songs, which vary in length. In a Fifteenth-Century copy of it, which now lies in Cambridge University, you will find there is a panel over it containing a number of letters and a representation of a gazelle and a dove. Although God and the Lord Jesus Christ are evident all through the song, the text itself, like the book of Esther, fails to use the word ]{.class-0}[God]{.class-2}[ or ]{.class-0}[Lord.]{.class-2}

[The author is undoubtedly Solomon (vs. 1), and Solomon appears seven times in the book (1:1, 5, 3:7, 9, 11, 8:11, 12). Naturally the majority of backslidden, apostate, Laodicean scholars deny Solomon's authorship. For example, the Jewish rabbis say the Song of Songs ]{.class-0}[suggests]{.class-2}[ (a "buzz word" used by highly educated College jackasses, especially when discussing evolution) that it reached its present form at a time when Aramaic had displaced Hebrew in Palestine (400 B.C.), which is nonsense.]{.class-0}

[Solomon could trace his genealogy back to Jacob, the grandson of Abraham. Jacob had a mother who was Syrian (Rebekah, the sister of Laban ]{.class-0}[the Syrian,]{.class-2}[ Gen. 28:5); Jacob married four wives, all of whom were Syrian, and gave birth to the twelve tribes of Israel. That Jew was taught to say this: ]{.class-0}["A SYRIAN ready to perish was my father, and he went down into Egypt, and sojourned there with a few, and became there a nation, great, mighty, and populous" ]{.class-1}[(Deut. 26:5).]{.class-0}

Aramaic (Syrian) was used by Moses all the way back in Genesis 31:47. Why would it be anything unusual for Solomon to use Aramaic words or expressions when he was commanded by God to remember his Syrian heritage?

[Another maneuver of the rabbis to get rid of Solomon as the author is to say that since the text mentions ]{.class-0}["Tirzah"]{.class-1}[ (6:4) that the book could not have been written until after the death of Solomon, when the kingdom split under Jeroboam and before Omri moved the capital of the northern kingdom to Samaria (800 B.C.). And that is about as much crap as anyone can take for one day. No capital had to be moved anywhere for Solomon to write anything in the Song of Solomon. He simply likened the woman to two cities: Tirzah and Jerusalem. Tirzah could be beautiful without having any capital in it and without Jeroboam being there. But who could not figure that out?]{.class-0}

Still another way to get rid of the text is to pretend that since the book includes such places as northern Israel, Syria, Transjordan, and Judah that several of the songs "MAY HAVE originated in that area"; i.e., by anyone other than whom God said wrote the book---Solomon. Now what could be funnier than a bunch of cloned jackasses attacking Solomon on that basis when Solomon's kingdom stretched from Israel's border with Lebanon in the north all the way down to the upper part of Saudi Arabia in the south, and from the shore of the Mediterranean in the west all the way to the banks of the Euphrates River in the east (2 Sam. 8:3; 1 Kings 4:21)? That area included all of northern Israel, a great deal of Syria, all of Transjordan, and Judah. Do you mean to tell me that in a forty-year reign Solomon never traveled around his own kingdom?

Now learn a lesson and get it "down pat." Highly educated Hebrew scholars born in Israel, or anyone else who can read, write, speak, and even teach Hebrew, whether they be Jews or Gentiles (even some professing Christians), are some of the dumbest "dumb thumps" that ever perverted the word of God. That is not Ruckman's opinion; that is God Almighty's opinion as recorded in Jeremiah 23:36; Psalm 107:11; and Jeremiah 8:8.

[Never get "Ruckman" confused with God or the Bible. More than 500 faculty members in America, since 1960, have done just that. And while calling "Ruckman" anything but white and sane, they have accused him of being the Holy Spirit---the one who teaches Bible-believing American Christians that the ]{.class-0}[KJV ]{.class-2}[is the Holy Scriptures in English. How they get me confused with the Holy Spirit I have no idea.]{.class-0}

Now, literature on the book is extensive; with works by W. F. Albright, R. Gordis, C. D. Ginsburg, G. D. Cohen, R. Soulen, H. H. Rowley, M. H. Segal, G. R. Driver, et al. Portions of the book appear in classical music (Bruckner, Chabrier, Leopold Damrosch) and oratorios by Enrico Bossi and Italo Montemezz. The Twentieth-Century composers include Ralph von Williams, Virgil Thompson, and a German text by Manfred Sturmann.

[The counterfeit to the Song of Solomon is called the ]{.class-0}[Song of Songs Rabbah.]{.class-2}[ It is what is known as an ]{.class-0}["Haggadic Midrash."]{.class-2}[ It is a rabbinical interpretation of the Song of Solomon based on the Jerusalem ]{.class-0}[Talmud]{.class-2}[, Jewish fables, and tradition (]{.class-0}[Israel: A Deadly Piece of Dirt,]{.class-2}[ 2001, pg. 133). It interprets the book as an allegory in which the love of God for His people is expressed. That is why the song is read by Jews at the Passover, when they believe Jehovah chose the nation of Israel as His bride. Modern liberal rabbis and Talmudic scholars, though, are quick to tell you that modern scholarship has abandoned this position.]{.class-0}

There is a partial truth in that view. The allegorical method is not the proper way to handle the Song at all, although much of its language is plainly figurative.

Other methods of interpreting the book are the literal view and the typical view (also called "the mystical view"). The literal view focuses mainly on the sexual content of the song. According to rabbinical tradition, no Jewish young man was permitted to read the Song of Solomon until he was thirty years old. (You can imagine how enforceable that restriction was with Jewish young men, growing up, who had access to the book.) The reason for this, of course, is the sensual nature of the book, which describes not merely true platonic love, but true sexual love. The Jewish Encyclopedia has one thing right when it says such "lyrical imagery and forthright expression are mentally sensual and suggestive, yet the poem is never coarse or vulgar." This is correct.

[Origen and Eusebius both took a profane view of the literal interpretation. They taught that the Song was a story about Solomon's two girlfriends (a shepherdess and a Queen) whom he played against each other. It is kind of like a modern soap opera with its "eternal (]{.class-0}[infernal ]{.class-2}[would be a better word) triangle."]{.class-0}

Bullinger, following the commentary of Dr. C. D. Ginsburg (London, 1857), does not fare much better. They both view the Song as a simple story where a girl falls in love with a shepherd and the King tries to seduce her by bringing her into the palace and making love to her and offering her the moon. She leaves the King and returns to her shepherd sweetheart. But if you let the Bible interpret itself, Scripture with Scripture, you will see pretty quick that Ginsburg and Bullinger are off their rockers in these matters.

[In that Bible, the King, in the Old Testament, is a type of God the Father; and a shepherd, throughout the Scriptures, is a type of ]{.class-0}["the good shepherd"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:14), Jesus Christ. When Bullinger sets a type on that shepherd in the Song, that is the type he sets. Do you think God the Father and God the Son are fighting over the Bride of Christ (Rev. 19; Eph. 5) to see who gets her? Nonsense.]{.class-0}

[Your modern Christian psychiatrists and counsellors, like James Dobson, take a completely literal view of the book, but they see nothing but a treatise on marital love between a husband and wife. If that is ]{.class-0}[all]{.class-2}[ you see in the book, then you are nothing but a sex-obsessed neurotic who reflects modern American society. That is precisely the view taken by Hugh Hefner and ]{.class-0}[Playboy]{.class-2}[ in their ]{.class-0}[X-rated Bible.]{.class-2}

The typical view is far closer to the truth when approaching the Song. That is, like many other places in the Old Testament, you have an historical account which God allows to be recorded and then uses the characters, events, and places in the account as types to teach spiritual truth. The definitive passage on such teaching is found in Galatians 4:21--31, where God uses the historical events recorded in Genesis 21 to define the New Testament doctrine of Law and Grace.

[In regards to the Song of Solomon, this method of interpretation is often called the ]{.class-0}[mystical]{.class-2}[ method. In other words, the types are in a mystery form that people in the Old Testament could not understand. And of course, there is a certain truth in that (see comments on 1 Pet. 1:11--12 in the ]{.class-0}[Bible Believer's Commentary on the General Epistles,]{.class-2}[ Vol. 1).]{.class-0}

The system of interpretation taken by Martin Luther on the book was mystical-doctrinal. Luther believed the doctrines of Christianity were in the Song of Solomon in a mystery form. Basil and Theodorus, two church fathers of the Eastern Orthodox Church in Greece around the time of Chrysostom, held to a mystical-spiritual view of the book. They believed God had put spiritual lessons in a mysterious form in the Song.

[The most ridiculous of the typical interpretations is espoused by the Catholic Church (you might have known). Catholic commentators teach that the Shulamite is a picture of the Church, but then they make the Church ]{.class-0}[Mary]{.class-2}[ for some peculiar reason. We call this view the ]{.class-0}[erotic]{.class-2}[-mystical approach to the book, and it is about as far out in left field as you can get; in fact, it is all the way out of the ball park.]{.class-0}

[Now, we shall approach the book as any book in ]{.class-0}["the holy scriptures"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 1:2). We shall approach it as the living word of the living God, containing the words God wants us to have in English. We won't change one word of it. Where the scholars have something legitimate to contribute (and that won't be often), we shall give you their comments. But where they change the Scriptures because they don't agree with it or cannot understand it, we will throw the whole lot of them out without a second thought.]{.class-0}

[We will have some "rough plowing" through the Song of Solomon. In many places, our comments will simply have to be ]{.class-0}["Ich weiss nicht,"]{.class-2}[ which in plain English means "I don't know." My enemies always say, "Ruckman thinks he is right and everyone else is wrong." When I am absolutely sure about what the Scriptures say concerning a matter, you'd better believe it, brother. I am right, and any other opinion does not matter. But I take that view based on ]{.class-0}[what the Scriptures say;]{.class-2}[ I don't take that view based on my own theology or opinion.]{.class-0}

[When it comes to places in the Scriptures that are unclear or that I don't understand, I have always kept an open mind; I have never been dogmatic on those passages. I have never claimed to be a Bible scholar; I am a ]{.class-0}[student]{.class-2}[ of the Scriptures. As a student, there are several places in the Scripture where I am still learning.]{.class-0}

As a teacher of the Scriptures, though, I will give you what I can; but where I don't know, I am not going to "snow" you or "shoot the bull" with you, like many of the other commentators do, to make you think I know what I'm talking about when I don't.

[The method of interpretation which we will take will be a mixed one. As we have taught in our other commentaries, every verse of Scripture can have ]{.class-0}[three]{.class-2}[ interpretations: (1) It can have a ]{.class-0}[doctrinal]{.class-2}[ interpretation, because ]{.class-0}["all scripture\...is profitable for doctrine"]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[first]{.class-2}[ (2 Tim. 3:16). Quite often that doctrinal interpretation will deal with ]{.class-0}[prophecy.]{.class-2}[ (2) It can have an ]{.class-0}[historical]{.class-2}[ interpretation. That is, the story was an actual event that took place in history. It is not ]{.class-0}[Übergeschichte]{.class-2}[, supra-history, which is just a fancy way of saying myths, legends, fables, etc. (3) It can have a ]{.class-0}[spiritual]{.class-2}[ interpretation. That is, we can get devotional thoughts and spiritual lessons from the passage and make practical application to our situation even though the book was not written to us.]{.class-0}

[So here we have the Song of Solomon. It has 8 chapters, 117 verses, and 2,661 words. Solomon is the King mentioned seven times in the book. Solomon is a son of David and is one of the greatest types in the Bible of the Lord Jesus Christ, ]{.class-0}[the]{.class-2}[ ]{.class-0}["Son of David."]{.class-1}

In the book, we will find some of the most poignant language, in type, of God's love for us. We will learn some great lessons on fellowship, prayer, and the return of the Christ both in the Rapture and the Advent. So as we enter the pages of the Song of Solomon, we will allow the King to speak to us (2:10), and we will receive instruction (8:2).

[]{#section-0_1_cb1c1036369fc7d_67db.xhtml}

CHAPTER 1

1:1 The song of songs, which is Solomon's.

2 Let him kiss me with the kisses of his mouth: for thy love is better than wine.

3 Because of the savour of thy good ointments thy name is as ointment poured forth, therefore do the virgins love thee.

4 Draw me, we will run after thee: the king hath brought me into his chambers: we will be glad and rejoice in thee, we will remember thy love more than wine: the upright love thee.

"[The song of songs"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 1). That is not "The Song of Songs" that Russ Columbo sang and that Bing Crosby copied before Perry Como and Dean Martin both picked it up. Those old love songs had a kind of Roman Catholic "apostolic succession" of dirty singers that performed them. That "Song of Songs" goes:]{.class-0}

Song of songs,

Song of memory

And broken melody of love and life,

Nevermore to me

Can that melody

Fill the heart

With the joy once it knew\....

It's a song about some fellow remembering some song he and his girl once enjoyed before she broke up with him and left.

[Before that song, there was one written by Irving Berlin called "Where is the Song of Songs for Me?" Well, it sure was not in the Bible. It was in a movie called ]{.class-0}[Lady of the Pavements,]{.class-2}[ or as it was called in England, ]{.class-0}[Lady of the Night.]{.class-2}[ I'll give you one guess as to what that movie was about.]{.class-0}

Now, that is the world's "Song of Songs." It is a love song written to illustrate some illicit affair or some jilted romance. Neither is worth listening to one time.

"[The song of songs, which is Solomon's."]{.class-1}[ The expression ]{.class-0}["song of songs"]{.class-1}[ means it is the ]{.class-0}[best]{.class-2}[ song, the song above all other songs. Well, if that is the case, then this must be some song. Solomon wrote 1,005 songs (1 Kings 4:32). Unlike the book of Proverbs, which contains 915 of the 3,000 proverbs that Solomon spake, the ]{.class-0}["song of songs"]{.class-1}[ is the only survivor of all of Solomon's compositions.]{.class-0}

Nevertheless, Solomon was quite an accomplished musician. Handel wrote 119 symphonies, 163 pieces for baritone, 15 masses, 5 oratorios, 42 German and Italian songs, and 365 English songs. The total body of his work was 1,536 compositions. So Solomon was not only the wisest man on earth, in his day he was the greatest composer on earth.

"[Let him kiss me with the kisses of his mouth"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 2). The speaker is clearly some woman, not some fruity, Frisco faggot or double-breasted fink. This is a song about normal, straight relations between a man and a woman. This is not two queers trying to get together so that they can get government benefits for married couples and drive up insurance rates when one of them dies from GRID (AIDS in the new media).]{.class-0}

Now, if we are going to make any application beyond literal, physical love, then we have to go into typology. Nearly all of the commentators hold that the woman in the Song is a type of the Bride of Christ. The reason is that Solomon is obviously a picture of Jesus Christ Himself.

[Jesus Christ was called the ]{.class-0}["Son of David"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 1:1; John 7:42; Rom. 1:3; Matt. 22:42--45). Well, Solomon was the literal son of David (1 Kings 2:12; 2 Kings 21:7; 1 Chron. 22:5, 29:22; 2 Chron. 1:1, 35:3, etc.).]{.class-0}

"[The sure mercies of David"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 55:3) were given to David's son (2 Sam. 7:12--16). Those ]{.class-0}["sure mercies"]{.class-1}[ are found in Psalm 89, especially verses 1--4, 20--37. Those ]{.class-0}["sure mercies"]{.class-1}[ are applied by the Holy Spirit through the Apostle Paul to the Lord Jesus Christ in Acts 13:34, and they are the New Testament promise of eternal security.]{.class-0}

Furthermore, Solomon is a type of Christ in the following particulars:

1\) Solomon has a Gentile bride (1 Kings 7:8); Christ has a Gentile bride (Eph. 2:11--22).

[2) Solomon is King of the Jews (1 Kings 11:42); Christ is ]{.class-0}["King of the Jews"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 2:2; Luke 1:31--33).]{.class-0}

3\) Solomon could answer any question put to him (1 Kings 10:1--3); Christ was able to answer any question put to Him (Matt. 22:15--46).

4\) Solomon got back all the land promised to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob (1 Kings 4:21; 1 Chron. 18:3); Christ will get it when He comes again (Ezek. 47--48).

5\) A Gentile Queen comes to see Solomon (1 Kings 10:1--13) just as the Gentiles will come to Christ in the Millennial kingdom (Zech. 14:16--19; Isa. 11:9--12; Matt. 8:11).

Of course, Solomon is also a type of the Antichrist. When the number 666 shows up in 1 Kings 10:44 and 2 Chronicles 9:13, the Bible starts discussing the sins of Solomon in regards to multiplying gold, horses, and wives (Deut. 17:14--17), then Solomon turns to idolatry (1 Kings 11) and becomes a type of the Antichrist. But up until that point, he is a type of Jesus Christ reigning in His Millennial kingdom.

If Solomon is a type of Christ, then any woman connected with him as a bride or a wife in the Song of Solomon has to be a type of the Church, the Body of Christ (Eph. 5:22--32). So when you get to Song of Solomon 2:8--12, you have the Bridegroom coming to get the Bride: it is a picture of the Rapture of the Church.

Of course, your Hyperdispensationalist will say, "No, the Church is an object of revelation, and it is not revealed until Paul shows up in the book of Acts. So the rapture of Song of Solomon 2 is a post-Tribulation rapture of Jewish saints." But that will not work. The Bride of the Song of Solomon is a singular entity like the Body of Christ (Eph. 4:4).

[Look at Song of Solomon 6:8. ]{.class-0}["There are threescore queens, and fourscore concubines, and virgins without number."]{.class-1}[ Those are all women in the household of Solomon. The typology is the different groups of saints in the Tribulation (Rev. 7), and although they are ]{.class-0}["without number"]{.class-1}[ here in the Old Testament, when you get to the New Testament, their exact number is given. It is 144,000, and they are said to be ]{.class-0}["virgins"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 14:4) in the very same passage where Christ appears for a post-Tribulation rapture (Rev. 14:14--20 cf. Matt. 13:37--43).]{.class-0}

[Jesus Christ Himself calls them ]{.class-0}["virgins" ]{.class-1}[in the Parable of the Ten Virgins (Matt. 25:1--13). Note in verse 6 of Matthew 25 that the virgins are called out to ]{.class-0}["meet"]{.class-1}[ the Bridegroom, not marry him. Those virgins can "run out" of the Holy Spirit, and the Bridegroom says of the virgins to whom that happens: ]{.class-0}["I know you not"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 25:12). That is not true of anybody in the Body of Christ (Rom. 8:29; Eph. 4:30; Phil. 1:6; 1 Cor. 1:7--8).]{.class-0}

[But go back and look at Song of Solomon 6:9. In distinction to ]{.class-0}["virgins without number,"]{.class-1}[ the Bride is said to be ]{.class-0}["but ONE; she is the ONLY ONE of her mother, she is the choice ONE of her that bare her."]{.class-1}[ That is three times in one verse.]{.class-0}

[The Bride of Christ is ]{.class-0}["one body"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 4:4). The marriage of Jesus Christ to the Church is likened to the original marriage of Genesis 2 where there was only ]{.class-0}[one]{.class-2}[ man and ]{.class-0}[one]{.class-2}[ woman (Eph. 5:30--32). When Paul talks about the Church as the Bride of Christ, he says, ]{.class-0}["For I have espoused you to one husband, that I may present you as A CHASTE VIRGIN]{.class-1}[ \[singular\]]{.class-0}[ to Christ"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 11:2).]{.class-0}

So the Bride in the Song of Solomon does not typify the Old Testament Jewish saint or the Tribulation Jewish saint. She is a picture of the New Testament Church. This teaches a great truth in regards to the "Dry Cleaner" heresy (Hyperdispensationalism). It is this: although the Church is not revealed in the Old Testament and its revelation is given to the Apostle Paul after Acts 9, it is there in type, and the Holy Spirit used the types found in the Old Testament (Eve, Rebekah, the bride here in the Song, etc.) to reveal the Church to Paul. That is why Paul quotes the Old Testament continuously in his epistles in regards to New Testament doctrine. Sure, you would not have known anything about it unless God had shown it to Paul, but that does not mean that it was not there.

The standard Hyperdispensationalist operating procedure is that there is nothing in my pocket until I take it out and show it to you. When I do that, the object miraculously appears from nowhere, for obviously you did not see it nor know it was there before. Do you see how ridiculous the position is?

"[Let him kiss me with the kisses of his mouth: for thy love is better than wine"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 2). In type, this Song is about the love relationship between Christ and His Church. The ]{.class-0}[kiss, ]{.class-2}[here, is defined as a kiss of love.]{.class-0}

[In the Bible, there are several different kinds of kisses. There is the ]{.class-0}[filial ]{.class-2}[or familiar kiss between family members or dear friends (Gen. 27:26; Ruth 1:14; 1 Sam. 20:41; 1 Kings 19:20). There is the ]{.class-0}[unholy ]{.class-2}[kiss like the strange woman gives the young man in Proverbs 7:13 when she is trying to seduce him. There is the ]{.class-0}[hypocritical ]{.class-2}[kiss, like Judas gives to Christ before he betrays Him (Mark 14:45), or like Joab gave to Amasa before he killed him (2 Sam. 20:9); it is the kind of kiss that a politician would give in order to get votes (2 Sam. 15:5). Paul also talks about a ]{.class-0}["holy kiss"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 16:16; 1 Cor. 16:20), which Peter calls ]{.class-0}["a kiss of charity"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 5:14), between members of the local church.]{.class-0}

[A kiss can be not only a token of love, it can be a token of willing submission and of reconciliation. In Psalm 2:12, the unsaved Gentiles are commanded to ]{.class-0}["kiss the Son, lest he be angry, and ye perish from the way."]{.class-1}[ In the Millennium, the Gentiles will come to Christ and bow before Him. I do not think they will kiss His ring like people do to the Pope today. They will probably do as people did in the Middle Ages when making obeisance to a King. They will kiss His hand, right where their eyes can see the nail prints as they do it (Zech. 12:10; John 20:25).]{.class-0}

[The kiss of Psalm 2:12, though, is not the kind of kiss that a Christian gives to Christ. We do not have to kiss Jesus Christ when we see Him in order to keep Him from being angry with us. We are already reconciled to Him (2 Cor. 5:18--20), and Paul said that we are already ]{.class-0}["accepted in the beloved"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 1:6). The kisses that we will give the Lord when we see Him will be like the kisses the sinful woman of Luke 7:37--38 gave Him. She kissed Him because ]{.class-0}[He forgave her sins]{.class-2}[ (Luke 7:40--50). The kisses we give to Jesus Christ will be kisses of love and gratitude for delivering us from sin, Satan, death, and Hell.]{.class-0}

[Back to verse 2:]{.class-0}[ "Thy love is better than wine."]{.class-1}[ Then a Christian does not have to fool with wine because he has something better: the love of Christ. A Christian does not need wine or liquor because of his status in Christ. Proverbs 31:4 says, ]{.class-0}["It is not for kings, O Lemuel, it is not for kings to drink wine; nor princes strong drink."]{.class-1}[ Then a Christian does not need to drink wine because the same Lord who ]{.class-0}["loved us, and washed us from our sins in his own blood\...hath made us KINGS and priests unto God and his Father"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 1:5--6).]{.class-0}

[For whom is wine made? Proverbs 31:6,]{.class-0}[ "Give strong drink unto him that is READY TO PERISH."]{.class-1}[ That is not you if you are saved. John 3:16, ]{.class-0}["For God so loved the world, that he gave his only begotten Son, that WHOSOEVER BELIEVETH IN HIM SHOULD NOT PERISH, but have everlasting life."]{.class-1}

"[And wine unto those that be of heavy hearts, Let him drink, and forget his poverty and remember his misery no more"]{.class-1}[ (Prov. 31:6--7). I can hear someone say, "You see, a Christian should drink wine when he is sad or poor so he can forget his troubles." That is not true; a Christian does not need to fool with liquor even in those circumstances. A Christian is not like an unsaved person. A Christian can have joy in the midst of sorrow, and his happiness is not dependent upon his possessions. Second Corinthians 6:10 says, ]{.class-0}["As sorrowful, yet ALWAY REJOICING; as poor, yet making many rich; as having nothing, and yet POSSESSING ALL THINGS."]{.class-1}

I made the mistake one time of joking with a pastor friend of mine who was in dire straits. He was having some bad trouble in his church. After sitting in his car with him for over an hour and listening to him pour out his woes, I tried to lighten the atmosphere a little. I said, "Well, Bro. So-and-So, there's only one thing to do in a situation like this, and that's to go out and get drunk." I laughed to show it was a joke, but he did not take it that way. He showed up at church drunk the next day, and when his parishioners asked him why, he said that Ruckman told him to do it!

[Now, a Christian can and will experience bad trouble in this life, but he does not need to turn to drugs or alcohol to drown his misery. I have been through two years in my life that I would ]{.class-0}[never]{.class-2}[ want to relive again, and I am here to tell you that you can come out victorious. The thing is, don't stay by yourself mulling over your troubles. Get outdoors. Go fishing or hunting. Work in the garden. Play golf. Jog. Just don't stay where the walls are "closing in" on you.]{.class-0}

Get with some friends who are happy in Christ and don't talk about your troubles all the time. Let some of their joy wash off on you. Get the brethren praying for you. I could not have made it through my troubles without the prayers of the brethren.

Consider the fact that your troubles are not as bad as other folk's. Karl Menninger, the dean of American psychiatrists, used to recommend that if you are depressed over your troubles all of the time that you "go across the tracks" and find someone who has some real problems (or problems worse than yours) and help him out. It will not only take your mind off your own problems, it will put those problems in their proper perspective.

[Be thankful for the good things God has given you and obey that command to ]{.class-0}["rejoice in the Lord alway; and again I say, rejoice"]{.class-1}[ (Phil. 4:4). If you start rejoicing in the Lord, you will find that you are able to deal with your troubles better because ]{.class-0}["the joy of the LORD is your strength:]{.class-1}[ (Neh. 8:10).]{.class-0}

And above all, stay on your knees in prayer and keep your nose in that Book. You may think that the heavens are brass and that you are not getting anything out of your Bible reading besides marking time. But when you are in real trouble, you need to keep the lines of communication open between you and God. You have to remember that the Lord's timing is not our timing. He will sometimes let something go past what you consider to be the point of no return before He will deal with you about the matter. If you are not constant in prayer and reading your Bible, you are liable to miss the Lord when He is ready to talk to you about your situation.

But whatever you do, do not turn to the bottle or a pill for your consolation. Though both alcohol and drugs may initially lower your inhibitions and give you a temporary euphoria, both will leave you feeling more miserable than you were to start with. Liquor will not help you with your trouble, Christian; it will only mock you in your problem. It is a liar; it is a cheat.

[Proverbs 20:1,]{.class-0}[ "Wine is a mocker, strong drink is raging; and whosoever is deceived thereby is not wise."]{.class-1}

[When it comes to alcohol and the Christian, that Bible says, ]{.class-0}["Ye have not eaten bread, neither have ye drunk wine or strong drink: that ye might know that I am the LORD your God"]{.class-1}[ (Deut. 29:6).]{.class-0}

[Paul said, ]{.class-0}["And be not drunk with wine, wherein is excess]{.class-1}[ \[notice that he did not say, "Do not drink wine in excess until you get drunk." The ]{.class-0}["excess"]{.class-1}[ is in the wine itself, and that is what brings on drunkenness\]]{.class-0}[;]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[but be filled with the Spirit"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 5:18).]{.class-0}

[The only legitimate use for wine or any other kind of alcoholic drink in the life of a Christian is as medicine. Paul told Timothy: ]{.class-0}["use a little wine for thy stomach's sake and thine often infirmities"]{.class-1}[ (1 Tim. 5:23). Every "sneaky pete" in every rescue mission from here to Fairbanks, Alaska knows that verse is in the Bible, and not one of them ever applies it right.]{.class-0}

[The verse said to ]{.class-0}["use"]{.class-1}[ the wine, not drink it. You say, "What's the difference?" The difference is between using a measured amount as medication and pouring a glass before dinner or having a "nightcap" or ordering a "jigger," etc. The verse did not say have a martini at social gatherings or a "shot" to steady your nerves.]{.class-0}

[The verse said to ]{.class-0}["use A LITTLE."]{.class-1}[ How little should you use? Look on the bottle of "NyQuil" or cough syrup and follow the directions. ]{.class-0}[That's]{.class-2}[ how little.]{.class-0}

If you are not sick enough to need medicine with alcohol in it, then do not use it. If you cannot use a small, measured amount when needing medicine, then do not drink it. Is that clear?

[Proverbs 23:32 says of wine, ]{.class-0}["At the last it biteth like a serpent, and stingeth like an adder."]{.class-1}[ If you do not want to get bitten, don't go into the rattlesnake den.]{.class-0}

"[Because of the savour of thy good ointments thy name is as ointment poured forth"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 3). So perfume makers put their names on their perfumes, and they are known by the quality of their product: Calvin Klein, Old Spice, Ralph Lauren, Estée Lauder, etc.]{.class-0}

[The Biblical application is recorded by Solomon in Ecclesiastes 7:1. ]{.class-0}["A good name is better than precious ointment."]{.class-1}

[Verse 3 is best illustrated in the story of Mary, the sister of Martha, anointing Christ's feet. John 12:3, ]{.class-0}["Then took Mary a pound of ointment of spikenard, very costly, and anointed the feet of Jesus, and wiped his feet with her hair: and the house was filled with the odour of the ointment."]{.class-1}

[Because she broke the alabaster box (Matt. 26:7) and released the odor of the ointment in service to Jesus Christ, the Lord gave her a good name. Matthew 26:13, ]{.class-0}["Verily I say unto you, Wheresoever this gospel shall be preached in the whole world, then shall also this, that this woman hath done, be told for a memorial for her."]{.class-1}

[Verse 3 is also a beautiful picture of Jesus Christ Himself. When Jesus Christ was crucified, the ]{.class-0}["box"]{.class-1}[ containing the perfume was broken, and the ]{.class-0}["sweet savour"]{.class-1}[ of Christ's sacrifice was released (Gen. 8:20--21). As a result, the name of Jesus Christ is poured out around the world.]{.class-0}

[Christ said, ]{.class-0}["And I, if I be lifted up from the earth]{.class-1}[ \[the crucifixion, cf. John 3:14\]]{.class-0}[,]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[will draw all men unto me"]{.class-1}[ (John 12:32). If Jesus Christ had not died and rose again for sinners, He would have been just some obscure wannabe prophet on the backside of the Roman Empire. More than likely, you would not know anything of the "teaching of the lowly Nazarene." But today, people in places like Mongolia, Patagonia, New Zealand, Point Barrow, Alaska, the Chad in Africa, Ho Chi Minh City (Saigon), and Hyderabad, India know the name of Jesus Christ. Why? Because ]{.class-0}["Christ died for our sins according to the scriptures; and that he was buried, and that he rose again the third day according to the scriptures"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 15:1--4). That is the Gospel. That is the Gospel Jesus told His disciples to take ]{.class-0}["unto the uttermost part of the earth"]{.class-1}[ (Acts 1:8) It is the Gospel which Paul sought to preach where Christ was not named (Rom. 15:20).]{.class-0}

[Verse 3:]{.class-0}[ "Therefore do the virgins love thee."]{.class-1}[ As we have already seen, those ]{.class-0}["virgins"]{.class-1}[ are a type of the Jewish saints in the Tribulation (Matt. 25; Rev. 14). Modern corruptions of the Bible, like the ]{.class-0}[RSV, NIV,]{.class-2}[ and ]{.class-0}[NASV]{.class-2}[, destroy the typology by changing the word ]{.class-0}["virgins"]{.class-1}[ here and in Revelation 14:4. But the Hebrew word is ]{.class-0}[alma,]{.class-2}[ just as in Isaiah 7:14, and the Holy Spirit's translation of the word is ]{.class-0}["virgin"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 1:23).]{.class-0}

[Notice that these virgins can love the Bridegroom without being married to Him. For those who believe that salvation is the same in every dispensation, it should be noted that the Tribulation saints can stand with the Lamb (Rev. 14:1), they can sing a new song which is ]{.class-0}["the song of the Lamb"]{.class-1}[ (along with ]{.class-0}["the song of Moses,"]{.class-1}[ by the way; Rev. 14:3 cf. Rev. 15:3), they can ]{.class-0}["follow the Lamb"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 14:4), they can be ]{.class-0}["the firstfruits\...to the Lamb"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 14:4) ]{.class-0}[without being]{.class-2}[ ]{.class-0}["the bride, the Lamb's wife"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 21:9), which is the position every saved person in the Church Age holds.]{.class-0}

"[Draw me"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 4). And that is why Jesus Christ was crucified (John 12:32). ]{.class-0}["Draw me."]{.class-1}[ And if the Lord does not draw you, you cannot come to Christ (John 6:44).]{.class-0}

The Calvinistic perversion of this doctrine is called "Irresistible Grace." It is the fourth point on Calvin's "TULIP." The idea is that if God has chosen you as one of "the elect," His Grace will draw you to receive Jesus Christ, and there is nothing you can do about it. In connection with Calvin's Limited Atonement, it is guaranteed that only the people who are "elect" will be drawn by the Father to receive Jesus Christ.

I have talked to some of the Hardshell Baptists and Presbyterians and Christian Reformed who believed all five points of Calvin's system and still did not know where they were going when they died. I have talked to an eighty-year-old man on his porch as he spat his tobacco juice into a number 5 honey bucket. His response to the question "Have you received Christ as your Saviour," was: "Well, no man cometh except the Father draw him; you believe that, don't cha?" I have talked to these fellows after they had just answered the invitation at a Ralph Barnard meeting (a five-point TULIP evangelist back in the 50s) and have had them say to me in a bland, monotone voice, "Well, Bro. Ruckman, I hope I am one of the elect." They accepted all five points of Calvin's TULIP and had no more assurance of their salvation than if they had believed in Easter lilies.

[Listen, if that Bible is right about Hell (and there is no doubt in my mind about it), and I believed like some of you TULIP sniffers believe, I would go in my room and shut the door. Then I would get on my face before God in prayer, and I would not get up until I knew I was one of the elect. You say, "What would you pray?" I would pray the prayer of Song of Solomon 1:4---]{.class-0}["Draw me."]{.class-1}[ I mean, if you cannot come to Jesus Christ "unless the Father draws you," then ]{.class-0}[ask the Father to draw you]{.class-2}[. Then I would ask God to ]{.class-0}[let me know for sure]{.class-2}[ that I am one of the elect. After all, Paul knew it (Rom. 8:38--39; 2 Tim. 1:12), Peter knew it (1 Pet. 1:3--4), and John knew it (1 John 5:13). Why don't you?]{.class-0}

[Who are you to talk about Perseverance of the Saints when you do not even know that you are a saint? I would not be a fool and ]{.class-0}[hope]{.class-2}[ that I was one of the "elect." I would ]{.class-0}[make sure]{.class-2}[ that I was one. There is no excuse for not being one of God's elect and knowing it.]{.class-0}

[Now, seriously, let's put the Calvinistic nonsense aside and find out exactly how the Father draws you to Jesus Christ. Well, the word for ]{.class-0}["draw"]{.class-1}[ in the Bible means to attract like a magnet. The first thing that God did in the New Testament to attract you to Jesus Christ was to show His love for you by sacrificing His own Son at Calvary (John 12:32). The next thing that He did was to send His Holy Spirit into the world to convict you of your sin and testify of Jesus Christ (John 15:26, 16:8--11). Then He sends you the Gospel message through the word of God; He gives that message to you through the medium of a preacher (Rom. 10:9--17). That preacher is any Christian (man, woman, or child) who gives the sinner a Gospel witness of some sort (Gospel tract, actual witness, a sermon, etc.). Moreover, God has put enough of His word in the physical creation and in the conscience to draw any man to more light until he comes to the Gospel and receives Christ ]{.class-0}[if he wants to]{.class-2}[ (see comments on Rom. 1--2 and 10:18 in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

[So God has given the blood atonement, the Holy Spirit, the word of God, and, quite often, a preacher of the Gospel to draw you to Jesus Christ. The drawing, though, is not the accepting. All men are drawn to the cross of Christ in one way or another, but not all men accept Christ and are saved. It takes more than God drawing you to be saved; it takes a positive response on your part to God's invitation. Rebekah was asked by her father and brother in regards to Eleazer, the steward of Abraham and Isaac, ]{.class-0}["Wilt thou go with this man?"]{.class-1}[ There is the "drawing." Her response was ]{.class-0}["I will go"]{.class-1}[ (Gen. 24:58). There is the acceptance.]{.class-0}

[Back in Song of Solomon 1:4, the woman prays ]{.class-0}["Draw me."]{.class-1}[ She then follows it up with ]{.class-0}["we will run after thee."]{.class-1}[ There is the ]{.class-0}[acceptance]{.class-2}[. It is not God dragging you irresistibly kicking and screaming into Heaven. It is God drawing you with the love and claims of Christ and you willingly responding to the Holy Spirit by trusting Jesus Christ and following Him.]{.class-0}

[That ]{.class-0}["we"]{.class-1}[ there in verse 4 is a problem. If you make it the Body of Christ and connect it to the ]{.class-0}["me"]{.class-1}[ before it, then it would be a reference to each individual member in the Church. But it could be a reference to the Bride and the virgins. Both have to believe on Christ for salvation (the Tribulation virgins have works added to their faith---Rev. 14:12).]{.class-0}

[If that ]{.class-0}["Draw me"]{.class-1}[ is a reference to the Rapture, then the ]{.class-0}["we will run after thee"]{.class-1}[ would have to include both the Rapture of the Church and the post-Tribulation rapture of the Jewish saints. Both the Bride and the virgins could ]{.class-0}["be glad and rejoice in thee"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["remember thy love more than wine."]{.class-1}[ The virgins love the King (vs. 3) without marrying Him, and verse 4 ends with ]{.class-0}["the upright love thee." "The upright"]{.class-1}[ is a reference to saints in the Old Testament and never, doctrinally, to New Testament Christians. Look up the references in a concordance. The word ]{.class-0}["upright"]{.class-1}[ appears only one time in the New Testament, and it has nothing to do with being a Christian or a saint at all (Acts 14:10). In the Old Testament, an ]{.class-0}["upright"]{.class-1}[ person is someone who not only trusts God but tries to live a righteous life.]{.class-0}

[So if you make the ]{.class-0}["we"]{.class-1}[ of verse 4 both the Bride and the virgins of verse 3, then what you have is both groups being caught up to Heaven in different raptures and both groups loving the King. But only one, the Bride, is taken into His chambers to marry Him.]{.class-0}

[Note once again in verse 4:]{.class-0}[ "we will remember thy love more than wine."]{.class-1}[ The solution for a chronic alcoholic is not "AA"; it is Jesus Christ. If a drunkard will fall in love with Jesus Christ and stay in love with Jesus Christ, he will get victory over the bottle, and he will not touch the stuff anymore.]{.class-0}

Groups like Alcoholics Anonymous can get you off liquor for a while. Many alcoholics have to go through the program several times because they keep "jumping off the wagon." In the more successful cases, the alcoholics get off liquor and do not take another drink, but they still have an appetite for it. That is why members claim they are still "recovering" alcoholics, even if they have not taken a drink for fifteen years.

[I am not making a blanket condemnation of programs like that when I say those things. I have recommended folks to go to AA when they had a particularly hard time trying to quit. I have sent a young man to go through a secular drug rehabilitation program to get off the junk. I understand that they can be helpful. But they are not the solution. Only Jesus Christ can get you off the bottle and cause you to ]{.class-0}[enjoy]{.class-2}[ being off it.]{.class-0}

When I got saved, I was not a chronic drunk yet, but I was well on my way to becoming one. I drank beer pretty consistently: two to eight bottles a day; I could polish off two cases over a weekend. But when I came to Christ, the Lord not only took the liquor away from me, He also took the taste for it away from me.

[When the Bible says ]{.class-0}["we will remember thy love more than wine,"]{.class-1}[ I know personally about what it is talking. If you want the memories that wine and liquor conjure up for me, read chapter 10 in my autobiography ]{.class-0}[The Full Cup.]{.class-2}[ I have entitled that chapter "Falling Into Ruin" because that is what alcohol was doing to my life. After reading that chapter, go get the book ]{.class-0}[Memoirs of a Twentieth Century Circuit Rider.]{.class-2}[ Those are the memories that my life in Christ bring to mind. You talk about a contrast!]{.class-0}

[I have summed up that contrast in the Epilogue to ]{.class-0}[The Full Cup.]{.class-2}[ I will briefly recount it here. When I was stationed in the Philippines, before I was saved, I remember one particularly bad night I had in Angeles City after a ten-day "binge." That night I had pulled out all the stops, and I nearly got myself killed in a brawl at a nightclub. I was walking back to the depot late that night. I was about half drunk. I stopped in a dry caribou wallow on the perimeter of the depot. I was so upset over the events of the night that I stopped right there and began crying out to the heavens for help. I ended up crying, rolling around in the dirt, and calling out, "God, if You're up there and I mean anything to you, I need some HELP!" Nothing happened then, but eventually God got me back home to the States. He let me get to the end of my rope; then He put a Bible in my hands and let me know, in no uncertain terms, that I was headed for Hell. God finally finished answering that prayer by sending Hugh Pyle to lead me to Christ.]{.class-0}

[I compare that experience with the next time I was in the Philippines. By then I had been saved 46 years. Those 46 years had been filled with planting three local churches; preaching in churches, prisons, Bible camps, revivals, Bible conferences, etc.; setting up a Bible school and training hundreds of young men and women in the Scriptures and in the ministry; and raising three families. This time I was not in the Philippines serving Uncle Sam and getting into trouble. I was in the service of the ]{.class-0}["captain of our salvation"]{.class-1}[ (Heb. 2:10) to teach Bible to 200 Filipino pastors.]{.class-0}

[After finding the very hole where I had prayed that night 49 years earlier, I headed back to Manila. On the way, I saw a small house with a sign in front of it saying "Bible Baptist Church, the Home of the ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible." The sign was six by ten foot with a painting taken from my tract "Tell It Like It Is." It was a perfect reproduction of Christ knocking at a sinner's door.]{.class-0}

I stopped and knocked at the door. A pretty, young Filipino woman answered the door. She was the pastor's wife. "Could I speak to your husband, please?" I asked. "He's not here right now," she said. "He's gone down to Iloilo to hear Dr. Peter Ruckman teach the Bible."

For a moment an incredible feeling came over me that I cannot sufficiently describe. I did not know who I was, what I was doing, or where I was going.

"[Dr. Peter Ruckman?" I asked myself incredulously. "Who is ]{.class-0}[Doctor]{.class-2}[ Peter Ruckman? Do I know a Dr. Peter Ruckman who teaches the Bible? This is Angeles City. I'm Lt. Peter S. Ruckman. Who is this Dr. Peter Ruckman she is talking about?"]{.class-0}

Out loud I did not say anything. I was too overwhelmed with the contrast of what God had done in my life. It was like a different man were standing there.

"[We will remember thy love more than wine."]{.class-1}

"[The upright love thee"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 4). We have already discussed ]{.class-0}["the upright"]{.class-1}[ from an Old Testament point of view. It has nothing to do with the doctrinal position of a sinner in nature. Doctrinally, we understand that ]{.class-0}["there is none righteous, no, not one: There is none that understandeth, there is none that seeketh after God\....For all have sinned, and come short of the glory of God"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 3:10--11, 23).]{.class-0}

[But practically speaking, God recognized the good works that a man did in the Old Testament. God called Job ]{.class-0}["perfect and upright"]{.class-1}[ (Job. 1:1) before Job ever repented of his self-righteousness (Job 42:1--6). So back in the Old Testament, and in the future in the Tribulation, being upright is connected with one's salvation.]{.class-0}

[If we applied Song of Solomon 1:4 to a New Testament setting, we would have to say this: although no man in the Church Age is saved by his good works in any way, shape, or form, nevertheless, if a man is a Gentile who has never heard the Gospel of Jesus Christ, living right ]{.class-0}[does ]{.class-2}[benefit him. When God sees an unsaved Gentile who is trying to live a righteous, moral life, and yet he has never heard anything about Jesus Christ, the blood atonement, the resurrection, the Gospel, etc., God Almighty obligates Himself to get the good news to that person (see comments on Rom. 2:6--10 in that Commentary). If a man is truly upright in character, and not merely self-righteous, when presented with the Gospel, he will love and accept Jesus Christ as his Saviour (see Cornelius in Acts 10).]{.class-0}

Bob Jones Sr. used to say that a woman is not a good woman if she turns down Jesus Christ. If she were truly a good woman, she would appreciate Someone who loved her enough to die for her.

[Look at Proverbs 8:35--36. In those verses, wisdom is personified as a woman speaking. But if you look at Colossians 2:3, you will see that in Jesus Christ is ]{.class-0}["hid all the treasures of wisdom and knowledge"]{.class-1}[; and in 1 Corinthians 1:30, Christ ]{.class-0}["is made unto us wisdom."]{.class-1}[ So we can read Proverbs 8:35--36 as if Jesus Christ were speaking.]{.class-0}

"[For whoso findeth me]{.class-1}[ (a man finds Christ) ]{.class-0}[findeth life]{.class-1}[ (eternal life)]{.class-0}[,]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[and shall obtain favour of the LORD. But he that sinneth against me wrongeth his own soul: all they that hate me love death."]{.class-1}

[So if you hate Jesus Christ, then you are not truly upright. You may be a self-righteous Pharisee seeking to justify yourself, but you are not ]{.class-0}["upright."]{.class-1}[ An upright man will find Christ when God presents Him to him, and when he does, he receives eternal life as a free gift. He will recognize that although he is trying to live right, that he has not always done so. He accepts God's testimony against him. So when presented with the righteousness of God through the sacrifice of a sinless man, he accepts that too, and he loves the One who did it.]{.class-0}

The self-righteous man will not accept God's testimony against him. He figures that he is the exception to what God says in Romans 3. He believes his good works will outweigh his bad works and gain him entrance into Heaven. So when told that Jesus Christ and His blood atonement are the only way, he disdains the sacrifice of Christ.

There is no neutral ground with the Lord. You either love Him and what He did for you on the cross, or you hate Him and embrace death in the Lake of Fire.

5 I am black, but comely, O ye daughters of Jerusalem, as the tents of Kedar, as the curtains of Solomon.

6 Look not upon me, because I am black, because the sun hath looked upon me: my mother's children were angry with me; they made me the keeper of the vineyards; but mine own vineyard have I not kept.

[Verse 5 is a definitive verse in the Song when trying to locate, historically, who the Bride is. The Bride is set in contrast to the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem." ]{.class-1}[She is Gentile, not Jewish. Moreover, she is a Gentile with black skin, which marks her out as a Nigress from ]{.class-0}["the land of Ham"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 105:23, 27; 106:22).]{.class-0}

[That Hamitic bride is found in 1 Kings 3:1, ]{.class-0}["And Solomon made affinity with Pharaoh king of Egypt, and took Pharaoh's daughter, and brought her into the city of David."]{.class-1}

[The Egyptians were descendants of Ham (Mizraim---Gen. 10:6). Egypt is located in Africa, and the Bible calls it ]{.class-0}["the land of Ham"]{.class-1}[ in Psalm 105:23, 27 and Psalm 106:22. The word ]{.class-0}[Ham]{.class-2}[ means "burnt black" in Hebrew.]{.class-0}

[Now, people like Elijah Mohammed and Malcolm X and Louis Farakan are so eager to convert all the major characters in the Bible into colored people in order to remove the stigma God placed on the race back in Genesis 9:25, that they miss some of the greatest typology in the Bible in regards to their lineage. Moreover, in their eagerness to distance themselves from a "white man's" religion like Christianity, they follow a man (Mohammed) whose religion still trades in black slaves to this day and practices mutilation of black women (female circumcision) throughout the areas of Africa where Islam is dominant. If you do not believe me, just check with any missionary in places like Niger, the Chad, the Sudan, Egypt, and Algeria. Go to somebody who knows what is going on because he lives among the people 24 hours a day, 7 days a week, 365 days a year; not some news media lackey who stays in the best motel in the country and is afraid to report the truth because the Moslems may kill him for being pro-Jewish or pro-Christian, and who only ventures out among the people to set up staged shots for publication of "poor, oppressed" Moslem children (see ]{.class-0}[Israel: A Deadly Piece of Dirt]{.class-2}[ for examples).]{.class-0}

If you are a black, then here are the facts about how God helped colored folk throughout the Bible transcend the curse He placed on them because of their father Ham.

1\) The first person saved in the New Testament exactly as we are saved today was a black man (Acts 8:37).

2\) Every Christian is likened to a slave knocked down on the block (see Commentary on Philemon).

3\) Jesus Christ used a black woman as an example of the Millennial gathering of the Gentiles (Matt. 12:42).

4\) Nearly every example of the Bride of Christ in the Old Testament is a woman with a Hamitic genealogy.

[Let's look at that last one. Joseph was one of the greatest types of Christ in the Bible; he was a type of Christ in 154 particulars. Joseph had a Gentile bride who was an Egyptian: ]{.class-0}["Asenath the daughter of Potipherah priest of On"]{.class-1}[ (Gen. 41:45).]{.class-0}

[Christ was a prophet like unto Moses, and Moses had an Ethiopian wife (Num. 12:1). Solomon was a type of Christ as the son of David; he not only took Pharaoh's daughter as his wife, the mother of Rehoboam, Solomon's son, was ]{.class-0}["Naamah the Ammonitess"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 14:21). The Ammonites were the offspring of an incestuous relationship between Lot and his daughters, who came from an Egyptian mother (see comments on Gen. 12--13 in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

Ruth, the great grandmother of King David, was a Moabitess, also with an Hamitic lineage through Lot's daughters. The whole book of Ruth is written to illustrate how the bridegroom, Boaz, redeems his Gentile bride, Ruth (Ruth 4:4).

[So the woman here in Song of Solomon is a Hamite: Pharaoh's daughter. She is a type of the Bride of Christ. She describes herself as ]{.class-0}["black, but comely."]{.class-1}[ That is, she may be a black woman who is not an Israelite, but she is still attractive. We would say today that she is pretty or beautiful or lovely.]{.class-0}

[Hence, the radical colored folks say, "Black is beautiful." They do not know from where they get it, but they get it from the Bible. A lot of common expressions are like that. If you want a thorough list of them, get the book ]{.class-0}[Just Say the Word!]{.class-2}[ from the Bible Baptist Bookstore.]{.class-0}

[Of course, the verse did not say the woman was beautiful ]{.class-0}[because ]{.class-2}[she was black. It said that she was beautiful ]{.class-0}[despite ]{.class-2}[the fact that she was black. She is not bragging about her race. In the Bible, black folk find mercy with God when they take a position of ]{.class-0}[humility.]{.class-2}[ In the Gospels, a Syro-Phoenician woman (the Phoenicians were Hamites---Gen. 10:16) comes to Jesus so her daughter can be delivered from a devil. Christ was rude to her and ignored her. When she finally bothered the disciples enough for them to get the Lord's attention in the matter, He called her a dog (Mark 7:27).]{.class-0}

[Do you know what the word for a female dog is? All of those corrupt Bibles that talk about translating the Scriptures into modern English would not ]{.class-0}[dare]{.class-2}[ translate what Christ called that woman in Matthew 15:26 and Mark 7:27 into ]{.class-0}[real]{.class-2}[ modern English.]{.class-0}

[But that woman got what she wanted from the Lord. Do you know why? Because she humbled herself and took her place under the Lord's table as one of ]{.class-0}[His dogs.]{.class-2}

[That Bible says, ]{.class-0}["God resisteth the proud, and giveth grace to the humble"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 5:5). The "Black Pride" movement is just as damnable and hellish as the "Gay Pride" movement. It goes far beyond being grateful to God for being born black and honoring one's heritage. It is actual pride that brings with it a spirit of obnoxious arrogance and conceit. It magnifies the most sinful characteristics of the black race.]{.class-0}

Don't believe me? Think I am just spouting bigoted, white-supremacist rhetoric? Ok, here we go.

Here is Martin Luther King Jr., a black Baptist "minister." After going all around the country with "peaceful civil disobedience" that resulted in race riots and looting wherever he went, after "I have a dream" and "Free at last, free at last; thank God Almighty, I'm free at last," do you know what he was doing the night before he got shot? He was shacking up with two women, neither of whom was his wife. Apparently being "free at last" meant free to fornicate and raise hell on a nationwide scale.

Here is Bishop Tutu, an Episcopalian "minister" from South Africa. He told the whole American populace that if they did not oppose the white "apartheid" government of South Africa that they could "go to Hell." That is some way for a Christian minister to talk, isn't it?

Do you know what happened when the whites were "kicked out" of office in South Africa and Nelson Mandela, a Marxist political terrorist awarded with the civilian Congressional Medal of Honor by Slick Willie, took control? The rape and murder rate perpetrated by blacks skyrocketed to a point higher than any other country in Africa. South Africa had been the most stable and economically prosperous country in Africa. It isn't anymore.

Here is Jesse Jackson, another "Baptist minister." What has he been doing the whole time he has been running around the country trying to take control of the Democratic Party? Why, he has been keeping a mistress on the side and raising a bastard child.

[Here is modern black "music" using the ]{.class-0}[F]{.class-2}[ word and describing sex in detail in songs and black women doing "the bumps and the grinds" on music videos. It is the kind of stuff that used to be confined to burlesque shows in the worst part of town. Darwin! Progress! Now it is pumped right into your living room via cable and satellite television.]{.class-0}

Here is Bill Cosby, a black actor and educator, being booed and called an "Uncle Tom" for telling the black folk to get an education, learn to talk right, stop using and listening to foul language and cursing, stop beating up on their wives, stop whoring around, get married, and raise their children to be responsible citizens. Can you imagine being booed for saying those things?

[That is "Black Pride." It is just as bad as "White Pride," "Gay Pride," or any other kind of pride. Pride is what is known as the "original sin." It is Lucifer saying, ]{.class-0}["I will ascend into heaven, I will exalt my throne above the stars of God\...I will be like the most High"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 14:13--14). It is Nebuchadnezzar strolling through his palace and bragging, ]{.class-0}["Is not this great Babylon, that I have built for the house of the kingdom by the might of my power, and for the honour of my majesty?"]{.class-1}[ (Dan. 4:30).]{.class-0}

[That is the kind of thing God ]{.class-0}[hates ]{.class-2}[(Prov. 6:16--17). He will knock you down flat on your face for that kind of attitude. He will fight against you.]{.class-0}

In the Scriptures, those black folk that humble themselves before God get their prayers answered and get exalted by their Creator, and where they don't, they get slapped down hard and destroyed if they keep it up.

"[I am black\...as the tents of Kedar, as the curtains of Solomon."]{.class-1}[ Kedar was the second son of Ishmael (Gen. 25:13). His descendants are an Arabic tribe that lived on the northwest corner of Saudi Arabia, and their land borders on Canaan. They traded in ]{.class-0}["lambs, and rams, and goats"]{.class-1}[ (Ezek. 27:21). The goats of Kedar had a jet-black coat that was used in making the tents in which the Bedouin Arabs lived and for making curtains that divided the living quarters from each other inside the tents (Jer. 49:28--29). The dark black color of the curtains provided privacy. Those were the same types of curtains used in the Tabernacle (Exod. 26:7). They prevented anyone on the outside from seeing inside to the Holy Place and the Holy of Holies.]{.class-0}

"[Look not upon me, because I am black"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 6). The ]{.class-0}["look,"]{.class-1}[ there, is a look of disapproval. It was looking at the woman with the kind of attitude that Miriam and Aaron had toward Moses' Ethiopian wife (Num. 12:1). ]{.class-0}["Because the sun hath looked upon me."]{.class-1}[ The woman was not only dark racially, her skin was black from spending a lot of time out in the sun. Not all Hamites are black like Negroes. Some, like the Egyptians, are a brownish color. If they are out in the sun a lot, that brown skin will burn black, but it is not quite the same kind of a black as actual black Africans.]{.class-0}

That is why the Egyptians made a distinction between themselves and the "Nubians" who came from further south in Africa. In South Africa, during "apartheid," a distinction was not only made between the whites and the blacks, the blacks made a distinction between the blacks and the "coloreds"; i.e., the black folk who were of mixed race. Even today, the Moslems still think of themselves as superior to the black Africans, even though they are from the same stock---Ham.

What you need to get straight, brethren, is that the three main races were created by God. They are not a product of evolution. The Darwinian anthropologists teach that each of the three main races evolved and developed separately and adapted to their environment, and that is the reason they are so different. The Caucasians come from Neanderthal Man and Cro-Magnon Man, and they developed up in a northern climate where there is not a lot of direct sunlight like there is at the equator, so their skin is fair. The Orientals developed from an orangutan type of creature, and that is why their skin is "yellow." The Africans developed from gorillas near the equator, so they have big, broad noses and big lips, and their skin is black.

Of course, that is nonsense. You have had black folk in the USA whose ancestors have been here for nearly three hundred years, and they are no more Caucasian than when they were first brought over on British and Yankee slave ships.

[Then you have the creationists who are currently trying to teach that there is nothing different about the races at all except for their culture. The races are only the product of interbreeding. If we can just get all the races together, we would go back to the way we were before the Flood. And to show that a black can produce a "white," one of these guys (I cannot remember who right now) published a picture of an albino Negro. Anyone who has actually seen an albino Negro knows that he is ]{.class-0}[not]{.class-2}[ Caucasian. He is a Negro with a defective gene. If he doesn't pass on that defective gene, his children will be black.]{.class-0}

God created the races; God divided the races to keep them out of trouble (Acts 17:26--27); and the Lord keeps them divided all the way into the New Heavens and the New Earth (Deut. 4:19; see comments under Rom. 4:13 in that Commentary).

Now, if you want some practical sermonic material from the first half of verse 6, then you can say that the Church has been blacked by sin, by scandal, and by sorrow. You know what I mean by the Church being blackened by sin if you have ever been out witnessing. If a person is trying to dodge receiving Christ, he will recite every sin which professing Christians have committed, of which he has personal knowledge. When you sin openly before the world, Christian, you are blackening the testimony of the saints before the lost.

Scandals like Jimmy Bakker and the PTL "Disneyworld" park (Heritage USA), and Jimmy Swaggart's whorehopping, smut the testimony of the saints. The lost never make distinctions between a bunch of Bible-believing Baptists and a bunch of crazy Charismatics making fools of themselves at some "Brownsville Revival." You may believe nothing like those people, yet the world will paint you just as black as them.

But sorrow can also blacken the Church. Christ told the women who cried for Him on the way to the cross to stop (Luke 23:28). Why? Because He was not like anybody else who died on a cross or by any other method. He had told His disciples that He would rise in three days; there was no need to sorrow. During the days of the Roman persecutions, a lot of those pagans turned to Jesus Christ because those Christians went to their deaths singing and rejoicing.

[The Apostle Paul commanded us not to sorrow ]{.class-0}["as others which have no hope"]{.class-1}[ (1 Thess. 4:13). When you do, you tell the world that there is nothing in you that makes you different from them when death comes. That is a bad testimony to the comforting work of the Holy Ghost in you. That blackens the Church when you act that way.]{.class-0}

[Verse 6: ]{.class-0}["My mother's children were angry with me; they made me the keeper of the vineyards; but mine own vineyard have I not kept."]{.class-1}[ I must admit that how this fits into the historical story of this book, I do not know. ]{.class-0}["My mother's children"]{.class-1}[ would seem to indicate that she and those children have the same mother but not the same father. That is the way it is used in Psalm 69:8, which is a reference to Christ's half-brothers and half-sisters (Mark 6:3). Mary was the mother of them all, but Joseph was not the father of Jesus Christ. But how that works out with Pharaoh's daughter, I have no idea.]{.class-0}

If you spiritualize the passage and stick by the types that have already been set down, then the mother would be New Jerusalem, for that is the mother of every Christian (Gal. 4:26). The children would be Jews resenting the saved Gentiles "butting in" to their dominion.

"[For ye, brethren, became followers of the churches of God which in Judaea are in Christ Jesus; for ye also have suffered like things of your own countrymen, even as they have of the Jews: who both killed the Lord Jesus, and their own prophets, and have persecuted us; and they please not God, and are contrary to all men: Forbidding us to speak to the Gentiles that they might be saved, to fill up their sins alway: for the wrath is come upon them to the uttermost"]{.class-1}[ (1 Thess. 2:14--16).]{.class-0}

That is the Jews resenting the Church coming in and getting the spiritual blessings that once belonged to Israel. That is the main theme of Romans 11 (see comments in that Commentary). It is the same attitude that the Moslems hold against the Jews because God gave those Jews His physical blessings in regards to the land of Palestine (Gen. 27:29).

In verse 6, you have the original "Cinderella" story. Here is a girl with a step-father instead of a step-mother, and her step-siblings are getting together to persecute her. She is keeping their vineyards instead of her own. Again, there is not much more that you can say from an historical perspective because you are not told anything about Pharaoh's daughter except that Solomon married her.

[Typically, there is not much that you can do with the passage either. The vineyard is an Old Testament picture of Israel. Isaiah 5:7 says, ]{.class-0}["For the vineyard of the LORD of hosts is the house of Israel, and the men of Judah his pleasant plant."]{.class-1}[ Notice that the verse says that the vineyard belongs to the Lord, not the Church.]{.class-0}

[But when Christ applies the Parable of the Vineyard in Matthew 21:33--40, He says this, ]{.class-0}["Therefore say I unto you, the kingdom of God]{.class-1}[ (and in the parable it is connected with the vineyard)]{.class-0}[ shall be taken from you, and given to a nation bringing forth the fruits thereof"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 21:43). Historically, that is a reference to the Church (see comments on the verse in the ]{.class-0}[Bible Believer's Commentary on Matthew]{.class-2}[; see also 1 Pet. 2:9).]{.class-0}

[In this age, ]{.class-0}["the kingdom of God is within you"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 17:21). You enter it by the New Birth (John 3:5). So although Paul never likens the Church to a vine or vineyard, he did preach the Kingdom of God (Acts 20:25). So we can certainly make practical application to our own spiritual lives.]{.class-0}

And that leads me to say this: when it comes to the Christian life, God is chiefly concerned with us maintaining our fellowship with Him and our continued spiritual growth. That comes before soulwinning, evangelism, church-planting, missions, or record attendances. Before you minister to anyone else, the Lord wants you to tend to your own spiritual fellowship and growth. You should always make sure that you are bearing fruit for Christ first before you try to help someone else be fruitful.

Preachers are bad about that sort of thing. I know from experience. In the ministry it is easy to lose your own spirituality and growth tending to somebody else's. The danger in the ministry is getting too formal and professional. If you don't watch out, you will end up spouting clichés and truisms and repeating things from memory like a conditioned reflex without any of it affecting you.

Lee Roberson used to say, "Everything rises or falls on leadership." That is true. As the preacher or teacher, you will set the spiritual temperature at which your congregation operates. As a consequence, "the pew cannot rise any higher than the pulpit"; i.e., no congregation can grow spiritually any further than its teacher or preacher.

[The reason you have these massive congregations of ]{.class-0}[baby ]{.class-2}[Christians who know nothing about the Scriptures is because there is a baby behind the pulpit who knows nothing about the Scriptures. The reason they cannot grow spiritually is because he has not grown spiritually.]{.class-0}

If a man is not lazy in the ministry, he tends to be so busy ministering to others that he cannot minister to himself. Preacher friend, I am here to tell you, after 55 years in the ministry, that you need to be ministered to. You need to find a way to do it. Plan to go to a Bible conference or revival (we call them Blowouts around here) once or twice a year, where you can just sit in the pew and soak up the preaching and teaching of the Scriptures for a while. Get you some tapes of good preaching and teaching if you cannot go off to a meeting. Listen to them whenever you get a chance.

And don't listen just to get a good sermon outline or illustration or points to make at your next Bible study. Listen to get something from GOD.

Whenever we have a guest speaker in (preacher, evangelist, missionary, etc.), I get close down to the front of the auditorium and soak it in like a sponge. I will drink it up like a thirsty man who has just found a spring in the desert. I have come to realize, even if you have not, that every Christian, including me, needs the Hell preached out of him and the Devil preached out of him at least once a week.

If you do not know that, you do not know much. If you do not know that, then you do not know much about yourself.

[I am always suspicious of these Christians who get so sanctified and so "separated" and so consecrated and so segregated and so "grace-and-faith, dispensational, ultra-universal church" that they will never come to a local church to get preached at. I am suspicious of a man who can sit under ]{.class-0}[teaching ]{.class-2}[but will not sit under ]{.class-0}[preaching]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

Teaching may impart knowledge of the Scriptures to you, but preaching demands you do something about what is preached. Preaching is pointed; if it is the right kind of preaching, it gets you under conviction.

That is what every Christian needs. He needs to be stirred up so that he does not feel comfortable or complacent in his sin or his worldliness or his carnality.

To my dying day, I will never understand why Christians cannot stand that kind of preaching and why they run from it. I appreciate all I can get of it. I never get enough of it.

So a preacher needs to keep up with his own spiritual life and his own prayer life. He needs to be sure that he is doing what he asks others to do.

Preacher, when you ask someone to "sell out" to the Lord and "surrender all," have you ever considered everything that involves? Job found out. It can involve losing all your property, your children, your health, and the support of your spouse.

If you do not keep that in your mind, preacher, you are a shallow minister. And if you have not applied that to yourself, then your own vineyard is not being kept. You cannot preach like that and expect anything out of your people if all the time you are figuring on a good pension when you retire and the kind of car you drive and your savings account and the suits you wear and your social standing in the community.

The churches today are shot through with spiritual dwarfs: "puny" Pentecostals, "bantam" Baptists, "midget" Methodists, "kitty cat" Catholics, etc. They are a bunch of babies. They are thin-skinned, touchy, and sensitive. They are like that because they are not "sold out" to the Lord. They are not "sold out" because they have never been brought to the point of surrender and sacrifice. They have never been brought to that point because, most of the time, the man who is "tending their vineyard" has never been brought there himself.

So what I say to preachers in general, I say to individual Christians as well. In this day and age, Christian---in Laodicea and the Great Apostasy---you cannot always count on going to church, Sunday School, and prayer meeting to be enough to keep your vineyard tended. Praise God if you have a good pastor who tears your hide off, but they are becoming fewer and "farther between" as the years go by. In your efforts to get out the word of God and to witness to people and to win souls to Christ and affect them with your testimony, you have to remember your own private time of prayer, your own private time of Bible reading, your own private time of Bible study, and you have to cultivate your own vine so it will continue to bear fruit before you can cultivate someone else's.

7 Tell me, O thou whom my soul loveth, where thou feedest, where thou makest thy flock to rest at noon: for why should I be as one that turneth aside by the flocks of thy companions?

8 If thou know not, O thou fairest among women, go thy way forth by the footsteps of the flock, and feed thy kids beside the shepherds' tents.

Verse 7 is addressed to the Bridegroom as a Shepherd. Ginsburg and Bullinger make the "shepherd lover" in opposition to the advances of King Solomon toward the woman in the Song. The King is trying to lure her into his harem with gold, perfume, and flattery; but she remains true to her "hillbilly" lover. The scene has been played out so many times in the movies and television that it has become tiresome.

I do not hold to that position because it ruins the typology that is found throughout the Old Testament. Jesus Christ is not only a King, like Solomon, and the Son of David, like Solomon, He is also a Shepherd.

"[The LORD is my shepherd; I shall not want"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 23:1).]{.class-0}

"[I am the good shepherd: the good shepherd giveth his life for the sheep"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:11).]{.class-0}

"[For ye were as sheep going astray; but are now returned unto the Shepherd and Bishop of your souls" ]{.class-1}[(1 Pet. 2:25).]{.class-0}

"[And when the chief Shepherd shall appear, ye shall receive a crown of glory that fadeth not away"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 5:4).]{.class-0}

[So I take the position that, historically in the Song of Solomon, the King and the Shepherd are the same person, and that person is Solomon. Solomon was a son of David. David was a ]{.class-0}[shepherd ]{.class-2}[before he was a King. David's sons kept sheep (see Absalom, for example, in 2 Sam. 13:23--24). So there would have been nothing unusual in Solomon being both a shepherd and a King at the same time.]{.class-0}

Now, I must confess, I do not completely understand everything from the historical perspective. But that is no reason for ruining one of the greatest types of Christ and the Church in the Old Testament with some stale plot from Hollywood. In the end, of course, every plot comes from the Bible, but we are not going to become so fixated on the carnal love story that we boot Jesus Christ out of His own Book.

"[Tell me, O thou whom my soul loveth"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 7). Now that is true love, when your ]{.class-0}[soul ]{.class-2}[loves someone. It goes beyond mere love of the ]{.class-0}[heart]{.class-2}[. That is why the Lord commanded that you love Him ]{.class-0}["with all thy heart and with all thy soul"]{.class-1}[ (Deut. 10:12).]{.class-0}

[This time, the ]{.class-0}[NASV]{.class-2}[ and the ]{.class-0}[RSV]{.class-2}[ agree with the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ that you can love the Lord with your soul. It is the ]{.class-0}[New International Version,]{.class-2}[ along with its companion translation the ]{.class-0}[New King James Version]{.class-2}[ (listen to the comments by Earl Kalland on the origins of the two translations on the video "The NIV Debate," available from the Bible Baptist Bookstore), that gets rid of the ]{.class-0}[soul ]{.class-2}[in verse 7: ]{.class-0}["Tell me, you whom I love." ]{.class-2}[The ]{.class-0}[NKJV]{.class-2}[ is not a "simplified" version of the ]{.class-0}[KJV]{.class-2}[ at all; it is a "Trojan horse" used to smuggle all of the corrupt readings of other modern versions into the Bible and deceive you into thinking it is still a ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible]{.class-0}[.]{.class-2}

Let us leave the "ridiculous," now, and return to the "sublime."

What are the marks of "true love" (always remembering, of course, that true love goes beyond sex)? Well, if you truly love someone, then you want to be with them. You miss them when they are not with you. You like to talk to them, and you like to hear them talk to you.

If you love someone, you will stick up for their friends. If you love someone, you will fight against their enemies. You will not listen to and believe the worst things about them. If you discover the worst to be true, you will not spread it around. And if you love someone, you will have their best interests at heart.
