If you love the Lord Jesus Christ as you should, all those things will be true of you in regards to Him.

"[Tell me\...where thou feedest, where thou makest thy flock to rest at noon."]{.class-1}[ Noon is the hottest part of the day. Typically, it would picture the troubles and trials of life. We say when we get into trouble: "Someone turned on the heat." When trouble comes, then we ought to rest in the Lord.]{.class-0}

[David said in Psalm 23:2, ]{.class-0}["He maketh me to lie down in green pastures: he leadeth me beside the still waters."]{.class-1}

[You are ]{.class-0}["to lie down in green pastures"]{.class-1}[; that is where you rest. But ]{.class-0}["green pastures"]{.class-1}[ is also where a sheep eats. He lies down and rests in the same place from which he gets his meal. His "bed" is his "table."]{.class-0}

As the Lord's sheep, we are to rest in the same place where the Lord feeds us. The Scriptures are our "pasture." They are where the Lord feeds us, and in times of trouble, that is where we should go to find comfort and solace in its promises.

"[Why should I be as one that turneth aside by the flocks of thy companions?"]{.class-1}[ This girl wanted to be fed, and she wanted to be fed right. Not any old pasture would do. She wanted the right pasture, she wanted the right flock, and she wanted the right shepherd.]{.class-0}

[Is that the language of your heart? Is that how you feel about those things, spiritually? Have you ever examined the other flocks to see how they fare? I am talking about the flocks that feed on the ]{.class-0}[Saturday Evening Post, Time, Life, Esquire, Playboy, U.S. News and World Report,]{.class-2}[ and all of that godless, depraved trash. Are they fed any better than you are? Are they happier than you are? Are they safer than you are? Are they any better off?]{.class-0}

Brethren, the slop of this world is for pigs; sheep do not eat that garbage (Luke 16:15). Sheep want something that will sustain them. That sustenance is found in the pasture, not the hog trough.

I have seen sheep go across a piece of ground that was flat as a bowling alley as far as vegetation was concerned. Those sheep were out in that field bent over with their mouths working the top of that ground. When I went out there and examined what they were eating, it was tiny blades of grass that were as close to nothing as you could get.

I learned by studying that situation that a sheep can get sustenance where no animal in the world could get it. I do not even think a chicken could have lived off the places where those sheep were grazing.

That tells me that a Christian can find sustenance where the world cannot get it. The world comes to the Book with incredulity. "Where did Cain get his wife?" "How did Noah get all the animals into the ark?" "How could the virgin birth take place?" "How could Christ have come up from the dead?"

The world views that Book as dull and judgmental and prudish and full of contradictions. It is like a barren wasteland to the lost. They cannot believe it.

But to the Christian, it is a dinner table full of roast beef, baked chicken, steak, hot biscuits, mashed potatoes, gravy, green beans, fried mullet, hush puppies, corn on the cob, butter, corn bread, jalapenos, nachos, etc.

[At verse 8, the speaker changes. I take it to be the King by what follows in verses 9--12. He addresses the woman as ]{.class-0}["thou fairest among women."]{.class-1}[ That is obviously a reference to the Bride of Christ. Notice how many times she is referred to as ]{.class-0}["fair"]{.class-1}[ or ]{.class-0}["fairest"]{.class-1}[: 1:15 (twice), 1:16, 2:10, 2:13, 4:1 (twice), 4:7, 4:10, 5:9, 6:1, 6:10, 7:6. That is fourteen references, including the one in verse 8 (7x2). All but two of them (5:9, 6:1) are the Bridegroom talking about the Bride.]{.class-0}

[Of course, the word ]{.class-0}["fair"]{.class-1}[ is not used as it is the modern sense. Today, ]{.class-0}[fair]{.class-2}[ is a term of mediocrity. The word ]{.class-0}["fair"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["fairest"]{.class-1}[ in the Bible are used like they are in the fairy tales (]{.class-0}[real fairies;]{.class-2}[ not the Frisco-faggot kind).]{.class-0}

"[Mirror, mirror on the wall, who's the fairest of them all?"]{.class-0}

"[Snow White, still is and always will be. And don't you forget it either."]{.class-0}

The word means "beautiful." Look at Genesis 12:11 and 14. This is a reference to Sarah when she was 65 years old.

"[And it came to pass, when he was come near to enter into Egypt, that he said unto Sarai his wife, Behold now, I know that thou art a fair woman to look upon\...And it came to pass, that, when Abraham was come into Egypt, the Egyptians beheld the woman that she was very fair."]{.class-1}

[When Abraham went down into Egypt, he looked at his wife. Even at 65 she was a good-looking woman. In addition to meaning beautiful, the word ]{.class-0}["fair"]{.class-1}[ can also mean a light complexion, so you will still hear today that a woman has "fair" skin. Abraham was worried that those dark-skinned Egyptians would want a pretty "white" woman and kill him to get her, so he asked Sarah to lie about her relation to him. As it turned out, Pharaoh took her into his harem because he thought she was only Abraham's sister.]{.class-0}

[Now, there are all kinds of things you can draw from that story, but here in Song of Solomon, we are mainly concerned about the meaning of the word ]{.class-0}["fair."]{.class-1}[ We know by verses 5--6 of Song of Solomon chapter one that the Bride is not fair-skinned, so it must refer strictly to her beauty. Of course, even then, you could say that her skin was fairer than most black women. The most beautiful black women, by the world's standards, are the ones whose skin is a brownish tan. Those are women like Lena Horn and Vanessa Williams. When I was growing up, we called them ]{.class-0}[mulatto]{.class-2}[ or "high yeller." The reason their skin is so much lighter than a normal colored woman's is because their "white heritage" is peeking out.]{.class-0}

If we are going to apply the verse symbolically, we can say this: twelve times in the Song of Solomon Jesus Christ calls His Bride beautiful or the most beautiful. I know it is normal for a man to say his wife is the most beautiful creature on earth, but let's just face it, ladies, most of you are not really Miss America or Miss Universe material. That does not mean your husband does not love you or does not find you attractive. It just means he is "stretching the truth" a bit for love's sake.

But if Jesus Christ, the Creator of the universe, calls you not only "beautiful" but the "most beautiful," that is no exaggeration or "sweet little lie." That is the absolute truth, brother, sister.

Now, if your "self-esteem" is low and you throw yourself a continual "pity party" (or as Lester Roloff used to say: "You're living with Elijah in juniper jungle"), then you need to think about that for a while. If you are saved, you are part of a Body that the Lord says is the most beautiful thing He has ever seen. That is quite a thing to say if you consider the source. You think the Lord has not seen some beauty? Why, He is the One who created every beautiful thing there is. And when He talks about His Bride, the Body of Christ, the Church, He says she is more beautiful than anything else.

[Back to verse 8: ]{.class-0}["If thou know not\...go thy way forth by the footsteps of the flock, and feed the kids beside the shepherd's tents."]{.class-1}[ In other words, if you want a good meal for your soul, go with the sheep. Do not go with the dogs or the pigs (2 Pet. 2:22) or the foxes (Luke 13:32) or the jackasses (Job 11:12) or the bats, buzzards, vultures, or "hoot" owls (Mark 4:4, 15). This world is looking for a handout at the bankrupt lunch counters of this world, and the people are starving to death.]{.class-0}

Brethren, everything the world has to offer is a great big buildup to absolutely nothing. Everything: that's TV, movies, good meals, fancy cars, beautiful women, expensive cigars, old liquor, etc. The whole lot of it is anticlimatic.

[Christ told that Samaritan woman: ]{.class-0}["Whosoever drinketh of this water shall thirst again: But whosoever drinketh of the water that I shall give him shall never thirst; but the water that I shall give him shall be in him a well of water springing up into everlasting life."]{.class-1}

When you come to Jesus Christ, He not only gives you something that can satisfy your soul, He gives you something that when you finally reach the climax, there is no letup. It just keeps getting better, and the Lord makes you so you can take it without exploding or going crazy.

"[If thou know not."]{.class-1}[ I have a note in my Bible here that adds: "But you should know." There is still enough of a witness to that ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible that any American "sheep" ought to be able to find that it is good pasture. I know it is becoming harder and harder. The Christian Colleges, Seminaries, and Universities do not want you to know. The conventions, presbyteries, and synods do not want you to know. But God has raised up all kinds of people across this nation to let you know.]{.class-0}

[If you do not want to take it from "Ruckman," then read the works by David Otis Fuller or Edward Hills. Are you a Southern Baptist? Then get ]{.class-0}[The Bible Translation Test]{.class-2}[ by James Son out in Lubbock, Texas. Are you part of the Southwide Baptist Fellowship or the ]{.class-0}[Sword of the Lord]{.class-2}[ crowd? Then get Hugh Pyle's booklet on ]{.class-0}[The One Book That Covers All the Bases]{.class-2}[ or Bill Grady's book on ]{.class-0}[Final Authority.]{.class-2}

[You do not have to worry about me anymore. God has raised up an army to defend and propagate that Book. There is Sam Gipp, Daryl Coats, David Reagan, Paul Heaton, James Sightler (son of the late Harold Sightler), Jack Chick, Mickey Carter, Charles Keen (Bearing Precious Seed in Milford, Ohio), Perry F. Rockwood, Chick Salliby (an Assembly of God evangelist who was kicked out of his association because of his stand on the ]{.class-0}[KJV]{.class-2}[), and Gail Riplinger.]{.class-0}

God really played a trick on the Body of Christ with that last one. Ruckman had been "kicked out" of every major Fundamental College in America, as well as the Southwide Baptist Fellowship. So God sends along a soft-spoken female and puts her on a dozen radio and television talk shows, several of them with nationwide coverage, and has her put out the facts about the Satanic corruptions found in the modern Bibles. She stirred up more "trouble," nationwide, in two or three years than "Ruckman" had managed to do in the last ten.

Now, there are only two reasons why people on this earth, saved or lost, do not know where to go to get their souls fed: 1) they refuse to listen when someone tells them, or 2) nobody has ever told them. It has been said that witnessing is simply a matter of one beggar telling another beggar where he can find a good meal. That is an apt metaphor for telling the lost about Christ in the Holy Bible.

The Old Testament picture is found in 2 Kings 7. The city of Samaria had been besieged by the Syrians, and the inhabitants were starving to death. Outside the gate sat three lepers. They were dying slowly from leprosy, and with the siege, they were dying more quickly from starvation. They decided to go to the camp of the Syrians and beg for food. They figured that the worst that could happen to them would be that the Syrians would kill them. When they arrived at the Syrian camp, they found it deserted because God had caused the Syrians to hear a great noise which they thought was a mercenary army coming to break the siege. The Syrians had all fled in a panic and had left everything, including all their food, behind.

Well, those three lepers stuffed themselves silly, and after they had made two or three trips to stash away some food and other goodies for a "rainy day," they got under terrible conviction.

"[Then they said one to another, We do not well: this day is a day of good tidings, and we hold our peace: if we tarry till the morning light, some mischief will come upon us: now therefore come, that we may go and tell the king's household"]{.class-1}[ (2 Kings 7:9).]{.class-0}

[If you are a Christian who does not witness, you ]{.class-0}["do not well."]{.class-1}[ You know where the good food is, and you are selfishly keeping it to yourself. ]{.class-0}["Some mischief"]{.class-1}[ is going to come upon you if you do not open your mouth for Jesus Christ.]{.class-0}

9 I have compared thee, O my love, to a company of horses in Pharaoh's chariots.

10 Thy cheeks are comely with rows of jewels, thy neck with chains of gold.

11 We will make thee borders of gold with studs of silver.

12 While the king sitteth at his table, my spikenard sendeth forth the smell thereof.

13 A bundle of myrrh is my wellbeloved unto me; he shall lie all night betwixt my breasts.

14 My beloved is unto me as a cluster of camphire in the vineyards of Engedi.

[The King is speaking here, for sure, because he makes a reference to ]{.class-0}["a company of horses in Pharaoh's chariots"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 9). Solomon has ]{.class-0}["a company of horses,"]{.class-1}[ and he got them from Pharaoh.]{.class-0}

"[And Solomon had horses brought out of Egypt\...And a chariot came up and went out of Egypt for six hundred shekels of silver, and an horse for an hundred and fifty"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 10:28--29).]{.class-0}

"[And Solomon had four thousand stalls for horses and chariots\...And they brought unto Solomon horses out of Egypt"]{.class-1}[ (2 Chron. 9:25, 28).]{.class-0}

[The Hebrew word for ]{.class-0}[horses]{.class-2}[, in verse 9, is in the feminine. The woman is being compared to a female horse. A female horse is called a "mare"; you do not often hear any woman called that. A boisterous Texan will sometimes call a young woman a "filly," which is the name given to a young mare. You will often hear some woman referred to as a "nag," which is an old, broken-down mare. The old song goes, "The old, gray mare just ain't what she used to be many long years ago." That is an unflattering song about a woman in her old age.]{.class-0}

[Now, the picture here is the same as it is in Matthew 21:2--3. There Christ told His disciples, ]{.class-0}["Go into the village over against you, and straightway ye shall find an ass tied, and a colt with HER: LOOSE THEM, and BRING THEM UNTO ME. And if any man say ought unto you, ye shall say, THE LORD HATH NEED OF THEM."]{.class-1}

[That female ass was ]{.class-0}["TIED by THE DOOR WITHOUT in a place WHERE TWO WAYS MET."]{.class-1}[ She is a picture of a lost person bound by Satan outside of Jesus Christ (]{.class-0}["the door"]{.class-1}[) where two ways---the broad way that leads to death and the narrow way that leads to life (Matt. 7:13--14)---meet. When a sinner is loosed by the Gospel, he is brought to Jesus Christ for service.]{.class-0}

[Here in the text, the picture is that of the Body of Christ (]{.class-0}["a company"]{.class-1}[) made up of individual Christians (]{.class-0}["horses"]{.class-1}[). Pharaoh, the King of Egypt, is a picture of Satan, the King of this world (Luke 4:5--6). Before you are saved, you are like a horse hitched up to Satan's juggernaut with his bit and bridle in your mouth. You move at his command; you are under his dominion. In 2 Timothy 2:26, Paul says that the lost ]{.class-0}["are taken captive"]{.class-1}[ by the Devil ]{.class-0}["at his will."]{.class-1}

[But when you get saved, the King unhooks you from Satan's chariot and brings you ]{.class-0}[up]{.class-2}[ to the Promised Land. Over there in 1 Kings, Solomon brought those horses ]{.class-0}[out]{.class-2}[ of Egypt. So your "stall," Christian, is up in God's stable, New Jerusalem.]{.class-0}

[Before going on to verse 10, here are a few ways that a Christian is like ]{.class-0}["a company of horses in Pharaoh's chariots."]{.class-1}

[First, a Christian is like a horse in ]{.class-0}[courage.]{.class-2}[ Over in Job 39:19--25, the Lord describes the courage of that horse in battle. He says, ]{.class-0}["He ]{.class-1}[\[the horse\]]{.class-0}[ mocketh at fear, and is not affrighted; neither turneth he back from the sword"]{.class-1}[ (Job 39:22); ]{.class-0}["He goeth on to meet the armed men"]{.class-1}[ (Job 39:21).]{.class-0}

I will be frank with you: I do not trust horses. I have ridden them, but I do not trust them. Every horse I have ridden has tried to get me off its back. They have rubbed their side against a rough, wooden rail when I have been on them; they have walked underneath a low branch trying to knock me off. They do not like me, and I do not like them.

I will tell you something else. Every horse I have personally known has been nervous. I cannot imagine an animal like that charging down a hill into gunfire, cannon fire, spears, bayonets, and swords, or going through another line of horses where the riders are swinging blades and maces at each other. I cannot imagine a horse looking forward to a mess where they are being shot out from under their riders and where they are kicking men and each other. I know they do because I have seen pictures and read the accounts of cavalry attacks throughout history.

If you lined up those beasts 200 or 500 in a line and blew a trumpet, they would just about charge Hell for you. During the Crimean War, there was a famous attack put to verse by Alfred Lord Tennyson. It is called "The Charge of the Light Brigade." That charge involved 600 horses and their riders charging down a valley about five miles long with cannon fire coming at them from the left, the right, and directly ahead of them. When they hit the parapets where the gunners were, there were riderless horses leaping those parapets into the gun pits and into the men there. Those horses would not turn back, despite the cannon and gunfire.

There is something about battle and the charge that gets that horse's blood boiling. Christians ought to be courageous like that. All the armor in Ephesians 6 that a Christian is commanded to don is for a forward attack; there is nothing to guard or protect the back in a retreat.

[Second, the horse is a strong animal. Job 39:19 says, ]{.class-0}["Hast thou given the horse strength? hast thou clothed his neck with thunder?"]{.class-1}[ That is God talking to Job, and He is telling Job that man has not given the horse his strength, but He (God) has. That is why, today, mechanical power is measured by "horsepower." The idea is the number of horses it would take to produce a certain amount of power.]{.class-0}

[Courage and strength go together in the Bible. The Lord told Joshua, ]{.class-0}["Be strong and of a good courage"]{.class-1}[ (Josh. 1:6, 9). Paul told the Corinthians to ]{.class-0}["quit you like men,"]{.class-1}[ which is another way of saying "be courageous." That command is followed by ]{.class-0}["be strong"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 16:13).]{.class-0}

[The Christian's strength, like the horse's, comes from God. Paul told his converts, ]{.class-0}["Finally, my brethren, be strong in the Lord, and in the power of his might"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 6:10) and ]{.class-0}["be strong in the grace that is in Christ Jesus"]{.class-1}[ (2 Tim. 2:1). He said in Philippians 4:13, ]{.class-0}["I can do all things through Christ which strengthen me."]{.class-1}

[A Christian is like a horse in that he can ]{.class-0}[benefit ]{.class-2}[from chastisement. Proverbs 26:3 says, ]{.class-0}["a whip for the horse, a bridle for the ass."]{.class-1}[ A farmer who knew something about wild jackasses once told me that a wild ass "can't understand no whippin' till he gets broke in." Well, every man is ]{.class-0}["born like a wild ass's colt"]{.class-1}[ (Job. 11:12). It is not until after he is saved that the Lord has trained him. When that happens, the saved man is like a horse and can "understand a whipping."]{.class-0}

[The writer of Hebrews says, ]{.class-0}["For whom the Lord loveth he chasteneth, and SCOURGETH]{.class-1}[ \[there is that ]{.class-0}["whip for the horse"]{.class-1}[\]]{.class-0}[ every son whom he receiveth"]{.class-1}[ (Heb 12:6).]{.class-0}

[And finally, a horse is a beautiful animal. That is historically what Solomon is saying about the woman here in verse 9. But as we have seen, the Lord considers His Bride to be more beautiful than any other group of saints in history. In Psalm 45:11, the Lord says in regards to His Bride, ]{.class-0}["So shall the king greatly desire thy beauty: for he is thy Lord; and worship thou him."]{.class-1}

[Verse 10:]{.class-0}[ "Thy cheeks are comely with rows of jewels, thy neck with chains of gold."]{.class-1}[ Oriental women are known for wearing a lot of jewelry on their face, head, and neck. If you want to see it today, just get you some ]{.class-0}[National Geographic]{.class-2}[ pictures of higher caste women in India. In the Bible, those ]{.class-0}["jewels"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["chains of gold"]{.class-1}[ can be found illustrated in a couple of places in the Scriptures. One reference is Judges 8:26. The context of the verse is the spoil taken from the Midianites by Gideon and his army of 300.]{.class-0}

"[And the weight of the golden earrings that he requested was a thousand and seven hundred shekels of gold; besides ornaments, and collars, and purple raiment that was on the kings of Midian, and beside the chains that were about their camels' necks."]{.class-1}

[Notice the jewelry that the Midianites wore on their face and head: ]{.class-0}["golden earrings\... ornaments\... collars."]{.class-1}[ Notice also that the camels had golden chains on their necks. So when Solomon talks about the woman having ]{.class-0}["chains of gold,"]{.class-1}[ it is probably an allusion back to the ]{.class-0}["company of horses in Pharaoh's chariots."]{.class-1}

[Now, in regards to those horses in the Bible, there are some important things to note. There are the fleshy horses that are hooked up to Pharaoh's chariots. Those are the kind of horses that God told Solomon ]{.class-0}[not]{.class-2}[ to multiply to himself, and he did it anyway.]{.class-0}

"[But he shall not multiply horses to himself, nor cause the people to return to Egypt, to the end that he should multiply horses: forasmuch as the Lord hath said unto you, Ye shall henceforth return no more that way"]{.class-1}[ (Deut. 17:16).]{.class-0}

[The Lord did not want that Jew returning to Egypt. That is one reason, among several others, for rejecting the ]{.class-0}[Septuagint ]{.class-2}[as Scripture. Any translation made by a bunch of apostate Jews who were down in Egypt is not worth the paper on which it was written.]{.class-0}

[But another reason that God did not want the King to ]{.class-0}["multiply horses to himself,"]{.class-1}[ whether they were Egyptian or not, was because the heathen nations that surrounded Israel dedicated their horses to the sun god. Some of you might remember, if you read any stories from Greek mythology when you were young, that Apollo hauled the sun across the sky in a chariot pulled by flying horses of fire. In the book of Revelation, Apollo is called ]{.class-0}["Apollyon"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 9:11). Apollyon is ]{.class-0}["the angel of the bottomless pit"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 9:11). The name means damnation. He is the ]{.class-0}["son of perdition,"]{.class-1}[ the Antichrist.]{.class-0}

When those horses were dedicated to the sun god, they were consecrated to the service of the Devil. So when Joshua conquered the land, the Lord commanded him to hock all the horses; i.e., to kill them by cutting their hamstrings so they could not stand up. This was because of Leviticus 18:23.

"[And the LORD said unto Joshua, Be not afraid because of them: for to morrow about this time, will I deliver them up all slain before Israel: thou shalt hough their horses, and burn their chariots with fire"]{.class-1}[ (Josh. 11:6).]{.class-0}

When David defeats the Syrians, he does the same thing (2 Sam. 8:4; 1 Chron. 18:4).

[Those are the fleshy horses in which the heathen nations put their trust (Psa. 20:7). God said they were ]{.class-0}["a vain thing for safety"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 33:17). That is another reason God did not want those Kings to gather a huge army of horses and chariots. The tendency would be to trust them to win the battle instead of God, and if they were decisive in the victory, those Jews would brag about their cavalry instead of glorifying God (Judg. 7:2). In other words, they would do exactly what America is doing today in Iraq, Afghanistan, and Kuwait.]{.class-0}

[But God's horses are not like that. He says in Zechariah 10:3, ]{.class-0}["Mine anger was kindled against the shepherds, and I punished the goats]{.class-1}[ \[that is a reference to the Judgment of the Nations (Matt. 25:31--46) that takes place at the Second Advent\]]{.class-0}[:]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[for the Lord of hosts hath visited his flock the house of Judah, and hath made them as HIS GOODLY HORSE in the battle."]{.class-1}

[So God has some horses that He considers ]{.class-0}["goodly."]{.class-1}[ Zechariah connects those horses with the Second Advent, and sure enough, Christ returns in Revelation 19 on ]{.class-0}["a white horse"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 19:11). Revelation 19:14, ]{.class-0}["And the armies which were in heaven followed him upon white horses."]{.class-1}

[And though these horses are white in color, they are not made of ]{.class-0}[flesh ]{.class-2}[with white coats of hair. They are horses made of ]{.class-0}[fire.]{.class-2}[ Old Apollo did not get his ]{.class-0}[fiery horses]{.class-2}[ and chariot from Zeus on Olympus; he got them from the Bible.]{.class-0}

"[And it came to pass, as they still went on, and talked, that, behold, there appeared a chariot of fire, and HORSES OF FIRE, and parted them both asunder; and Elijah went up by a whirlwind into heaven"]{.class-1}[ (2 Kings 2:11).]{.class-0}

"[And Elisha prayed, and said, Lord, I pray thee, open his eyes, that he may see. And the Lord opened the eyes of the young man; and he saw: and, behold, the mountain was full of HORSES AND CHARIOTS OF FIRE round about Elisha" ]{.class-1}[(2 Kings 6:17).]{.class-0}

During the Millennium, these horses are in Jerusalem and in Israel. When they are, they have ornaments put on them.

"[In that day shall there be upon the bells of the horses, HOLINESS UNTO THE LORD"]{.class-1}[ (Zech. 14:20).]{.class-0}

That inscription is the same inscription that was put on a plate of gold and tied around the miter that was worn on the head of the high priest (Exod. 28:36--37). On those horses is gold that survives contact with fire intact (1 Cor. 3:12--14).

The lesson for the Christian is plain. What you have belongs to God. All the creation is God's, and if you have any part of God's creation, it ought to be consecrated to God.

A former pastor of Trinity Baptist Church in Jacksonville, Florida decided that any car God gave him would always be used to pick someone up, other than his family, for church. Throughout all of his pastorates, he always used his car to bring elderly folk to church. He did that personally, in addition to his bus ministry. Whatever vehicle he drove was dedicated to the Lord.

[Walter Wilson was a medical doctor who did a lot of personal work. The Bookstore sells a book that gives accounts of the different encounters he had in the ministry; it is called ]{.class-0}[Strange Short Stories by the Doctor.]{.class-2}[ In one of those accounts, Dr. Wilson dealt with a big, fat fellow who came to one of his meetings. When he met him after the message, he asked him if he had enjoyed the meeting. The fellow replied, "Not particularly."]{.class-0}

[But Dr. Wilson was not going to let him go that easily. He asked the man to go home and read Leviticus 3:16, and the guy said he would. That man returned to that church and got saved. When someone asked him what had changed his mind, he said, "Well, I went home and read Leviticus 3:16 like Walter Wilson asked. The end of the verse says, ]{.class-0}['all the fat is the Lord's.']{.class-1}[ I figured that if ]{.class-0}['all the fat is the Lord's,' ]{.class-1}[then I have enough of it, so I decided to give it all to the Lord and get saved."]{.class-0}

"[We will make thee borders of gold with studs of silver."]{.class-1}[ Obviously these are more ornaments and jewelry as we saw in verse 10. What they have to do symbolically with Jesus Christ and the Church, I have no idea. The Jews were commanded to put borders on their garments, and on those borders they were to put a fringe of blue (Num. 15:38). The ]{.class-0}["studs,"]{.class-1}[ here, are settings for jewels. Gold stands for deity, and silver for redemption. But how all those things fit into the typology of the Song, I do not know.]{.class-0}

[It is not even clear exactly who is speaking in verse 11. Verses 9 and 10 are the King speaking to the woman. Verses 12--14 are the woman speaking to the King. But who the ]{.class-0}["we"]{.class-1}[ of verse 11 is who is making golden borders and silver studs for ]{.class-0}["thee"]{.class-1}[ I do not know---either the ]{.class-0}["we"]{.class-1}[ or the ]{.class-0}["thee."]{.class-1}[ Back in verse 4, the ]{.class-0}["we"]{.class-1}[ was the woman and the virgins of verse 3 speaking together. The ]{.class-0}["thee" ]{.class-1}[to whom they were speaking was Solomon. In type, you have the individuals that make up the Bride of Christ speaking to the Bridegroom. But I am not sure that you can make the same application here.]{.class-0}

[The ]{.class-0}["spikenard"]{.class-1}[ of verse 12 is a powerful perfume made out of a fluid gum. Oriental women usually keep it in a leather pouch which is worn around the neck and hung near the heart. Spikenard is not only said to be a precious perfume (Matt. 26:7), it is also very expensive (John 12:3).]{.class-0}

The word appears five times in the Scriptures: three times here in the Song of Solomon (1:12, 4:13, 14) and twice in the New Testament in connection with the anointing of Christ by Mary (Mark 14:3; John 12:3). Five is the number of death; specifically, in this instance, the death of Jesus Christ.

[Verse 12 took place literally in John 12. Christ, the King, was sitting at the table with Lazarus, the brother of Mary and Martha (John 11:1--2), when Mary came in with an alabaster box of ointment. The ointment was spikenard (John 12:3). She broke the box of ointment and anointed Christ's head (Mark 14:3) and His feet (John 12:3). When she did, the Bible says, ]{.class-0}["the house was filled with the odour of the ointment"]{.class-1}[ (John 12:3), just like in Song of Solomon 1:12 where the ]{.class-0}["spikenard sendeth forth the smell thereof."]{.class-1}[ Christ said, ]{.class-0}["Against the day of my burying hath she kept this" ]{.class-1}[(John 12:7). So the spikenard is connected with the ]{.class-0}[death ]{.class-2}[and ]{.class-0}[burial ]{.class-2}[of Jesus Christ.]{.class-0}

[That being the case, look at verse 13 of Song of Solomon chapter 1.]{.class-0}[ "A bundle of MYRRH is my wellbeloved unto me."]{.class-1}[ When Christ was buried, Nicodemus ]{.class-0}["brought a mixture of MYRRH and aloes"]{.class-1}[ to prepare the body for burial (John 19:39). When the Lord hung on the cross, the soldiers tried giving Him ]{.class-0}["wine mingled with myrrh"]{.class-1}[ to drink, but He turned it down (Mark 15:23). So both spikenard and myrrh are connected with the ]{.class-0}[death and burial of the Lord.]{.class-2}

The lesson from this is that if any sinner is going to know the love of God (either him loving God or God loving him), he will have to come to the one place where God offers that love to a sinner: Calvary. Americans are so love-crazy that they cannot accept the fact that apart from a personal faith in Christ's blood atonement for their sins, God does not love them. No sinner, in his natural state, dwells in God's love. A sinner dwells in God's wrath, not His love (John 3:36).

"[He that believeth on the Son hath everlasting life: and he that believeth not the Son shall not see life; but the wrath of God abideth on him"]{.class-1}[ (John 3:36).]{.class-0}

"[He that believeth on him is not condemned: but he that believeth not is condemned already, because he hath not believed in the name of the only begotten Son of God"]{.class-1}[ (John 3:18).]{.class-0}

Now, thank God that He loved us, even when we were sinners, enough to want to see us saved.

"[For God so loved the world, that he gave his only begotten Son, that whosoever believeth in him should not perish, but have everlasting life"]{.class-1}[ (John 3:16).]{.class-0}

"[But God commendeth his love toward us, in that, while were were yet sinners, Christ died for us"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 5:8).]{.class-0}

[But do not kid yourself into believing that love for sinners extends any further than the foot of the cross. If a sinner rejects Jesus Christ as his Saviour, the Lord will not have any compunction at all at booting him straight into the Lake of Fire. When that time comes, the Lord will not shed one tear for any Christ-rejecting sinner. It will be Proverbs 1:26, ]{.class-0}["I also will laugh at your calamity; I will mock when your fear cometh"]{.class-1}[ (see Rev. 20:15).]{.class-0}

If you want the kind of love, spiritually, that Solomon describes here in these verses, in type, then you must come to God in repentance over your sinful state and trust completely in the sacrifice that Jesus Christ made for you on the cross.

[First John 4:10, ]{.class-0}["Herein is love, not that we loved God, but that he loved us, and sent his Son to be the propitiation for our sins."]{.class-1}[ That is, God the Father is satisfied with Christ's sacrifice on our behalf.]{.class-0}

[Look on down that chapter to verse 16: ]{.class-0}["And we have known and believed the love that God hath to us. God is love; and he that dwelleth in love dwelleth in God, and God in him."]{.class-1}

[What is the love about which John is talking in verse 16? Why, it is the love he defined back in verse 10. It is God sending ]{.class-0}["his Son to be the propitiation for our sins."]{.class-1}

Back in Song of Solomon 1:13, myrrh has five qualities in the Scriptures that picture Jesus Christ in relation to His Bride, the Church.

[First, myrrh has purifying properties. Esther 2:12,]{.class-0}[ "Now when every maid's turn was come to go in to king Ahasuerus, after that she had been twelve months, according to the manner of the women, (for so were the days of their purifications accomplished, to wit, six months with oil of myrrh, and six months with sweet odours, and with other things for the purifying of the women)."]{.class-1}

[When a sinner accepts Christ, he believes on Him with his heart (Rom. 10:9--10). That heart is the seat of your emotions, and it is located]{.class-0}[ "betwixt the breasts." ]{.class-2}[Believing with your heart (i.e., a complete and utter trust) is different from believing with your head. It is what differentiates a real Christian from a professing Christian.]{.class-0}

James McGinlay used to say in that heavy Scotch brogue of his, "The longer I live, the more I am impressed with the fact that most Christians are serving an historical Christ instead of loving a living Lord." His point was that love reaches the heart, not the head.

[When the Lord enters your body, He purifies your heart from sin. Simon Peter said, speaking of the conversion of the Gentiles in Acts 10, ]{.class-0}["And God, which knoweth the hearts, bare them witness, giving them the Holy Ghost, even as he did unto us: And put no difference between us and them, PURIFYING THEIR HEARTS BY FAITH"]{.class-1}[ (Acts 15:8--9).]{.class-0}

[That purification is the difference between carnal love and Christian love. The love of lost sinners is a mere ]{.class-0}[carnal ]{.class-2}[love. It is a response to fulfil physical lust. That is true even in a society where the couple has to behave themselves because of the Christians' influence on the culture.]{.class-0}

[For love to have its right relationship between a boy and a girl, or between a man and a woman, the first thing that is necessary is a change of heart in both parties. That change has to be one of ]{.class-0}[purity]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[The Apostle James said, ]{.class-0}["But the wisdom that is from above is first PURE"]{.class-1}[ (James 3:17).]{.class-0}

The attitude of the world is "all is fair in love and war"; i.e., as long as you have feelings for someone, that justifies any action you take to gain and keep that person's affections. Not if those feelings are strictly carnal; no, it does not. In the Bible, love is more than the satiation of carnal lusts.

Marriage is of God, and the Lord governs the marriage of two Christians. If your love and marriage is not centered on God and His word and the person of Jesus Christ and prayer, all you have is a carnal, fleshy mess.

[Secondly, myrrh is ]{.class-0}[costly]{.class-2}[. Myrrh was one of the gifts brought to the Christ child by the wise men; there it was called a ]{.class-0}[treasure]{.class-2}[ (Matt. 2:11). The Lord Jesus is said to be ]{.class-0}["precious"]{.class-1}[ four times in the book of 1 Peter (see comments on 1 Pet. 19, 2:4, 6, 7). If you have Jesus Christ, you are rich beyond measure.]{.class-0}

[The Apostle Paul said, ]{.class-0}["For ye know the grace of our Lord Jesus Christ, that, though he was rich, yet for your sakes he became poor, that ye thorough his poverty might be rich"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 8:9).]{.class-0}

[That Bible says,]{.class-0}[ "For all things are your's; Whether\...the world, or life, or death, or things present, or things to come; all are your's; And ye are Christ's; and Christ is God's"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 3:21--23).]{.class-0}

If you have Jesus Christ as your personal Saviour, you have something more valuable than the world and everything in it from now to eternity. You talk about "costly"; that is costly!

Thirdly, myrrh has a bitter quality. In every Christmas pageant that I was in, growing up, I had to play the third wise man because I had the deepest voice. I always had to sing that fourth verse of "We Three Kings of Orient Are":

"[Myrrh is mine; its bitter perfume breathes a life of gathering gloom;]{.class-0}

Sorrowing, sighing, bleeding, dying, sealed in a stone cold tomb."

[The Lord is like that "little book" that He had John eat in Revelation 10:10. In your mouth, He is as ]{.class-0}["sweet as honey."]{.class-1}[ The Psalmist says, ]{.class-0}["O taste and see that the Lord is good" ]{.class-1}[(Psa. 34:8). But when He gets down inside you, there is a bitterness about Him in regards to the world and those Christians who aren't living in fellowship with Him and in accord with the Book. Jesus Himself said, ]{.class-0}["Think not that I am come to send peace on earth"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 10:34). How is that for a Merry Christmas and "peace on earth to men of good will." Jesus Christ said He did not come into this world ]{.class-0}["to send peace on earth."]{.class-1}[ Well, if He did not come to bring peace, then why did He come. Matthew 10:34 continued, ]{.class-0}["I came not to send peace, BUT A SWORD."]{.class-1}

[Jesus Christ came to the earth to take that two-edged ]{.class-0}["sword of the Spirit"]{.class-1}[ (Heb. 4:12--13; Eph. 6:17) and make a clear division between those who are trusting Him and His righteousness and those who are trusting their own goodness to get them to Heaven. He came to make a clear-cut distinction between those who live by the Book as their final authority and those who live by their own opinions and traditions, or those of others, as their final authority.]{.class-0}

[Matthew 10:35--36, ]{.class-0}["For I am come to set a man at variance against his father, and the daughter against her mother, and the daughter in law against her mother in law. And a man's foes shall be they of his own household."]{.class-1}

[Any Christianity that is built on ]{.class-0}[mutual friendship ]{.class-2}[apart from Jesus Christ and the Bible is straight out of Hell. Abraham was a friend of God (James 2:23) because he left the world and would not have anything to do with the world. The Bible says, ]{.class-0}["Know ye not that the friendship of the world is enmity with God? whosoever therefore will be a friend of the world is the enemy of God" ]{.class-1}[(James 4:4).]{.class-0}

More Christians get out of the will of God and become fruitless because they try to remain friends with someone who is out of fellowship with God. That is not to say that you cannot be friendly and kind to the lost and to backslidden Christians. But your closest friends, those with whom you have continual fellowship, should be people who commit everything to God in prayer and who pass out tracts and witness and who attend church on a regular basis and who bear fruit for Jesus Christ.

If you want to check your spiritual temperature, then check the kind of people who hang around you and whom you hang around. "Birds of a feather flock together." If you are spiritual, chances are that you will attract spiritual friends, and if you are not spiritual, you will not.

[Mark 15:23, ]{.class-0}["And they gave him to drink wine mingled with myrrh: but he received it not." ]{.class-1}[You will notice in the parallel passage in Matthew 27:34 that that ]{.class-0}["wine mingled with myrrh"]{.class-1}[ is called ]{.class-0}["vinegar\...mingled with gall."]{.class-1}[ Gall describes the bitterness of the myrrh. Like that myrrh, Jesus Christ can bring bitterness to our relationships with those who are not following Him.]{.class-0}

[Another quality myrrh shares with the Lord is ]{.class-0}[fragrance]{.class-2}[. Psalm 45:8, ]{.class-0}["All thy garments smell of myrrh, and aloes, and cassia, out of the ivory palaces, whereby they have made thee glad."]{.class-1}

And that is where we get the song "Ivory Palaces." The first verse says, "My Lord has garments so wondrous fine, and myrrh their texture fills; its fragrance reached to this heart of mine, with joy my being thrills." Myrrh is known for its fragrant smell. It is a strong smell, it is a pungent smell, but it is a pleasant smell.

Myrrh is like tobacco smoke. If you have been in a room with either, you will come out smelling like it. That is how strong it is.

If you are living in fellowship with Jesus Christ, people will be able to tell it. The world can tell it by the way you talk and by the things at which you look and by the music to which you listen. That influence of Jesus Christ is so strong that sometimes you cannot get rid of it if you try.

I am reminded of an incident in the life of Evangelist Rex Harrison. Before he got right with God and entered the ministry, he used to play piano in nightclubs. One night, some floozie came over to the piano as he was playing. She leaned up against the piano with her drink and said, "You must be a Christian."

Harrison was shocked. "Yes, I am," he said, "but how did you know?"

"[I could just tell by the way you played 'the blues,'" she said.]{.class-0}

[I tell my people that when they sit under my Bible teaching for a few years that I will ruin them for life. By that I mean that no matter where they go or what they do in life, and no matter how they live, that Book will always be there in their minds as the final authority. I know graduates of my Bible school right now who are living like hell (the other schools do too; their leaders just will not admit it), but they cannot get away from talking about that Book or thinking about that Book or having that Book actively influence their daily lives. The "smell" of that ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible reeks from them, and they cannot get it off.]{.class-0}

[Verse 14:]{.class-0}[ "My beloved is unto me as a cluster of camphire in the vineyards of Engedi."]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}["Camphire"]{.class-1}[ is obviously another aromatic plant used as a perfume by women. It only appears twice in the Bible, both times in the Song of Solomon (1:14, 4:13).]{.class-0}

[This is one of those places in the Song of Solomon where the Scholars' Union "goes to pieces" over the reading in the ]{.class-0}[Authorized Version.]{.class-2}[ Dr. William Smith, in the ]{.class-0}[Smith's Bible Dictionary,]{.class-2}[ is quick to tell you: "There can be no doubt \[how is that for a divine fiat? He is about to tell you that no one doubts that what he is about to say is true\] that ]{.class-0}['camphire']{.class-1}[ is an INCORRECT RENDERING OF THE HEBREW TERM."]{.class-0}

[Izzat so? And what is the evidence that the good doctor has for making such a statement? "The margin in both passages has 'cypress.'" Therefore, since the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ translators made a ]{.class-0}[marginal]{.class-2}[ reference as to what they ]{.class-0}[thought]{.class-2}[ the meaning of the word might be, the reading ]{.class-0}[in the text]{.class-2}[ is "an incorrect reading."]{.class-0}

[Now, the Hebrew word here is ]{.class-0}[copher.]{.class-2}[ The Hebrew word for ]{.class-0}[cypress]{.class-2}[ is ]{.class-0}[tirzah,]{.class-2}[ and it appears ]{.class-0}[in the text]{.class-2}[ only one time in Isaiah 44:14. Obviously, the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ translators had enough sense to distinguish between ]{.class-0}["camphire"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["cypress"]{.class-1}[ in the ]{.class-0}[text]{.class-2}[ of the Bible. The two are not the same, not even in the Hebrew Bible.]{.class-0}

[Most scholars agree that ]{.class-0}["a cluster of camphire"]{.class-1}[ refers to the henna plant which is native to Egypt where the Nubians call it ]{.class-0}[khofreh.]{.class-2}[ If you want a thorough description of the plant, read the entry under "Camphire" in ]{.class-0}[Smith's Bible Dictionary.]{.class-2}[ It will give you all the trivia you need to know about the plant, and when you get done, it will no more help you explain the text than if you had never consulted it to begin with.]{.class-0}

[A much more helpful note is found in the ]{.class-0}[Easton Bible Dictionary:]{.class-2}[ "The margin of the ]{.class-0}[Authorized Version]{.class-2}[\...has 'or cypress,' NOT WITH REFERENCE TO THE CONIFER SO CALLED, but to the circumstance that one of the most highly appreciated species of this plant \[the henna\] grew in the island of Cyprus."]{.class-0}

[So the ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible was not so far off as Dr. William Smith made it out to be---either in its text or its marginal note. The translators transliterated the word from the Hebrew in the text. All translations do this in one place or another. Then in the margin, they gave you the particular species to which they believed Solomon was referring. Even if they were wrong on that point, it still would not have affected the text one way or another.]{.class-0}

Dr. Smith was just shooting off his mouth trying to make you think he knew about what he was talking. He did not.

When in doubt, throw ALL the scholars out. That's O-U-T; OUT!

Engedi is a city on the central western shore of the Dead Sea (Josh. 15:62). David hid there when he was running from Saul (1 Sam. 23:29, 24:1). It was also called Hazazontamar (2 Chron. 20:2). In the Millennium, it will be the place where the Dead Sea opens up to flow into the Mediterranean, thus curing the Dead Sea of its "deadness" (Ezek. 47:10). (The Dead Sea is dead because it has no outlet for its waters. As a result, the water evaporates leaving huge salt deposits that kill normal sea life.)

During Solomon's time, a botanical garden (with vineyards) was located there, and that was the only place in Palestine where the henna plant (camphire) was grown.

[Having thus discussed the historical aspects of the passage, let us look at the typical application. Notice the two groups of three found in verses 10--11 and 12--14. The Bride has three types of ]{.class-0}[ornaments ]{.class-2}[and three types of ]{.class-0}[perfume]{.class-2}[. The ornaments are jewels, gold, and silver; and the rewards at the Judgment Seat of Christ are gold, silver, and precious stones (1 Cor. 3:12). The Bride wears the ornaments of her rewards for serving Christ.]{.class-0}

[And the three ]{.class-0}[fragrances ]{.class-2}[point to the three ]{.class-0}[offices ]{.class-2}[of Christ which He provides to His Bride: prophet, priest, and King. The King is connected with the spikenard in verse 12; myrrh is associated with His office as a prophet; and that leaves camphire to go with His priesthood.]{.class-0}

15 Behold, thou art fair, my love; behold, thou art fair; thou hast doves' eyes.

16 Behold, thou art fair, my beloved, yea, pleasant: also our bed is green.

17 The beams of our house are cedar, and our rafters of fir.

This passage is probably the King once again addressing the Bride. So what you have is the Bride talking to the King in verses 1--7, the King talking to the Bride in verses 8--11, the Bride describing the King in verses 12--14, and the King speaking to the Bride again in verses 15--17.

[The word ]{.class-0}["fair"]{.class-1}[ appears three times in these verses and is a reference to the Bride down in chapter 2 verses 10 and 13 and chapter 4 verses 1, 7, and 10. That is why we assign these verses to the Lord addressing the Church.]{.class-0}

"[Thou hast doves' eyes"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 15). The eyes of a dove are grey and piercing, and they seem to see in all directions at the same time. But not only does the Bride have ]{.class-0}["doves' eyes,"]{.class-1}[ but the Bridegroom has them as well. Song of Solomon 5:12, ]{.class-0}["His eyes are as the eyes of doves."]{.class-1}[ His eyes are like her eyes.]{.class-0}

[Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["the light of the body is the eye"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 6:22). Well, Christ is ]{.class-0}["the light of the world"]{.class-1}[ (John 9:5). If you are a Christian, then you have ]{.class-0}["Christ in you, the hope of glory"]{.class-1}[ (Col. 1:27). So as a Christian, your eyes should be His eyes: i.e., you ought to see things the way He sees them. You ought to look at the things at which He would look, and you ought not to look at the things at which He would not look.]{.class-0}

[Habakkuk 1:13 says, ]{.class-0}["Thou art of purer eyes than to behold evil, and canst not look on iniquity."]{.class-1}

[David said, ]{.class-0}["I will set no wicked thing before mine eyes: I hate the work of them that turn aside; it shall not cleave to me"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 101:3).]{.class-0}

[Now look at verses 16 and 17. ]{.class-0}["Our bed is green. The beams of our house are cedar, and our rafters of fir."]{.class-1}[ Those verses imply that the honeymoon for these two lovers is ]{.class-0}[outdoors]{.class-2}[. If that seems kind of odd, remember that Adam and Eve were wedded in a garden, ]{.class-0}[outdoors]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

That is the goal of all science and education: it is a return to Eden without God's involvement. All that science and education are trying to do is to get everyone to run around naked in a perfect environment, with a perfect climate of their own making and by their own means.

[Of course, God will make this world like it was back in Genesis 1--2, but it will be on His terms. God will cause all the predators to get along with their prey, He will make all the carnivores herbivores, and He will cause children to play with dangerous beasts without fear of harm. But He will do it when He sets up the ]{.class-0}["root of Jesse"]{.class-1}[ as His ]{.class-0}["ensign"]{.class-1}[ of the Jews to all the nations of the earth (Isa. 11:10, 12).]{.class-0}

In other words, no Jesus Christ, no peace. It is that simple.

Until that time, it is bigger and better wars, asteroids falling to the earth, animals going on rampages, demoniac monsters from the pit, cannibalism as a religious rite practiced universally, and environmental catastrophes that make Krakatoa (1883), the Indian Ocean Basin Tsunami (2004), and hurricanes Ivan, Andrew, and Camille (2004, 1992, 1969) look like firecrackers on a breezy day. That is all found in Revelation 6--18. That is God's "peace plan" for the United Nations. Hollywood has been showing it to you for over fifty years now.

[Historically, this could be a reference to one of the three houses Solomon built in Jerusalem or ]{.class-0}["the house of the forest of Lebanon"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 7:2). The three houses he built in Jerusalem were the Temple, his own house, and a house for Pharaoh's daughter. All of the houses had beams of cedar (1 Kings 7:1--2), but only the Temple is said to have had fir in it as well (1 Kings 6:15). Unlike the house of Song of Solomon 1:17, the fir was in the planks on the floor, not in the rafters.]{.class-0}

[But in type, for the Christian, the earth is going to be restored to an Edenic state, and the Christian ]{.class-0}["will dwell in the house of the Lord for ever"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 23:6). Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["In my Father's house are many mansions\...I go to prepare a place for you" (John 14:2).]{.class-1}

[]{#section-0_1_cb3c55cdc99c2178_67dc.xhtml}

CHAPTER 2

2:1 I am the rose of Sharon, and the lily of the valleys.

2 As the lily among thorns, so is my love among the daughters.

[The first two verses of chapter 2 are obviously spoken by Solomon. But the first two words of verse 1 put the interpretation, doctrinally, beyond Solomon. ]{.class-0}["I AM"]{.class-1}[ is the name by which Jehovah first revealed Himself to Israel as a nation (Exod. 3:14).]{.class-0}

[In the Gospel of John, Jesus used the phrase in reference to Himself. John 8:58, ]{.class-0}["Jesus said unto them, Verily, verily, I say unto you, Before Abraham was, I AM."]{.class-1}

[In the Garden of Gethsemane, Christ, for one brief moment, released the power of that name when Judas and the soldiers came to take Him.]{.class-0}[ "As soon then as he had said unto them, I AM he, they went backward, and fell to the ground"]{.class-1}[ (John 18:6).]{.class-0}

Seven times in the Gospel of John, the Lord used the expression to introduce some aspect of His being.

[1) ]{.class-0}["I am the bread of life\...I am the living bread"]{.class-1}[ (John 6:35, 51).]{.class-0}

[2) ]{.class-0}["I am the light of the world"]{.class-1}[ (John 8:12, 9:5).]{.class-0}

[3) ]{.class-0}["I am the door of the sheep"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:7).]{.class-0}

[4) ]{.class-0}["I am the good shepherd"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:11).]{.class-0}

[5) ]{.class-0}["I am the resurrection, and the life"]{.class-1}[ (John 11:25).]{.class-0}

[6) ]{.class-0}["I am the way, the truth, and the life" ]{.class-1}[(John 14:6).]{.class-0}

[7) ]{.class-0}["I am the true vine\...I am the vine"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:1, 5).]{.class-0}

The Lord does the same thing in the book of Revelation.

[1) ]{.class-0}["I am Alpha and Omega, the beginning and the ending\...I am the first and the last"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 1:8, 11, 17, 22:13).]{.class-0}

[2) ]{.class-0}["I am he that liveth, and was dead; and, behold I am alive for evermore"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 1:18).]{.class-0}

[3) ]{.class-0}["I am the root and offspring of David, and the bright and morning star" ]{.class-1}[(Rev. 22:16).]{.class-0}

[That is how verse 1 is used. It is Jesus Christ, in the Old Testament, speaking prophetically, through Solomon, about Himself. ]{.class-0}["I am the rose of Sharon, and the lily of the valleys"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 1).]{.class-0}

[There are all kinds of ideas as to exactly which flower Solomon was referring when he wrote ]{.class-0}["I am the rose of Sharon."]{.class-1}[ You can go to a nursery and buy several different flowering plants, bushes, and shrubs bearing that name, but those probably have no more to do with the text than the plant called "the lily of the valley."]{.class-0}

[We can say this: the word for ]{.class-0}["rose"]{.class-1}[ (in regards to a flower) only appears one other time in the Scriptures. Isaiah 35:1--2 says, ]{.class-0}["The wilderness and the solitary place shall be glad for them; and the desert shall rejoice, and blossom as the ROSE. It shall blossom abundantly, and rejoice even with joy and singing: the glory of Lebanon shall be given unto it, the excellency of Carmel and SHARON, they shall see the glory of the LORD, and the excellency of our God."]{.class-1}

You will hear a lot of prophetic expositors talk about that first verse as if it is being fulfilled in Israel by the irrigation of farmlands, but that isn't about what the verse is talking. The first two verses of Isaiah 35 take place after the Second Advent, during the Millennium.

[That ]{.class-0}["desert"]{.class-1}[ isn't just the Judean wilderness surrounding the Dead Sea, although that is part of it. That ]{.class-0}["desert"]{.class-1}[ includes all the barren land from the Nile River in Goshen to the Euphrates River (Gen. 15:18). It is all part of the original land grant God gave to Abraham.]{.class-0}

[Moreover, it doesn't ]{.class-0}["blossom as the rose"]{.class-1}[ due to modern, "scientific" methods of farming; it blossoms because the Rose of Sharon gives it life by His word, just as He did in the recreation of Genesis 1:11--13. So when the Lord says, ]{.class-0}["I am the rose of Sharon,"]{.class-1}[ it is a prophetic reference to His ability to restore the Promised Land (i.e., all the land promised to Abraham) to the state that He described in Deuteronomy 11:9--12.]{.class-0}

[The Lord also said, ]{.class-0}["I am\...the lily of the valleys." ]{.class-1}[Of course, that is where we get the song: "He's the Lily of the Valley." But notice that the verse didn't say that. The verse said ]{.class-0}["valleys"]{.class-1}[---plural. The ]{.class-0}["s"]{.class-2}[ on the end of that word makes the difference between life and death.]{.class-0}

[Over in 1 Kings 20, the Syrians fought against Israel and got whipped (vss. 1--20). Before they came up against them the second time, they said this: ]{.class-0}["And the servants of the king of Syria said unto him, Their gods are gods of the hills; therefore they were stronger than we; but let us fight against them in the plain, and surely we shall be stronger than they"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 20:23).]{.class-0}

[Because they said that, the Lord let them get beat a second time. ]{.class-0}["And there came a man of God, and spake unto the king of Israel, and said, Thus saith the LORD, Because the Syrians have said, The LORD is God of the hills, but he is not God of the valleys, therefore will I deliver all this great multitude into thine hand, and ye shall know that I am the LORD" ]{.class-1}[(1 Kings 20:28). When Ben-hadad missed that plural, it cost the lives of 127,000 of his men (1 Kings 20:29--30).]{.class-0}

There is an old hillbilly song that goes: "And the God of the mountains is the God of the valleys\...and the God of the good times is still God in the bad times, and the God of the day is still God in the night."

[The spiritual application for the Christian is tremendous. He's called ]{.class-0}["the lily of the valleys"]{.class-1}[ because you will go through more than one valley in your life. He is not merely in one valley; He's in every "valley."]{.class-0}

[Now, you take that lily. It appears fifteen times in Scripture (both singular and plural). All except one of those references (Hos. 14:5) is associated with Solomon in some way. Solomon had lilies engraved on different parts of the Temple (1 Kings 7:19, 22, 26; 2 Chron. 4:5). The word ]{.class-0}["lily"]{.class-1}[ or ]{.class-0}["lilies"]{.class-1}[ shows up eight times in the Song itself. In the New Testament, Christ said, ]{.class-0}["Consider the lilies how they grow: they toil not, they spin not; and yet I say unto you, that Solomon in all his glory was not arrayed like one of these"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 12:27).]{.class-0}

In the world, the lily is common at weddings and funerals. It is also the flower associated with Easter and the resurrection of Jesus Christ.

Talmage said, "Hovering over the marriage ceremony like a wedding bell or folded like a chaplet over the pulseless heart of the dead," in reference to the lily.

[That's significant because it means the lily is associated with death and marriage. Christ had to ]{.class-0}[die]{.class-2}[ to get His ]{.class-0}[Bride.]{.class-2}[ And the fact that that lily is associated with Christ's resurrection shows that marriage is permanent and binding. Romans 7:2 says, ]{.class-0}["For the woman which hath an husband is bound by the law to her husband so long as he liveth."]{.class-1}[ So Christian, as long as Jesus Christ lives, you are bound to Him. The song goes, "Bound to Him ETERNALLY by love's strong cord." You can't lose it.]{.class-0}

[Now, in verse 1, Christ is ]{.class-0}["the lily of the valleys,"]{.class-1}[ but in verse 2, the Bridegroom says of the Bride, ]{.class-0}["As the lily among thorns, so is my love among the daughters."]{.class-1}[ So you have another situation here where the Bride is like the Bridegroom.]{.class-0}

[That is true of the Christian. Jesus Christ is ]{.class-0}["the light of the world"]{.class-1}[ (John 8:12), yet He said that we ]{.class-0}["are the light of the world"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 5:14). He is the Son of God; we are the sons of God (John 1:12). He is the Lamb of God; we are His sheep and His lambs (John 21:15--17). The Christian is to be like his Lord. The word ]{.class-0}[Christian]{.class-2}[ means "little Christ."]{.class-0}

[Notice also the comparison in verse 2: ]{.class-0}["As the lily among thorns, so is my love among the daughters."]{.class-1}[ The picture is a pure, white flower in the middle of a briar patch. ]{.class-0}["The lily"]{.class-1}[ is the Bride. Those thorns, in the Bible, are often a picture of unsaved people.]{.class-0}

[Hebrews 6:7--8, ]{.class-0}["For the earth which drinketh in the rain that cometh oft upon it, and bringeth herbs meet for them by whom it is dressed, receiveth blessing from God; But that which beareth thorns and briars is rejected, and is nigh unto cursing; whose end is to be burned."]{.class-1}

[Second Samuel 23:6--7,]{.class-0}[ "But the sons of Belial shall be all of them as thorns thrust away, because they cannot be taken with hands: But the man that shall touch them must be fenced with iron and the staff of the spear; AND THEY SHALL BE UTTERLY BURNED WITH FIRE in the same place."]{.class-1}[ (See Heb. 6:7--8.)]{.class-0}

[Micah 7:2--4, ]{.class-0}["The good man is perished out of the earth: and there is none upright among men\...The best of them is as a brier: the most upright is sharper than a thorn hedge."]{.class-1}

The unsaved man is likened to thorns because thorns are part of the curse God put on the ground when He drove Adam and Eve out of the Garden of Eden.

[Genesis 3:17--18,]{.class-0}[ And unto Adam he said, Because thou hast hearkened unto the voice of thy wife, and hast eaten of the tree, of which I commanded thee, saying, Thou shalt not eat of it all the days of thy life; Thorns also and thistles shall it bring forth to thee."]{.class-1}

[Since man is from the ground (Gen. 2:7), if the ground is cursed, then man is cursed. If the cursed ground brings forth thorns, then a man in his natural state is likened to a thorn since he comes from the cursed ground as well. So one application of verse 2 could be that the Bride of Christ stands out in this sin-cursed world like a ]{.class-0}["lily among thorns."]{.class-1}

[But in this case, the comparison is applicable to more than just unsaved people. Verse 2 says, ]{.class-0}["so is my love among the daughters."]{.class-1}[ What ]{.class-0}["daughters"]{.class-1}[? Song of Solomon 1:5,]{.class-0}[ "ye daughters of Jerusalem."]{.class-1}[ Song of Solomon 2:7, ]{.class-0}["ye daughters of Jerusalem."]{.class-1}[ You will find the same thing in 3:5, 10--11, 5:8, 16; and 8:4. Solomon considers his bride (1:5) to be so much more beautiful than the]{.class-0}[ "daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ that he is comparing her to a white ]{.class-0}["lily among thorns."]{.class-1}

[In type, the Lord is saying that the Bride of Christ stands out among all the other saved "women" of the Bible. These women are listed in Song of Solomon 6:8, ]{.class-0}["There are threescore queens, and fourscore concubines, and virgins without number."]{.class-1}

[So other saved people, outside of this dispensation from Acts 2 to the Rapture, are represented in type in Song of Solomon 6:8 as ]{.class-0}["queens," "concubines," ]{.class-1}[and ]{.class-0}["virgins."]{.class-1}[ Those are the ]{.class-0}["thorns"]{.class-1}[ of verse 2.]{.class-0}

"[The lily"]{.class-1}[ is found in Song of Solomon 6:9. ]{.class-0}["My dove, my undefiled is but one; she is the only one of her mother, she is the choice one of her that bare her. The daughters saw her, and blessed her; yea, the queens and the concubines, and they praised her."]{.class-1}[ And if you compare Song of Solomon 6:9 with 6:8, you will see that ]{.class-0}["daughters"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 9) has been substituted for the ]{.class-0}["virgins"]{.class-1}[ in verse 8.]{.class-0}

[Now, those groups (the one Bride, the queens, the concubines, and the virgins) make up what Paul called ]{.class-0}["the household of God"]{.class-1}[ in Ephesians 2:19; we call it the ]{.class-0}[family]{.class-2}[ of God (Eph. 3:15). Our part of the family is ]{.class-0}["the church, which is his body"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 1:22--23). That Body, like the Bride in Song of Solomon 6, is said to be ]{.class-0}["one body"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 4:4).]{.class-0}

Other parts of God's family include: Old Testament saved Gentiles, Old Testament saved Jews, Tribulation Gentiles saints, Tribulation Jewish saints, and Millennial saints. When the Lord looks across the groups, the Bride stands out above all the rest.

[In light of that, if you consider the statement, that is quite a thing to say. Here you are as a Christian. When the Lord looks at you, He sees you as part of a Body ]{.class-0}[that is pure and white.]{.class-2}[ Then He looks over at some of those other saints, and He says, "Those are thorns in comparison with those Christians." Who is He talking about? Oh, He is talking about saints like Noah, Job, and Daniel (Ezek. 14:14), three of the most righteous men the Lord could find in the Old Testament. He is talking about Moses and Samuel (Jer. 15:1), two of the greatest prayer warriors in the Old Testament. He is talking about David, a man after God's own heart (1 Sam. 13:14; Acts 13:22). He's talking about those souls under the altar in Revelation 6:9 ]{.class-0}["that were slain for the word of God, and for the testimony which they hold"]{.class-1}[ and who ]{.class-0}["loved not their lives unto the death"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 12:11). Those are all the "thorns" the Lord is talking about in Song of Solomon 2:2.]{.class-0}

[Now, how can that be? When you compare the best Christian that you personally know today to that group, would you say that he or she is a]{.class-0}[ "lily"]{.class-1}[ compared to all those ]{.class-0}["thorns"]{.class-1}[ I just listed? Could you honestly say that any Christian you know is better that Noah, Job, Daniel, Moses, Samuel, David, or the Tribulation martyrs?]{.class-0}

[But you have to remember, God isn't looking at your ]{.class-0}[personal righteousness]{.class-2}[ in comparison with theirs. There are plenty of Christians in the Body of Christ who will ]{.class-0}["be saved; yet so as by fire"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 3:15), whose personal righteousness comes nowhere near to the saints of other dispensations, and yet who are still part of a Body the Lord calls a ]{.class-0}["lily."]{.class-1}

[The reason is because you are living in an age where God ]{.class-0}[gives ]{.class-2}[the New Birth to His saints. When you are regenerated, the Lord Himself takes up residence in you and gives you ]{.class-0}[His righteousness]{.class-2}[. At the same time, He separates your sinful flesh from your regenerated spirit and soul and adopts you into His family as an individual son of God. And if that weren't enough, He also makes you a part of His own spiritual Body. So when God looks at you, He isn't looking at your ]{.class-0}[individual righteousness,]{.class-2}[ which He does in regards to all of those other groups. He is seeing you as ]{.class-0}[part of His own Son,]{.class-2}[ Jesus Christ. Well, the Lord is ]{.class-0}["the lily of the valleys,"]{.class-1}[ and you are part of Him. So he likens us to a ]{.class-0}["lily"]{.class-1}[ because of our position in Him. Those other saints are ]{.class-0}["thorns"]{.class-1}[ in comparison because they are ]{.class-0}[not]{.class-2}[ in Him.]{.class-0}

[Having said that, let me make it clear that the Lord loves those other saints. Solomon had a thousand wives, and the Bible says he]{.class-0}[ "loved"]{.class-1}[ them ]{.class-0}["together with the daughter of Pharaoh"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 11:1), but Pharaoh's daughter was his "O-A-O": his "One And Only." That is the same relationship that Christ has with His Bride. The Lord loves Israel ]{.class-0}["with an everlasting love"]{.class-1}[ (Jer. 31:3). But the love Christ has for the Church is more intimate and special than even His love for Israel. Christ not only died for the Church (Eph. 5:25), He has entered into a spiritual relationship with it into which He has not entered with any other group of saved people, including Israel (Eph. 5:31--32).]{.class-0}

3 As the apple tree among the trees of the wood, so is my beloved among the sons. I sat down under his shadow with great delight, and his fruit was sweet to my taste.

4 He brought me to the banqueting house, and his banner over me was love.

5 Stay me with flagons, comfort me with apples: for I am sick of love.

6 His left hand is under my head, and his right hand doth embrace me.

7 I charge you, O ye daughters of Jerusalem, by the roes, and by the hinds of the field, that ye stir not up, nor awake my love, till he please.

The Bride picks up her part of the Song again in verse 3. It appears that she is the speaker through the rest of the chapter, but in verses 10--14, she is relating something the Bridegroom says to her.

In verse 2, the Bridegroom makes a comparison of the Bride to other women. In verse 3, the Bride returns the favor and compares the Bridegroom to other men. The comparison is that of a fruit-bearing tree being better than a bunch of trees in a forest that bear no fruit.

[In the Bible, the apple is considered the best of fruits. In Proverbs 25:11, Solomon writes, ]{.class-0}["A word fitly spoken is like apples of gold in pictures of silver."]{.class-1}

[Throughout the Old Testament, Israel is called "the apple of God's eye" (Deut. 32:10; Lam. 2:18; Zech. 2:8). The apple of the eye is a reference to the ]{.class-0}[pupil ]{.class-2}[of the eye (see comments on Psa. 17:8 in ]{.class-0}[The Bible Believers' Commentary on Psalms,]{.class-2}[ Vol. 1). The idea is that since the pupil is the eye gate to the body (Matt. 6:22), and protected because of its value, that God would value and protect Israel in the same way.]{.class-0}

[Because of references to apples like these in the Bible, the Catholics teach that the fruit of the Tree of Knowledge in the Garden of Eden was an apple. And where the larynx projects out on a man's throat is called an ]{.class-0}[Adam's apple]{.class-2}[ (supposedly where the piece of the apple that Adam ate got stuck in his throat).]{.class-0}

And then you have the old adage: "An apple a day keeps the doctor away."

Of course, the scholars have a hard time "identifying" the apple of the Bible. Evidently, they spend all their time in air-conditioned offices bullshooting over whether apples are really "apples" and roses are really "roses" and lilies are really "lilies" in the Bible, instead of getting out into the real world and shopping in a produce market.

Several types of apples were cultivated and transplanted throughout the Middle East (including Canaan) by 2000 B.C., nearly 1,000 years before Solomon was born. Today, apples are the number one non-citrus fruit produced by the State of Israel. So you can take all the trivial speculations of the scholars on quinces and citrons and apricots and deposit them in File 13 where they belong. They don't add anything to your knowledge or faith in the Scriptures. As usual, they are nothing but the infidelic meanderings of men who think a knowledge of Hebrew and botany equips them to sit in judgment on God Almighty and His words. Men like that aren't fit to judge a tiddley-winks contest.

[The apples of the Bible are ]{.class-0}[apples.]{.class-2}[ They may not be exactly like a Rome, Granny Smith, Red Delicious, Golden Delicious, Fuji, etc.; but they are true "apples" in the apple family.]{.class-0}

[Verse 3: ]{.class-0}["so is my beloved among the sons."]{.class-1}[ Those ]{.class-0}["sons"]{.class-1}[ are "the sons of men." They are any male descendant of Adam. Jesus Christ stands out among men like the sun against a forty-watt electric light bulb.]{.class-0}

[Moses, Elijah, and David were great men, but they didn't (and couldn't) do anything ]{.class-0}[for you.]{.class-2}[ Moses gave us the Law; David gave us the Psalms. The prophets and writers of Scripture were used by God to give us His words, but in and of themselves they couldn't do anything for us. Jesus Christ came that we ]{.class-0}["might have life, and that ]{.class-1}[\[we\]]{.class-0}[ might have it more abundantly"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:10).]{.class-0}

[John 6:32--33, 35, ]{.class-0}["Then Jesus said unto them, Verily, verily, I say unto you, Moses gave you not that bread from heaven; but my Father giveth you the true bread from heaven. For the bread of God is he which cometh down from heaven, and giveth life unto the world\....I am the bread of life: he that cometh to me shall never hunger; and he that believeth on me shall never thirst."]{.class-1}

[John 15:5,]{.class-0}[ "I am the vine, ye are the branches: He that abideth in me, and I in him, the same bringeth forth much fruit: for without me ye can do nothing."]{.class-1}

[1 John 5:11--12, ]{.class-0}["And this is the record, that God hath given to us eternal life, and this life is in his Son. He that hath the Son hath life; and he that hath not the Son of God hath not life."]{.class-1}

[That is what sets Jesus Christ apart from all the other trees in the forest; especially wormy, rotten, hollow ones like Mohammed. I asked a Mohammedan one time what his "prophet" ever did for him. His reply was that Mohammed gave him the ]{.class-0}[Koran.]{.class-2}[ I said, "I didn't ask you that. I said, 'What did your prophet ever ]{.class-0}[do for you]{.class-2}[?'" He said, "I don't understand what you mean." I said, "My Prophet ]{.class-0}[died for me.]{.class-2}[ What did your prophet ever do for you?" He didn't have an answer; no "Moslem" does. That's because neither Mohammed nor "Allah" ever did ]{.class-0}[anything]{.class-2}[ for ]{.class-0}[any]{.class-2}[ of their followers.]{.class-0}

"[I sat down under his shadow with great delight"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 3). David said, ]{.class-0}["Because thou hast been my help, therefore in the shadow of thy wings will I rejoice"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 63:7).]{.class-0}

"[His fruit was sweet to my taste"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 3). Hence, the Bible says, ]{.class-0}["O taste and see that the LORD is good"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 34:8). The way you taste the Lord is to believe what He said. First Peter 2:2--3 says, ]{.class-0}["As newborn babes, desire the sincere milk of the word, that ye may grow thereby: If so be ye have tasted that the Lord is gracious."]{.class-1}

The Catholics have a real problem with that concept in John 6. That is their proof text for the Mass. Of course, neither the Mass nor the Lord's Supper is even in mind during Christ's Bread of Life Discourse, but that is the only place they can justify eating Christ's literal flesh and blood.

[John 6:53--56,]{.class-0}[ "Then Jesus said unto them, Verily, verily, I say unto you, Except ye eat the flesh of the Son of man, and drink his blood, ye have no life in you. Whoso eateth my flesh, and drinketh my blood, hath eternal life; and I will raise him up at the last day. For my flesh is meat indeed, and my blood is drink indeed. He that eateth my flesh, and drinketh my blood, dwelleth in me, and I in him."]{.class-1}

[There you go: you have to eat Christ's flesh and drink His blood in order to get eternal life. You can't be in the Body of Christ unless you do ]{.class-0}[that.]{.class-2}

Well, how do you do that when Christ has ascended up to Heaven and is seated at the right hand of God the Father (John 6:62)? That's easy. Just have some black-robed African witchdoctor take a starchy cookie and a bottle of hootch and say some magic words in Latin over them. All of a sudden what you have is the very flesh of Christ that was broken on the cross 2,000 years ago and the blood that was shed from Gethsemane to Calvary. IT JUST LOOKS LIKE A STARCHY COOKIE AND SHINNY! (Don't you know!)

[Is that what Christ meant when He said what He said in John 6:53--56? Did He mean for some child-molesting bachelor to practice black magic, cannibalism, and vampirism every Sunday morning at 12:00? Did He contradict Himself ]{.class-0}[after forbidding you to eat or drink blood]{.class-2}[ three times in the Scriptures (Gen. 9:4; Lev. 3:17; Acts 15:20)? Don't be absurd! Jesus never taught transubstantiation in the Lord's Supper or anywhere else. He said, ]{.class-0}["As the living Father hath sent me, and I live by the Father: so he that eateth me, even he shall live by me"]{.class-1}[ (John 6:57). Do you think Jesus Christ cuts off a piece of His Father and devours it every time He goes by the throne up in Heaven. Of course not!]{.class-0}

[And if that weren't clear enough, look at His further explanation in verse 63 of John 6: ]{.class-0}["It is the spirit that quickeneth; the FLESH PROFITETH NOTHING: THE WORDS I SPEAK UNTO YOU, THEY ARE SPIRIT, AND THEY ARE LIFE."]{.class-1}

[So you partake of the Lord spiritually (]{.class-0}[not physically]{.class-2}[) when you put your faith in His words. Until you do that, you will never know He is good; you will never know that He is gracious; and you will never know how sweet He can be.]{.class-0}

[Lester Roloff used to sing, "There's something mighty sweet about the Lord; there's something mighty sweet about the Lord. It really doesn't matter just what the people say. There's something mighty sweet." That's the truth, but you'll never ]{.class-0}[know ]{.class-2}[the truth of it until you try the Lord out yourself and find out just how sweet He is.]{.class-0}

[Americans are some of the craziest nuts in the world when it comes to this matter. When a company develops a new product, they will send samples of it out to as many people as possible. People will take that sample at no risk to them and try it to see if it does what the company says it will do. But when it comes to trying]{.class-0}[ the Lord]{.class-2}[ out and seeing if He was telling the truth, Americans will come up with all kinds of excuses.]{.class-0}

"[My priest told me no one could know." "I'm not that bad." "I was born a Catholic (or Baptist or Lutheran or Methodist, etc.), and I'm going to die a Catholic (or Baptist, Lutheran, Methodist, etc.)." "Well, I wasn't raised to believe that." "That's too easy."]{.class-0}

[Listen, you crazy nut, just try the Lord out. What have you got to lose? You're headed for Hell right now (Luke 13:5; John 3:36). If what I say isn't so, then you'll still be headed there anyway.
