But if what that Bible says is so (and well over a billion people since A.D. 33 have found it to be so), then by rejecting your church, your religion, your parents (in some instances), and your own goodness, and putting your complete trust in Jesus Christ and His blood atonement, you can have an eternal home ]{.class-0}[in Heaven.]{.class-2}

[I'll guarantee you one thing: as long as you stay the way you are, you will be just as ignorant and stupid and lost as you are right now. I'll tell you something else: any agnostic who has never received Jesus Christ is not only stupid, he is ]{.class-0}[dishonest]{.class-2}[. If he were an honest skeptic, he would test the Lord out and say, "Well, I tried it, and I found out it wasn't true." The reason he doesn't is because he is a puffed-up, egotistical hypocrite. He wants everyone to think he is an open-minded intellectual when he's not.]{.class-0}

"[His fruit"]{.class-1}[ is defined in Galatians 5:22--23. ]{.class-0}["But the fruit of the Spirit is love, joy, peace, longsuffering, gentleness, goodness, faith, Meekness, temperance: against such there is no law."]{.class-1}

Now, there are other fruits of a Christian listed in the New Testament, and we have listed these and commented on them in our Commentary on Romans (Rom. 1:13). But these are the fruits produced by the Christian in witnessing, praising, and giving. They are works of personal righteousness performed by the Christian.

"[The fruit of the Spirit,"]{.class-1}[ however, is not the works of the Christian. It is character traits produced in us by the Holy Spirit as we allow Him to work in us. (For further study, see our comments on Gal. 5:22--23 in that Commentary.)]{.class-0}

"[He brought me to the banqueting house, and his banner over me was love"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 4). That's where Al Smith got the words for his song that the teenagers sing: "I'm feasting at His banqueting table, and His banner over me is love."]{.class-0}

[Now look at that verse. When God wants to draw a sinner to Himself, He appeals to]{.class-0}[ two things]{.class-2}[ in that sinner's flesh: love and food.]{.class-0}

[Look at Matthew 22:2. ]{.class-0}["The kingdom of heaven is like unto a certain king, which made a marriage for his son."]{.class-1}[ What you are about to read is a parable that Christ tells to illustrate a Gospel invitation.]{.class-0}

[Matthew 22:4, ]{.class-0}["Again, he sent forth other servants, saying, Tell them which are bidden, Behold, I have prepared my dinner." ]{.class-1}[There's the food. "]{.class-0}[All things are ready: come unto the marriage."]{.class-1}[ And there's the love.]{.class-0}

[In Revelation 19:9, the Lord says, ]{.class-0}["Blessed are they which are called unto the marriage supper of the Lamb."]{.class-1}[ There are those fleshy appeals again: love and a good meal.]{.class-0}

When you have love and a good meal, that's the acme. And although those are fleshy things, they are pictures of our communion with Jesus Christ.

[Revelation 3:20, ]{.class-0}["Behold, I stand at the door, and knock: if any man hear my voice, and open the door, I will come in to him, and will SUP with him, and he with me."]{.class-1}

[The ]{.class-0}["banqueting house"]{.class-1}[ of verse 4 is defined in the book of Esther. The banquet is a ]{.class-0}["banquet of wine"]{.class-1}[ (Esth. 5:6, 7:2). If there is any doubt about that, look at that ]{.class-0}["fruit"]{.class-1}[ in verse 3. That is the ]{.class-0}["fruit of the vine"]{.class-1}[ of which Christ speaks in Matthew 26:29. Look at those ]{.class-0}["flagons"]{.class-1}[ in verse 5. Those are vessels used for drinking wine (2 Sam. 6:19; 1 Chron. 16:3; Isa. 22:24; Hos. 3:1).]{.class-0}

[After what Solomon says in chapter 1 (vs. 4 and the comments associated with it), why does the Lord talk about bringing the Bride to a banquet where they drink wine? Answer:]{.class-0}[ It's not the same kind of wine.]{.class-2}

Christians don't use the same kind of wine as the heathen do. We don't chant Latin incantations over a jug of "moonshine" or "white lightning" and pretend it turns to blood.

[That Bible says, ]{.class-0}["For their rock is not as our Rock, even our enemies themselves being judges."]{.class-1}[ Our Church (the Body of Church) is not founded on Satan like the churches of the heathen are (Matt. 16:18,23; 1 Cor. 10:20). ]{.class-0}["For their vine is of the vine of Sodom, and of the fields of Gomorrah."]{.class-1}[ So their priests are well known for molesting boys and young men who serve at the altar. ]{.class-0}["Their grapes are grapes of gall, their clusters are bitter: Their wine is the poison of dragons, and the cruel venom of asps"]{.class-1}[ (Deut. 32:31--33).]{.class-0}

There's that wine found in Proverbs 23:29--32. That's the kind of wine made by "Christian" Brothers Distillery. Churches that make that kind of wine have no problem owning controlling stock in the Budweiser Beer Brewery.

You say, "Dr. Ruckman, what church are you talking about?"

I won't tell you. I'll let you figure it out for yourself. All I will say right now is: "If the shoe fits, wear it."

[The kind of wine used by the Lord is ]{.class-0}[grape juice ]{.class-2}[that has not been spoiled by fermentation.]{.class-0}

"[But I say unto you, I will not drink henceforth of this fruit of the vine, until that day when I drink it NEW with you in my Father's kingdom"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 26:29).]{.class-0}

[What is ]{.class-0}["new wine"]{.class-1}[?]{.class-0}

[Isaiah 65:8, ]{.class-0}["Thus saith the LORD, As the new wine is found IN THE CLUSTER, and one saith, Destroy it not; for a blessing is in it: so will I do for my servants' sakes, that I may not destroy them all."]{.class-1}

"[New wine is found in the cluster,"]{.class-1}[ so it is not fermented.]{.class-0}[ It is squeezed directly from the fruit into the cup.]{.class-2}[ If you want to see the operation in Scripture, then turn to Genesis 40:9--11.]{.class-0}

"[And the chief butler told his dream to Joseph, and said to him, In my dream, behold, a vine was before me; And in the vine were three branches: and it was as though it budded, and her blossoms shot forth; and the clusters thereof brought forth ripe grapes: And Pharaoh's cup was in my hand: AND I TOOK THE GRAPES, AND PRESSED THEM INTO PHARAOH'S CUP, AND I GAVE THE CUP INTO PHARAOH'S HAND."]{.class-1}

[So when Christ is at the table at the Last Supper, He takes a cluster of grapes and squeezes their juice into a cup and passes that cup around to each of His disciples. He doesn't drink it Himself because He will not drink it again until He drinks it the same way at the Marriage Supper of the Lamb. Following Christ's example, Bible-believing Baptists don't use fermented liquor in the Lord's Supper; we use ]{.class-0}["the fruit of the vine."]{.class-1}

[That is what is happening here in Song of Solomon 2:3--5. The King brings the bride into the house for a ]{.class-0}["banquet of wine"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 4) and squeezes the ]{.class-0}["fruit"]{.class-1}[ of verse 3 into the ]{.class-0}["flagons"]{.class-1}[ of verse 5. That is a picture of the Marriage Supper of the Lamb.]{.class-0}

[Spiritually, we can say this: that "new wine" is a picture of the Holy Spirit coming to live in the body of a Christian. He produces His fruit in the Christian. The first thing listed in that fruit is ]{.class-0}["love"]{.class-1}[ (]{.class-0}["his banner over me was love"]{.class-1}[).]{.class-0}

[You are to be ]{.class-0}["filled with the Spirit"]{.class-1}[ in contrast to being ]{.class-0}["drunk with wine"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 5:18). The Holy Spirit ]{.class-0}[sustains ]{.class-2}[the believers (Psa. 55:22) and ]{.class-0}[keeps ]{.class-2}[the believer (1 Pet. 1:5), which is spiritually how we are "stayed with flagons." And of course, the Holy Spirit ]{.class-0}[comforts ]{.class-2}[us (John 14:16, 26) through His words (Rom. 15:4 cf. Prov. 15:11)---]{.class-0}["comfort me with apples"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 5).]{.class-0}

[When the scholars hit verse 5, they start their mantras of: "Unfortunately, the ]{.class-0}[AV ]{.class-2}[has mistranslated the word here," "The original Hebrew says," and "A better translation should be." If you pick up any English Bible translated after 1880, you will see that ]{.class-0}["flagons"]{.class-1}[ is translated as "cakes of raisins" or "raisins." Even the ]{.class-0}["New" King James]{.class-2}[ reads that way.]{.class-0}

[The easy way out is to say that one of the meanings of ]{.class-0}["flagons"]{.class-1}[ is a pressed cake of raisins or grapes, and then make a marginal note here at Song of Solomon 2:5. But the only way that you get that is by going to the Hebrew. Every English dictionary you pick up defines the word ]{.class-0}[flagon ]{.class-2}[as a drinking vessel for wine or liquor.]{.class-0}

[The Hebrew word in verse 5 is ]{.class-0}[ashishah,]{.class-2}[ and it means "a cake of pressed raisins." It is translated by the ]{.class-0}[KJV]{.class-2}[ translators as ]{.class-0}[flagon(s).]{.class-2}[ The other word for ]{.class-0}[flagon]{.class-2}[ is ]{.class-0}[nebel,]{.class-2}[ and it means a "bottle" or "vessel." That is the word used in Isaiah 22:24. Everywhere else (vs. 5; 2 Sam. 6:19; 1 Chron. 16:3; Hos. 3:1), the word ]{.class-0}[ashishah]{.class-2}[ is used.]{.class-0}

[Now, "a cake of raisins" could work in 2 Samuel and 1 Chronicles. There, ]{.class-0}["of wine"]{.class-1}[ in the ]{.class-0}[KJV]{.class-2}[ is in italics. But look at Hosea 3:1. There ]{.class-0}["of wine"]{.class-1}[ is ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[in italics; it is part of the Hebrew text. So to cover their tracks, the new "Bibles" will either drop the ]{.class-0}["of wine"]{.class-1}[ without telling you, or they will put something in there about the cakes being "pagan" or "sacred," which appears in no Hebrew text at all. (At least the ]{.class-0}[NKJV]{.class-2}[ is honest at this point and puts "of the pagans" in italics to let you know that they added it with no textual basis for doing so.)]{.class-0}

[Jay Green's Interlinear Hebrew-English Old Testament gives a literal translation of "cakes of raisins of grapes." You mean the Jews knew of raisins that weren't from grapes? That's rather a silly construction considering that other dried fruits aren't called "raisins" at all. You couldn't even say that the construction is a "hendiady" as in Titus 2:13 (where two names of the same thing or person are connected by an ]{.class-0}["and"]{.class-1}[).]{.class-0}

[So what do you do when it seems like every source you pick up indicates that the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ is wrong? Well, what you don't do is change what God said.]{.class-0}

[Now, I have been in this predicament before. I have called the Bible correctors everything but white for changing Joseph's ]{.class-0}["coat of many colors"]{.class-1}[ in Genesis 37:3 to a "coat of many pieces." I did that when every lexicon, commentary, and Bible dictionary that I picked up said "coat of many pieces."]{.class-0}

You say, "Ruckman, that's not a very scholarly way to write a commentary."

[No, it isn't. But then I never claimed to be a scholar to begin with. I claimed to be a ]{.class-0}[student ]{.class-2}[of the Scriptures who believes every word in them from cover to cover, including the cover ("Holy Bible").]{.class-0}

So I put my pen down and prayed and said, "God, I've gone out on a limb for you now. I need some help here. You have to show me how these guys are wrong."

[And one day I picked up a copy of ]{.class-0}[National Geographic]{.class-2}[ and saw a picture there from some archaeological dig over in Egypt. The scene is a group of ambassadors from Canaan bowing before Pharaoh. Pharaoh is wearing a coat made like a patchwork quilt of several pieces, and every piece a ]{.class-0}[different color]{.class-2}[. I said, "Thank you, Lord," and went right back to writing my commentary and castigating the scholars.]{.class-0}

[You see, I am not against "scholarship," per se (although I have been around long enough to be suspicious of all higher education and "intellectualism"). What I am against is any man who plays God by setting himself up as a judge over that Book. I have known some actual scholars in my time that actually believed and honored the ]{.class-0}[AV.]{.class-2}[ But they are the exception to the rule. Most scholars aren't worth shooting.]{.class-0}

[In regards to ]{.class-0}[ashishah,]{.class-2}[ the Hebrew Rabbis themselves do not even believe it should be translated as "a cake of raisins" or "raisins" every time it shows up in the Scriptures. A Rabbi Samuel said that the translation should be "a cask of wine" based upon the construction of Hosea 3:1. So the word ]{.class-0}["flagons"]{.class-1}[ is a ]{.class-0}[possible translation,]{.class-2}[ and seeing as how the Holy Spirit chose that word for the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ text, we will accept His interpretation of the text over that of the Hebrew scholars. A ]{.class-0}[flagon,]{.class-2}[ in the Scriptures, is any number of vessels, large or small, skins or pottery, cups or pitchers (and possibly barrels), used to hold wine; in this case,]{.class-0}[ new wine.]{.class-2}

[The Bride is asking, in verse 5, to be sustained on the new wine of the King. The ]{.class-0}["flagons"]{.class-1}[ is used in a metaphorical sense to represent the contents of the flagon. This is the same way that the ]{.class-0}["cup"]{.class-1}[ is used in 1 Corinthians 11:25 where Paul records Christ at the institution of the Lord's Supper as saying, ]{.class-0}["This cup is the new testament in my blood: this do ye, as oft as ye drink it."]{.class-1}[ What is the ]{.class-0}["it"]{.class-1}[? It is the ]{.class-0}["cup."]{.class-1}

[Well, the disciples weren't literally drinking the cup; they were drinking the ]{.class-0}[contents]{.class-2}[ of the cup. The cup wasn't the symbol of the blood; it was the new wine in the cup that represented the blood.]{.class-0}

When you hear a Catholic say that he takes the Lord literally in the Mass, you can mark it down, either he is lying through his teeth, or he doesn't know about what he is talking. No Catholic takes 1 Corinthians 11:25 literally. If he did, he would have to drink molten metal, because the Lord in that passage said to drink the cup, not the wine.

"[Comfort me with apples."]{.class-1}[ We have already commented on the spiritual application of this verse. Historically, one of the uses for the types of apples that were grown in Israel was for aromatic therapy: their smell had a soothing quality.]{.class-0}

"[I am sick of love."]{.class-1}[ She is not sick ]{.class-0}[of]{.class-2}[ loving the King. She is sick ]{.class-0}[from]{.class-2}[ loving. We call it "love-sickness" today. It is someone pining over the one he or she loves. You often see it in teenagers who are in "puppy love." (And as one preacher said, "It may be only 'puppy love,' but it's real to the puppy.")]{.class-0}

[The Scriptural illustration of the phrase is found in 2 Samuel 13:1--2. ]{.class-0}["And it came to pass after this, that Absalom the son of David had a fair sister, whose name was Tamar; and Amnon the son of David loved her. And Amnon was so vexed, that he fell sick for his sister Tamar; for she was a virgin; and Amnon thought it hard for him to do anything to her."]{.class-1}

Verse 6 is a typical embrace of lovers and is so well illustrated in the movies and on the covers of "romance" novels that it needs no comment.

[Verse 7 is addressed to Israel just as 1:5 was. ]{.class-0}["Roes"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["hinds"]{.class-1}[ are both different kinds of deer. The ]{.class-0}[roe]{.class-2}[ is a gazelle; the ]{.class-0}[hind]{.class-2}[ is a female red deer. Proverbs 5:18--19 says, ]{.class-0}["Rejoice with the wife of thy youth. Let her be as the loving hind and pleasant roe."]{.class-1}

[Down in Song of Sol. 2:9, the Bible says, ]{.class-0}["My beloved]{.class-1}[ \[the Bridegroom\]]{.class-0}[ is like a roe or a young hart."]{.class-1}[ The ]{.class-0}["hart"]{.class-1}[ is a young male red deer.]{.class-0}

[What you have here is the Bride giving the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ a warning based upon the relationship the Bride has toward the King. In type, the Church is warning Israel not to get the Lord up until He is ready to get up.]{.class-0}

[In this age, the Church Age, the Lord is pictured as resting and taking a nap. Of course, He isn't sleeping. Psalm 121:4 says, ]{.class-0}["Behold, he that keepeth Israel shall neither slumber nor sleep."]{.class-1}[ So He is not really sleeping. But He is seated up in Heaven right now, resting from His work of atonement (Heb. 4:10), until the time when He returns to establish His kingdom here on earth (Acts 3:21; Heb. 10:12--13). When He does that, He is likened to a man awaking ]{.class-0}["out of sleep."]{.class-1}

[Psalm 78:65--66,]{.class-0}[ "Then the Lord awaked as one out of sleep, and like a mighty man that shouteth by reason of wine. And he smote his enemies in the hinder parts: he put them to a perpetual reproach."]{.class-1}

[Psalm 78:65--66 is a reference to the Second Advent. (See our comments on the passage in ]{.class-0}[The Bible Believer's Commentary on the Psalms,]{.class-2}[ Vol. 2.)]{.class-0}

[So in Isaiah 51:9, again a reference to the Second Advent, Isaiah writes, ]{.class-0}["Awake, awake, put on strength, O arm of the LORD; awake, as in the ancient days, in the generations of old."]{.class-1}[ And what follows is Revelation 12--20.]{.class-0}

When the Bible speaks of Christ being "asleep" in this age, it means that He isn't working overtly, supernaturally, or miraculously. As we discussed in the Introduction to our Commentary on Esther, today, the Lord is working behind the scenes, providentially. He is directing events and working through men and circumstances. There is no Pentecostal "Latter Rain" of miracles, tongues, and healing.

But once the Rapture of the Church occurs (Rev. 4:1), the Lord gets out of His seat and steps up to the throne and takes the book of judgment out of the Father's hand (Rev. 5:7) and all hell breaks out on this earth. If you want to see "the day of miracles," just reject Christ and stick around for the Tribulation, and you will see them, I kid you not. Of course, most of them will be NEGATIVE miracles of JUDGMENT, but when has a Charismatic ever gotten the Scriptures right on such matters?

I have a note in my Bible at Psalm 78:65 that says, "I don't want to be in the barroom when He begins to mop it up." And I won't be either, brother. I'm coming down with the "Mopper"; I'm not going to be one of the "moppees."

I like the sign that a little boy put on his bike. "Jesus Christ is coming back soon, and, boy, is He ever mad!" How true that is, and how horribly and terribly true people are going to find that to be. It's amusing now; it won't be funny then.

8 The voice of my beloved! behold, he cometh leaping upon the mountains, skipping upon the hills.

9 My beloved is like a roe or a young hart: behold, he standeth behind our wall, he looketh forth at the windows, shewing himself through the lattice.

10 My beloved spake, and said unto me, Rise up, my love, my fair one, and come away.

11 For, lo, the winter is past, the rain is over and gone;

12 The flowers appear on the earth; the time of the singing of birds is come, and the voice of the turtle is heard in our land;

13 The fig tree putteth forth her green figs, and the vines with the tender grape give a good smell. Arise, my love, my fair one, and come away.

[The Bride is still speaking here, but there is a paragraph mark at verse 8. She has just gotten through warning the Jews, in type, not to awaken the Lord until He is ready. Now she is about to describe what happens in relation to ]{.class-0}[her]{.class-2}[ (not the daughters) when He does.]{.class-0}

I will often speak of the Second Coming of the Lord as synonymous with the Advent, but the fact is that the Second Coming has two parts to it. First, Christ returns as the Head of the Church to take His Body home to Heaven. It is the Bridegroom returning to get His Bride. That is the "Rapture" of the Church. The second part is the Advent where Christ returns as a conquering King.

[The world has reason to fear the Second Coming. They have nothing to look forward to but the Lord's ]{.class-0}["indignation," "fierce anger,"]{.class-1}[ and being ]{.class-0}["devoured with the fire"]{.class-1}[ of God's jealousy. They are the ]{.class-0}["prey,"]{.class-1}[ and the Lord is the predator (Zeph. 3:8).]{.class-0}

[But the Christian isn't under God's wrath (John 3:36). He is ]{.class-0}["blessed\...in Christ," "chosen\...in him," "holy and without blame before him in love," "predestinated\...unto the adoption of children by Jesus Christ of himself"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["accepted in the beloved"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 1:3--6). We are looking ]{.class-0}["for his Son from heaven\...even Jesus, which delivered us from the wrath to come"]{.class-1}[ (1 Thess. 1:10). To us, His return is a comfort (1 Thess. 4:18) and a hope (Tit. 2:13).]{.class-0}

It's the difference between a judge coming home to his wife and kids after a day on the bench hearing the case against a murderer who was just found guilty. The next day he will go in to pronounce a death sentence on the convicted man for his crimes. When that judge comes home, his wife and children don't see him in the same way as the convicted murderer does when he steps into the courtroom. The wife and kids are eager to see their husband and daddy come home every day, while the prisoner is dreading a condemning judge.

The passage here isn't the Second Advent. The judgment of God isn't falling here. Jesus Christ isn't coming back to kill the armies of the Antichrist.

The passage here is the Bride being called out by her Lover. It is a picture of the Rapture of the Church.

"[The voice of my beloved!"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 8). That's what we're waiting for. We are not waiting for the Antichrist to show up. We are not waiting for the temple to be rebuilt. We are not waiting for the revived Roman Empire to be reestablished in Europe. It may be that those things will happen before the Rapture. If they do, we will certainly take note of them and mark them down as the fulfillment of Bible prophecy. But that is not what we are anticipating.]{.class-0}

[We are listening for a sound, not looking for a sign. We are listening for ]{.class-0}["a shout"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["the voice of the archangel"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["the trump of God."]{.class-1}[ We are listening for our Lord to call us each by name (John 10:3). We are listening for a command that will change our bodies ]{.class-0}["in a moment, in the twinkling of an eye"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 4:1; 1 Cor. 15:52). We are waiting for the ]{.class-0}["Come up hither."]{.class-1}[ We are looking for the Uppertaker, not the undertaker.]{.class-0}

"[Behold, he cometh leaping upon the mountains, skipping upon the hills."]{.class-1}[ Again, this is a picture of the Rapture and not the Advent. At the Advent, He does more than leap or skip on mountains and hills. He comes ]{.class-0}[down from them ]{.class-2}[to fight in battle (Joel 2:1--2). When He leaps on the mountains at the Advent, He won't be ]{.class-0}[alone:]{.class-2}[ He'll be accompanied by an army of supernatural horsemen that decimate the land (Joel 2:3--5).]{.class-0}

[That is not the picture here. ]{.class-2}[Here, the picture is a loving Bridegroom bringing joy at His coming. He is calling His Bride to come away with Him (vs. 10). The Bridegroom is alone here in Song of Solomon 2; no army accompanies Him.]{.class-0}

[When the Lord says that ]{.class-0}["he cometh leaping upon the mountains, skipping upon the hills,"]{.class-1}[ He is talking about His return into the lower atmosphere. Paul is very clear in 1 Thessalonians 4:17 that, at the Rapture, the Lord does not ]{.class-0}[land ]{.class-2}[on the ground. When we meet Him, we meet Him ]{.class-0}["in the clouds\...in the air."]{.class-1}

[Verse 9:]{.class-0}[ "My beloved is like a roe or a young hart."]{.class-1}[ In the context, the Bride is talking about the speed of the two deer as they leap and skip. Hence, Santa Claus has to have deer pull his sleigh, and they are deer that can travel completely around the world, visiting every child in one night. (The world has to imitate the Bible whether or not they believe it or practice it.)]{.class-0}

[Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["Behold, I come quickly"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 22:12). Paul says the Rapture will take place ]{.class-0}["in a moment, in the twinkling of an eye"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 15:52). The last recorded words of Jesus in the Bible are: ]{.class-0}["Surely I come quickly"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 22:20).]{.class-0}

"[Behold, he standeth behind our wall, he looketh forth at the windows, shewing himself through the lattice."]{.class-1}[ This part of verse 9 gets into what scientists call "the fabric of the universe." It is the kind of thing that Paul prayed the saints would comprehend when he spoke of ]{.class-0}["the breadth, and length, and depth, and height"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 3:18 and comments in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

From the verse, we learn that God is separate from His creation. God is on the other side of a wall that separates the third heaven from the rest of the universe. He may hold the universe together (Col. 1:17) and even wear it like a garment (Heb. 1:10--12), but He is not the creation. His essence, His being, dwells in a place that is divided from His creation by a wall.

Within that wall are windows and a door. From those windows God can pour out spiritual blessings or physical water.

[Malachi 3:10, ]{.class-0}["Bring ye all the tithes into the storehouse, that there may be meat in mine house, and prove me now herewith, saith the LORD of hosts, if I will not open you the WINDOWS OF HEAVEN, and pour you out a blessing, that there shall not be room enough to receive it."]{.class-1}

You say, "That's metaphorical, Dr. Ruckman."

Is it? Look at Genesis 7:11.

"[In the six hundredth year of Noah's life, in the second month, the seventeenth day of the month, the same day were all the fountains of the great deep broken up, and the WINDOWS OF HEAVEN were opened."]{.class-1}

[Over a quarter of a million people bet their lives on God not having literal windows in Heaven, and they lost. God considers this such an important "fundamental of the faith" that]{.class-0}[ He would kill you if you didn't believe it.]{.class-2}

[In 2 Kings 7, Samaria was besieged by the Syrians, and there was a famine. When the King sought a word from the Lord through Elisha, the prophet said, ]{.class-0}["To morrow about this time shall a measure of fine flour be sold for a shekel, and two measures of barley for a shekel, in the gate of Samaria"]{.class-1}[ (2 Kings 7:1).]{.class-0}

[When that word came back to the King, one of his advisors said, ]{.class-0}["If the LORD would make windows in heaven, might this thing be?"]{.class-1}[ (2 Kings 7:2).]{.class-0}

[Wrong thing to say, buddy. The Lord ]{.class-0}[did]{.class-2}[ put ]{.class-0}["windows in heaven."]{.class-1}[ But because that fellow didn't believe that to be true, God said, ]{.class-0}["Behold, thou shalt see it with thine eyes, but shalt not eat thereof."]{.class-1}

[The next day when God broke the siege and ended the famine, the King put that guy in charge of letting the people out through the gate of the city to get the food. That fellow was mobbed and stomped to death]{.class-0}[ because he didn't believe what God said.]{.class-2}

[That is why I do not call myself a ]{.class-0}[Fundamentalist.]{.class-2}[ It is not that I don't believe in the fundamentals; I do. But brethren, there is a lot more in that Book than the ]{.class-0}[fundamentals]{.class-2}[, no matter by whose creed you go. I am a ]{.class-0}[Bible believer;]{.class-2}[ that will cover the fundamentals. That means that I believe everything in that Book from cover to cover. I believe it as God wrote it and then preserved it for me in the English ]{.class-0}[Authorized Version.]{.class-2}

[I believe that Book has been preserved by God without proven error. When I hold up a ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible and say, "This Book doesn't ]{.class-0}[contain]{.class-2}[ the word of God; it ]{.class-0}[is]{.class-2}[ the word of God," I mean what I say. In other words, I actually believe what the Christian celebrities profess to believe without really believing it.]{.class-0}

[Now, you take that ]{.class-0}["wall"]{.class-1}[ and that ]{.class-0}[door ]{.class-2}[and those ]{.class-0}["windows."]{.class-1}[ I don't profess to understand everything about what I am going to show you. I am no astrophysicist, and I am not sure even they would understand it even if they believed it. But I can give you what the Bible says, and we'll leave the subject right there.]{.class-0}

[Job 26:7, ]{.class-0}["He stretcheth out the north over the empty place."]{.class-1}[ About what is He talking there? He is talking about the place where God dwells.]{.class-0}

"[For promotion cometh neither from the east, nor from the west, nor from the south"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 75:6). What direction did the Lord leave out? He left out the ]{.class-0}[north.]{.class-2}[ Look at the next verse: ]{.class-0}["But God is the judge"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 75:7). He substituted ]{.class-0}["God"]{.class-1}[ for north. So ]{.class-0}["north"]{.class-1}[ in Job 26:6 is Heaven.]{.class-0}

[Job 26:8, ]{.class-0}["He bindeth up the waters in his thick clouds; and the cloud is not rent under them."]{.class-1}[ The creationist will say those are rain clouds, but that won't work. Look at Job 26:9.]{.class-0}

"[He holdeth back the face of his throne, and spreadeth his cloud upon it."]{.class-1}[ Those ]{.class-0}["thick clouds"]{.class-1}[ are one ]{.class-0}["cloud"]{.class-1}[ in verse 8, and in verse 9 that cloud is before ]{.class-0}["the face of his throne."]{.class-1}

[Now, what does that cloud do? It binds up the waters in Job 26:8 and 10. Where are those ]{.class-0}["waters"]{.class-1}[? Well, they sure aren't the cumulus, stratus, and cirrus clouds up in the sky. The context is between the second and third heavens (Job 26:7, 9--11, 13).]{.class-0}

[Turn over to Job 38:8, ]{.class-0}["Or who shut up the sea with doors, when it brake forth, as if it had issued out of the womb?"]{.class-1}[ What's the context? Job 38:4--7; it's ]{.class-0}["the foundation of the earth."]{.class-1}[ It's Genesis 1:1.]{.class-0}

[That sea broke forth, and the earth was overflowed with it (2 Pet. 3:5--6) in Genesis 1:2. And the Lord made]{.class-0}[ "a firmament in the midst of the waters"]{.class-1}[ which divided ]{.class-0}["the waters from the waters"]{.class-1}[ (Gen. 1:6--7), He took that water and shoved it clear out past Alpha Draconis, the galaxies, the nebulae, the pulsars, and the quasars (Gen. 1:14--17). That process is described in Job 38:9--11.]{.class-0}

"[When I made the cloud the garment thereof, and thick darkness a swathingband for it. And brake up for it my decreed place, and set bars and doors, And said, Hitherto shalt thou come, but no further: and here shall thy proud waves be stayed?"]{.class-1}

[Of course, you can certainly make some application to the Atlantic and the Pacific when it comes to God "staying" the waves, but what do you do with that ]{.class-0}["cloud"]{.class-1}[ and that ]{.class-0}["thick darkness"]{.class-1}[? There is no cloud or thick darkness which surrounds the oceans and seas of this earth to prevent them from overflowing the land.]{.class-0}

This is what we call the doctrine of the "great deeps" (see chart at the end of this Commentary), and simply stated it is this: the entirety of God's physical creation is shaped like a pyramid, because a pyramid is the only structure to have four physical dimensions (Eph. 3:18). At the bottom of this structure is the Lake of Fire (Isa. 14:15). In the middle is what we perceive as the universe. It is the firmament created in Genesis 1:6--7 and in which God placed the sun, moon, stars, planets, etc. It is what we call the second heaven or outer space. This firmament divides a body of water so huge that the combined waters of all the oceans, seas, rivers, lakes, and fountains on earth would be less than a drop in it.

At the top of this structure, in the north, sits "Heaven." It is positioned as the capstone to the pyramid. Hence, if you look on the back of a dollar bill, you will see a pyramid with the capstone separated from it, and in the capstone is an all-seeing eye. That symbol is a picture of, among other things, the universe. God is that all-seeing eye (Psa. 5:3), and He lives in a Heaven which is separated from the rest of the universe.

The thing that separates the universe from "Heaven" is that body of water above the universe that is set in bounds by a cloud and thick darkness. I believe the common expression is "a wall of water" (Exod. 14:22). That wall is a literal wall, for it is solid.

[Job 38:30,]{.class-0}[ "The waters are hid AS WITH A STONE, and the face of the deep is FROZEN."]{.class-1}

[Revelation 4:6, ]{.class-0}["And before the throne there was a SEA OF GLASS like unto crystal"]{.class-1}[ (cf. Job 26:9 and 38:8).]{.class-0}

[In that solid wall of water is set bars and doors (Job 38:10) and windows. So in Revelation 4:1, John writes, ]{.class-0}["After this I looked, and, behold, a DOOR was opened in heaven."]{.class-1}

[Of course, for us, that ]{.class-0}["door"]{.class-1}[ is personified in Jesus Christ who said, ]{.class-0}["I am the door of the sheep"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:7). But the spiritual truth of a thing does not negate its physical reality. There is a physical "door" in Heaven that opens through a body of water whose top is ]{.class-0}[frozen solid.]{.class-2}

[When you get to the New Jerusalem, there are twelve gates on that city (Rev. 21), and the names of those gates are given in the book of Nehemiah (see the list on pg. 217 of the ]{.class-0}[Bible Believer's Commentary on Ezra, Nehemiah, Esther,]{.class-2}[ Bible Baptist Bookstore, 2004). I don't know if those are the same as the doors and windows to Heaven itself, but if they are, then you have a situation where, right now, different gates would be used for different purposes.]{.class-0}

[When the Lord gets ready for the Rapture, He will exit the ]{.class-0}[sheep gate]{.class-2}[ (John 10:3) and bring you in through the ]{.class-0}[fish gate]{.class-2}[ (Matt. 4:19). At the Advent, the Lord would come out that ]{.class-0}[horse gate]{.class-2}[ on his white Arabian stallion, followed by the armies of Heaven. At the White Throne Judgment, He would take the unsaved (and finally the Devil) and pitch them out the ]{.class-0}[dung gate]{.class-2}[ into the Lake of Fire.]{.class-0}

[Now, between our comments on 1 Thessalonians 4, 1 Corinthians 15, and John 10 in those Commentaries, we have pretty well covered the doctrine of the Rapture of the Church. But the thing to remember about the Rapture is that it is not merely a "catching away." The Bible calls it an ]{.class-0}["appearing." "Looking for that blessed hope, and the glorious APPEARING of the great God and our Saviour Jesus Christ"]{.class-1}[ (Tit. 2:13).]{.class-0}

"[Henceforth there is laid up for me a crown of righteousness, which the Lord, the righteous judge, shall give me at that day: and not to me only, but unto all them also that love his APPEARING"]{.class-1}[ (2 Tim. 4:8).]{.class-0}

"[I charge thee therefore before God, and the Lord Jesus Christ, who shall judge the quick and the dead at his APPEARING and his kingdom"]{.class-1}[ (2 Tim. 4:1).]{.class-0}

"[Beloved, now are we the sons of God, and it doth not yet appear what we shall be: but we know that, when HE SHALL APPEAR, we shall be like him; for we shall SEE him as he is"]{.class-1}[ (1 John 3:2).]{.class-0}

[Paul said, ]{.class-0}["For now we see through a glass, darkly; but then face to face"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 13:12).]{.class-0}

[The text here in Song of Solomon 2:9 says, ]{.class-0}["he looketh forth at the windows, SHEWING HIMSELF THROUGH THE LATTICE."]{.class-1}

So before we are caught up through the door in Heaven at the Rapture, the Scriptures seem to imply that the Lord looks out of one of the windows in Heaven like a man looking out of a window with "blinds" on it and He shows Himself to us.

Now, some of what I am about to give is speculation because it is not very clear in Scripture. Nevertheless, I will take what little the Scriptures say about it and try to make some sense of it for you.

[When it comes to the order of the Rapture, the first thing you will hear will be a ]{.class-0}[trumpet blast]{.class-2}[. That will be the first in a series of "trumps" (the sound that a trumpet makes) that you will hear. When Israel was in the wilderness in the book of Numbers, the Lord had Moses make ]{.class-0}["two trumpets of silver\...for the calling of the assembly, and for the journeying of the camps"]{.class-1}[ (Num. 10:2). Those trumpets were blown to gather all the congregation to the door of the Tabernacle (Num. 10:3). Then the trumpets were blown to start Israel on its journeys through the wilderness.]{.class-0}

"[When ye blow an alarm, then the camps that lie on the east parts shall go forward. When ye blow an alarm the second time, then the camps that lie on the south side shall take their journey: they shall blow an alarm for their journeys"]{.class-1}[ (Num. 10:5--6).]{.class-0}

[Notice that ]{.class-0}[two alarms]{.class-2}[ are blown for the camps to set out. There are two groups of saints that are taken up at the Rapture. The first are dead saints. Numbers 10:5 says, ]{.class-0}["the camps that lie on the east parts shall go forward."]{.class-1}[ So in every cemetery the bodies ]{.class-0}[face east]{.class-2}[. As I have said before, the Bible lays down the rules, and the world has to follow them whether it believes that Book or not. That ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible runs the world.]{.class-0}

[The second group of saints are ]{.class-0}[living]{.class-2}[. Since they are being gathered to the ]{.class-0}[north]{.class-2}[ (see pg. 112), Numbers 10:6 says, ]{.class-0}["then the camps that lie on the south side shall take their journey."]{.class-1}

[So the first time that trumpet sounds, it is to let you know that you are about to be gathered together at the door (Rev. 4:1). Then the Lord looks out of the windows in Heaven ]{.class-0}["through the lattice."]{.class-1}

[Can you imagine looking up in the sky and seeing this gigantic face looking at you? I am sure that it will be frightening; after all, He nearly scared the disciples half to death when He came to them ]{.class-0}["walking on the sea"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 14:25--27). That was a picture of the Rapture. But won't it be something to hear Him say, ]{.class-0}["Come,"]{.class-1}[ and you begin to ]{.class-0}[walk on]{.class-2}[ ]{.class-0}[air ]{.class-2}[to go to Him just like Peter ]{.class-0}[walked on water]{.class-2}[ (Matt. 14:28--29).]{.class-0}

I don't know how much time will elapse between the time He appears to us and the time He calls us up. But if there is any amount of time that transpires at all, don't you know that all the Christians will be running around like a bunch of maniacs.

You are with your wife in the car when you hear that first trumpet sound. You both look at each other hoping your spouse won't think you are crazy. "Did you just hear what I just heard?" you say in unison.

Then you look out of the window and see this big face in the sky, and the Holy Spirit inside you says, "That's the Lord. That's the one who saved you; that's the one you love (1 Pet. 1:8)."

Suddenly, you both realize "This is it! It's the Rapture! He's about to call us home!"

[By now, traffic has come to a halt because all the Christians scattered through all the vehicles have stopped in the middle of the road. Half a dozen of them have grabbed tracts and are running up and down through the middle of all those cars screaming, "Ya' gotta get saved! Ya' gotta get saved! The Lord's coming back]{.class-0}[ right now!"]{.class-2}

All the lost will be cursing you and calling you a religious "nut" and a "Bible-thumping" fanatic. Janet Reno will be trying to haul you off to prison as a terrorist. Then the next trumpet blast sounds.

[Revelation 4:1 says, ]{.class-0}["And the first voice which I heard was as it were of a trumpet talking with me."]{.class-1}

[When the Father answers the prayer of Jesus in John 12, the Bible says, ]{.class-0}["The people therefore, that stood by, and heard it, said that it thundered: others said, An angel spoke to him."]{.class-1}

[So the Apostle Paul writes, ]{.class-0}["For the Lord himself shall descend from heaven with a shout, with the voice of the archangel, and with the trump of God: and the dead in Christ shall rise first"]{.class-1}[ (1 Thess. 4:16).]{.class-0}

[As those trumpets are going off, all the unsaved hear is a crash of ]{.class-0}[thunder ]{.class-2}[so loud they will think someone has pushed "the button" and started World War III. But the saved hear words in those trumpets, and like the song says, "Some day that trumpet's gonna sound so loud that it will raise the dead."]{.class-0}

[Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["For the hour is coming, in the which all that are in the graves shall hear his voice, And shall come forth; they that have done good, unto the resurrection of life" ]{.class-1}[(John 5:28--29). And for ]{.class-0}["the dead in Christ,"]{.class-1}[ that hour is come.]{.class-0}

[It won't matter if they have just suffered a massive heart attack and have only been dead a few hours (like Jairus' daughter) or if they are embalmed for burial (like the widow of Nain's son) or have been dead long enough to decay into dust (like Lazarus), those physical bodies of the dead saints will hear Christ call them ]{.class-0}[by name]{.class-2}[ to come out of the grave like He called Lazarus in John 11.]{.class-0}

[Paul said, ]{.class-0}["For the trumpet shall sound, and the dead shall be raised incorruptible"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 15:52).]{.class-0}

[A lady came to James McGinlay one time and asked, "Bro. McGinlay, if all Christians are one in Jesus Christ, why is it that at the Rapture the dead rise ]{.class-0}[first."]{.class-2}

McGinlay sent up one of those quick "Nehemiah" prayers and replied, "Because, dear lady, the dead have six feet farther to rise than we do, so the Lord lets them get a head start so that we can all rise to meet Him together."

That's a "cute" response, of course, but it's not Bible. In the Bible, the example we have of the resurrection of dead saints is found in Matthew 27:52--53.

"[And the graves were opened; and many bodies of the saints which slept arose, And came out of the graves after his resurrection, and went into the holy city, and appeared unto many."]{.class-1}

Of course, I do not know for sure, but the Lord may let those resurrected saints walk around for a couple of hours and appear to a lot of people before they are caught up, as one final witness from the Body of Christ to a lost world. You have to admit, it would shake a lost young man up to have his Christian grandmother, whom he buried last month, show up at his door and say, "Won't you please accept Christ before it is too late?"

And then there is one final trumpet sound and that is the signal for the living saints to take off.

"[Behold, I shew you a mystery; We shall not all sleep, but we shall all be changed, In a moment, in the twinkling of an eye, at the last trump"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 15:51--52).]{.class-0}

Like the dead saints, we also hear our names called (John 10:3). When that last blast of the trumpet sounds, I'll hear "Peter Sturges Ruckman, Come up hither!" And brother, I'll be gone!

I am ready to go right now. "Let 'er rip" is my attitude. And the sooner, the better!

[Now, we're not done with the doctrine of the Rapture here in the Song of Solomon, yet. There is more here about it than there is in the Pauline epistles. Paul says, ]{.class-0}["But of the times and the seasons, brethren, ye have no need that I write unto you"]{.class-1}[ (1 Thess. 5:1), but he never tells what they are. Solomon does.]{.class-0}

[The Song says, ]{.class-0}["Rise up, my love, my fair one, and come away"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 10). That's the Bridegroom speaking to the Bride. It's the Rapture.]{.class-0}

[When does it take place?]{.class-2}[ Look at verse 11. ]{.class-0}["For, lo, the winter is past."]{.class-1}[ So it isn't in December, January, or February.]{.class-0}[ "The rain is over and gone."]{.class-1}[ It's not April. The early rains are through.]{.class-0}

"[The flowers appear on the earth"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 12). The saying is: "April showers bring May flowers." The implication of the verse is ]{.class-0}[May]{.class-2}[. Verse 13 sets the time in May.]{.class-0}

"[The fig tree putteth forth her green figs"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13). Christ said, ]{.class-0}["Now learn a parable of the fig tree; When his branch is yet tender, and putteth forth leaves, ye know that summer is nigh"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 24:32). So the time is]{.class-0}[ late spring]{.class-2}[ leading into summer. On the calendar that's the end of ]{.class-0}[May ]{.class-2}[and the beginning of ]{.class-0}[June]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[That is the time of year for the Feast of Pentecost. So the Feast of Trumpets has nothing to do with the Rapture of the Church. The Feast of Trumpets points to a ]{.class-0}[post-Tribulation rapture of the Jews]{.class-2}[ within weeks of the Second Advent at the Feast of Tabernacles or the Day of Atonement. If the Church, the Body of Christ, is going to go up on a feast day, then it will be the feast at which it was born: the Feast of Pentecost.]{.class-0}

I can hear the apostate Fundamentalists now saying, "Oh, there goes Ruckman, again, setting a date for the Rapture. Cult leader! Heretic!"

I have never set a definite date for the Rapture in my life. I have made some guesses based on Scripture, and that's all I have ever made---guesses.

You say, "Well, what if you're wrong about this one too?"

Oh, I'll probably feel disappointed for a second, if that long. You really don't believe that I am going to wallow in self-pity over an incorrect exegesis of the Scripture when my Saviour shows up, do you?

Listen, people, I'll say it one more time so you can get it: I am not looking to be absolutely correct in everything I say so I can vindicate myself to my students. I am looking for my Lord to come back and take me home to Glory. If He decides to do that in the Winter or the Summer or the Fall, that is perfectly all right with me. If He does, then I will answer to the Lord at the Judgment Seat of Christ for what I have taught, and I will take my lumps gladly.

The Lord will say, "Ruckman, why did you teach My people that I was going to return in the Spring?"

"[Well, Lord. I read Song of Solomon 2:8--13 in your Book, and it sure seemed like it was talking about the Rapture. After all, that Bridegroom told the Bride to ]{.class-0}['Rise up\...come away']{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}['Arise\...and come away.']{.class-1}[ What was I to believe?"]{.class-0}

"[Well, you were wrong," the Lord will say. "As punishment you will have to serve all of these good, godly scholars (who knew all I was talking about was a love triangle between Solomon, a shepherdess, and her shepherd lover) a thousand years each. You'll have to do whatever they say. They all knew the answer was to be found in the 'original Hebrew' while you were fooling around with that old, archaic ]{.class-0}[Authorized Version.]{.class-2}[ What do you have to say about that?"]{.class-0}

"[Yes, Lord. Very good, Lord. I'll get right on it, Lord. ]{.class-0}[Befel ist befel!"]{.class-2}

That's what I'll say. If I am wrong, I'll take my licks. But if they are wrong, they will pay for every child of God whom they caused to doubt God's words and question God's words and change God's words and not believe God's words. In the meantime, I will stick with what the Scriptures say and let the scholars babble on.

"[The turtle"]{.class-1}[ of verse 12 is a turtledove, as in Jeremiah 8:7.]{.class-0}

14 O my dove, that art in the clefts of the rock, in the secret places of the stairs, let me see thy countenance, let me hear thy voice; for sweet is thy voice, and thy countenance is comely.

15 Take us the foxes, the little foxes, that spoil the vines: for our vines have tender grapes.

"[O my dove, that art in the clefts of the rock"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). That can be a good thing or a bad thing, depending upon the rock in which you are hiding. Those Edomites in Obadiah 3 were puffed up with pride because they thought their rock fortress of Selah-Petra was invulnerable. They were wrong. The Lord says much of the same thing about the Jews in Jeremiah 49:16.]{.class-0}

[But if God does the hiding, He will hide you in the ]{.class-0}[right ]{.class-2}[Rock, and you will be safe. Deuteronomy 32:31 says, ]{.class-0}["For their rock is not as our Rock, even our enemies themselves being judges."]{.class-1}[ He hid Moses in a cleft of the rock and kept him safe]{.class-0}[ ]{.class-1}[while the Lord passed by in His glory (Exod. 33:18--23). Moses was in the "Rock of Ages."]{.class-0}

[We sing the hymn "He hideth my soul in the cleft of the Rock that shadows a dry thirsty land." That song is written that way because Paul says, ]{.class-0}["And did all drink the same spiritual drink: for they drank of that spiritual Rock that followed them; and that Rock was Christ"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 10:4).]{.class-0}

[Colossians 3:3 says, ]{.class-0}["For ye are dead, and your life is hid with Christ in God."]{.class-1}

So the picture in Song of Solomon 2:14 is the eternal security of the believer.

"[In the secret places of the stairs"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). Now we are back to the Rapture and the structure of the universe.]{.class-0}

[Back in Genesis 28:12, Jacob dreamed about ]{.class-0}["a ladder set up on the earth, and the top of it reached to heaven: and behold the angels of God ascending and descending on it."]{.class-1}

[Jesus told Nathanael, ]{.class-0}["Hereafter ye shall see heaven open, and the angels of God ascending and descending upon the Son of man"]{.class-1}[ (John 1:51).]{.class-0}

That means that between the Christian and His Lord is a passageway that can take you to the third heaven after you have been changed in less than a second (1 Cor. 15:52).

The scientist and the science fiction writers talk about "wormholes." Those are "short cuts" through the "space-time continuum" that allow energy and matter to travel from one point in the universe to another faster than light could make the journey in normal space. It is one of those corollaries based on Einstein's theory of relativity.

[The original is found in a ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible]{.class-0}[,]{.class-2}[ first published in 1611. Modern man doesn't have to go "back to the Bible"; he has to run to catch up with it.]{.class-0}

[That Bible says that when the Queen of Sheba visited Solomon and saw ]{.class-0}["his ascent by which he WENT UP UNTO THE HOUSE OF THE LORD; there was no more spirit in her"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 10:5). In type, that means the biggest "wormhole" the scientists could research is the one by which Christ went to Heaven and back in a space of less than two hours (John 20:17 cf. Matt. 28:9).]{.class-0}

[That phrase ]{.class-0}["in the secret places of the stairs"]{.class-1}[ is a great example of the Holy Spirit putting His words in such simple terms that anybody in any age could get them. Just think for a minute. If you were God and you were trying to tell Solomon about a passage way to the third heaven, how else would you explain it? You couldn't say ]{.class-0}[escalator]{.class-2}[ or ]{.class-0}[elevator;]{.class-2}[ nobody from 1000 B.C. to A.D. 1900 would know about what you were talking. If you said "wormhole," they would think about something you found in a rotten apple. No, when the Holy Spirit speaks to man, He speaks in plain, simple language.]{.class-0}

[So there is a direct pathway from earth to Heaven. Moses calls it a ]{.class-0}["ladder"]{.class-1}[ (Gen. 28:12); Solomon calls it ]{.class-0}["stairs"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). Again, for the Christian, that passage is personified in Jesus Christ.]{.class-0}

[John 14:6, ]{.class-0}["Jesus saith unto him, I am the WAY, the truth, and the life: no man COMETH unto the Father, BUT BY ME."]{.class-1}

As we have seen, that is not speaking in a spiritual sense only: it is also literal.

I spoke with a scientist one time about these matters, and he told me this: the main thing that prevents us from travelling at the speed of light is friction. Friction is created when two material objects rub against each other. That friction goes all the way down to the molecular level. If you could remove all friction down to the molecules, there is nothing that could prevent your continued acceleration.

He said the only place that could occur is in a perfect vacuum. Outer space is not a perfect vacuum. It contains cosmic dust and other particles that create friction and slow a spacecraft down.

That scientist proposed this: when the Lord returns, He creates a perfect vacuum from you to Him. Then you get sucked up to Him, faster than light can travel. Of course, I don't know if that is so, but there you have it. I'll leave somebody else who is better with mathematics than I am to work on it and figure it out.

"[Let me see thy countenance, let me hear thy voice; for sweet is thy voice, and thy countenance is comely"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). This is still the Bridegroom speaking to the Bride. He wants to see her. When you get over into chapter 3, you read that the Bride wants to see him. That's an ideal love situation.]{.class-0}

Let's look at this matter from the standpoint of the Bridegroom first. The Bridegroom wants to see his Bride; he wants to hear her voice. That's a picture, first, of our fellowship and communion with the Lord.

[Christian, the Lord wants to see your face as you come to His Book to get His words. Paul says, ]{.class-0}["But we all, with open face beholding as in a glass the glory of the Lord, are changed into the same image from glory to glory, even as by the Spirit of the Lord"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 3:18).]{.class-0}

[When you read your Bible and let the Holy Spirit apply His words to your heart in belief, you are transformed day by day into the image of Christ. That's why the Lord sees you as ]{.class-0}["comely."]{.class-1}[ He is seeing you in His glory and in His image.]{.class-0}

[The Lord wants to hear you pray. The Lord describes ]{.class-0}["the prayers of saints"]{.class-1}[ in Revelation 5:8 as ]{.class-0}["golden vials full of odours."]{.class-1}[ Those prayers are like the incense offered upon the altar in the Tabernacle and the Temple (Rev. 8:3).]{.class-0}

The question, then, is: "Has the Lord heard your voice, today?"

When Hurricane Camille hit the Gulf Coast back in 1969, a couple of "darkees" were talking about it afterwards. One colored fellow said to his pastor, "I tell you what, I sho' did call on de' Lawd last night. I ain't called on Him in a long time." And the pastor replied, "Yeah, I imagine de Lawd heard a lot of strange voices." Don't let the only time the Lord hears from you be when you are in trouble.

[Next, the passage is a picture of the Lord calling the Christian home. When the Lord calls a believer home to Heaven, whether it be in death or whether it be at the Rapture, it is because He wants to see Him. The Psalmist says, ]{.class-0}["Precious in the sight of the LORD is the death of his saints"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 116:15).]{.class-0}

I have come to the conclusion that that is the only reason why God calls some of the brethren home. How else would you explain God taking Lester Roloff home and leaving us with Benny Hinn? When the Lord takes one of His children home in death, it is because He wants to see him.

And Christian, your sentiments towards the Lord should be the same as His sentiments toward you. You should love Him and want to see Him.

Of course, the Christian has the tougher part in this love relationship with the Lord. Unlike the Lord, you are participating in the love affair blindly, by faith.

[After the resurrection, Thomas said, ]{.class-0}["Except I shall see in his hands the print of the nails, and put my finger into the print of the nails, and thrust my hand into his side, I will not believe"]{.class-1}[ (John 20:25). We really shouldn't be too hard on Thomas. All of the other disciples didn't believe in the resurrection until they saw Christ themselves (Luke 24:11, 36--40).]{.class-0}

[But when Jesus appeared to Thomas, He said, ]{.class-0}["Reach hither thy finger, and behold my hands; and reach hither thy hand, and thrust it into my side: and be not faithless, but believing"]{.class-1}[ (John 20:27).]{.class-0}

Thomas got to see the resurrected Christ. He operated by sight, not by faith, when it came to believing on the Lord. And for all of Paul's talk about faith (Rom. 1:17; Gal. 3:11; Heb. 10:38), he was in the same boat. Not only did he get to see Jesus Christ (1 Cor. 15:8), he got to see Heaven (2 Cor. 12:1--4).

[That is not your case nor mine. Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["Blessed are they that have not seen, and yet have believed"]{.class-1}[ (John 20:29). And Peter said, ]{.class-0}["Whom having not seen ye love"]{.class-1}[ in reference to Jesus Christ (1 Pet. 1:8--9). That was the kind of relationship Rebekah was in when Abraham sent his servant to get a wife for Isaac. Have you ever thought about what made Rebekah enter into a blind marriage? No one forced Rebekah to go with Abraham's servant.]{.class-0}

[Genesis 24:58,]{.class-0}[ "And they called Rebekah, and said unto her, Wilt thou go with this man? And she said, I will go."]{.class-1}

What made her decide to go with a man that she had known less than 24 hours?

[Well, Rebekah wasn't anybody's fool. She figured out that Isaac was "a good catch" based on the evidence. She saw Eliezer, Abraham's servant, there at the well with ten camels. She knew that Isaac had to be "well off" financially; after all, not everybody has a ten "car" garage. When she took Eliezer to her house, she saw that he gave gifts to the family, so she figured Isaac must be ]{.class-0}[generous]{.class-2}[. Then Eliezer wouldn't eat until he had told his errand, so she knew he was trained by a man who wasn't ]{.class-0}[carnal]{.class-2}[. Moreover, Rebekah knew that Isaac must be a ]{.class-0}[good]{.class-2}[ master, because all Eliezer did the whole time at the table was ]{.class-0}[brag ]{.class-2}[about his master. She saw Eliezer pray and figured Isaac must be a ]{.class-0}[spiritual ]{.class-2}[fellow.]{.class-0}

Rebekah put all of that together and envisioned a rich young man who was generous and not selfish or greedy, who was not only good but spiritual as well. So when her father and brother asked her if she would go with Eliezer and become Isaac's wife, she compared what she had seen in Eliezer of his master with the hometown boys and figured she couldn't do any better and might do a whole lot worse. That's why she agreed to go.

That's true of our relationship with Jesus Christ. None of us have ever seen Him. I have been bragging about Him going on 62 years now, and I've never even laid eyes on Him. I sure am someone to talk, aren't I?

[But I sure have some evidence! Hebrews 11:1 says, ]{.class-0}["Now faith is the substance of things hoped for, the EVIDENCE of things not seen."]{.class-1}[ I ]{.class-0}[know]{.class-2}[ what is on the other side by the ]{.class-0}[evidence]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[I have met the Master's ]{.class-0}[Servant]{.class-2}[, the Holy Spirit. I have experienced the ]{.class-0}[gifts ]{.class-2}[He gives, not the least of which is a changed life. He took a drunken, fornicating, cussing dance band drummer and disc jockey and cleaned him up and called him to preach the Gospel. You talk about a change! And brother, if you don't think that was a gift, you're crazy. I couldn't have accomplished that change by myself no matter how hard I tried.]{.class-0}

[And on top of that, I have a whole Book by the Master's Servant in which He brags about His Master the whole way through. I have seen the ]{.class-0}[riches]{.class-2}[ of the Master; I have seen the ]{.class-0}[generosity]{.class-2}[ of the Master; I have seen the ]{.class-0}[goodness]{.class-2}[ of the Master. I have read what the Holy Spirit ]{.class-0}[thinks ]{.class-2}[of His Master and ]{.class-0}[says ]{.class-2}[about His Master.]{.class-0}

[After all that, I have come to the conclusion that He's some Master! I know for sure He's better than my ]{.class-0}[old master,]{.class-2}[ the Devil. So when the Holy Spirit asked me ]{.class-0}["Wilt thou go with this man,"]{.class-1}[ I said, "Count me in; I'm leaving. I'm blowing this joint and going with You!"]{.class-0}

To me, the greatest moment in my Christian life will be to see Him. I think everything else will be anticlimactic. I know that there will be all kinds of wonderful things to see, but I don't think anything else will compare to seeing Him.

[He has kept us in suspense for so long, and living by faith for so long without ]{.class-0}[sight]{.class-2}[, that sometimes the Devil and flesh get working on us. They put doubts in our minds and make us think the Bible's not true and this life is all there is.]{.class-0}

I want the Lord to come back just so I can shut the Devil up and dump this body of sinful flesh so I won't have to listen to either of them ever again. I want to say to them, "See, I told you so. There He is! I've been talking about Him ever since 1949, and you wouldn't believe me. You told me it was all a fairy tale, but you were WRONG! Nanny, nanny, boo--boo!"

[Verse 14:]{.class-0}[ "and thy countenance is comely."]{.class-1}[ That's the Lord bragging about the saved sinner.]{.class-0}

[Now, I can see us bragging about the Lord. That's what we are supposed to do. It's called ]{.class-0}[worship.]{.class-2}[ But the Lord bragging on ]{.class-0}[us?]{.class-2}[ That's hard to imagine. But that's the Lord. He brags about His children. He got to bragging about Job so much that the Devil challenged Him on it (Job 1:8--11). He called Abraham ]{.class-0}["the Friend of God"]{.class-1}[ (James 2:23). He brags about Moses and says, ]{.class-0}["Moses was faithful in all his house"]{.class-1}[ (Heb. 3:2).]{.class-0}

I dare say that there are times when the Lord brags about us. It's usually when you have been doing right and serving God, and then things start falling apart. The Lord has bragged about you, and Satan has taken a special interest in you, like he did Job, in order to shut the Lord up.

That is one of the reasons I don't brag about my friends and students very often. I'd like to give out more compliments than I do, but I have observed that when I do, something bad usually happens to the person I'm complimenting. So I keep my mouth shut.

[I got to bragging about Bro. Weldon Jones down in Guadalajara, Mexico. He came to PBI when I was pastoring the Brent Baptist Church over on St. John Street. That fellow was a Bible believer and a veteran missionary. He had a speech impediment where he couldn't pronounce his ]{.class-0}[Rs]{.class-2}[ correctly. But he started learning Spanish, and that speech impediment became an asset to him, because you don't pronounce ]{.class-0}[Rs]{.class-2}[ the same way in Spanish as you do in English. That guy could speak Spanish better than some Mexicans.]{.class-0}

Moreover, he wasn't a lazy missionary; he got the job done. He planted several churches and trained pastors for them. He started a Bible camp up in the mountains for the teenagers. He used to host youth groups that came down to Mexico to learn about the mission field. He set up some meetings down there for me and translated for me the whole time. He was the best translator that I had ever had. I counted him as one of my trophies in the ministry.

Then he was driving a bus with a bunch of teenagers up to the mountains when a semi-truck pulled suddenly in front of him. Bro. Weldon swerved to avoid hitting it and wrecked the bus. But because of his quick thinking, only two people in that whole bus died: a teenage girl and him. If he had hit the truck, no one might have walked away from that wreck alive.

A similar thing happened when I started bragging about Rick DeMichele's work in Boise, Idaho. He's one of our PBI graduates. When he went out to Boise, the Lord started blessing his work, and today he has one of the largest churches in the State. But when I got to complimenting him and his work, he found out that he had leukemia.

That's why I am not too complimentary of my students. It's not that I don't love them or notice what they are doing or don't appreciate what they are doing. I just want them to live long enough to keep on doing it.

[Knowing, then, that the Lord brags about us should cause us to do two things: 1) Get under conviction and ]{.class-0}[stay ]{.class-2}[under conviction about our service for the Lord. Have you done anything to cause the Lord to brag about you? 2) Don't get "cocky" against the Devil. He's not an adversary to be ridiculed or treated lightly. Don't be like these crazy Charismatics who often make fun of him. Peter says in regards to the Christian's attitude toward the Devil, ]{.class-0}["Be SOBER, be vigilant; because your adversary the devil, as a roaring lion, walketh about, seeking whom he may devour"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 5:8; see comments in that Commentary). You had better take the Devil seriously.]{.class-0}

"[Take us the foxes, the little foxes, that spoil the vines: for our vines have tender grapes"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 15). The word ]{.class-0}["take,"]{.class-1}[ there, means to ]{.class-0}[capture.]{.class-2}[ The word is still used that way today. In a fight or in a game, one side says they can "take on" the other. Well, they aren't going to pick them up and carry them off somewhere; they are going to defeat them in combat or competition.]{.class-0}

[Now, the grapevines of verse 15 are in a vineyard that belongs to the Bride (Song of Sol. 1:6, 8:12), and yet the verse says ]{.class-0}["our vines."]{.class-1}[ Well, there are only two speakers in the whole chapter: Solomon and his bride. So although the vineyard was hers, it was given to her by Solomon for their mutual enjoyment together (cf. vss. 4--5).]{.class-0}

[The spiritual lesson here is that every Christian has been given a vineyard by the Lord to tend. The Lord wants you to bear fruit (John 15:2--8), and that fruit is listed in Galatians 5. Notice that Galatians 5:22--23 gives ]{.class-0}["the fruit]{.class-1}[ \[singular\]]{.class-0}[ of the Spirit,"]{.class-1}[ but it lists nine items. The picture is that of a cluster of grapes.]{.class-0}

[In order for the Bride to bring her grapes to maturity, she is warned to capture ]{.class-0}["the little foxes, that spoil the vines."]{.class-1}[ Why ]{.class-0}["the little foxes"]{.class-1}[? Because ]{.class-0}["the little foxes"]{.class-1}[ are able to get through holes in or under the fence through which the big foxes cannot get.]{.class-0}

A humorist said one time, "You can dodge an elephant, but you can't dodge a fly." The truth of that statement is that we have more problems with little things than we do with big things. A small nail can produce lockjaw if you step on it. A small insect like a mosquito can spread a disease like yellow fever or malaria. It was fleas and rats that actually spread the Black Plague during the Middle Ages.

There is a famous illustration used by preachers of a five-hundred-year-old redwood out in California that toppled over one day. That redwood had withstood five hundred summers and five hundred winters. It had survived forest fires, avalanches, lightning strikes, earthquakes, and mudslides. When the park rangers investigated the reason for its collapse, they found it was eaten out by bugs on the inside.

[The greatest dangers you will ever face, Christian, will not be from the outside. Christians get to the place in their lives where they have cleaned up on the outside, but they let the inside "go to pot." They give up drinking, smoking, dancing, going to the movies, wrong companions, etc.; but they stop loving the word of God, they lose their burden for souls, and they cease to enjoy communion with the Lord. Those are ]{.class-0}["the little foxes"]{.class-1}[ that will ]{.class-0}[kill]{.class-2}[ your grapes.]{.class-0}

In the Bible, the foxes are likened to two types of people, when they are likened to people at all.

[Ezekiel 13:3--4 says, ]{.class-0}["Thus saith the Lord GOD; Woe unto the foolish prophets, that follow their own spirit, and have seen nothing! O Israel, thy prophets are like the foxes in the desert."]{.class-1}

Anybody who claims to have gotten something from God when they didn't is a fox. That includes all of these Charismatic fakirs who say "God led me" or "God told me." That includes Michael Luther King Jr.'s "I had a dream." And that includes all of the professors in Christian Colleges, Universities, and Seminaries who pretend God showed them something from "the original Greek" or "the original Hebrew," when they were cloned by a bunch of jackasses who were just like them (and I say that with apologies to every four-footed, braying critter in the pasture).

[Jesus also likened a fox to a ]{.class-0}[dishonest skeptic ]{.class-2}[like King Herod (Luke 13:31--32). That will cover all of the atheists, agnostics, evolutionists, humanists, and libertines in the Federal and State educational systems. That would also include nearly all the philosophers from Solon to Victor Frankl and most of the scientists after Charles Darwin.]{.class-0}

If those two definitions are true, that means that any education outside of the basics of reading, writing, and arithmetic, or any education outside of learning a trade, or any education outside learning and applying the Scriptures, exists for the express purpose of killing any real, Biblical, spiritual life the pupil has or may have. That goes for secular or "Christian" education. The Devil has created more barren, fruitless lives through higher education than by any other means.

16 My beloved is mine, and I am his: he feedeth among the lilies.

17 Until the day break, and the shadows flee away, turn, my beloved, and be thou like a roe or a young hart upon the mountains of Bether.

[The ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ places a paragraph mark at the beginning of verse 16, because once more, the speaker changes. The Bride is once more talking about her ]{.class-0}["beloved."]{.class-1}

"[My beloved is mine, and I am his"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 16). That's the relationship between Christ and the Christian. As a Christian, you belong to God. He has bought and paid for you (1 Cor. 6:20). At the same time, Christ belongs to you. Paul says, ]{.class-0}["Christ in you, the hope of glory"]{.class-1}[ (Col. 1:27). In keeping with the picture of the husband and wife, Paul says, ]{.class-0}["The wife hath not power of her own body, but the husband: and likewise also the husband hath not power of his own body, but the wife"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 7:4).]{.class-0}

In a marriage relationship, the wife owns the husband, and the husband owns the wife. In the spiritual relationship between Christ and His Bride, the Lord owns the Bride, and the Bride owns her Lord.

"[He feedeth among the lilies."]{.class-1}[ And this is one of those places where I will have to plead ignorance. I don't know what the text means, and there is not enough in the Scriptures to interpret the passage.]{.class-0}

[Song of Solomon 4:5 says that roes, the gazelle that lived in Palestine, ]{.class-0}["feed among the lilies."]{.class-1}[ So the lilies are in the pastures where the deer feed. But in Song of Solomon 4:5, the picture is of the Bride, not the Bridegroom. Yet Song of Solomon 2:16 is repeated about the Bridegoom in Song of Solomon 6:3.]{.class-0}

[The Bridegroom's lips, through which a man would eat, are likened to lilies in Song of Solomon 5:13. But if you make that ]{.class-0}["feedeth among the lilies,"]{.class-1}[ I still don't know where you would go with it. ]{.class-0}[Ich weiss nicht!]{.class-2}

[Song of Solomon 6:2 says that when the Bridegroom goes into ]{.class-0}["his garden\...to feed"]{.class-1}[ that He gathers lilies. That is closer to the meaning of the text, for the next verse says ]{.class-0}["he feedeth among the lilies."]{.class-1}[ But again, we are at a dead end, for beside the reference to the Lord Himself being ]{.class-0}["the lily of the valleys"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 1), there is no Scripture that defines the lilies among which the Bridegroom feeds or which He gathers.]{.class-0}

[When it comes to the Lord "feeding," it should be obvious to anyone that God, as a Spirit (John 4:24), does not need to eat. In Psalm 50:12, the Lord says in sarcasm, ]{.class-0}["If I were hungry, I would not tell thee: for the world is mine, and the fulness thereof."]{.class-1}[ Then He asks a rhetorical question in Psalm 50:13, ]{.class-0}["Will I eat the flesh of bulls, or drink the blood of goats?"]{.class-1}[ The obvious answer is ]{.class-0}[no,]{.class-2}[ He won't.]{.class-0}

[In the Lord's incarnated state, He still never asked anybody to give Him food to satisfy His human hunger. In John 4, when the disciples returned from buying meat in Sychar (John 4:8, 31), the Lord turned it down saying, ]{.class-0}["I have meat to eat that ye know not of\....My meat is to do the will of him that sent me, and to finish his work"]{.class-1}[ (John 4:32, 34).]{.class-0}

[In Mark 6:38, at the feeding of the 5,000, the Lord asked the disciples, ]{.class-0}["How many loaves have ye?"]{.class-1}[ But that was to feed the multitude, not to satisfy His own hunger. In response to that miracle, Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["As the living Father hath sent me, AND I LIVE BY THE FATHER: so he that eateth me, even he shall live by me"]{.class-1}[ (John 6:57). Again, Jesus indicated that even in His human form, the "meat" and "food" that sustained Him was the spiritual relationship He had with HIS FATHER.]{.class-0}

The one time the Bible says that Jesus was hungry, physically, He never asked for food even then. He sought a fig tree that He had made. When He found no figs on it, He cursed it (Mark 11:12--14). The lesson He taught His disciples from that incident was to have faith in God (Mark 11:20--24).

[After the resurrection, the Lord twice asked for food. Once was in Luke 24:41 when He appeared to the disciples in the upper room. He ate a piece of broiled fish and honeycomb (Luke 24:4243), but that was ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[to satisfy His hunger. He ate to show the disciples that He had risen bodily from the grave.]{.class-0}

[The last time Jesus asked for food on this earth was in John 21:5, and again, He was not asking to satisfy ]{.class-0}[His own hunger]{.class-2}[. The resurrection body of Jesus Christ did not require food to stay alive. He asked in order to show His disciples that He was the resurrection Christ when He performed the second miracle of the great draught of fishes. And although John makes it very clear that the Lord fed the disciples with bread and fish there by the Sea of Galilee, it never says that Christ ate any of it Himself.]{.class-0}

One day in Heaven, the Lord will prepare a great supper for His Bride. That will be the Marriage Supper of the Lamb (Rev. 19:7). At that supper, however, the Lord does not eat. Instead, He serves those who were faithful to Him (Luke 12:37).

[In the meanwhile, the only "supping" that Jesus Christ does is a ]{.class-0}[spiritual communion]{.class-2}[ with His saints.]{.class-0}

[Revelation 3:20, ]{.class-0}["Behold, I stand at the door, and knock: if any man hear my voice, and open the door, I will come into him, and will sup with him, and he with me."]{.class-1}

That is about as thorough a discussion as I can give you on Jesus Christ "feeding," and it still has not touched the text. None of the passages, nor any of the ones on lilies, gives you any idea at all about what a lily is if Christ is "feeding" among them.

[Now, you could treat the word ]{.class-0}[feed]{.class-2}[ as we treated it in Song of Solomon 1:7. There it was the Bridegroom, as a shepherd, feeding His flock. But the best you can do in that sense is to say that the Bridegroom ]{.class-0}[feeds His flock]{.class-2}[ and, as we saw back in Song of Solomon 1:7, the Bride in the same place the roes feed (Song of Sol. 4:5)---in the valleys where the lilies grow (cf. vs. 1). But that still doesn't tell you much.]{.class-0}

[In the chapter, the lily is likened to Christ in verse 1 and to the Church His Bride in verse 2, and what that has to do with either one ]{.class-0}[feeding among both,]{.class-2}[ I have no idea.]{.class-0}

[Verse 17 is much easier to get. ]{.class-0}["Until the day break."]{.class-1}[ That's the Second Advent. Peter says, ]{.class-0}["Until the day dawn, and the day star arise in your hearts"]{.class-1}[ (2 Pet. 1:19 and comments in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

"[And the shadows flee away."]{.class-1}[ And that's clear. This present age is described as night time. The Psalmist says, ]{.class-0}["Weeping may endure for a night, but joy cometh in the morning"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 30:5 and comments in that Commentary). It's the end of the Tribulation.]{.class-0}

"[Be thou like a roe or a young hart upon the mountains of Bether."]{.class-1}[ And that goes back to verses 8 and 9 where it is a reference to the Rapture.]{.class-0}

[So verse 17 is a prayer by the Bride for the Rapture to take place. She is saying that until the time for the Tribulation and the Second Advent to take place, the Bridegroom is to be ready to come in the Rapture. That's the ]{.class-0}[last prayer]{.class-2}[ of the Bible; it's a prayer for Jesus Christ to come back.]{.class-0}[ "Even so, come, Lord Jesus"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 22:20).]{.class-0}

"[The mountains of Bether."]{.class-1}[ No one but the Lord knows where that is. No map of Palestine at the time of Solomon has it. The word ]{.class-0}["Bether"]{.class-1}[ means "division" or "separation." Verse 17 is the only place it appears in the Bible.]{.class-0}

[In all the references in Song of Solomon to the Second Coming, it is always pictured as Christ coming down from the mountains. Look at 2:8, ]{.class-0}["The voice of my beloved! behold he cometh leaping upon the MOUNTAINS, skipping upon the HILLS."]{.class-1}

[Turn over to chapter 4 verse 8: ]{.class-0}["Come with me from Lebanon, my spouse, with me from Lebanon: look from the top of Amana]{.class-1}[ \[that's a mountain\]]{.class-0}[, from the top of Shenir]{.class-1}[ \[that's a mountain\] ]{.class-0}[and Hermon ]{.class-1}[\[and that's a mountain\]]{.class-0}[, from the lion's dens ]{.class-1}[\[watch it!\]]{.class-0}[ from the MOUNTAINS of the leopards.]{.class-1}

[And with that observation, we are back to the basic structure of the universe. All of those mountains in the Song of Solomon are pictures of ]{.class-0}[the mountain]{.class-2}[ up in Heaven.]{.class-0}

[Hebrews 12:22, ]{.class-0}["But ye are come unto MOUNT Sion, and unto the city of the living God, the heavenly Jerusalem."]{.class-1}
