[Psalm 48:1--2,]{.class-0}[ "Great is the LORD, and greatly to be praised in the city of our God, in the MOUNTAIN of his holiness. Beautiful for situation, the joy of the whole earth, is mount Zion, on the sides of the north, the city of the great king."]{.class-1}

[That's not a reference to the EARTHLY Jerusalem or Mount Zion. How do you know? Look at that expression in Psalm 48:2, ]{.class-0}["the sides of the north."]{.class-1}[ Jerusalem is NOT in the north of Palestine; it's in the south. Moreover, Mount Zion, where David's city was located, is on the southeast side of Jerusalem.]{.class-0}

"[The sides of the north"]{.class-1}[ is where Lucifer attempted to ascend when he was trying to ]{.class-0}["be like the most High"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 14:14).]{.class-0}

[Isaiah 14:12--13,]{.class-0}[ "How art thou fallen from heaven, O Lucifer, son of the morning\...For thou hast said in thine heart, I will ascend into HEAVEN, I will exalt my throne ABOVE THE STARS of God."]{.class-1}

[That throne is in Heaven; it is ]{.class-0}["above the stars."]{.class-1}[ Given that, look at the rest of the verse:]{.class-0}[ "I will sit upon the MOUNT of the congregation, IN THE SIDES OF THE NORTH."]{.class-1}

[If you want to know where Heaven is, get you a compass. The needle points ]{.class-0}[north.]{.class-2}[ If you follow that out into outer space and keep going past "the edge of the universe," past the "Great Deeps," and past the ]{.class-0}["sea of glass," you will come to a "mount" that contains Heaven and the New Jerusalem. And as anyone know, the peak of a mountain is shaped like the top of a pyramid, as we stated back on pages 113--114.]{.class-1}

[]{#section-0_1_26e6b44101e27d02_67dd.xhtml}

CHAPTER 3

3:1 By night on my bed I sought him whom my soul loveth: I sought him, but I found him not.

2 I will rise now, and go about the city in the streets, and in the broad ways I will seek him whom my soul loveth: I sought him, but I found him not.

3 The watchmen that go about the city found me: to whom I said, Saw ye him whom my soul loveth?

4 It was but a little that I passed from them, but I found him whom my soul loveth: I held him, and would not let him go, until I had brought him into my mother's house, and into the chamber of her that conceived me.

5 I charge you, O ye daughters of Jerusalem, by the roes, and by the hinds of the field, that ye stir not up, nor awake my love, till he please.

The Bride continues her part of the Song in chapter 3 staring with verse 1. Chapter 2 ended with the Rapture that took place in verses 8--14. If the book is laid out in any kind of prophetic order (and it is), then the next event that follows should be the Tribulation.

[The first two words of verse 1 mark the passage as a type of the Tribulation: ]{.class-0}["by night."]{.class-1}[ There is no doubt that chapter 3 is a picture of the Tribulation, for look at verse 6. It is the Son of David (cf. vs. 7) coming ]{.class-0}["out of the wilderness"]{.class-1}[ as He will at the Second Advent (Psa. 68:7). He comes with ]{.class-0}["pillars of smoke"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 6) as He will at the Second Advent (Joel 2:30). He is accompanied by an army (vss. 7--8) as He will be at the Second Advent (Joel 2:1--11).]{.class-0}

So what you have in chapters 2 and 3 of the Song is the standard premillennial outline of the future, given 1,000 years before Jesus Christ ever shows up at the First Advent. Chapter 2 is the Rapture. Chapter 3 from verse 1 to verse 5 is the Tribulation. Chapter 3 from verse 6 to verse 10 is the Second Advent, followed by the conversion of the Jewish remnant at the Advent in verse 11 (cf. Zech. 12:10--14). And if that weren't enough, the end of verse 11 refers back to the Marriage of the Lamb, which takes place in the verse before the King's return (cf. Rev. 19).

You will see this phenomenon repeated several times in Scripture. One of the most notable places is in the order of the Old Testament books from 2 Chronicles to Psalms. At the end of 2 Chronicles, the Jews are cast out of the land, as they were in A.D. 70. In Ezra and Nehemiah, the Jews return to the land, as they did between 1918--1948.

In Esther, a Gentile bride is being put away, and a Jewish bride becomes the Queen. The book starts out with a marriage feast in the King's palace (Rev. 19:7--9), and the theme is Satan trying to wipe out that Jew, which will take place in Revelation 12.

In Job, Job is being persecuted here on earth for 42 chapters; in the Great Tribulation, that Jew is persecuted here on earth for 42 months. Job is rescued at the end of the book by God showing up and "returning the captivity" of Job just as the Jew will be rescued at the end of the Tribulation by Jesus Christ showing up and returning their captivity then.

The book of Psalms pictures the exaltation of Jesus Christ to the throne of David in the Millennium (Psa. 2, 21, 24, 45, 47, 48, 50, etc.).

Now, you won't find that in any "original Hebrew text." The canon of the Hebrew Old Testament is arranged differently and ends with 2 Chronicles instead of Malachi (Matt. 23:35). The last thing a Jew is told in his Scriptures is to return to the land.

[Moreover, you won't find that teaching in the works of the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ translators. The translators of the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ were brilliant men, and they faithfully translated the text God gave them, and the Holy Spirit used them to do so. But when it came to theology, the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ translators were Amillennialists or Postmillennialists. So the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ text is not slanted to match the theology of its translators and editors as the modern translations are.]{.class-0}

[What you have in the premillennial order of Bible books and here in Song of Solomon 2 is what I call "advanced revelations" in the Scriptures. That is, it is something which the Holy Spirit clearly revealed through the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ text that He did not reveal through any "original manuscripts."]{.class-0}

[Egotistical stuffed shirts like Gary Hudson, James White, and "Hot Dog" Hymers call that a "heresy." But the truth is that the Holy Spirit has revealed more truth to the Body of Christ in the 400 years that the ]{.class-0}[KJV]{.class-2}[ has been around than He did in the previous 3,000 years of the "original manuscripts" and "original texts" and the "original languages."]{.class-0}

[The fact of the matter is that God didn't use the Hebrew Old Testament or the Greek New Testament to bring about any nationwide revival or worldwide missionary movement since the canon was closed at the end of the First Century A.D. That ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible has won more souls to Jesus Christ and called more Christians to the ministry and reached more of the "heathen" with the Gospel than any other book around---and that includes other ]{.class-0}[good]{.class-2}[ translations of the Scriptures.]{.class-0}

[So if there is one thing that you don't have to worry about, it's "Ruckman's advanced revelations" in a ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible]{.class-0}[.]{.class-2}[ If you don't believe me, just check out the ones I've listed in ]{.class-0}[King James Onlyism versus Scholarship Onlyism]{.class-2}[ and volumes 1 and 3 of the reprints of the ]{.class-0}[Bible Believers' Bulletin.]{.class-2}

"[By night on my bed I sought him whom my soul loveth."]{.class-1}[ In regards to physical, marital love, it is a woman dreaming about her lover or husband and wanting to see him. If you likened the Church to the woman, it is the Bride of Christ in this age seeking the Lord like she was doing back in chapter 1, verses 7--8. The only problem with that is the next phrase in verse 1.]{.class-0}

"[I sought him, but I found him not."]{.class-1}[ In the case of a married couple, it is like the wife waking up in the middle of the night and finding her husband gone, but when she searches the house for him, she can't find him.]{.class-0}

[Now, you will have a rough time putting ]{.class-0}[that ]{.class-2}[application doctrinally on the Bride of Christ. As a Christian, you can find the Lord any time you want. He has not abandoned His Bride.]{.class-0}

As a Christian, you have access to the Lord 24 hours a day, 7 days a week. All you have to do is come to Him in prayer.

[Hebrews 4:16, ]{.class-0}["Let us therefore come boldly unto the throne of grace, that we may obtain mercy, and find grace to help in time of need."]{.class-1}

When I want to see the Lord in prayer, I don't have to go through any secretary or bureaucracy. I don't need St. Peter, Mary, "blessed Joseph," or "blessed John the Baptist." I go straight into the throne room and see the King.

[The Christian doesn't need to "find" the Lord. He has already found Him at salvation, and the Lord lives in his body in the person of the Holy Spirit. It is ]{.class-0}["Christ in you, the hope of glory"]{.class-1}[ (Col. 1:27). Paul said, ]{.class-0}["Christ liveth in me"]{.class-1}[ (Gal. 2:20), and that is true of every Christian. Jesus said, praying to His Father for His disciples, ]{.class-0}["I in them, and thou in me, that they may be made perfect in me"]{.class-1}[ (John 17:23).]{.class-0}

When it comes to "finding" Christ, I found Him on March 14, 1949, and I haven't been separated from Him since (Rom. 8:35--39).

[Yet, there is a practical sense in which you can apply verse 1 to the Christian. In this age, starting at Pentecost in Acts 2 and continuing to the Rapture of the Church, the Christian does not see the Lord Jesus Christ. Jesus told Thomas, ]{.class-0}["Blessed are they that have not seen, and yet have believed"]{.class-1}[ (John 20:29). Peter wrote, ]{.class-0}["Whom having not seen, ye love"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 1:8). That's the present state of any Christian.]{.class-0}

[Nevertheless, the desire of every Christian is to see his Lord. So right before Peter writes about the Christian loving a Saviour he has never seen, he talks about ]{.class-0}["the appearing of Jesus Christ"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 1:7). Paul says, ]{.class-0}["Looking for that blessed hope, and the glorious appearing of the great God and our Saviour Jesus Christ"]{.class-1}[ (Tit. 2:13).]{.class-0}

[So the Christian is looking for his Saviour, but he won't find Him here on earth. We are looking UP ]{.class-0}["to meet the Lord in the air: and so shall we ever be with the Lord"]{.class-1}[ (1 Thess. 4:17).]{.class-0}

That is the sense in which the Christian is "seeking the Lord" in this age. That is why Paul says this:

"[Therefore we are always confident, knowing that, whilst we are at home in the body, we are absent from the Lord: (For we walk by faith, not by sight:) We are confident, I say, and willing rather to be absent from the body, and to be present with the Lord"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 5:6--8).]{.class-0}

[While a Christian may be ]{.class-0}[spiritually]{.class-2}[ one with Jesus Christ, he is ]{.class-0}[physically]{.class-2}[ separated from Him. The Lord Jesus Christ is seated, ]{.class-0}[physically,]{.class-2}[ up in Heaven at the right hand of God; we are here on earth. And as long as we are in these bodies of flesh, we will be separated from the Lord. That is why Paul said, ]{.class-0}["For I am in a strait betwixt two, having a desire to depart\...."]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}["Depart"]{.class-1}[ what? Depart from his ]{.class-0}[body ]{.class-2}[and this ]{.class-0}[world ]{.class-2}[through death (vs. 21). ]{.class-0}["And to be with Christ; which is far better"]{.class-1}[ (Phil. 1:23).]{.class-0}

So when a Christian dies, his soul does not sleep in his decaying corpse or in the grave (Jehovah's Witnesses). It goes to be in a heavenly body prepared for it (2 Cor. 5:1 and comments in that Commentary) in the physical presence of the Lord. If you are going to apply verse 1 to the Christian, that is how to apply it.

"[I will rise now, and go about the city in the streets, and in the broad ways I will seek him whom my soul loveth: I sought him, but I found him not"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 2).]{.class-0}

Well, the reason she didn't find Him was because she was looking in the wrong place. If you find Christ in the streets, it won't be because you were looking for Him there. It will be because the Lord sent someone out looking for you.

[Luke 14:23, ]{.class-0}["And the lord said unto the servant, Go out into the highways and hedges, and compel them to come in, that my house may be filled."]{.class-1}

I remember the night before Hugh Pyle led me to Christ. I was running all around downtown Pensacola in the rain on Garden, Palafox, and Wright Streets trying to find an open church where I could "find Christ." I went into a Methodist church on Wright Street. I fell down at the altar and prayed, "Lord, I want to come HOME! Would you please take me HOME?" Although there was a choir practicing in some back room, there was no one there to lead me to Christ. I didn't "find" Jesus Christ until the next day when the Lord sent a skinny, little Baptist preacher into the radio station at WEAR where I worked.

I remember one New Year's Eve, before I was saved, being in downtown New York in Times Square, surrounded by a million people. No one witnessed to me; no one gave me a tract.

Brethren, there are literally millions of lost souls wandering the streets and byways of the USA looking for salvation, and they won't find it unless you go and give it to them.

That is why we train our young men at PBI to preach on the streets. Every community should have a public witness that keeps its residents stirred up on a continual basis.

[The general complaint by the brethren is that it doesn't do any good, but we have never had a street preaching season (April to September every year) where we have not seen at least a dozen folks saved on the streets. When the brethren say "street preaching doesn't do any good," what they mean is that it doesn't increase ]{.class-0}[attendance or giving.]{.class-2}

"[In the broad ways I will seek him\...but I found him not."]{.class-1}[ The spiritual application is plain.]{.class-0}

"[Enter ye in at the strait gate: for wide is the gate, and BROAD IS THE WAY, THAT LEADETH TO DESTRUCTION, and many there be which go in thereat: Because strait is the gate, and narrow is the way, which leadeth unto life, and few there be that find it"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 7:13--14).]{.class-0}

The broad way is where the multitude and the majority are, and that's the wrong place to be. The broad way is so broad that it allows Buddha, Mohammed, Allah, the Popes, the Campbellites, the Jehovah's Witnesses, the Mormons, Liberal Protestants, atheists, humanists, agnostics, Satanists, etc., to go down it; and each one professes to be leading its followers in the right way.

[God's way is so narrow that it is one man:]{.class-0}[ Jesus Christ.]{.class-2}[ It is so narrow that you have to meet Him at one place:]{.class-0}[ Calvary.]{.class-2}[ It is so narrow that if you don't go up it His way, ]{.class-0}[by faith,]{.class-2}[ you will be counted as ]{.class-0}["a thief and a robber"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:1) and be thrown out.]{.class-0}

[Now, as you get deeper into this passage, the interpretation becomes more difficult. (I don't profess to know or understand everything in the Bible, and I never have. I am a Bible ]{.class-0}[student,]{.class-2}[ not a Bible ]{.class-0}[scholar.)]{.class-2}

This is one of those passages where I will give you what I can from the Scriptures. A lot of it will just be spiritual application because you will have serious problems if you try to press a doctrinal application on all of these verses.

[There are two ways of looking at verses 2 and 3. The first is that the Bride here is Israel in the Tribulation. Now why do I say that? Look at verse 2: ]{.class-0}["I will seek him whom my soul loveth: I sought him, BUT I FOUND HIM NOT."]{.class-1}

I have a cross-reference in my Bible here to Hosea 5:6 where the Lord is talking about Israel and Judah (Hos. 5:5).

"[They shall go with their flocks and with their herds to seek the Lord; but they shall not find him; he hath withdrawn himself from them."]{.class-1}

[That is the state Israel is in right now. Back in the Gospels, those Jews rejected their Messiah. They told Pilate, ]{.class-0}["We have no king but Caesar"]{.class-1}[ (John 19:15), and ]{.class-0}["His blood]{.class-1}[ \[Christ's blood\]]{.class-0}[ be on us, and on our children"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 27:25).]{.class-0}

[God gave them another chance under Peter and Paul in the book of Acts, and they turned the Lord down, as a nation, then too. Paul ends his witness to the Jews in Rome with: ]{.class-0}["Be it know therefore unto you, that the salvation of God is sent unto the Gentiles, and that they will hear it"]{.class-1}[ (Acts 28:28).]{.class-0}

[So since A.D. 70, those Jews have been seeking the Lord, as a people, and they can't find Him. He went back to Heaven, and He didn't deal with them as a nation again until 1948. Even then it was merely on a ]{.class-0}[physical level]{.class-2}[ to preserve them in their return to the land.]{.class-0}

[Brethren, don't you know those Rabbis in Treblinka, Auschwitz, Belsen-Belsen, and the rest of those concentration camps during World War II were reading the Psalms and praying and claiming the promises the whole time? But God didn't do anything: He didn't answer their prayers. He let six million of them die before He sent in American troops to liberate them. That is why most Jews in Israel today are ]{.class-0}[atheists]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

The problem wasn't in the promises or power of God, though. The problem was that they rejected Jesus Christ, and the Lord was giving them what they asked for: Caesar as a King (Hitler was a Roman Catholic ruler) and the blood-guilt of the crucifixion of Jesus Christ. The Lord had withdrawn Himself at their own request (John 19:15; Matt. 27:25).

[Then, in verse 3, there are ]{.class-0}["watchmen."]{.class-1}[ Well, there are watchmen in the Tribulation in Ezekiel. The Lord told Ezekiel: ]{.class-0}["Son of man, I have made thee a watchman unto the house of Israel: therefore hear the word at my mouth, and give them warning from me"]{.class-1}[ (Ezek. 3:17). The context is the ]{.class-0}[Tribulation ]{.class-2}[(Ezek. 3:1--3 cf. Rev. 10:9--10).]{.class-0}

[Isaiah 21:11--12 says, ]{.class-0}["Watchman, what of the night? Watchman what of the night? The watchman said, The morning cometh, and also the night: if ye will enquire, enquire ye: return, come."]{.class-1}[ Again, the context is the ]{.class-0}[Tribulation ]{.class-2}[(Isa. 21:9 cf. Rev. 18:2).]{.class-0}

[What happens with the ]{.class-0}["watchmen"]{.class-1}[ in verse 3 is that they give no answer, and the Bride ends up finding her lover in verse 4. But look at the second time she encounters the watchmen in Song 5:7.]{.class-0}

"[The watchmen that went about the city found me, they smote me, they wounded me; the keepers of the walls took away my veil from me."]{.class-1}

Obviously there has been a change in the attitude of the watchmen toward this woman. They leave her alone in chapter 3, but they smack her around in chapter 5.

[If you look at that thing ]{.class-0}[dispensationally]{.class-2}[, what you have is that Jew in the Tribulation. The first three and a half years are relatively peaceful. If that Jew wants to find Christ in that first half, he can without much trouble.]{.class-0}

But in the middle of the Tribulation, the Antichrist breaks his covenant with those Jews and takes away their sacrifice and begins to persecute them. So in the second half of the Tribulation, if a Jew wants to "find Christ," he will do so at the risk of his life.

[Now, that interpretation may be stretched a bit, but it is the only thing you can come up with if you make the woman ]{.class-0}[Israel]{.class-2}[. Of course, that interpretation is not without its problems.]{.class-0}

[First, if those watchmen are Tribulation witnesses like Ezekiel, then what are they doing ]{.class-0}[not telling ]{.class-2}[the woman where to find the Bridegroom? Do you think the two witnesses in Revelation 11 or the 144,000 Jewish evangelists in Revelation 7 couldn't tell a sinner how to find Christ in the Tribulation? And if they are the same watchmen as in Song 5:7, then what are they doing persecuting that Jew?]{.class-0}

[You see, you can't just charge roughshod through the Book and try to make it fit even what you know to be so. There are just too many things the Holy Spirit does not clearly define in the text. All you can say, sometimes, is ]{.class-0}[if]{.class-2}[ this is so, then ]{.class-0}[this]{.class-2}[ interpretation will follow.]{.class-0}

[Another problem you have with making the woman Israel here is that she distinguishes herself from the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ in verse 5 just as she did back in 1:5 and 2:7. So the primary application can't be to the Jew.]{.class-0}

[Well, if the woman there is the Bride of Christ, the Church, then your application is nearly all ]{.class-0}[spiritual]{.class-2}[. If you try to make it ]{.class-0}[doctrinal]{.class-2}[, it just won't come out right. Let's go through the passage making the woman the Church this time, and you will see what I mean.]{.class-0}

[Verse 1: ]{.class-0}["By night on my bed."]{.class-1}[ Right away the Christian is in trouble. The time of a Christian's rest and ease is not in this age. But you see, that is a practical, spiritual application. Doctrinally, the Christian ]{.class-0}["has ceased from his own works"]{.class-1}[ and has ]{.class-0}["entered into his]{.class-1}[ \[God's\]]{.class-0}[ rest"]{.class-1}[ (Heb. 4:10).]{.class-0}

[But Paul says in 1 Thessalonians 5:6, ]{.class-0}["Therefore, let us not sleep, as do others; but let us watch and be sober."]{.class-1}[ During this age of darkness, a Christian is to be ]{.class-0}[wide awake,]{.class-2}[ alert, and active.]{.class-0}

[Over in Ephesians 5:14, the Apostle Paul writes, ]{.class-0}["Awake thou that sleepest, and arise from the dead, and Christ shall give thee light."]{.class-1}[ The context of that remark is not a lost person getting saved; it is a ]{.class-0}[saved person]{.class-2}[ who is living like a ]{.class-0}[lost person.]{.class-2}[ Paul wants him to wake up and start living like a ]{.class-0}[live Christian]{.class-2}[ instead of a ]{.class-0}[dead sinner.]{.class-2}

[The spiritual picture here is a Christian living at ease in this world, without any fellowship or communion with the Lord. He wants that fellowship back, so he gets up and goes looking for the Lord. Well, he won't find that fellowship in the ]{.class-0}["broad ways"]{.class-1}[ where the majority of people live their lives. There is service in the ]{.class-0}["broad ways"]{.class-1}[ if you are trying to reach sinners, but that fellowship is something else.]{.class-0}

If you want fellowship with the Lord Jesus Christ, then turn off the TV and the radio and get alone by yourself with His Book and pluck some "precious promises" from its pages. You'll have a hard time doing that in rush hour traffic or at the mall or at the ballpark or anywhere there's a crowd of people.

[Those ]{.class-0}["watchmen"]{.class-1}[ in verse 3 would be a picture of Christians who are wide awake. And though the passage does not say it, the implication is that they told her where to find her lover, for it doesn't take long before he is in her arms again (vs. 4).]{.class-0}

[Again, this is ]{.class-0}[spiritual application,]{.class-2}[ and all of the commentators and expositors do it. It makes great preaching. It doesn't make much good doctrine. After all, a Christian doesn't have to find Christ and hang onto Him for dear life to stay saved. He doesn't have to worry about becoming careless and letting the Lord go and having to find Him over again.]{.class-0}

[As we have already stated, a Christian, upon salvation, is put into the Body of Christ by the Holy Ghost, and Jesus Christ lives in the body of a Christian in the person of the Holy Spirit. A Christian couldn't lose the Lord Jesus Christ if he tried. But he can lose his ]{.class-0}[fellowship ]{.class-2}[with the Lord; and the only way of getting it back is to get down on his knees, search his heart, confess his sins, judge himself, and start living right.]{.class-0}

"[I held him, and would not let him go"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 4). The picture is that of Jacob holding on to the Angel of the Lord in prayer. If you want the fellowship and communion with God you should have as a Christian, then you will have to seek Him in prayer as Jacob did. The Lord called it ]{.class-0}["importunity"]{.class-1}[ and described it in the Parable of the Importunate Friend in Luke 11:5--10 and the Parable of the Unjust Judge in Luke 18:1--8.]{.class-0}

[The point of both of those parables is that God isn't like that fellow in bed or the "unjust" judge. If you are persistent in seeking God in prayer, you are sure to find Him. The Lord loves you and wants to have fellowship with you, so if you have done everything you are supposed to do, then it will only be ]{.class-0}["but a little"]{.class-1}[ until you find Him. The key is, once you've found Him, don't let Him go.]{.class-0}

[Back to verse 4:]{.class-0}[ "until I had brought him into my mother's house, and into the chamber of her that conceived me."]{.class-1}[ For the Christian, that's the New Jerusalem. It sure ain't Mary!]{.class-0}

[Galatians 4:26, ]{.class-0}["But Jerusalem which is above is free, which is the mother of us all."]{.class-1}

In the Scriptures, the man does the "begatting," and the woman does the "conceiving." The Holy Spirit does the begetting of the Christian, and the New Jerusalem does the conceiving. I don't profess to understand that, but it is so.

[There are all kinds of things like that in the Scriptures. For instance, are you a saved ]{.class-0}[man]{.class-2}[ reading this Commentary? Then how can you be part of a ]{.class-0}[female]{.class-2}[ bride that is going to marry Jesus Christ someday? To go even further, every Christian, whether he is male or female, is a ]{.class-0}[son]{.class-2}[ of God. So what is Jesus Christ doing marrying a bunch of ]{.class-0}[sons]{.class-2}[?!]{.class-0}

[You take that New Jerusalem. Right now, it is considered to be your ]{.class-0}[mother]{.class-2}[, but it is a place where the saints live after death (Heb. 12:22--24). Yet it is the ]{.class-0}[Bride of Christ]{.class-2}[ herself in Revelation 21:2. Do you profess to understand all of that? I sure don't.]{.class-0}[ Ich weiss nicht.]{.class-2}

Brethren, there are things in that Bible that you never will understand until you get to Heaven, and no amount of "clearer translations" or "up-to-date modern versions" or "new archaeological light on the ancient Scripture" is going to solve anything. You are just going to have to trust God and believe what He said, as He said it, even if you don't understand it.

[Back in Song 1:4, the King brought this woman ]{.class-0}["into his chambers,"]{.class-1}[ but now she brings him into her ]{.class-0}["mother's house."]{.class-1}[ I'm sure there is probably some spiritual application you can get out of that, but what it is, I don't know.]{.class-0}[ Ich weiss nicht.]{.class-2}

[Verse 5 is a repeat of chapter 2 verse 7. It is plainly a prayer for the Rapture. The speaker sets herself apart from the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem,"]{.class-1}[ so she is not Israel.]{.class-0}

Now, what I gather from chapters 2 and 3 is this: in chapter 2, the Bride of Christ is caught out; in chapter 3, the Tribulation starts. If that is the case, then the woman can't be the Church, but then again, she is not Israel either.

[In Revelation 7:9--17, there is a third group that is saved. There is a large multitude of ]{.class-0}[saved Gentiles ]{.class-2}[in the Tribulation. I gather that those Gentiles have to hunt for Christ to find Him. You have a situation, as in the Gospels, where the Gentiles came to find Christ like the centurion in Matthew 8:5, the Syrophenician woman in Mark 7:25--26, and those Greeks at the Passover in John 12:20--21.]{.class-0}

[There will be a rapture of Tribulation saints at the end of the Tribulation. This will be a rapture of two bodies of believers, not ]{.class-0}[one ]{.class-2}[as in the Church Age. If that woman in chapter 3 represents the Gentile body of believers in the Tribulation, then those Gentiles are telling those Jews not to stir up the Lord to come back until He is ready.]{.class-0}

[Now, I don't understand why they would do that. The prayer of the Apostle John is not "Don't come back until you feel like it, Lord"; it is ]{.class-0}["Even so, come, Lord Jesus."]{.class-1}[ The ]{.class-0}["blessed hope"]{.class-1}[ for the Christian is an eager expectation that the Lord will return in his lifetime. In fact, you really don't find a prayer like Song 3:5 anywhere else in the Bible outside of the Song of Solomon.]{.class-0}

[When it comes to Gentile salvation in the Tribulation, there is only one thing that has to happen before the post-Tribulation rapture. Before the Lord can come back before the end of the Tribulation, ]{.class-0}["the gospel must first be published among all nations"]{.class-1}[ (Mark 13:10). That ]{.class-0}["gospel"]{.class-1}[ is not ]{.class-0}["the gospel of the grace of God"]{.class-1}[ (Acts 20:24); it is the ]{.class-0}["gospel of the kingdom"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 24:14). So perhaps the Gentile believers are asking the Jewish believers not to stir up the Lord to come back before that can happen. And if that is not the explanation, then I have no idea why they say verse 5.]{.class-0}

6 Who is this that cometh out of the wilderness like pillars of smoke, perfumed with myrrh and frankincense, with all powders of the merchant?

7 Behold his bed, which is Solomon's; threescore valiant men are about it, of the valiant of Israel.

8 They all hold swords, being expert in war: every man hath his sword upon his thigh because of fear in the night.

9 King Solomon made himself a chariot of the wood of Lebanon.

10 He made the pillars thereof of silver, the bottom thereof of gold, the covering of it of purple, the midst thereof being paved with love, for the daughters of Jerusalem.

11 Go forth, O ye daughters of Zion, and behold king Solomon with the crown wherewith his mother crowned him in the day of his espousals, and in the day of the gladness of his heart.

Verse 6 is a reference to the Second Advent. When Christ comes back to earth, He comes back to the wilderness before He comes to the Mount of Olives (see Deut. 33:2; Hab. 3:3).

[The ]{.class-0}["myrrh and frankincense, with all powders of the merchant"]{.class-1}[ are connected with the Marriage of the Lamb in Heaven right before His return (Rev. 19).]{.class-0}

[Look at Psalm 45:8.]{.class-0}[ "All thy garments smell of myrrh, and aloes, and cassia, out of the ivory palaces, whereby they have made thee glad."]{.class-1}[ In Psalm 45, from verse 8 to verse 17, you have the marriage of Jesus Christ to His Bride. But notice the context is the Second Advent (Psa. 45:3--6).]{.class-0}

"[Who is this that cometh out of the wilderness like pillars of smoke"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 6). When the Jews came out of the land of Egypt, the Lord led them through the wilderness with a pillar of cloud by day and a pillar of fire by night. Well, smoke is a cloud that arises from something that is on fire. So the Exodus of Israel from Egypt is a picture of the return of Jesus Christ to take His kingdom.]{.class-0}

The first place the Lord met with Israel as a nation was Mount Sinai. When the people refused to enter the land at Kadesh-barnea, the Lord took them through the wilderness of Sin and then on the King's highway just east of the Dead Sea. If Edom had let them travel "the King's highway," they would have gone through Selah-Petra and by Mount Seir and Mount Paran in Edom. They ended up crossing the Jordan River where Jesus was baptized. That route is the path the Lord will take at the Second Advent. It starts out at Mount Sinai and ends up at the Mount of Olives.

As we run the references for this route, you will notice that they cover the Old Testament. There's more in the Old Testament on the Second Coming of Jesus Christ than there is in the New Testament. The reason why most Christians find the Old Testament a dead and dull book is because they have been taught that all of the Old Testament has been fulfilled already in the New Testament, making the whole thing past history.

[Less than a quarter of the Old Testament has been fulfilled. ]{.class-2}[In fact, the only part of the Old Testament that has been fulfilled is the part that deals with the coming of a suffering Messiah to make a substitute payment for sin by a blood atonement. If you think that's all there is to the Old Testament, then you have never read the Old Testament. That is not even the ]{.class-0}[main theme]{.class-2}[ of the Old Testament, nor is it the main body of its content. As anyone who has read the entire Bible through knows, the main theme of the Bible in either Testament is ]{.class-0}[the Second Coming of Jesus Christ.]{.class-2}

[All right, here we go. Deuteronomy 33:2, ]{.class-0}["The Lord came from Sinai, and rose up from Seir unto them; he shined forth from mount Paran, and he came with ten thousands of saints: from his right hand went a fiery law for them."]{.class-1}

[If you pick up any commentary by any Bible teacher at random, you will read that that verse is a reference to Exodus 20. Mount Seir and Mount Paran don't even show up in the book of Exodus. In Numbers, Mount Seir shows up in a prophecy made by Balaam about the Second Advent. Israel pitched in the ]{.class-0}[wilderness]{.class-2}[ of Paran in Numbers, but the Lord never shined forth from there.]{.class-0}

That "shining forth" is the glory of the Lord at the Second Advent. Look at Isaiah 60:1.

"[Arise, shine; for thy light is come, and the glory of the Lord is risen upon thee."]{.class-1}

[Poor old Handel, bless his heart, put that verse in his ]{.class-0}[Messiah]{.class-2}[ oratorio and associated it with the First Advent. Handel was a great musician and composer. His ]{.class-0}[Messiah]{.class-2}[ is one of the most glorious, Christ-exalting pieces of music ever penned by a man. But when it came to understanding the Scriptures, George Frederick Handel didn't know about what he was talking.]{.class-0}

[Handel ran ]{.class-0}["the glory of the Lord"]{.class-1}[ back to Isaiah 40:3--5, and he ran that ]{.class-0}["light"]{.class-1}[ back to Isaiah 9:1--2. Because both passages have the First Advent in the immediate context, he figured Isaiah 60:1 was fulfilled in the Gospels.]{.class-0}

[Isaiah 60:1 has nothing to do with Christ's First Coming.]{.class-2}[ Look at the context of Isaiah 60:1.]{.class-0}

"[For, behold, the darkness shall cover the earth, and gross darkness the people: but the Lord shall arise upon thee, and his glory shall be seen upon thee"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 60:2).]{.class-0}

[That darkness is not the ]{.class-0}[spiritual darkness]{.class-2}[ of Isaiah 9:1--2 that was fulfilled in Matthew 4:15--16. That darkness is a ]{.class-0}[physical darkness]{.class-2}[ that God sends on the earth at the end of the Tribulation.]{.class-0}

"[And the fifth angel poured out his vial upon the seat of the beast; and his kingdom was full of darkness; and they gnawed their tongues for pain"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 16:10).]{.class-0}

"[And I beheld when he had opened the sixth seal, and lo, there was a great earthquake; and the sun became black as sackcloth of hair, and the moon became as blood"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 6:12).]{.class-0}

"[Immediately after the tribulation of those days shall the sun be darkened, and the moon shall not give her light, and the stars shall fall from heaven, and the powers of the heavens shall be shaken"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 24:29).]{.class-0}

When Jesus Christ returns at the Second Advent, it is described as the sun rising in the morning.

"[But unto you that fear my name shall the SUN OF RIGHTEOUSNESS ARISE with healing in his wings"]{.class-1}[ (Mal. 4:2). What's the context? ]{.class-0}["The great and dreadful day of the Lord"]{.class-1}[ (Mal. 4:5).]{.class-0}

[The Apostle Peter writes, ]{.class-0}["We have also a more sure word of prophecy; whereunto ye do well that ye take heed, as unto a LIGHT THAT SHINETH in a dark place, until THE DAY DAWN, and THE DAY STAR ARISE in your hearts"]{.class-1}[ (2 Pet. 1:19).]{.class-0}

[Again, the context is the Second Coming. Second Peter 1:16, ]{.class-0}["For we have not followed cunningly devised fables, when we made known unto you the POWER AND COMING of our Lord Jesus Christ, but were eyewitnesses of his majesty. For he received from God the Father honour and glory, when there came such a voice to him from the excellent glory, This is my beloved Son, in whom I am well pleased."]{.class-1}

[So the transfiguration of Jesus Christ in Matthew 17 was a picture of the Second Advent. Christ said, ]{.class-0}["There be some standing here, which shall not taste of death, till they see the SON OF MAN COMING IN HIS KINGDOM"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 16:28).]{.class-0}

[Well, if that's the case, what happened to Christ at His transfiguration? Matthew 17:2, ]{.class-0}["And was transfigured before them: and his face did SHINE AS THE SUN,]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[and his raiment was WHITE AS THE LIGHT."]{.class-1}

[So when the Bible talks about the Lord "arising" and "shining forth," it has nothing to do with ]{.class-0}[anything ]{.class-2}[that took place in Exodus or Numbers.]{.class-0}

[Furthermore, look again at Deuteronomy 33:2. ]{.class-0}["He came with ten thousands of saints."]{.class-1}[ Well, those aren't the Jews that Moses led out of Egypt. ]{.class-0}[That's the Second Advent as prophesied by Enoch.]{.class-2}

"[And Enoch also, the seventh from Adam, prophesied of these, saying, Behold, the Lord cometh with TEN THOUSANDS OF HIS SAINTS"]{.class-1}[ (Jude 14).]{.class-0}

[Those ]{.class-0}["saints"]{.class-1}[ are Christians that return with the Lord in Revelation 19:14. How do you know that for sure? Look at Deuteronomy 33:3. ]{.class-0}["All his saints are in thy hand." ]{.class-1}[Moses said, ]{.class-0}["All HIS saints."]{.class-1}[ Those are God's saints. But he didn't say, ]{.class-0}["All his saints are in HIS hand."]{.class-1}[ He said, ]{.class-0}["All his saints are in THY hand."]{.class-1}[ To whom does the ]{.class-0}["thy"]{.class-1}[ refer? Why, it's Jesus Christ.]{.class-0}

"[My sheep hear my voice, and I know them, and they follow me: and I give unto them eternal life; and they shall never perish, neither shall any man pluck them out of MY HAND"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:27--28). That's Christ speaking (John 10:25).]{.class-0}

[So Deuteronomy 33:2 is a reference to Christ's return at the Second Advent and ]{.class-0}[not]{.class-2}[ the Exodus from Egypt. So when He comes, the first place to which He comes is Sinai. Then He goes up the Sinaitic coast by the Gulf of Aquaba to Mount Seir and Mount Paran in Edom.]{.class-0}

Look at Judges 5:4--5 and see a reference to the same thing.

"[Lord, when thou wentest out of Seir, when thou marchedst out of the field of Edom, the earth trembled, and the heavens dropped, the clouds also dropped water. The mountains melted from before the Lord, even that Sinai from before the Lord God of Israel."]{.class-1}

[That's ]{.class-0}["Deborah and Barak"]{.class-1}[ singing about their victory over Sisera at Megiddo (Judg. 5:19). That is up in northern Israel.]{.class-0}[ It isn't within 100 miles of Edom or Sinai.]{.class-2}[ Moreover, Sinai didn't melt in Exodus 19 or 20.]{.class-0}

[That isn't all. Look at Judges 5:12. ]{.class-0}["Lead thy captivity captive."]{.class-1}[ That's a prophetic reference to Jesus Christ's resurrection. It's ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[Jehovah God at the giving of the Law.]{.class-0}

"[Wherefore he saith, When he ascended up on high, HE LED CAPTIVITY CAPTIVE, and gave gifts unto men"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 4:8).]{.class-0}

The song of Deborah not only deals with the defeat of Sisera in Judges 4; it also deals with the Second Advent of Jesus Christ. Look at Judges 5:20.

"[They fought from heaven."]{.class-1}[ Who's ]{.class-0}["they"]{.class-1}[? ]{.class-0}["The stars in their courses fought against Sisera"]{.class-1}[ (Judg. 5:20). Not in Judges 4 they didn't. But they will against the Antichrist in Revelation 19.]{.class-0}

[Paul said, ]{.class-0}["And to you who are troubled rest with us, when the Lord Jesus shall be revealed from heaven with his mighty angels, In flaming fire taking vengeance on them that know not God, and that obey not the gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class-1}[ (2 Thess. 1:8--9).]{.class-0}

[There are those ]{.class-0}["stars"]{.class-1}[ fighting against Sisera, a type of the Antichrist. Those ]{.class-0}["stars"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["angels"]{.class-1}[ are Christians in their glorified bodies who return with Jesus Christ. The Lord said, ]{.class-0}["For in the resurrection they neither marry, nor are given in marriage, but are as the ANGELS OF GOD IN HEAVEN"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 22:30).]{.class-0}

You can also find the Christian in Judges 5:10.

"[Speak ye that ride on white asses, ye that sit in judgment, and walk by the way."]{.class-1}[ Those ]{.class-0}["white asses"]{.class-1}[ are a picture of the ]{.class-0}["white horses"]{.class-1}[ on which we'll ride at the Second Advent.]{.class-0}

[Judges 5:11, ]{.class-0}["They that are delivered from the noise of archers in the places of drawing water, there shall they rehearse the righteous acts of the Lord, even the righteous acts toward the inhabitants of his villages in Israel: then shall the people of the Lord go down to the gates."]{.class-1}

[So in the theater, they talk about having a "dress rehearsal." You can't get away from a ]{.class-0}[King James ]{.class-2}[Bible]{.class-0}[.]{.class-2}[ When you come down with the Lord, you are]{.class-0}[ "clothed in fine linen, white and clean"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 19:14), and that ]{.class-0}["fine linen is the righteousness of saints"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 19:8).]{.class-0}

[So when you come down with the Lord, you will be dressed according to how you served Jesus Christ ]{.class-0}[right now.]{.class-2}[ And when you come down, you will testify to the remnant of the Jews that get saved at the end of the Tribulation everything God did for them. ]{.class-0}["Then shall the people of the Lord]{.class-1}[ \[that's you, if you are saved\] ]{.class-0}[go down to the gates."]{.class-1}[ And down we come, brother!]{.class-0}

[Once more "with feeling." Psalm 68:1--2, ]{.class-0}["Let God arise, let his enemies be scattered: let them also that hate him flee before him. As smoke is driven away, so drive them away: as wax melteth before the fire, so let the wicked perish at the presence of God.]{.class-1}

Now, that's a famous Jehovah's Witness text. They use it to prove you are buried in Hell (the grave), and that's the end of you. But did you notice that Hell doesn't even show up in the verses?

[The reference is obviously to the Second Advent where the Lord returns and burns up His enemies. That's that ]{.class-0}["fiery law"]{.class-1}[ back in Deuteronomy 33:2. It has nothing to do with the Ten Commandments given on Mount Sinai. It's a law that says if you reject Jesus Christ in the Tribulation, you will be burnt alive by the Lord when He comes back.]{.class-0}

"[In flaming fire taking vengeance on them that know not God, and that obey not the gospel of our Lord Jesus Christ"]{.class-1}[ (2 Thess. 1:8).]{.class-0}

[That is the end of the United Nations.]{.class-2}[ Zephaniah 3:8, ]{.class-0}["Therefore wait ye upon me, saith the Lord, until the day that I rise up to the prey: for my determination is to gather the nations, that I may assemble the kingdoms\...."]{.class-1}[ So in downtown New York City, you have the United Nations ]{.class-0}[Assembly]{.class-2}[. ]{.class-0}["To pour upon them mine indignation, even all my fierce anger: for all the earth shall be devoured with THE FIRE of my jealousy."]{.class-1}

The J.W.s never could get the Scriptures straight.

[Back to Psalm 68. The whole chapter is about the Second Advent. ]{.class-0}["The wilderness"]{.class-1}[ of Song of Solomon 3:6 shows up in verse 7, where the Lord goes before His people. Sinai shows up in verse 8. There you are in verse 17, just as you were back in Judges 5. Jesus Christ shows up in verse 18 exactly as He did back in Judges 5:12 and Ephesians 4:8.]{.class-0}

So as we have seen in three passages so far, when the Lord returns, He starts out by landing on Mount Sinai. When He does, a great earthquake takes place and the mountain is moved under Him and melts. Then he goes north to Mount Seir and Mount Paran in Edom.

[Isaiah 63:1, ]{.class-0}["Who is this that cometh FROM EDOM, with dyed garments from Bozrah? this that is glorious in his apparel, travelling in the greatness of his strength?"]{.class-1}

[Why are the Lord's garments dyed red (vs. 2)? Verse 3: ]{.class-0}["I have trodden the wine press alone; and of the people there was none with me: for I will tread them in mine anger, and trample them in my fury; and their blood shall be sprinkled upon my garments, and I will stain all my raiment."]{.class-1}

[That takes place in Revelation 19, at the Second Advent, when Christ is ]{.class-0}["clothed with a vesture dipped in blood"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 19:13) and ]{.class-0}["treadeth the winepress of the fierceness and wrath of Almighty God"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 19:15). Isaiah 63 is ]{.class-0}[not]{.class-2}[ a reference to the cross. Christ didn't "tread any winepress" of God's wrath at Calvary. ]{.class-0}[He drank the cup of God's wrath that was already poured out.]{.class-2}[ When He returns, He treads the grapes of God's wrath, and the kings of the earth drink ]{.class-0}[that cup.]{.class-2}

That means when Julia Ward Howe (who was a Unitarian that didn't even believe in the Deity of Christ), wrote, "Mine eyes have seen the glory of the coming of the Lord. He is tramping out the vintage where the grapes of wrath are stored," she was lying through her teeth. Northerners killing Southerners in the War Between the States had nothing to do with the Lord's return at all. It was just one more conflict where Gentiles were killing Gentiles. There have been more than 177 conflagrations like it since the UN was founded as "our last, best hope for peace."

[Julia didn't see any glory, any coming, any treading, any grapes of wrath, or any "truth marching on," either, brother. All she saw was a bloody mess that turned the entire United States over to the control of the Federal government and a "Civil Rights Act" that unleashed uncontrolled VD, abortion, pornography, sodomy, and profanity on society and took away any real "civil rights" that you had (see ]{.class-0}[Roots and Methodology,]{.class-2}[ Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1992).]{.class-0}

[Habakkuk 3:3, ]{.class-0}["God came from Teman, and the Holy One from mount Paran. Selah."]{.class-1}[ There's Mount Paran, again, in Edom. The context is the Second Coming (vss. 3, 4, 8, 11, 13, 15). Notice ]{.class-0}["Teman."]{.class-1}[ That's Esau's grandson (Gen. 36:11), and he became one of Edom's chief rulers (Gen. 36:15). The region is mentioned in Obadiah 9; the book of Obadiah is a prophecy against the nation of Edom (Obad. 1). In fact, though ]{.class-0}["Selah"]{.class-1}[ is often defined like a ]{.class-0}[rest]{.class-2}[ in a musical score, it is also the name of a rock city in Edom (Selah-Petra) to where the Jews will flee during the Tribulation.]{.class-0}

He says in Jeremiah 46:28, ]{.class-0}["For I will make a full end of all the nations whither I have driven thee: but I will not make a full end of thee."]{.class-1}

"[Threescore valiant men are about it, of the valiant of Israel. [The ]{.class-0}["chariot"]{.class-1}[ of verse 9 is an Oriental conveyance known as a ]{.class-0}[palanquin.]{.class-2}[ A palanquin is a royal litter with a bed or chair on it with a canopy over it to keep the sun out; it also usually has curtains between the pillars holding up the canopy so the person being carried can have some privacy. Normally, it is born by four men. In China, they put the contraption on two wheels and have it pulled by one man instead of four and call it a ]{.class-0}[ricksha.]{.class-2}

[In Solomon's case, it sits on wheels and is more than likely drawn by horses like a royal coach was in England and France in the Middle Ages. CHAPTER 4

The whole chapter, except for the last verse, is the Bridegroom speaking to the Bride. In type, it is Christ talking to the Church. The Bridegroom (Christ) is describing His love for the Bride (the Church).

4:1 Behold, thou art fair, my love; behold, thou art fair; thou hast doves' eyes within thy locks: thy hair is as a flock of goats, that appear from mount Gilead.

2 Thy teeth are like a flock of sheep that are even shorn, which came up from the washing; whereof every one bear twins, and none is barren among them.

3 Thy lips are like a thread of scarlet, and thy speech is comely: thy temples are like a piece of a pomegranate within thy locks.

4 Thy neck is like the tower of David builded for an armory, whereon there hang a thousand bucklers, all shields of mighty men.

5 Thy two breasts are like two young roes that are twins, which feed among the lilies.

In verses 1--5, the Bridegroom brags about the physical characteristics of the Bride. Any woman likes to be bragged about and told she's beautiful; she likes to be raved about and made a lot of---even the ugly ones do.

Women are peculiar that way. They never get tired of that sort of thing, no matter how old they are or what they look like. I never did understand that, and I don't guess any man could ever understand it.

Here's a 75-year-old man who says to his seventy-year-old wife, "Honey, you're the prettiest woman in all the world." (He knows he's lying, and she knows he's lying, but it's the one kind of a lie women seem to appreciate.)

[So in the first five verses of this chapter, the Bridegroom brags about His Bride, and from a natural standpoint, that's the way it ought to be. But when you consider that, spiritually speaking, this is Christ describing the Church, it takes on a different meaning. You might tell your spouse those "little white lies" she loves to hear, but Christ won't. He is telling us not what we are right now, but what we will be when He finishes His work in us (Eph. 5:27) and we are ]{.class-0}["conformed to the image of his Son"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 8:29). In the meantime, it is the goal of the Christian life to put down the sinful flesh and allow the Holy Spirit to work out these spiritual characteristics in us so that we can be as much like the Saviour as we can this side of Heaven.]{.class-0}

"[Behold, thou art fair"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 1). Again, ]{.class-0}["fair"]{.class-1}[ here means ]{.class-0}[beautiful]{.class-2}[ or ]{.class-0}[pretty]{.class-2}[ (see comments on 1:8). He says in Song 6:4, ]{.class-0}["Thou art beautiful, O my love."]{.class-1}[ The psalmist says of the Bride of Christ: ]{.class-0}["So shall the king greatly desire thy beauty: for he is thy Lord; and worship thou him"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 45:11).]{.class-0}

"[Thou hast doves' eyes."]{.class-1}[ Since we have already made comments on this under 1:5, we will just draw your attention, once again, to the fact that her eyes (the Bride's) are like His eyes (the Bridegroom's); see 5:12. That is one of two comparisons made in the book, so far, between the Bridegroom and the Bride. Back in 2:1--2, Christ is called]{.class-0}[ "the lily of the valleys,"]{.class-1}[ and the Church is likened to a ]{.class-0}["lily among thorns."]{.class-1}[ The point is that the Christian should be like his Lord. In the case here, he ought to "see" things the way the Lord sees them, and of course, the only way to do that is to spend more time with Him in the Book and in prayer.]{.class-0}

"[Within thy locks."]{.class-1}[ That's the hair that comes down over the forehead and across the eyes. I believe the modern term is ]{.class-0}[bangs.]{.class-2}

"[Thy hair is as a flock of goats."]{.class-1}[ Those ]{.class-0}["goats"]{.class-1}[ are the ]{.class-0}[black goats]{.class-2}[ of Kedar (see comments on 1:5). Solomon is saying that not only is the skin of Pharaoh's daughter ]{.class-0}["black,"]{.class-1}[ but so is her hair. The Bride's hair is likened to a smooth, rippling black mass of goats coming down a hillside. In the Song, the Bride's hair is ]{.class-0}["black"]{.class-1}[ just like her Lover's (see 5:11). Again, the Bride of Christ should match her Saviour.]{.class-0}

[In the Bible, hair is ]{.class-0}["a covering"]{.class-1}[ (see comments on 1 Cor. 11:5--15 in that Commentary). Long hair is given to a woman as a covering for her head. Well, the covering for a Christian is Christ (1 Cor. 11:3). When the New Testament talks about ]{.class-0}["the helmet of salvation"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 6:17), that's a covering for the head. The head covering of a Christian should be like his Lord's.]{.class-0}

[The Apostle Paul wrote: ]{.class-0}["But let us, who are of the day, be sober, putting on the breastplace of faith and love; and for an HELMET]{.class-1}[ \[there's that head covering\]]{.class-0}[, the HOPE OF SALVATION. For God hath not appointed us to wrath, but to obtain SALVATION BY OUR LORD JESUS CHRIST"]{.class-1}[ (1 Thess. 5:8--9).]{.class-0}

Now, the Bride ought to match her Husband in the ways we have just listed, and as we've said, the only way that is going to happen is if they spend time together. Have you ever seen a married couple that lived together for forty or fifty years? They rub off on each other until they pick up the same expressions, tones, habits, and sometimes even facial characteristics. I've seen photographs of couples that were married back in the 1910s and 1920s, and you never saw two more different-looking individuals in all your life. And then I have talked to those same people when they were well up in age, around seventy someplace, and you could hardly tell them apart.

[The moral for the Christian should be clear: the Christian should have fellowship with the Lord so he begins to "match Him" in a sense. There's something about every Christian that ought to be "Christ-like." Now maybe you aren't Christ-like at all; after all, we're all still sinners and live in a sinful body of flesh. But if you are a Christian, there ought to be ]{.class-0}[something]{.class-2}[ about you that reminds people of Jesus Christ, and if there's ]{.class-0}[nothing]{.class-2}[ about you that reminds people of Jesus Christ, you haven't spent a lot of time with Him. You can't spend time in His word and talking to Him in prayer without Him "rubbing off" on you somewhere.]{.class-0}

[That Bible says that the chief priests and scribes ]{.class-0}["took knowledge"]{.class-1}[ of Peter and John ]{.class-0}["that they had been with Jesus"]{.class-1}[ (Acts 4:13). They had spent so much time with the Lord that even in a backslidden condition people could tell they were disciples of Christ (Mark 14:66--70; John 18:17, 25). He had spent so much time with them that they were marked permanently.]{.class-0}

"[As a flock of goats, that appear from mount Gilead."]{.class-1}[ Mount Gilead is located on the east side of Jordan. It was the land chosen by Reuben, Gad, and the half tribe of Manasseh because it was good pasture land for cattle (Num. 32:1--5). It is where Jacob made the covenant with Laban (Gen. 31:21--25, 44--48). The judge Jephthah was from Gilead (Judg. 11:1), as was Elijah (1 Kings 17:1).]{.class-0}

[Verse 2:]{.class-0}[ "Thy teeth are like a flock of sheep that are even shorn]{.class-1}[ \[they are white\]]{.class-0}[, which came up from the washing]{.class-1}[ \[they are clean\]]{.class-0}[; whereof every one bear twins ]{.class-1}[\[they match\]]{.class-0}[, and none is barren]{.class-1}[ \[none of them are missing\]]{.class-0}[."]{.class-1}[ Notice where the Bridegroom starts when describing the Bride's beauty. He starts with the ]{.class-0}[face]{.class-2}[ (vss. 1--4), not the ]{.class-0}[form]{.class-2}[ (vs. 5). He describes her ]{.class-0}[eyes]{.class-2}[ (vs. 1), her ]{.class-0}[teeth]{.class-2}[ (vs. 2), her ]{.class-0}[lips]{.class-2}[ and ]{.class-0}[temples]{.class-2}[ (vs. 3), and her ]{.class-0}[neck]{.class-2}[ (vs. 4) before He ever talks about her ]{.class-0}[body]{.class-2}[ (vs. 5).]{.class-0}

[When it comes to appreciating a woman's beauty, Americans have become ]{.class-0}[African]{.class-2}[ in their thinking. The average unsaved American male has been looking for so long at half-naked women on billboards and TV, doing the bumps and the grinds to African sex music, that they gravitate to a woman's form. In the Bible, it's a woman's ]{.class-0}[face]{.class-2}[ that is to attract a man.]{.class-0}

[Now if you don't know that, ]{.class-0}[advertisers ]{.class-2}[do. That is why you have so many commercials about toothpaste, mouthwash, makeup, eyeliner, hair products, etc. Of course, what they don't tell you is all the things they have to do to those models to make them look like they do. If you saw some of those women out of their makeup, it would scare you out of a year's growth.]{.class-0}

There's a story about a man who fell in love with an opera singer. He thought she was the most beautiful thing he had ever seen, and she had a beautiful voice to go along with her looks. Well, he courted her and eventually married her. When he woke up beside her the morning after his honeymoon, he saw her hair was a wig mounted over the night stand. Beside it were her false teeth in a glass. He looked at her without her makeup and said, "Honey, sing something, quick!"

Now, you take those movie stars with their perfect teeth. What you don't know is that a lot of those actors and actresses had all their teeth pulled and bought plates because the fake teeth were better looking than their real ones. Just remember that the next time you see an ad for the latest "whitener" and "total tooth care" paste or mouthwash.

Of course, beauty is not considered the same in all parts of the world. In some South Sea Islands, it's considered a sign of beauty when a woman has some of her teeth missing. There is one island where the tribal custom is that a man won't even marry a woman unless she has one of her front teeth missing because it's a sign of beauty. So every year around "mating season," the women get rocks and bust out their front teeth. You have to have real convictions to do that!

[Verse 3: ]{.class-0}["Thy lips are like a thread of scarlet."]{.class-1}[ She has thin red lips that match the color in her cheeks. It's a natural color, not lipstick or makeup.]{.class-0}

Over in the Orient, scarlet makeup was associated with prostitutes, even up until the time of Christ and much later (e.g., see 2 Kings 9:30); as a matter of fact, it's largely that way almost anywhere. The Americans picked up the practice of women wearing makeup and lipstick mainly from France after 1918 (WWI). You can look through pictures, drawings, and photographs from 1890 to around 1920 and find very little of it. Up to that point, the only people who wore makeup all the time were the French. It wasn't a common thing even among Italians or Spaniards, never among the Germans, and rarely among the English.

The reason the French wore makeup was because they were a sickly people. Back in the 1700s and 1800s, a woman's beauty depended on her health. The French city dwellers were part of the European ballroom crowd, and that is where you found people wearing makeup. The kind of people who spent all of their time in ballrooms and drawing rooms were sickly people.

Now I am not going to preach to you women about wearing makeup. The Holiness crowd used to say it was a sin to wear it, but then they got on television and changed their minds in order to raise money for their million-dollar stages. If you were to kiss some of these Charismatic women on TV, like Tammy Bakker and Jan Crouch, it would give you lead poisoning.

I'm not going to tell you ladies that it's wrong to wear makeup; after all, some of your "barns" need a little "paint" on them. But the original cure for a bad complexion was not makeup; it was staying outdoors. Back in the Nineteenth Century, if a woman was any kind of a woman at all, she was outdoors, working on a scrub board or cooking over a kettle. She got plenty of sun, fresh air, and exercise. She was in good health, and her lips were red, and her cheeks were pink.

[Now notice what else the Bridegroom says about the mouth: ]{.class-0}["thy speech is comely."]{.class-1}[ So it's not just that she had pretty lips, it's what comes out of them that makes her beautiful as well.]{.class-0}

[Solomon said, ]{.class-0}["As a jewel of gold in a swine's snout, so is a fair woman which is without discretion"]{.class-1}[ (Prov. 11:22).]{.class-0}

[Proverbs 31:26 says of the ]{.class-0}["virtuous woman"]{.class-1}[: ]{.class-0}["She openeth her mouth with wisdom; and in her tongue is the law of kindness."]{.class-1}

[Back to verse 3: ]{.class-0}["thy temples are like a piece of pomegranate within thy locks."]{.class-1}[ He says the same thing again in 6:7. The pomegranate was the fruit represented on the robe of the high priest (Exod. 28:33--34) and the two great pillars of the Temple (1 Kings 7:18, 20). It was one of the fruits used to describe the prosperity of the Promised Land (Num. 13:23; Deut. 8:8). The Bridegroom is using the ]{.class-0}["pomegranate"]{.class-1}[ to describe the Bride's temples beneath her hair as desirable.]{.class-0}

"[Thy neck is like the tower of David"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 5). He says in 7:4, ]{.class-0}["Thy neck is a tower of ivory."]{.class-1}[ The idea here is ]{.class-0}[strength.]{.class-2}

"[Builded for an armory, whereon there hang a thousand bucklers, all shields of mighty men."]{.class-1}[ The power of David (from a human standpoint) was in this armory. Here, the ]{.class-0}["thousand bucklers"]{.class-1}[ are defined as ]{.class-0}["all shields of mighty men."]{.class-1}[ A buckler was a small shield held by leather straps at the back. You will sometimes see it distinguished in Scripture from larger shields; e.g., ]{.class-0}["both the shields and the bucklers"]{.class-1}[ (Ezek. 39:9). Undoubtedly the picture here in verse 4 is to the ]{.class-0}["chains of gold"]{.class-1}[ around the neck of the Bride back in 1:10 (see also vs. 9 in this chapter).]{.class-0}

Now I know that the description of verse 4 doesn't sound very flattering to a modern woman; no woman is going to be flattered today by telling her she has a thick neck. It sounds more like the description of an Amazon or Valkyrie (the warrior women of Greek and German mythology).

[But the modern idea of a beautiful woman is not what it used to be. Did you ever compare the ]{.class-0}[Venus de Milo]{.class-2}[ with the beauty pageant contestants or models of today? Just look at any painting from the Eighteenth or Nineteenth Centuries. Back then, a beautiful woman would be what we call today "pleasantly plump": she had some "meat" on her. The average idea of a beautiful woman today is a female who is about 25 pounds underweight. Some of those professional "supermodels" actually starve themselves (anorexia) or purge themselves (bulimia) until they are as skinny as a scarecrow.]{.class-0}

"[Thy two breasts are like two young roes that are twins, which feed among the lilies"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 5). The roe is another name for a gazelle. The gazelle was known for its delicateness and loveliness. The verse is an intimate description of the Bride.]{.class-0}

6 Until the day break, and the shadows flee away, I will get me to the mountain of myrrh, and to the hill of frankincense.

7 Thou art all fair, my love; there is no spot in thee.

8 Come with me from Lebanon, my spouse, with me from Lebanon: look from the top of Amana, from the top of Shenir and Hermon, from the lions' dens, from the mountains of the leopards.

[And now we are back on the Rapture and the Second Advent. Look at verse 6: ]{.class-0}["Until the day break ]{.class-1}[\[that's the Advent, see Mal. 4:2; 2 Pet. 1:19\]]{.class-0}[, and the shadows flee away ]{.class-1}[\[those ]{.class-0}["shadows"]{.class-1}[ are the Tribulation---Zeph. 1:14--15)]{.class-0}[."]{.class-1}[ So until the Tribulation and the Advent, the Bridegroom has gotten Himself ]{.class-0}["to the mountain of myrrh, and to the hill of frankincense."]{.class-1}[ In Psalm 45:8, that's a reference to Heaven. Notice again the premillennial order---despite the theology of the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ translators. Right now, in the Church Age, Jesus Christ is in Heaven at the right hand of God the Father (Heb. 1:3), having fulfilled His offices of Prophet and Priest (Heb. 3:1); that's what the ]{.class-0}["myrrh"]{.class-1}[ and the ]{.class-0}["frankincense"]{.class-1}[ stand for. He won't be King (]{.class-0}[gold]{.class-2}[) until He returns to defeat the Antichrist and the UN.]{.class-0}

"[Thou art all fair, my love; there is no spot in thee"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 7). That's the condition in which the Bride of Christ is ]{.class-0}[after]{.class-2}[ the Judgment Seat of Christ---]{.class-0}[not now]{.class-2}[ (see Eph. 5:27). The song goes: "Tis a glorious church ]{.class-0}[without spot or wrinkle,]{.class-2}[" but that isn't true right now. If it were, Paul wouldn't have had to turn Christians over to ]{.class-0}["Satan for the destruction of the flesh"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 5:5), and he wouldn't have had to warn you about ]{.class-0}["the works of the flesh"]{.class-1}[ (Gal. 5:19--21). The Church ]{.class-0}[will]{.class-2}[ be without ]{.class-0}["spot, or wrinkle,"]{.class-1}[ but it's ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[that way now. The Church won't be spotless, wrinkleless, or blemish free until the Judgment Seat of Christ.]{.class-0}

"[Thou art ALL fair, my love"]{.class-1}[; i.e., the Bride is completely clean. That means the description of verses 1--5 is probably of the Church in Heaven, not on earth.]{.class-0}

[Now, at the Rapture, you get a new body just like that of Jesus Christ (Phil. 3:21; 1 John 3:2). But even then, you won't be completely spotless or wrinkleless until all the works connected with the old body have been purified, purged, straightened up, and ironed out (1 Cor. 3:13--15). To get out spots, you have to use a spot remover; to get out wrinkles, you have to iron them out. When you get to the Judgment Seat of Christ, there will be three kinds of things going on: 1) You will be given clothing of ]{.class-0}["fine linen"]{.class-1}[ to fit the righteousness you did on earth (Rev. 19:8). 2) "Spot remover" will have to be applied to get the spots out of the linen; according to Ephesians 5:26, that "spot remover" will be ]{.class-0}["the washing of water by the word."]{.class-1}[ 3) The wrinkles will have to be "ironed out" of the linen.]{.class-0}

[Verse 8:]{.class-0}[ "Come with me."]{.class-1}[ That's the Bridegroom speaking to the Bride. It's a picture of the Rapture. When He says ]{.class-0}["from Lebanon,"]{.class-1}[ He's the one coming ]{.class-0}["from Lebanon"]{.class-1}[ to get her. Look at the next three places He names in the verse: ]{.class-0}["Amana," "Shenir,"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["Hermon"]{.class-1}[; all three places are in Lebanon. Solomon had a house there (1 Kings 7:2).]{.class-0}

"[Look from the top of Amana."]{.class-1}[ Now there's more to the verse than just Solomon taking Pharaoh's daughter on a "honeymoon" to Lebanon. The word ]{.class-0}["Amana"]{.class-1}[ means "a settled provision"; it can also mean "truth." In modern times, it is the name of a line of "deep freezes" and refrigerators.]{.class-0}

[Now before you dismiss that last item, look at the chart at the back of the book. Compare the map of Palestine with the layout of the universe. At the top of Palestine you have a body of water (the Sea of Galilee); at the bottom of Palestine you have a body of water (the Dead Sea). In between them you have a "firmament" (Canaan). Below the lower body of water you have the place where God rained fire and brimstone down on Sodom and Gomorrha; that is where the lake of fire will be in the Millennium (Isa. 34). And ]{.class-0}[above ]{.class-2}[the upper body of water there is a mountain that just happens to be the name picked out for a ]{.class-0}[deep freeze,]{.class-2}[ kind of like ]{.class-0}["the face of the deep is frozen"]{.class-1}[ (Job 38:30). And here in Song 4:8, the Bridegroom is said to be in ]{.class-0}["Hermon,"]{.class-1}[ which just happens to be called ]{.class-0}["mount Sion"]{.class-1}[ (Deut. 4:48), as in ]{.class-0}["mount Sion\...the city of the living God, the heavenly Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ (Heb. 12:22), located ]{.class-0}["on the sides of the north"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 48:1--2 cf. Isa. 14:13). The reason why God picked the land of Palestine as the Promised Land, instead of anywhere in Asia, Africa, Europe, Australia, or North or South America, is because Palestine is a perfect picture of the universe.]{.class-0}

"[From the top of Shenir and Hermon."]{.class-1}[ Those are two names for the same place (see Deut. 3:9).]{.class-0}

"[From the lions' dens"]{.class-1}[; that's where the lions live and from where they're going to come. That could be a reference to ]{.class-0}["the Lion of the tribe of Juda"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 5:5) and a bunch of saints who are just like Him (Rev. 5:10); after all, they are going to come out of their ]{.class-0}["dens"]{.class-1}[ at the end of the Tribulation (Jude 14--15; 2 Thess. 1:7--8). But it could just as well refer to the Devil, who is ]{.class-0}["as a roaring lion"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 5:8).]{.class-0}

[Why do I say that? Look at the next part of the verse:]{.class-0}[ "from the mountains of the leopards."]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[That's a reference to the Antichrist]{.class-2}[ (Rev. 13:1--2).]{.class-0}

[What you have in the Tribulation is Satan and his angels up in the third heaven fighting against Michael the archangel and his angels (Rev. 12:7). That war ends with Satan and his angels being cast out of Heaven (Rev. 12:9). John Milton, in ]{.class-0}[Paradise Lost,]{.class-2}[ taught that took place back at Satan's original rebellion (Isa. 14; Ezek. 28), but that's ]{.class-0}[not true.]{.class-2}[ In Revelation 12, Satan's casting out occurs after Christ's ascension and during the Tribulation (see Rev. 12:5--6).]{.class-0}

[When Satan is cast out of Heaven along with his angels, he comes down to the earth (Rev. 12:12), and when he does, up pops the Antichrist in the next chapter (Rev. 13). Along with him come up a whole "slew" of false Christs (Matt. 24:5). So you have ]{.class-0}["lions"]{.class-1}[ (the Devil and his angels) and ]{.class-0}["leopards"]{.class-1}[ plural (the Antichrist and false Christs).]{.class-0}

[Now, there are two commands in verse 8:]{.class-0}[ "Come"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["look."]{.class-1}[ So the picture is that, in the Tribulation, the Church is up in Heaven with Christ, looking down at what takes place on the earth. That is what takes place in the book of Revelation with John (who is a type of the Church---see comments on Rev. 4:1 in that Commentary). When ]{.class-0}["the Lamb"]{.class-1}[ opens the seven-sealed book (which releases God's judgments on the earth during the Tribulation), He tells John to ]{.class-0}["Come and see"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 6:1, 3, 5, 7), and John sees what's going on down here.]{.class-0}

Now, how the Lord does that, I don't know, but I'm sure if man can do it with satellites and television, then the Lord can certainly do it. Man is so egotistical. He photographs something, breaks it down into a stream of electrons, transmits it through the air over thousands of miles, reassembles it in a TV set in your living room so you can see it, and he thinks the God who created the electrons and the photons and the laws by which they operate can't see what he's doing. If a man can do all that, don't you know God has something "up His sleeve"?

I've made hundreds of hours of recordings in the classrooms, in churches, and in private studios. That tape or disk picks up everything I say: all the breathing, all the movements, all the noise in the congregation; you might even get some of the spit. I've got stuff I recorded over thirty years ago, and it's still going out where people can hear it. People like Lester Roloff, Maze Jackson, and Oliver B. Greene are still preaching on the radio, and they've been dead for years. That's those tapes they made back in 1950s, 1960s, 1970s, and 1980s. I've got enough material on tape and "MP3" that I'll be giving the apostate Fundamentalists a fit 25 years after I'm dead.

[With that kind of technology, sinful man is still arrogant enough to think that God doesn't have a record of what he's thinking and what he's saying and what he's doing. ]{.class-0}[If man can do it, God can do it;]{.class-2}[ after all, He's bound to have more sense than man. If God is who He is and can control several billion stars and galaxies, while feeding all the birds, fish, insects, and animals, He's not going to have any trouble keeping a record of nearly seven billion people.]{.class-0}

[The indication of verse 8 is that during the Tribulation, you'll be up in Heaven with the Lord, looking at what goes on down here on earth. Naturally the question arises, "Do our loved ones up in Heaven know what's going on with us ]{.class-0}[right now]{.class-2}[?" I often get that question when a mother or father dies. And the answer is that there are Scriptures which indicate that they ]{.class-0}[could]{.class-2}[ if the Lord wanted them to (e.g., Heb. 12:1), but there are none that actually say that they do. So whether they do or not, I don't know.]{.class-0}

9 Thou hast ravished my heart, my sister, my spouse; thou hast ravished my heart with one of thine eyes, with one chain of thy neck.

10 How fair is thy love, my sister, my spouse! how much better is thy love than wine! and the smell of thine ointments than all spices!

11 Thy lips, O my spouse, drop as the honeycomb: honey and milk are under thy tongue; and the smell of thy garments is like the smell of Lebanon.

"[Thou hast ravished my heart, my sister, my spouse"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 9). The word ]{.class-0}["ravished"]{.class-1}[ is usually used in a bad sense, meaning ]{.class-0}[raped]{.class-2}[ (see Isa. 13:16; Lam. 5:11; Zech. 14:2). But in the sense here, it means "entranced" or "enraptured." The ]{.class-0}[KJV]{.class-2}[ translators gave an alternate translation of "taken away." In the verses in Isaiah, Lamentations, and Zechariah, the women are taken away and abused, but here, the Bridegroom's heart has been taken away ]{.class-0}[in love]{.class-2}[ by the Bride.]{.class-0}

[Proverbs 5:19--20 says, ]{.class-0}["Let her]{.class-1}[ \[]{.class-0}["the wife of thy youth"]{.class-1}[---vs. 4\]]{.class-0}[ be as the loving hind and pleasant roe; let her breasts satisfy thee at all times; and be thou RAVISHED]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-15}[always with her love. And why wilt thou, my son, be RAVISHED with a strange woman, and embrace the bosom of a stranger?"]{.class-1}

[Notice that the Bride is called ]{.class-0}["my sister, my spouse."]{.class-1}[ The idea is that when a man and woman come together and their bodies are joined in marriage (Eph. 5:31), they are not only man and wife, but in a sense, brother and sister. That is because the first man and woman who came together both had the same Father. Adam's Father was God; Eve's Father was God. When they came together, although they were husband and wife, they were also brother and sister.]{.class-0}

[That is spiritually true in a Christian marriage. When a Christian man and a Christian woman come together, you have a ]{.class-0}["brother]{.class-2}[ in Christ" marrying a ]{.class-0}["sister]{.class-2}[ in Christ." Both have the same spiritual Father: God. So the Apostle Paul says, ]{.class-0}["Have we not power to lead about A SISTER, A WIFE"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 9:5).]{.class-0}

[Now Paul uses that terminology to refer to the wife of Peter (see Matt. 8:14). Catholics call Peter the first "Pope." Well, if he was, then he was an awfully strange one, because he was ]{.class-0}[married to a wife.]{.class-2}[ The Catholic hierarchy sports a bachelor priesthood of men called "Fathers" (see Matt. 23:9), Bishops, Archbishops, Monsignors, Cardinals, and Popes; only Monks are called "Brother."]{.class-0}

[No Catholic Priest in your town calls any female member of his congregation "sister." He refers to ]{.class-0}[Nuns]{.class-2}[ as "Sisters." Catholics say those things as if they are using Christian expressions, but they aren't.]{.class-0}

[The reason they do that is because the Priest is supposed to be married to ]{.class-0}[Christ]{.class-2}[, so he doesn't get married to a ]{.class-0}[woman;]{.class-2}[ the ]{.class-0}[Nun ]{.class-2}[is supposed to be married to Christ, so ]{.class-0}[she ]{.class-2}[doesn't get married to a man. Their relationship is that they're both married in a spiritual sense but not in a physical sense in that they are considered to be married to Christ.]{.class-0}

[Now that would be fine if you were talking about a real Christian man or woman. (As one Mexican woman said when she was asked if she was a Christian: "No, I'm a ]{.class-0}[Catholic."]{.class-2}[) Every Christian woman is "married to Christ" in the sense that she is part of His Body; every Christian man is married to Christ in the sense that he is part of His Body. A Christian can be in that state and have a normal married life.]{.class-0}

[But when a Catholic talks about a Priest or Nun being "married to Christ," it's just ludicrous. It's not the real thing; it's just unbiblical, pagan nonsense. All it results in is fornication between Priests and Nuns, abortions of bastard children, homosexual Priests, Lesbian Nuns, and child-molesting Priests. ]{.class-0}[That]{.class-2}[ is Catholic "celibacy" and "marriage to Christ."]{.class-0}

[In the case of the Church, the Body of Christ, ]{.class-0}["we are members of his body, of his flesh, and of his bone"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 5:30). We are in the same relationship to Christ as Eve was to Adam (Eph. 5:32). So the Bride is addressed as ]{.class-0}["my sister, my spouse."]{.class-1}

[Back to verse 9: ]{.class-0}["thou hast ravished my heart with one of thine eyes, with one chain of thy neck."]{.class-1}[ The ]{.class-0}["one chain"]{.class-1}[ of the verse is one of the ]{.class-0}["chains of gold"]{.class-1}[ back in 1:10. Someone said that the Bridegroom was ravished by one of the Bride's eyes when she ]{.class-0}[winked]{.class-2}[ at Him. I don't know about that, but what you have here is a figure of speech known as "hyperbole": an exaggeration used for the purpose of ]{.class-0}[emphasis]{.class-2}[. A woman might be flattered to hear a man say such a thing of her, but it is hard to believe that a woman could captivate a man's heart with just one of her eyes or with one chain about her neck.]{.class-0}

But that's not the biggest problem with the text. I wonder why His love for us is so great and our love for Him is so cold? Could you honestly look the Lord in the face and say, "Lord, you've captured my heart with one of your fingers or one of your eyes"?
