Think about what the Lord had to do for you before He got you to love Him. He had to be beaten beyond recognition, spat on and mocked, crowned with thorns, and die one of the most horrible deaths devised by man---crucifixion. That's what He had to do before you ever loved Him.

[Yet He says about the Bride that she is so desirable that one of her eyes has captured His heart. That's a reference to the Christian. It's a reference to you if you're saved. That's real love, and our love for Him, I'm afraid, isn't anywhere near that good. All we can say is: ]{.class-0}["We love him, because HE FIRST LOVED US"]{.class-1}[ (1 John 4:19).]{.class-0}

"[How much better is thy love than wine!"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 10). And of course, that's the Bridegroom talking about the Bride. He says of her what she said of Him back in 1:2 (see comments under that verse).]{.class-0}

The idea, here, is that the Bride's love for the Bridegroom does Him more good, makes Him happier, thrills Him more, and is a greater blessing to Him than a bottle of wine. Now I understand how Christ's love for us could be better than wine; after all, Christ loved us when we were His enemies (Rom. 5:8--10). But what does the Lord get out of our loving Him?

[Brethren, one of the attributes of God is ]{.class-0}[self-sufficiency;]{.class-2}[ i.e., He is completely sufficient in and of Himself and needs nothing. The whole universe could blow up tomorrow, and it wouldn't affect God one way or another. He doesn't ]{.class-0}[need]{.class-2}[ fellowship with any man; before Genesis 1:1, there was perfect harmony and fellowship between the Father, the Word, and the Holy Spirit.]{.class-0}

[But God ]{.class-0}[wants]{.class-2}[ fellowship with His creation; that's why He created Adam. And that's why He made an atonement for him in Genesis 3:21. That's why God ]{.class-0}[saves ]{.class-2}[any sinner (1 John 1:3).]{.class-0}

Now, given Christ's desire for your love and fellowship, and what He went through to get it, how much love do you show Him, Christian? One of the marks of love is you like to spend time with the one you love. How much time do you spend with Him?

A famous writer who lived in the Nineteenth Century had a sickly wife who was bedridden. He was a busy man, but from time to time, he would go up to her bedroom and spend time with her. When she died, he found among her effects a diary. It had entries that read: "He didn't come to see me today; if he only knew how much I look forward to his visits" and "He spent an hour with me today; it was like heaven." Reading that diary broke his heart, and he said, "If I had only known, I would have spent more time with her."

[Now, Christian, you have no excuse. If you had no idea before, you know it now. Christ counts your love as ]{.class-0}["better\...than wine."]{.class-1}[ He wants your love and fellowship, and as a Christian, you have an obligation to love your Saviour (1 Cor. 2:9, 8:3, 16:22).]{.class-0}

"[And the smell of thine ointments than all spices."]{.class-1}[ The ]{.class-0}["ointments"]{.class-1}[ are a reference to ]{.class-0}[perfume]{.class-2}[ (see Prov. 27:9). When Esther was "purified" to be brought before King Ahasuerus, she spent a whole year being "perfumed" so she would smell good to the King. So of course, this part of verse 10 has to do with human love.]{.class-0}

[But when it comes to the relationship between Christ and the Church, there are some things you can do as a Christian to make yourself "smell good" to God. When you follow God and ]{.class-0}["walk"]{.class-1}[ in the love of God, you are likened to the ]{.class-0}["sweetsmelling savour"]{.class-1}[ of Christ's sacrifice for us (Eph. 5:1--2). When you sacrificially give to the work of the Lord, that is ]{.class-0}["an odour of a sweet smell, a sacrifice acceptable, wellpleasing to God"]{.class-1}[ (Phil. 4:18). When we witness about Jesus Christ, we are ]{.class-0}["unto God a sweet savour of Christ"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 2:14--15).]{.class-0}

"[Thy lips, O my spouse, drop as the honeycomb: honey and milk are under thy tongue"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 11).]{.class-0}

[The ]{.class-0}["honeycomb"]{.class-1}[ of the verse is associated with ]{.class-0}["words"]{.class-1}[ (Prov. 16:24), especially the words found in the Scriptures (Psa. 19:10). But notice that the ]{.class-0}["strange woman"]{.class-1}[ of Proverbs 5:3, a type of the Great Whore of Babylon (Rev. 17), can imitate the speech of the true Church. Her speech is ]{.class-0}["good words and fair speeches"]{.class-1}[ used to ]{.class-0}["deceive the hearts of the simple"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 16:18).]{.class-0}

[The real Christian's speech is ]{.class-0}["sound speech"]{.class-1}[ (Tit. 2:7) and ]{.class-0}["wholesome words"]{.class-1}[ (1 Tim. 6:3) based on ]{.class-0}[sound doctrine]{.class-2}[ and ]{.class-0}[Biblical exhortation]{.class-2}[ (1 Tim. 6:2--3; Tit. 2:7--9). To the world, that speech is not ]{.class-0}["good,"]{.class-1}[ but ]{.class-0}["rude"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 11:6) and ]{.class-0}["contemptible"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 10:10). A Christian's ]{.class-0}["speech"]{.class-1}[ may ]{.class-0}["be alway with grace,"]{.class-1}[ but it is to be ]{.class-0}["seasoned with salt"]{.class-1}[ (Col. 4:6), and salt ]{.class-0}[stings]{.class-2}[ when put in a wound.]{.class-0}

"[Honey and milk are under thy tongue"]{.class-1}[ (see 5:1). The ]{.class-0}["honey"]{.class-1}[ speaks of ]{.class-0}[sweetness,]{.class-2}[ and the ]{.class-0}["milk"]{.class-1}[ of ]{.class-0}[nourishment.]{.class-2}[ Both are pictures of the word of God (Psa. 119:103; 1 Pet. 2:2). The Christian is commanded to ]{.class-0}["speak as the oracles of God"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 4:11 and comments in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

"[And the smell of thy garments like the smell of Lebanon."]{.class-1}[ This is what the Lord says of Israel in Hosea 14:6--7.]{.class-0}

[Now, ]{.class-0}["the smell of Lebanon"]{.class-1}[ is the smell of ]{.class-0}[cedar.]{.class-2}[ Over and over again in the Old Testament, you read about ]{.class-0}["the cedars of Lebanon"]{.class-1}[ (Judg. 9:15; Psa. 29:5, 104:16; Isa. 2:13, 14:8). David's house was built out of these cedars (2 Sam. 5:11, 7:2), as were the Temple (1 Kings 5:5--10, 6:9--10, 15--20), Solomon's house in ]{.class-0}["the forest of Lebanon"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 7:2--3), and his palace and the house he built for Pharaoh's daughter (1 Kings 7:8--12).]{.class-0}

[The smell of cedar is an outdoor kind of a smell. That's why people put garments in a "cedar chest," because the smell gets on the garments. The idea, here, is that since in the context Lebanon is a picture of Heaven (vs. 8), there should be something about the Christian that brings to mind God and Heaven. That "smell" will mean different things to different people. To the saved, it's a pleasant reminder of home, but to the lost, it ]{.class-0}[stinks ]{.class-2}[(2 Cor. 2:15--16)---not everyone likes the smell of cedar.]{.class-0}

12 A garden inclosed is my sister, my spouse; a spring shut up, a fountain sealed.

13 Thy plants are an orchard of pomegranates, with pleasant fruits; camphire, with spikenard,

14 Spikenard and saffron; calamus and cinnamon, with all trees of frankincense; myrrh and aloes, with all the chief spices:

15 A fountain of gardens, a well of living waters, and streams from Lebanon.

"[A garden inclosed is my sister, my spouse"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 12). The word ]{.class-0}["garden"]{.class-1}[ indicates that what you are about to read in the passage is a picture of the Bride of Christ as the New Jerusalem (see Rev. 21:9). If there is any doubt in your mind about that, notice that Solomon lists ]{.class-0}[twelve ]{.class-2}["plants"]{.class-1}[ found in this ]{.class-0}["garden."]{.class-1}

[1. ]{.class-0}["Pomegranates"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13).]{.class-0}

[2. ]{.class-0}["Pleasant fruits"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13).]{.class-0}

[3. ]{.class-0}["Camphire"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13).]{.class-0}

[4. ]{.class-0}["Spikenard"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13).]{.class-0}

[5. ]{.class-0}["Spikenard"]{.class-1}[ again (vs. 14).]{.class-0}

[6. ]{.class-0}["Saffron"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14).]{.class-0}

[7. ]{.class-0}["Calamus"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14).]{.class-0}

[8. ]{.class-0}["Cinnamon"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14).]{.class-0}

[9. ]{.class-0}["Frankincense"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14).]{.class-0}

[10. ]{.class-0}["Myrrh"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14).]{.class-0}

[11. ]{.class-0}["Aloes"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14).]{.class-0}

[12. ]{.class-0}["All the chief spices"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14).]{.class-0}

[That's a picture of ]{.class-0}["the tree of life, which is in the midst of the paradise of God"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 2:7). That ]{.class-0}["paradise"]{.class-1}[ is the New Jerusalem (Rev. 21:2--3 cf. 22:1--2). ]{.class-0}["Paradise"]{.class-1}[ is a Persian word which means "an animal garden" (see comments on Esth. 1:5 in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

[In the New Jerusalem, there is the River of Life flowing out of the throne of God (Rev. 22:1), so in the ]{.class-0}["garden"]{.class-1}[ in this passage, you have ]{.class-0}["a fountain of gardens, a well of living waters, and streams from Lebanon"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 15). The ]{.class-0}["garden"]{.class-1}[ here is ]{.class-0}["inclosed"]{.class-1}[ just as the New Jerusalem is ]{.class-0}["inclosed"]{.class-1}[ by ]{.class-0}["a wall great and high"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 21:12). The whole passage is a picture of New Jerusalem.]{.class-0}

[Now, from a practical standpoint, notice that the Bride is ]{.class-0}["inclosed," "shut up," ]{.class-1}[and ]{.class-0}["sealed."]{.class-1}[ Proverbs 5:15 commands the husband to ]{.class-0}["Drink waters out of thine own cistern, and running water out of thine own well."]{.class-1}[ The man is to be faithful to his wife, and she is to be faithful to him. Proverbs 5:17 says, ]{.class-0}["Let them be only thine own, and not strangers' with thee."]{.class-1}

[From a spiritual standpoint, the Christian is to remain faithful to his Lord. Christian, when you become a friend of this sinful world by conforming to it (Rom. 12:2), you are committing ]{.class-0}[spiritual adultery]{.class-2}[ (James 4:4): you are "stepping out" on your Husband.]{.class-0}

[Doctrinally speaking, a Christian is ]{.class-0}["inclosed"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:28--29), he is ]{.class-0}["shut up"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 8:38--39; 1 Cor. 1:8; Phil. 1:6), and he is ]{.class-0}["sealed"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 4:30) so that he can never lose his salvation no matter what he does (1 Cor. 5:5; 2 Tim. 2:13). But from a practical, spiritual standpoint, you can "defile the temple" with idols (2 Cor. 6:16) until God has to destroy it (1 Cor. 3:17).]{.class-0}

[Verses 13--14 list the ]{.class-0}["plants"]{.class-1}[ found in this garden, so we will take them one at a time.]{.class-0}

"[Pomegranates"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13). We have discussed the promegranate under verse 3. The pomegranate is a large fruit about the size of a small grapefruit. It has a leathery skin with a thing like a crown at the top of it. When you break into it, it has a bunch of things like the individual parts of a berry, only bigger and juicier. So in the sense that it is several fruits in one fruit, it is a type of the Body of Christ.]{.class-0}

"[Pleasant fruits"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13). Those fruits are not identified, but they could include fruits like grapes, figs, dates, and apples (see Joel 1:12). Among those, the grape vine is probably what's referred to here. Amos 5:11 talks about ]{.class-0}["pleasant vineyards."]{.class-1}

[Spiritually speaking, these ]{.class-0}["pleasant fruits"]{.class-1}[ might have some reference to the Scriptures. Song 7:13 talks about ]{.class-0}["all manner of pleasant fruits, NEW AND OLD,"]{.class-1}[ and Matthew 13:52 says, ]{.class-0}["every scribe which is instructed unto the kingdom of heaven is like unto a man that is an householder, which bringeth forth out of his treasure things NEW AND OLD."]{.class-1}[ The scribes copied and taught the Scriptures.]{.class-0}

"[Camphire"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13). This is the henna plant we discussed under 1:14.]{.class-0}

"[Spikenard"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13 and again in vs. 14). We have discussed this perfume under 1:12. Here it is used as synonymous with the plant from which it comes, a plant the Arabs called ]{.class-0}[sunbul Hindi]{.class-2}[---meaning the "Indian spike"---which grows in the Himalaya mountains.]{.class-0}

"[Saffron"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). This is the only place the word appears in Scripture. ]{.class-0}["Saffron"]{.class-1}[ is a spice taken from the crocus plant.]{.class-0}

"[Calamus"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). The word appears three times in Scripture: here; Exodus 30:23; and Ezekiel 27:19. It was one of the ingredients used in the ]{.class-0}["holy anointing oil"]{.class-1}[ the Lord commanded Moses to make (Exod. 30:22--25). ]{.class-0}["Sweet calamus"]{.class-1}[ is called ]{.class-0}["sweet cane"]{.class-1}[ in Isaiah 43:24 and Jeremiah 6:20.]{.class-0}

"[Cinnamon"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). A common spice today that was grown only in India and China in Solomon's time. It also was one of the ingredients in the ]{.class-0}["holy anointing oil"]{.class-1}[ (Exod. 30:23).]{.class-0}

"[All trees of frankincense"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). Here is the famous second gift of the wise men to the Christ child (Matt. 2:11). It's the ]{.class-0}[resin ]{.class-2}[from a tree native to Arabia. It was the main ingredient in the incense used in the Tabernacle (Exod. 30:34) and the Temple (1 Chron. 9:29; Neh. 13:5, 9) at the altar of incense (Luke 1:9--11). It is connected with prayer (Psa. 141:2; Rev. 5:8, 8:3) and speaks of Christ as our High Priest (Heb. 3:1).]{.class-0}

The song says: "Frankincense to offer have I, Incense owns a Deity nigh; Prayer and praising, all men raising, Worship Him, God on high."

"[Myrrh"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). See our comments under 1:13. Myrrh came from the gum of the acacia tree. It too was used in the ]{.class-0}["holy anointing oil"]{.class-1}[ (Exod. 30:23).]{.class-0}

"[Aloes"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). The ]{.class-0}["aloes"]{.class-1}[ of the Bible aren't like the "aloes" that you buy at the drugstore for burns. It is the wood from the ]{.class-0}["lign aloes"]{.class-1}[ trees (see Num. 24:6); specifically the gum extracted from the wood and turned into a perfume (Prov. 7:17). It was used along with myrrh to embalm bodies (see John 19:39).]{.class-0}

"[All the chief spices"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). The spices listed in Scripture, outside of the ones given above, are ]{.class-0}["cassia"]{.class-1}[ (Exod. 30:24) and ]{.class-0}["stacte," "onycha,"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["galbanum"]{.class-1}[ (Exod. 30:34).]{.class-0}

[Verse 15:]{.class-0}[ "A fountain of gardens, a well of living waters, and streams from Lebanon."]{.class-1}[ That ]{.class-0}["fountain"]{.class-1}[ and those ]{.class-0}["living waters"]{.class-1}[ are references to the Lord Himself. In Jeremiah 2:13 and 17:13, the Lord is called ]{.class-0}["the fountain of living waters."]{.class-1}

[Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["But whosoever drinketh of the water that I shall give him shall never thirst; but the water that I shall give him shall be in him a well of water springing up into everlasting life"]{.class-1}[ (John 4:14).]{.class-0}

That's a reference to Jesus Christ indwelling the believer in the person of the Holy Spirit (cf. Col. 1:27). Look at John 7:37--39.

"[In the last day, that great day of the feast, Jesus stood and cried, saying, If any man thirst, let him come unto me, and drink. He that believeth on me, as the scripture hath said, out of his belly shall flow rivers of living water. (But this spake he of the Spirit, which they that believe on him should receive: for the Holy Ghost was not yet given; because that Jesus was not yet glorified.)"]{.class-1}

[Prophetically, the ]{.class-0}["living waters" ]{.class-1}[are a reference to the river that flows out of Jerusalem during Christ's Millennial reign (Zech. 14:8). This river comes out of the Millennial temple and flows into the Dead Sea where it brings life back to that body of water (Ezek. 47:1--12). That's not a reference to the "River of Life" in the New Jerusalem, but it is a picture of it.]{.class-0}

16 Awake, O north wind; and come, thou south; blow upon my garden, that the spices thereof may flow out. Let my beloved come into his garden, and eat his pleasant fruits.

The paragraph mark at verse 16 marks a change of speaker: now the Bride is speaking (or at least in the last half of the verse). What you have is a prayer by the Bride for the return of her Lover.

[Now I can't get all of the similitudes worked out in the verse, but they're obviously a reference to some aspect of Christ's Second Coming. The reference could be to the Rapture or the Advent, or there could be a double application to both. We discussed that ]{.class-0}["awake"]{.class-1}[ back in 2:7. That could be a reference to either the Rapture of the Church or the post-Tribulation rapture of the Jewish and Gentile saints (cf. Isa. 26:19). Of course, neither one of those interpretations are without their problems.]{.class-0}

If we make it a reference to the Rapture of the Church, what are those north and south winds there, and what do they have to do with the catching out of the Bride of Christ?

[Over in John 3:8, the Lord likens the Holy Spirit to wind. ]{.class-0}["The wind bloweth where it listeth, and thou hearest the sound thereof, but canst not tell whence it cometh, and whither it goeth: so is every one that is born of the Spirit."]{.class-1}[ Both the Greek and the Hebrew words for ]{.class-0}[spirit]{.class-2}[ have to do with ]{.class-0}[wind.]{.class-2}

[So maybe what you have in Song 4:16 is a reference to the work of the Holy Spirit in the Rapture. When the Apostle John (a picture of the Church) is caught up to Heaven in Revelation 4:1--2, he ]{.class-0}["heard as it were of a trumpet talking"]{.class-1}[; there's that ]{.class-0}["sound thereof"]{.class-1}[ from John 3:8.]{.class-0}

[Then the passage goes on to say ]{.class-0}["immediately I was in the spirit,"]{.class-1}[ and John's in Heaven before the throne. That ]{.class-0}["in the spirit"]{.class-1}[ isn't a reference to being in the Holy Spirit as part of the Body of Christ (1 Cor. 12:13); it doesn't even mean being ]{.class-0}["out of the body"]{.class-1}[ as Paul was in 2 Corinthians 12:1--4. At the Rapture, the spirit of a Christian is placed into a brand new body like Christ's (1 Cor. 15:51--53; Phil. 3:20--21). It's talking about a miraculous transference of the believer by the Holy Spirit from the earth to the third heaven (see comments on Rev. 1:10 in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

[Now, a similar thing happens in the post-Tribulation rapture. In Ezekiel 37:9, Ezekiel is told to ]{.class-0}["Prophesy unto the wind\...and say to the wind, Thus saith the Lord GOD; Come from the four winds, O breath, and breathe upon these slain, that they may live."]{.class-1}[ When he does, a bunch of dead Jews come back to life.]{.class-0}

[That's what happens in the rapture at the end of the Tribulation. Isaiah wrote, ]{.class-0}["Thy dead men shall live, together with my dead body shall they arise, Awake and sing, ye that dwell in dust: for thy dew is as the dew of herbs, and the earth shall cast out the dead"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 26:19).]{.class-0}

So the passage in the Song of Solomon could have application to either rapture, but for now, we will apply it in the typology of the book as being to the Bride of Christ.

"[Blow upon my garden, that the spices thereof may flow out."]{.class-1}[ The picture is a breeze blowing through a spice garden and wafting the fragrance out. When the Church leaves this world, any influence for good it might have had is taken with it, and the Devil is given free rein to do what he wants. As the old saying goes: "When we nuts are gone, you squirrels will be 'up a tree.'"]{.class-0}

"[Let my beloved come into his garden, and eat his pleasant fruits."]{.class-1}[ There is some question as to whether the first part of the verse is spoken by the Bride or the Bridegroom; notice the change from ]{.class-0}["my garden"]{.class-1}[ to ]{.class-0}["his garden."]{.class-1}[ Whatever the case, the second half of the verse is definitely spoken by the Bride.]{.class-0}

[The passage is speaking of the proper relationship between a man and his wife in the sense of enjoying marital love and fellowship. As far as the Church is concerned, Christ says,]{.class-0}[ "Behold, I stand at the door, and knock: if any man hear my voice, and open the door, I will come into him, and will sup with him, and he with me"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 3:20). That ]{.class-0}[wasn't]{.class-2}[ an invitation to a lost man to receive Christ, although you can use it that way in personal work. That was written to a Christian to partake of fellowship with his Lord.]{.class-0}

[What that verse describes in a ]{.class-0}[spiritual]{.class-2}[ sense, you will one day experience in a ]{.class-0}[literal]{.class-2}[ sense. If you are saved, someday when you get drawn up to Glory, you are going to sit down with your Saviour, around the same table, and enjoy the same food together (Rev. 19:9).]{.class-0}

[]{#section-0_1_c09fd6105f68857a_67df.xhtml}

CHAPTER 5

5:1 I am come into my garden, my sister, my spouse: I have gathered my myrrh with my spice; I have eaten my honeycomb with my honey; I have drunk my wine with my milk: eat, O friends; drink, yea, drink abundantly, O beloved.

[Verse 1 is the Bridegroom speaking to the Bride. He continues the similitude that he began back in 4:12 of likening the Bride to a garden that bears fruit. Psalm 128:3 says, ]{.class-0}["Thy wife shall be as a fruitful vine by the sides of thine house: thy children like olive plants round about the table."]{.class-1}

A husband is to care for his wife as a husbandman cares for a garden. A garden needs to be tended and cultivated and taken care of. In a Christian marriage, the husband is to do that through the Scriptures. When the Bible speaks of watering a garden so that it brings forth fruit, it is a similitude of ministering the word.

"[For as the rain cometh down, and the snow from heaven, and returneth not thither, but watereth the earth, and maketh it bring forth and bud, that it may give seed to the sower, and bread to the eater: So shall my word be that goeth forth out of my mouth: it shall not return unto me void, but it shall accomplish that which I please, and it shall prosper in the thing whereto I sent it"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 55:10--11).]{.class-0}

[A husband should read the Bible to his wife and minister the word to her. The Apostle Paul commanded the women in the church at Corinth: ]{.class-0}["And if they ]{.class-1}[\[the women\]]{.class-0}[ will learn any thing, let them ask their husbands at home"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 14:35). A Christian woman is to be under the teaching authority of her husband, and a Christian husband ought to know the Scriptures well enough to answer his wife's questions.]{.class-0}

[It is like watering a garden. The man takes care of his ]{.class-0}["garden"]{.class-1}[ when he ministers the word to his spouse. Just as a garden can't bear fruit without water, so a Christian wife can't bear fruit without the word.]{.class-0}

[Christ said: ]{.class-0}["Now ye are clean through the word which I have spoken unto you. Abide in me, and I in you. As the branch cannot bear fruit of itself, except it abide in the vine; no more can ye, except ye abide in me" ]{.class-1}[(John 15:3--4).]{.class-0}

[Notice that the Lord equates abiding in Him to bearing fruit with His ]{.class-0}["word."]{.class-1}[ Look at verses 7 and 8 in John 15.]{.class-0}

"[If ye abide in me, and my words abide in you, ye shall ask what ye will, and it shall be done unto you. Herein is my Father glorified, that ye bear much fruit; so shall ye be my disciples"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:7--8).]{.class-0}

[Now Christian man, a woman realizes what your responsibility is as the spiritual leader of the family whether you do or not. There is something in a woman's nature that realizes she is ]{.class-0}["the weaker vessel"]{.class-1}[ (see 1 Pet. 3:7 and comments in that Commentary), no matter how much she may pretend otherwise. A woman wants to be cared for, and a Christian woman wants her husband to be the spiritual leader in the family and minister the word of God to her. And if the husband will take his responsibility seriously and read the Bible to his wife and pray with her, he will cause her to bear fruit as a Christian.]{.class-0}

Now, in verse 1, the Bridegroom is responding to the invitation of the Bride at the end of chapter four. The whole verse is a picture of the marriage being consummated. It is pictured as gathering spices, as eating, and as drinking.

[First he says, ]{.class-0}["I have gathered my myrrh with my spice."]{.class-1}[ You will remember that both were found in the garden back in 4:14. That is where Christ gets His perfumes when He returns in 3:6.]{.class-0}

[Then he says, ]{.class-0}["I have eaten my honeycomb with my honey."]{.class-1}[ That's a reference to Jesus Christ. Concerning Christ, Isaiah 7:15 says, ]{.class-0}["Butter and honey shall he eat, that he may know to refuse the evil, and choose the good."]{.class-1}[ That's Jesus as a human child learning the Scriptures so that He would ]{.class-0}["know to refuse the evil, and choose the good."]{.class-1}[ When Christ answered the Devil's temptations with ]{.class-0}["It is written,"]{.class-1}[ that was stuff He had learned as a child.]{.class-0}

"[I have drunk my wine with my milk."]{.class-1}[ Undoubtedly the ]{.class-0}["wine"]{.class-1}[ here is ]{.class-0}[new wine,]{.class-2}[ for the Lord says it's ]{.class-0}["MY wine"]{.class-1}[ (see comments on John 2:3--10 in that Commentary). In the Scriptures, "new wine" can be a picture of the blood of Christ (Matt. 26:28--29 and comments in that Commentary), or it can be a picture of the Holy Spirit (Matt. 9:17 and comments). The milk, of course, is a picture of the word of God (1 Pet. 2:2; Heb. 5:12--13).]{.class-0}

[Practically and spiritually, we can say that the passage is speaking about fellowship: the fellowship between a man and his wife, and the fellowship between the Lord and us. In a Christian marriage, a man ought to enjoy fellowship with his wife. That fellowship ought to be sweet as honey. It ought to ]{.class-0}[satisfy]{.class-2}[ both of them; it should]{.class-0}[ nourish]{.class-2}[ and ]{.class-0}[sustain]{.class-2}[ them.]{.class-0}

[The ]{.class-0}["wine"]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-15}[speaks of ]{.class-0}[joy]{.class-2}[ in the marriage (Judg. 9:13; Eccl. 10:19). The Christian home should be a happy home. ]{.class-0}["Milk"]{.class-1}[ speaks of a home in which the love between a husband and wife grows and becomes strong.]{.class-0}

[Peter wrote, ]{.class-0}["Likewise, ye husbands, dwell with them according to knowledge, giving honour unto the wife, as unto the weaker vessel, and as being heirs together of the grace of life; that your prayers be not hindered"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 3:7).]{.class-0}

Paul tells the husbands not to be bitter against their wives (Col. 3:19).

[Now I know circumstances don't always work out that way, but a Christian marriage should be marked by ]{.class-0}[Biblical]{.class-2}[ marital fellowship. That fellowship consists of the wife learning to love her husband, submitting herself to him, and being a help to him (Tit. 2:4; Col. 3:18). It consists of the husband loving the wife, honoring her, and nourishing and cherishing her just as Christ does for us (Eph. 5:25--29).]{.class-0}

[Above all, both the husband and the wife need to keep in mind that each of them belongs to the Lord. They are "brother and sister" in Christ; they ought to treat each other as such. If a Christian husband and a Christian wife can treat other Christians better than they treat ]{.class-0}[each other,]{.class-2}[ something is wrong in that marriage and needs to be fixed.]{.class-0}

[From a spiritual point of view, verse 1 is a picture of our fellowship with Jesus Christ. Look at the end of the verse: ]{.class-0}["Eat, O friends."]{.class-1}

[The Lord told His disciples:]{.class-0}[ "Greater love hath no man than this, that a man lay down his life for his friends. Ye are my friends, if ye do whatsoever I command you. Henceforth I call you not servants; for the servant knoweth not what his lord doeth: but I have called you friends; for all things that I have heard of my Father I have made known unto you"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:13--15).]{.class-0}

If you are saved, you are saved because the Lord treated you as one of His friends and died for you. Well, if the Lord treated you with friendship, you should return the favor and have fellowship with Him.

[Back to verse 1: ]{.class-0}["drink, yea, drink abundantly, O beloved."]{.class-1}[ Paul said that Christ ]{.class-0}["hath made us accepted in the beloved"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 1:6). The Lord said,]{.class-0}[ "I am come that they might have life, and that they might have it more abundantly"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:10).]{.class-0}

[Note in Isaiah 55:1 that the ]{.class-0}["wine"]{.class-1}[ and the ]{.class-0}["milk"]{.class-1}[ of Song 5:1 are offered freely to anyone who wants to partake.]{.class-0}

"[Ho, every one that thirsteth, come ye to the waters, and he that hath no money; come ye, buy, and eat; yea, come, buy wine and milk without money and without price."]{.class-1}

[The price of the blood atonement was paid by the Lord Himself, but to you, eternal life is a ]{.class-0}[free gift ]{.class-2}[(Rom. 5:18, 6:23). When the Lord feeds you with ]{.class-0}["the sincere milk of the word"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 2:2), it doesn't cost you anything but your time. In Isaiah 55:1, if you want the water of life, if you want ]{.class-0}["the pure blood of the grape"]{.class-1}[ (Deut. 32:14), if you want ]{.class-0}["the sincere milk of the word,"]{.class-1}[ all you have to be is ]{.class-0}[thirsty.]{.class-2}[ In addition to that, you have to ]{.class-0}[come]{.class-2}[ of your own free will and ]{.class-0}[drink.]{.class-2}

Now, I understand the benefits I get from all of that. When I read the Bible, it does something for me. When I pray, it does something for me. I get a greater satisfaction from fellowship with the Lord than I get from a good hunting or fishing trip.

[But what I can't understand is what the Lord gets out of all that. How does it satisfy ]{.class-0}[Him]{.class-2}[? Evidently it must, for in Song 5:1, He comes to the garden first, He makes all of the preparations, and then He invites us to be with Him.]{.class-0}

[In Psalm 34:1, David wrote, ]{.class-0}["I will bless the LORD at all times."]{.class-1}[ That doesn't just mean that he will ]{.class-0}[say]{.class-2}[ "bless the LORD."]{.class-1}[ It means that he will actually ]{.class-0}[do]{.class-2}[ something to make the Lord "happy."]{.class-0}

If you want to make the Lord happy, have fellowship with Him; He enjoys it. I must confess that I don't know why, but He does.

2 I sleep, but my heart waketh: it is the voice of my beloved that knocketh, saying, Open to me, my sister, my love, my dove, my undefiled: for my head is filled with dew, and my locks with the drops of the night.

3 I have put off my coat; how shall I put it on? I have washed my feet; how shall I defile them?

4 My beloved put in his hand by the hole of the door, and my bowels were moved for him.

5 I rose up to open to my beloved; and my hands dropped with myrrh, and my fingers with sweet smelling myrrh, upon the handles of the lock.

6 I opened to my beloved; but my beloved had withdrawn himself, and was gone: my soul failed when he spake: I sought him, but I could not find him; I called him, but he gave me no answer.

7 The watchmen that went about the city found me, they smote me, they wounded me; the keepers of the walls took away my veil from me.

[Verse 2 introduces a problem passage. Up to this point, the Bride has been a picture of the Church, the Body of Christ. But unlike the passage back in chapter 2 verses 1--5, the woman seeks the Bridegroom but ]{.class-0}[does not find Him.]{.class-2}[ That being the case, then the woman in the passage can't ]{.class-0}[doctrinally]{.class-2}[ be the Church.]{.class-0}

[Brethren, if you are saved, you are ]{.class-0}[part]{.class-2}[ of Jesus Christ. You ]{.class-0}[can't]{.class-2}[ seek Him and not find Him. He's ]{.class-0}[inside]{.class-2}[ of you, and you are ]{.class-0}[inside]{.class-2}[ of Him.]{.class-0}

[Now let's review where we have been so we can see where we stand doctrinally. In chapter 1, there is a picture of salvation. In chapter 2, there is a picture of the Rapture: the Bridegroom tells the Bride to ]{.class-0}["rise up\...and come away"]{.class-1}[ (2:10), and up she goes. In chapter 3 (vss. 6--10), there is a picture of the Advent: the Bridegroom comes out of the wilderness with an armed troop just as Christ will at the Second Coming, and at the end of the chapter, the ]{.class-0}["son of David"]{.class-1}[ is crowned King just as Christ will be at the Advent. In chapter 4, the Bride is with the Bridegroom up in Heaven, having communion and looking down on what's taking place in the Tribulation.]{.class-0}

[So when you get to the paragraph mark at 5:2, if you want to make a doctrinal application, you will have to do one of two things; both ways will have the woman ]{.class-0}[down here on earth]{.class-2}[. Either you can make the woman a picture of the Jews in the Tribulation, which is the best doctrinal application you can make, or you can make a practical application to the Christian under conviction.]{.class-0}

"[I sleep, but my heart waketh"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 2). That is the heart seeking something. It's aware even though the body is asleep. That's real love. It is the kind of love that when the body quits, the heart doesn't.]{.class-0}

"[It is the voice of my beloved that knocketh."]{.class-1}[ Then the Lord's voice speaks to your heart, not your head. That's the purpose of memorizing Scripture---to get what God says in your heart.]{.class-0}

[Proverbs 4:4, ]{.class-0}["He taught me also, and said unto me, Let thine HEART retain my WORDS."]{.class-1}

[Psalm 119:11, ]{.class-0}["Thy WORD have I hid in mine HEART, that I might not sin against thee."]{.class-1}

[Jeremiah said, ]{.class-0}["His WORD was in mine HEART as a burning fire"]{.class-1}[ (Jer. 20:9).]{.class-0}

[The Lord told Ezekiel: ]{.class-0}["Son of man, all my WORDS that I shall speak unto thee receive in thine HEART, and hear with thine ears"]{.class-1}[ (Ezek. 3:10). The Lord wants you to listen to Him with your heart first, and ]{.class-0}[then ]{.class-2}[with your ears.]{.class-0}

[In speaking of the Gospel, the Apostle Paul says, ]{.class-0}["The WORD is nigh thee, even in thy mouth, and in thy HEART: that is, the word of faith, which we preach"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 10:8). That's what Moses said about the Law (Deut. 30:14).]{.class-0}

[So when God speaks to you through the Scriptures, He's aiming at your ]{.class-0}[heart]{.class-2}[. He may have to get them there through the eye gate or the ear gate, but the ]{.class-0}[heart ]{.class-2}[is where He wants them.]{.class-0}

"[It is the voice of my beloved that knocketh, saying, Open to me, my sister, my love, my dove, my undefiled."]{.class-1}[ Christ said, ]{.class-0}["Behold, I stand at the door, and knock: if any man hear my voice, and open the door, I will come in to him"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 3:20). That was said to the Laodicean church right before the Rapture (Rev. 4:1).]{.class-0}

[Notice in verse 2 that it is the ]{.class-0}["voice"]{.class-1}[ that knocks. There is a similar construction in Genesis 3:8---]{.class-0}["And they heard the VOICE of the LORD God WALKING in the garden."]{.class-1}[ In both of those passages, ]{.class-0}["the voice"]{.class-1}[ of God is given human attributes as if it had hands and feet.]{.class-0}

[Back to 5:2, ]{.class-0}["for my head is filled with dew, and my locks with the drops of the night."]{.class-1}[ The picture is Christ coming to someone at nighttime.]{.class-0}

[Notice that the Bridegroom had spent the night outdoors. His hair is soaked with dew. That was typical of the Lord at His First Advent. In John 7:53, the Bible says that ]{.class-0}["every man went unto his own house,"]{.class-1}[ but when John 8:1 continues the narrative, it says, ]{.class-0}["Jesus went unto the mount of Olives."]{.class-1}[ While everyone else was going home to a nice warm bed, the Lord was sleeping outdoors in Gethsemane. He said one time,]{.class-0}[ "Foxes have holes, and birds of the air have nests; but the Son of man hath not where to lay his head"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 9:58; Matt. 8:20). Christ slept outdoors at night.]{.class-0}

[Now, the Bridegroom is addressing the Bride: ]{.class-0}["My sister, my love, my dove, my undefiled."]{.class-1}[ That is the Bride of Christ in 6:9. In that verse she is called ]{.class-0}["the only one of her mother"]{.class-1}[: that's the ]{.class-0}["one body"]{.class-1}[ of Ephesians 4:4 and 1 Corinthians 12:13. And yet, what you are about to read in verses 3--6 ]{.class-0}[can't possibly]{.class-2}[ be the Bride of Christ doctrinally because a Christian can't lose the Lord and be unable to find Him (Rom. 8:38--39). So let's spiritualize the passage to apply it to the Bride of Christ.]{.class-0}

[Verse 2:]{.class-0}[ "I sleep."]{.class-1}[ You can apply that to a Christian: Christians can "go to sleep at the wheel," spiritually speaking. Matthew 13:25 says, ]{.class-0}["while men slept,]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[his enemy came and sowed tares among the wheat."]{.class-1}[ In that verse, the Christians are not only the wheat, but the ]{.class-0}["men"]{.class-1}[ who ]{.class-0}["slept."]{.class-1}

[Paul told the Thessalonian Christians: ]{.class-0}["Therefore let us not sleep, as do others; but let us watch and be sober. For they that sleep sleep in the night; and they that be drunken are drunken in the night"]{.class-1}[ (1 Thess. 5:6--7). A Christian can go to sleep, spiritually, to the point where he has to be woken up (Eph. 5:14).]{.class-0}

"[I sleep, but my heart waketh"]{.class-1}[: she's saved, but her spiritual condition is not operating. Being "asleep" doesn't change the Christian's status concerning his salvation (1 Thess. 5:10).]{.class-0}

"[It is the voice of my beloved."]{.class-1}[ Then it's a saved person who recognizes when his Lord speaks to him. Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["My sheep hear my voice, and I know them, and they follow me"]{.class-1}[ (John 10:27).]{.class-0}

[So if you apply verse 2 ]{.class-0}[spiritually ]{.class-2}[to the Church, it is a picture of a Christian asleep ]{.class-0}[spiritually ]{.class-2}[in the night of the last days right before the Second Coming. The Lord comes knocking at the door of his heart seeking fellowship just as He does to the Laodicean church in Revelation 3:20.]{.class-0}

[Verse 3, the Bride talking:]{.class-0}[ "I have put off my coat; how shall I put it on? I have washed my feet; how shall I defile them?"]{.class-1}[ The woman tells the man: "Well, I've retired for the night. How can I get up and go back to work? I've washed my feet, and if I get up and go back out in the streets, I'll get my feet dirty again."]{.class-0}

[The picture is a Christian retiring ]{.class-0}[before ]{.class-2}[it's time to retire. It is also a type of a Christian who uses the world as an ]{.class-0}[alibi ]{.class-2}[to quit working.]{.class-0}

[Now what do I mean by that? Well, the Bible says, ]{.class-0}["How beautiful upon the mountains are the feet of him that bringeth good tidings, that publisheth peace; that bringeth good tidings of good, that publisheth salvation"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 52:7 cf. Rom. 10:15). The Christian is to have his ]{.class-0}["feet shod with the preparation of the gospel of peace"]{.class-1}[ and to be going ]{.class-0}["into the streets and lanes of the city"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 14:21) to get people saved.]{.class-0}

[But the Christian in 5:3 has taken off his shoes and washed his feet. In the Orient, a person takes off his shoes when he enters a house. In ancient times, because of the dirt roads, a person would also wash his feet so as not to get dirt, dust, and mud all over his house. So the spiritual typology here is a Christian who has taken off his Gospel shoes and ]{.class-0}[stopped witnessing]{.class-2}[ before his Lord's return.]{.class-0}

[Moreover, the reason he has stopped going out and witnessing is because he doesn't want to ]{.class-0}["defile"]{.class-1}[ himself. So he sequesters himself away like a Monk or Nun. He's quit hanging out in the world, and he's thoroughly consecrated and completely separated, and ]{.class-0}[he's not worth a dime.]{.class-2}

[Brethren, if you are going to reach people for Jesus Christ, you are going to have to get out in that world and rub shoulders with them. That doesn't mean you have to partake of their sin, but you have to be around them, and if you are around them, you are bound to get defiled somehow. You'll hear their filthy music; you'll see them half-dressed; you'll hear their cussing and dirty talk; you'll see their pornographic pictures. You can't be around a bunch of lost sinners without being ]{.class-0}[exposed ]{.class-2}[to their sins. A Christian gets defiled in his pilgrim walk through this world; sure he does. But there's a big difference between getting your feet dirty and wallowing in the mud hole with the pigs.]{.class-0}

Listen! when Hugh Pyle led me to Christ in the radio studio of WEAR in Pensacola, I cussed all the way through "the sinner's prayer." You don't think that wasn't defiling to a man like Hugh Pyle who never drank anything stronger than buttermilk? Sure it was, but he didn't let it shake him. He just "considered the source" and questioned me to see if I had genuinely received Christ.

[Brethren, there's nothing wrong with personal separation, but you can't be so separated that you lose all contact with lost sinners. You have to remember that when you separate yourself for the Lord's work, the Lord's work is in ]{.class-0}["the highways and hedges"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 14:23), not the monastery or the hermitage. You can't hide behind ten-foot fences with razor wire at the top and a guardhouse at the gate.]{.class-0}

So the Bridegroom comes in the night seeking communion, seeking fellowship, and the Bride has retired. The lesson for the Christian is not to retire too early.

[There are ]{.class-0}[flat-tired]{.class-2}[ Christians, ]{.class-0}[rubber-tired]{.class-2}[ Christians,]{.class-0}[ just plain tired]{.class-2}[ Christians, and ]{.class-0}["re-tired"]{.class-2}[ Christians. A retired Christian quits before it's quitting time.]{.class-0}

My experience in the ministry is that good Christians in the local church tend to serve for about twenty years and then they begin to reduce their service back to just church attendance and giving. But that's not the way Christian service is supposed to work.

Do you know how old Moses was when God called him? He was eighty years old. If he had retired at 62, he never would have led Israel out of Egypt.

[Now I'll grant you that he lived another forty years to be 120, but still, two-thirds of his life was over before God called him. If you allow a life span of seventy years today (Psa. 90:10), that would mean a ministry would ]{.class-0}[begin]{.class-2}[ at 46. My ministry didn't "take off" until after I was 62 (after 1984).]{.class-0}

[Verse 3: ]{.class-0}["My beloved put in his hand by the hole of the door."]{.class-1}[ In ancient times, the latch of a door was on the ]{.class-0}[inside:]{.class-2}[ it was a bar across the inside of a door. In the door was a small hole through which someone on the outside could reach and lift up the bar unless it was secured by a pin. The old pioneer homes in America had a variation of that: it was known as a "latch-string." A piece of buckskin was tied around the bar and strung through a small hole at the top of the door so that it hung outside. If the latch-string was outside the door, a visitor was welcome to pull it to lift the bar and come on in.]{.class-0}

In the case here, the woman had secured the bar with a pin so the man could not lift the bar. That would require her to get out of bed to let him in.

[Salmon Warner has a famous picture of Jesus knocking at a door. There's no handle on the door. The idea is that Christ can't come in unless ]{.class-0}[you ]{.class-2}[let Him in.]{.class-0}

"[My bowels were moved for him."]{.class-1}[ We have discussed in many of our commentaries how medical doctors have taken the word ]{.class-0}["bowels"]{.class-1}[ and confined it to a bodily function of the lower viscera. The original meaning of the word is the ]{.class-0}[inside]{.class-2}[ of something, like the bowels of a ship. So the ]{.class-0}["bowels"]{.class-1}[ of a man refer to the inside of his body cavity. That would ]{.class-0}[include ]{.class-2}[his heart, lungs, stomach, liver, etc.; not just his ]{.class-0}[colon.]{.class-2}

Now I know the doctors didn't make that change with the intention of getting people to think the Bible has smutty stuff in it. All it is, is what we call "tradesman's terminology": words made up or used in a way peculiar to a certain profession. It's just medical talk.

But it is typical of how the Devil perverts the word of God to get folks to turn up their noses at it. I can think of about five words, off hand, that the Devil has seen to it that if you read those words from the pulpit, you will get a bunch of giggling in the congregation because they think you said something "dirty."

[The most recent one is the word ]{.class-0}["gay."]{.class-2}[ You can't talk about ]{.class-0}["gay clothing"]{.class-1}[ (James 2:3) without everyone thinking about a Frisco faggot or a crossdresser. The word ]{.class-0}[gay]{.class-2}[ has nothing to do at all with being a ]{.class-0}[queer]{.class-2}[. That's just what the news media brainwashed you to think it meant.]{.class-0}

[The word ]{.class-0}[gay]{.class-2}[ means "bright," "happy." If you're feeling ]{.class-0}[gay,]{.class-2}[ you're feeling ]{.class-0}[happy.]{.class-2}[ "Queers" are some of the most miserable, depressed, egotistical people you will ever meet; they aren't happy. That's why they take drugs and demand you accept their "lifestyle."]{.class-0}

[When the Christmas song says "Don we now our ]{.class-0}[gay apparel,"]{.class-2}[ it's not talking about dressing up like a double-breasted "fink." It's talking about putting on your ]{.class-0}[best clothes]{.class-2}[ to go to a party.]{.class-0}

Every Memorial Day weekend the sex perverts descend on Pensacola Beach. One year a Baptist church here in town got some of its people to stand out on the turn-off to the beach with a big banner that read "Remember When Gay Meant Happy?". The perverts just threw a fit over that sign and cried "hate speech!" and raised a big stink.

[That sign didn't say anything about "hating" faggots; it didn't say anything about them being sex perverts; it didn't say anything about them being ]{.class-0}["sinners before the LORD exceedingly"]{.class-1}[ (Gen. 13:13); and it didn't say anything about their dirty, rotten, filthy sin being an ]{.class-0}["abomination"]{.class-1}[ before the Lord (Lev. 18:22). All it said was "Remember When Gay Meant Happy?". But those queers wanted you to associate the word only with their ]{.class-0}[perversion]{.class-2}[. That is how the Devil operates when it comes to that Book.]{.class-0}

[When the Bride says ]{.class-0}["my bowels were moved for him,"]{.class-1}[ she is saying she had deep ]{.class-0}[inner feelings]{.class-2}[ of love for the Bridegroom. It's a reference to the ]{.class-0}[heart,]{.class-2}[ which physically is located in the ]{.class-0}[upper viscera,]{.class-2}[ above the waste.]{.class-0}

"[I rose up to open to my beloved"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 5). She's moved by her love for Him, so she gets up and goes over to the door to open it for Him.]{.class-0}

"[My hands dropped with myrrh, and my fingers with sweet smelling myrrh, upon the handles of the lock."]{.class-1}[ The ]{.class-0}["myrrh"]{.class-1}[ here is not her perfume, but His (see 1:13, 3:6). It is the ]{.class-0}["myrrh"]{.class-1}[ He ]{.class-0}["gathered"]{.class-1}[ in verse 1. It was left on ]{.class-0}["the handles of the lock"]{.class-1}[ when He reached in through ]{.class-0}["the hole of the door"]{.class-1}[ in verse 4. That is how she knows it is more than a dream; she knows He has been there by the perfume He left behind.]{.class-0}

The picture is the Lord calling the Christian to do something and the Christian puts it off. When he finally gets around to doing what the Lord called him to do, he discovers the Lord had been there ahead of him.

In my own life, there have been times when I felt the Lord pressing me to deal with someone, and for one reason or another, I put the thing off. Finally the impression became urgent, and I went and dealt with that person. When I did, it was just as if the person was a piece of ripe fruit falling off the tree in my hand, as far as the person receiving Christ was concerned. The Lord had been there ahead of me; I could tell by what He had done in the heart of the person with whom I dealt. I haven't seen that a lot, but I have seen that on several occasions.

"[I opened to my beloved; but my beloved had withdrawn himself, and was gone"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 6). And here is where the trouble starts. The woman goes to the door to open it for her Lover, and He's gone, and she can't find Him. That has nothing to do with New Testament salvation at all. If you apply Revelation 3:20 to a lost person, then the promise is that if a man will ]{.class-0}["open the door,"]{.class-1}[ Christ ]{.class-0}["will come in to him."]{.class-1}

[Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["him that cometh to me I will in no wise cast out"]{.class-1}[ (John 6:37). If you come to Christ in repentance and faith, there is no way you won't be able to find him.]{.class-0}

[Now, Revelation 3:20 wasn't written to a lost man; it was written to a backslidden ]{.class-0}[saved ]{.class-2}[person. But you still can't make it fit into the situation of Song 5:6. The promise is still there in Revelation 3:20 that the Lord will come in and have fellowship with the Christian if he will just ]{.class-0}["open the door."]{.class-1}

[If you want to put a practical application on the verse for a Christian, then you will have to put it on ]{.class-0}[Christian service.]{.class-2}[ When the Lord comes to you and wants a certain thing out of you, and you put Him off and put Him off and put Him off, then there's a possibility that when you come to answer the call and do what He told you to do, that He won't be interested.]{.class-0}

I told you earlier about putting off witnessing to a person and the Lord going ahead of you and working so that when you finally do talk to the person about Christ, he gets saved easily and right away. But there is just as much the possibility that when you finally get around to it, the conviction of the Holy Spirit has grown cold or the person has become distracted by something or the person dies; I've seen those kinds of things happen too. You can't always count on everything turning out all right when you put the Lord off. Sometimes delay means an opportunity is lost forever.

[Now if you want to apply Song 5:6 ]{.class-0}[doctrinally to salvation]{.class-2}[, then you will have to put it on a lost person in the Tribulation. The case is like Matthew 25:1--13. There you have ten virgins who are waiting for the Bridegroom to show up. All ten of them fall asleep, but five are prepared and five aren't. When the Bridegroom shows up and calls them, the five who are prepared answer His call, and the other five don't. Later on, when the five foolish virgins come knocking at the door seeking to be let in, the Bridegroom turns them away.]{.class-0}

[You can see the same thing in Proverbs 1:24--28. The Lord calls to the foolish in verse 24, and they ]{.class-0}[refuse]{.class-2}[ Him. So at the Second Advent (see the ]{.class-0}["whirlwind"]{.class-1}[ in Prov. 1:27), he says, ]{.class-0}["Then shall they call upon me, BUT I WILL NOT ANSWER; they shall seek me early, BUT THEY SHALL NOT FIND ME"]{.class-1}[ (Prov. 1:28).]{.class-0}

[Look at verse 6 again:]{.class-0}[ "my soul failed when he spake: I sought him, but I COULD NOT FIND HIM; I called him, BUT HE GAVE ME NO ANSWER."]{.class-1}[ The verse matches what you just read in Proverbs 1:28.]{.class-0}

[Because of that, I say that the woman, in this instance, is very definitely someone ]{.class-0}[in the Tribulation.]{.class-2}[ Proverbs 1:24--28 is a reference to a time when the Lord will give a man an opportunity to get saved, and then, BAM!, it's gone.]{.class-0}

[Now that makes good preaching in this age to put pressure on a man to get saved right ]{.class-0}[now]{.class-2}[. That's right and that's proper. Even the Apostle Paul does it (2 Cor. 6:2). I don't hesitate to preach ]{.class-0}["now is the accepted time"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 6:2), ]{.class-0}["Boast not thyself of to morrow"]{.class-1}[ (Prov, 27:1), and ]{.class-0}["Seek ye the LORD while he may be found, call ye upon him while he is near"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 55:6). But that's not technically ]{.class-0}[doctrinal]{.class-2}[ truth for ]{.class-0}[this age.]{.class-2}

Some of the brethren go further than I do. Evangelist J. Harold Smith used to preach a message called "God's Three Deadlines." In that sermon, he said the Lord draws certain lines that if a man crosses them he can't get saved. But that isn't true either.

[I believe a man can get saved any time he will receive Christ. I believe a fellow has a chance to do that until he is ]{.class-0}[dead]{.class-2}[. I don't teach or preach any "unpardonable sin" in this age where if a fellow crosses some line God has drawn that he can't get saved.]{.class-0}

[But of course, the danger is that if you keep putting off Christ, you are less liable to say "I will." That's the truth of it. The more you reject the Lord, the thinner your ]{.class-0}[chances ]{.class-2}[get.]{.class-0}

I preach a sermon called "The Wasted Life" in which the Lord comes to a man when he is a child and the boy turns down salvation. Christ comes again when the fellow is a teenager, then when he is a young man, then when he has a family, then when he is middle-aged, and finally when he is an old man. Each time he turns down Christ, the voice of the Lord becomes fainter and fainter, and the conviction of the Holy Spirit becomes less and less, until the Lord stops dealing with him about salvation.

[The problem is ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[that the Lord won't save him; it is that the fellow has gotten into the ]{.class-0}[habit]{.class-2}[ of rejecting Christ until ]{.class-0}[he can't respond any other way]{.class-2}[ to the Lord.]{.class-0}

It's called a "conditioned response" in psychology. A behavioral psychologist named Pavlov performed an experiment where he would ring a bell and give a dog food, causing the animal to salivate. He did it so much that he could ring the bell and the dog would salivate whether it got food or not.

[You can see the thing down South. Some of these "good old boys" have been to two revival meetings a year for thirty years, and they've turned the Lord down year after year. So when the invitation is given and the choir or congregation begins to sing "Just As I Am," he closes the thing down right there because he's done it twice, four times, six times, eight times, ten times, etc.; it's ]{.class-0}[automatic.]{.class-2}

[The great practical lesson for the Christian is that it's always good to yield to the Lord at any point and to yield ]{.class-0}[right away]{.class-2}[. When you yield to that point, you are in the will of God, and when you don't, you aren't.]{.class-0}

[You are surrendered to the will of God when you're ]{.class-0}[willing]{.class-2}[ to do what He asks you to do. When you're willing, you're surrendered; when you're ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[willing, you are not ]{.class-0}[surrendered]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[Willingness ]{.class-2}[is the issue about which God is going to deal with you. Are you willing to stay single? Are you willing to be childless? Are you willing to preach? Are you willing ]{.class-0}[not]{.class-2}[ to preach? Are you willing to be a missionary? Are you willing to stay home and support the work? The Lord may not put any of those things on you, but He wants to know if you are ]{.class-0}[willing ]{.class-2}[to do them if He asks you.]{.class-0}

[For me, the temptation was to be ]{.class-0}[an evangelist.]{.class-2}[ I wanted to be like Billy Graham and see hundreds of grown men walk the aisle and get saved. The Lord didn't let me do that until I was willing ]{.class-0}[not]{.class-2}[ to be an evangelist and surrendered to the call to ]{.class-0}[teach.]{.class-2}[ After that, the Lord started opening doors in ]{.class-0}[prisons]{.class-2}[ all over Texas, Florida, and Alabama where the "fish" were (see Matt. 4:19). The Lord got me into prisons with 500-6,000 inmates each, and I've seen more grown men and women saved in one year of prison meetings than I saw in ten years of local church evangelism. But the Lord didn't do that until I surrendered ]{.class-0}[not]{.class-2}[ to be an evangelist!]{.class-0}

[Those are personal things that are different for every Christian. The reason there are so many churches today filled with nothing but a bunch of spiritual babies is because of the lack of preaching on those things. A Christian ]{.class-0}[grows ]{.class-2}[as he ]{.class-0}[yields]{.class-2}[, and where he doesn't ]{.class-0}[yield]{.class-2}[, there is no ]{.class-0}[growth]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[The hard part of the Christian life is ]{.class-0}[willingness ]{.class-2}[to yield to what God asks you to do. It's not a question of what's "expedient" or "good." The issue is: 1) what does God want me to do, and 2) ]{.class-0}[am I willing to do it.]{.class-2}[ Once you've settled those two things, you will find out what God's will for you is.]{.class-0}

[Verse 7, ]{.class-0}["The watchmen that went about the city found me, they smote me, they wounded me; the keepers of the walls took away my veil from me."]{.class-1}[ Notice how different this reaction is to the response she got back in 3:3--4. In chapter 3, ]{.class-0}["the watchmen"]{.class-1}[ leave her alone; but here they slap her around, hurt her, and humiliate her. If this is a lost man in the Tribulation (see comments on vs. 6), then this would be the ]{.class-0}["distress and anguish"]{.class-1}[ of Proverbs 1:27.]{.class-0}

8 I charge you, O daughters of Jerusalem, if ye find my beloved, that ye tell him, that I am sick of love.

9 What is thy beloved more than another beloved, O thou fairest among women? what is thy beloved more than another beloved, that thou dost so charge us?

10 My beloved is white and ruddy, the chiefest among ten thousand.

11 His head is as the most fine gold, his locks are bushy, and black as a raven.

12 His eyes are as the eyes of doves by the rivers of waters, washed with milk, and fitly set.

13 His cheeks are as a bed of spices, as sweet flowers: his lips like lilies, dropping sweet smelling myrrh.

14 His hands are as gold rings set with the beryl: his belly is as bright ivory overlaid with sapphires.

15 His legs are as pillars of marble, set upon sockets of fine gold: his countenance is as Lebanon, excellent as the cedars.

16 His mouth is most sweet: yea, he is altogether lovely. This is my beloved, and this is my friend, O daughters of Jerusalem.

[Trouble again!]{.class-0}[ "I charge you, O daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 8). Then the woman here can't be a type of the Jew in the Tribulation. She distinguishes herself from the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ here just as she did back in 1:5.]{.class-0}

[Furthermore, what follows is obviously the Bride of Christ describing the Lord. Since the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ puts a paragraph mark at verse 9, you might get away with putting verse 8 with verses 6 and 7, but still, it's hard. The woman of verse 8 speaks of being in ]{.class-0}["love"]{.class-1}[ with her beloved, but people of Proverbs 1:24--28 are said to have ]{.class-0}["hated knowledge, and did not choose the fear of the LORD"]{.class-1}[ (Prov. 1:29).]{.class-0}

"[I am sick of love."]{.class-1}[ The expression is not used like it is today in the sense of being tired of something or annoyed with something. She is saying her love for the Bridegroom is so great, and she is seeking Him without being able to find Him so much, that it is making her sick. Today, we would say that she is "lovesick."]{.class-0}

"[What is thy beloved more than another beloved, O thou fairest among women? what is thy beloved more than another beloved, that thou dost so charge us?"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 9). The speakers are obviously the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ from the previous verse, since they are the ones who were given the ]{.class-0}["charge."]{.class-1}[ In the context, they are probably Tribulation Jews.]{.class-0}

[In this verse, the Bride has been raving and bragging about her Lover, and the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ are asking what's so special about Him and why He is so much better than anyone else? But of course, in the eyes of love, the one you love always looks different and better than anybody else. When you love somebody, you always tend to think he or she is better looking, smarter, wiser, or stronger than anyone else, because love paints a picture for you.]{.class-0}

The old saying is: "True love is blind." That's kind of a half truth. The adage means that love fails to see all the imperfections and faults in the one who is loved and it tends to overlook them as though they weren't there.

[But that isn't what ]{.class-0}[true ]{.class-2}[love is like. In fact, if your love is "blind," it is not real love. ]{.class-0}[True ]{.class-2}[love is seeing all the faults and imperfections in a person and still loving him or her anyway. Any love that refuses to take into account the imperfections or faults of the other party is not going to come out very well in the long run, because faults and imperfections are going to show up.]{.class-0}

Now when it comes to the Christian's love for his Saviour, you will find that those who don't love Him can't understand what the Christian sees in Jesus Christ. When you rave about the Lord and brag about Him, don't expect the world to understand about what you're talking.

[The reason why people don't get enthusiastic about the word of God and Jesus Christ is because they don't love Him. Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["If the world hate you, ye know that IT HATED ME before it hated you"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:18). He said, ]{.class-0}["He that is of God heareth God's words: ye therefore hear them not, because ye are not of God" ]{.class-1}[(John 8:47). You can't expect a lost person to understand your love for Jesus Christ, because there is nothing in him to help him understand it (1 Cor. 2:14).]{.class-0}

[The attitude of people is: "Well, you Christians have the Bible, the Moslems have the ]{.class-0}[Koran,]{.class-2}[ and the Hindus and the Buddhists have their 'sacred scriptures'; what's so special about your Book?" They say, "There are a billion and a half Moslems, there are 900 million Hindus, and there are 376 million people who profess to follow Buddha; all those people can't be wrong, can they?" They say, "What makes Jesus Christ any different than Mohammed, Buddha, Lao Tse, or Confucius?"]{.class-0}

"[What is thy beloved more than another beloved\...?"]{.class-1}

[Now, there are two ways of answering that question. You can answer it from a ]{.class-0}[personal]{.class-2}[ viewpoint, or you can answer it from an ]{.class-0}[objective]{.class-2}[ viewpoint. The truth is that God has given an unsaved man enough evidence that, if he is honest, he will have to admit that no other "sacred scripture" is like the Bible and no other "founder of a religion" is like Jesus Christ.]{.class-0}

[The thing that sets the Bible apart from such amateur works as the ]{.class-0}[Vedas, ]{.class-2}[the ]{.class-0}[Shastas,]{.class-2}[ and the ]{.class-0}[Puranas]{.class-2}[ (Hinduism), the ]{.class-0}[Tripitaka]{.class-2}[ (Buddhism), the ]{.class-0}[Zend Avesta]{.class-2}[ (Zoroastrianism), and the ]{.class-0}[Koran]{.class-2}[ (Mohammedanism) is ]{.class-0}[prophecy.]{.class-2}[ The Bible is the only Book that can predict 48 particulars of a man's life anywhere from 400 to 1,500 years before He is born and have every single one of them "come through on the money."]{.class-0}

[A professional mathematician and statistician named Dr. Peter Stoner (in his work ]{.class-0}[Science Speaks]{.class-2}[) proved that the chances of that happening was one out of 10]{.class-0}[157]{.class-22}[ (that's ten with 157 zeros after it). There are not that many electrons in four universes the size of this one. Moreover, according to the laws of statistical probability, if the chances of an event taking place is one out of 10]{.class-0}[50]{.class-22}[, there is no ]{.class-0}[natural]{.class-2}[ chance of that event ever taking place. ]{.class-0}[Bible prophecy defies human explanation.]{.class-2}

[You won't find that phenomenon in ]{.class-0}[any]{.class-2}[ other religious book. Take the whole lot combined, and you wouldn't find two prophecies (and I mean real prophecies, not lucky guesses that have a fifty-fifty chance of taking place) of anything that is fulfilled ]{.class-0}[in history]{.class-2}[ (not at the "Last Judgment").]{.class-0}

[Mohammed, as a "prophet," is a sad joke. A lost sinner in the Old Testament (Balaam) could make more ]{.class-0}[historical prophecies]{.class-2}[ in two chapters (Num. 23--24) than Mohammed could in 114 "Suras." You will find more prophetic material in Obadiah (the ]{.class-0}[shortest book]{.class-2}[ in the Old Testament) than in the ]{.class-0}[Koran]{.class-2}[ and the ]{.class-0}[Hadith]{.class-2}[ combined.]{.class-0}

[And what makes Jesus Christ ]{.class-0}["more than another beloved"]{.class-1}[ is the fact that ]{.class-0}[He didn't stay dead]{.class-2}[---He came up bodily. Mohammed, Buddha, Zoroaster, Confucius, et al., ]{.class-0}[stayed down in the ground.]{.class-2}[ In fact, the resurrection of Jesus Christ is the chief proof of His Deity.]{.class-0}

"[And declared to be the Son of God with power, according to the spirit of holiness, BY THE RESURRECTION FROM THE DEAD"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 1:4).]{.class-0}

"[Because he hath appointed a day, in the which he will judge the world in righteousness by that man whom he hath ordained; whereof he hath given assurance unto all men, in that he hath RAISED HIM FROM THE DEAD"]{.class-1}[ (Acts 17:31).]{.class-0}

[And before some atheist or agnostic tries to convince you that Jesus Christ is just a bunch of Jews copying pagan mythology and astrology (Osiris, Balder, etc.), just remember that the Gospels are the ]{.class-0}[eyewitness]{.class-2}[ accounts of people who lived, worked, ate, and traveled ]{.class-0}[with ]{.class-2}[Christ (Luke 1:1--2). They recorded, in writing, what they ]{.class-0}[saw ]{.class-2}[and ]{.class-0}[experienced ]{.class-2}[within thirty to sixty years of the events (Scofield places the date of Matthew at A.D. 37, within ]{.class-0}[four years]{.class-2}[ of the resurrection of Christ). Paul told you that there were over 500 witnesses at one time who saw the resurrected Christ and that, if they had wanted to, the Corinthians could have gone and met them and talked to them about what they had seen because most of them were still ]{.class-0}[alive ]{.class-2}[when Paul wrote (1 Cor. 15:6). The evidence for the resurrection of Jesus Christ is so strong that a Jewish lawyer named Simon Greenleaf, who was the leading expert on evidence in his day (1783--1853), got ]{.class-0}[converted ]{.class-2}[when he examined it.]{.class-0}

[Now all of that is ]{.class-0}[objective, scientific]{.class-2}[ proof for the uniqueness of the Bible and Jesus Christ, and if a man is an ]{.class-0}[honest]{.class-2}[ skeptic (like Simon Greenleaf was), he will yield to the evidence and believe the Bible and trust Christ as his Saviour. But the love of the Bride for the Bridegroom doesn't view Him through mathematics or legal evidence. She takes an intimate, personal experience.]{.class-0}

[I was witnessing to a doctor one time who thought he was pretty smart. When I started to give him the Scriptures on salvation, he said, "Don't quote that Bible to me. Tell me something you ]{.class-0}[know."]{.class-2}[ He should have never said that to me. I started giving him my personal testimony, and by the time I got through, he wished I had gone back to quoting Scripture!]{.class-0}

[One of the best ways for a Christian to start witnessing is to give his testimony and tell someone what Jesus Christ did for him. If a Christian were asked, "What's Jesus Christ more than anyone else," he ought to be able to take off and give an hour-and-a half discourse of how the Lord has worked in his life and what the Lord means to him. I ended up writing 600 pages on the subject (]{.class-0}[The Full Cup]{.class-2}[ and ]{.class-0}[Memoirs of a Twentieth-Century Circuit-Riding Preacher]{.class-2}[).]{.class-0}

So in verses 9--18, the woman gives a physical description of her lover just as He did of her back in 4:1--5. The passage describes what she thinks is so special about the Bridegroom.

[Verse 10:]{.class-0}[ "My beloved is WHITE."]{.class-1}[ That's WHITE as opposed to BLACK (1:5). There go Martin Luther King Jr., Malcolm X, Jesse Jackson, Louis Farakhan, Al Sharpton, Jeremiah Wright, and Barack Obama. Jesus Christ was NOT a black man as the Black Muslims and Black Liberationists teach, and as some of our black brethren picture.]{.class-0}

Someone gave me a book once that pictured all the people in the Bible who were supposed to be black. The book had Adam and Eve being black (based on "Lucy" in Africa), David being black because he had a Moabite great grandmother (Ruth), Solomon being black because Bathsheba was supposed to have been a Hittite since she had been married to a Hittite (Uriah), et al. And of course, they had Jesus as a black man because He had three Hamite women in His lineage (Tamar, Rahab, and Ruth; Matt: 1:3--5 cf. Luke 3:31--33).

[The fact is that Bathsheba wasn't a Hittite; she was a ]{.class-0}[Jewish]{.class-2}[ woman married to a Hittite (2 Sam. 11:3 cf. 23:34). Whatever Hamite heritage was in his lineage, Solomon the son of David---a type of Jesus Christ the Son of David---was ]{.class-0}[white,]{.class-2}[ not black; and a black woman recognized that.]{.class-0}

"[And ruddy"]{.class-1}[ (cf. 1 Sam. 16:12, 17:42). The word means "reddish brown"; it's the original color of Adam (see comments on Gen. 2:19 in that Commentary). So Christ is white in distinction to black, and His complexion is reddish brown.]{.class-0}

[The three races (Shem, Ham, and Japheth---Oriental, Negroid, and Caucasian) are often classified as black, white, and yellow. But the white race isn't really "white" (white is the color of this paper; that's "white." If a white man were "white," he'd be ]{.class-0}[dead]{.class-2}[); it's ]{.class-0}[pink.]{.class-2}[ The yellow race isn't "yellow"; it's brown. Chinese, Japanese, and Koreans are more of yellow brown, almost goldish. David, Solomon, and Christ were all reddish brown, like an American Indian.]{.class-0}

"[The chiefest among ten thousand"]{.class-1}[ (cf. David as a type of Christ; see 2 Sam. 18:3). The idea is that if you took the top ten thousand men, the Bridegroom would be "number one." So the song says Jesus is "the fairest of ten thousand to my soul" ("The Lily of the Valley").]{.class-0}

[In other words, if you take Bach, Beethoven, Mozart, Mohammed, Buddha, Confucius, the Pope (any of them), Darwin, Hawking, Leakey, Picasso, Rembrandt, Michaelangelo, Washington, Lincoln, Marx, Lenin, Napoleon, Mandela, Clinton, Bush, Obama, et al., and put them on one side and put Jesus Christ on the other, Jesus Christ comes out better every time. Brethren, when you get to know Jesus Christ, the heroes of this world become mighty commonplace; they really come down quick. I don't mean when you know His ]{.class-0}[teachings;]{.class-2}[ I mean when you know ]{.class-0}[Him.]{.class-2}

[Verse 11:]{.class-0}[ "His head is as the most fine gold]{.class-1}[ \[He's an Oriental Shemite\]]{.class-0}[, his locks are bushy, and black as a raven."]{.class-1}[ Notice how this description differs from that of the Liberal "Christ." Movies like "The Robe," "The Greatest Story Ever Told," "Jesus of Nazareth," etc., have Jesus with brown hair, blond hair, red hair---anything but what the Bible says. He swishes around in long robes, he's tall and thin and six-foot-four, he has a deep bass voice, and he always has this far-away look like he's half in a trance. There's a famous painting called "Inspiration" by Salmon Warner that pictures Christ as an effeminate ]{.class-0}[red-haired Irishman.]{.class-2}

[Jesus was a ]{.class-0}[Jew.]{.class-2}[ He had black hair, dark eyebrows, and a dark beard. He probably had a big nose with a crook in it and fairly thick lips.]{.class-0}

[He was a ]{.class-0}[man.]{.class-2}[ He worked for nearly eighteen years as a carpenter; his hands were undoubtedly calloused and rough. He didn't have long, tapering fingers like a sewing woman.]{.class-0}

"[His eyes are as the eyes of doves"]{.class-1}[ (see comments on 1:15). A dove's eyes are gray. They sit on the side of the bird's head and can see better than 180 degrees in all directions. A dove has an innocent, harmless look, but it has a piercing stare.]{.class-0}

"[By the rivers of waters, washed with milk, and fitly set."]{.class-1}[ His eyes are clear and sparkling. They are clean; Habakkuk 1:13 says, ]{.class-0}["Thou art of purer eyes than to behold evil, and canst not look on iniquity."]{.class-1}[ They are properly set in His head like a piece of jewelry. The old superstition about criminals was that their eyes were too close together; that was a sign in criminology for years and years. The Bridegroom's eyes are set properly on His face so that they are balanced: not too far down, up, back, or forward on the head.]{.class-0}

"[His cheeks are as a bed of spices, as sweet flowers"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13). The ]{.class-0}["spices"]{.class-1}[ are all those perfumes mentioned back in 4:13--14. The Bridegroom's ]{.class-0}["cheeks"]{.class-1}[ are sweet smelling; that's why men wear cologne today. His ]{.class-0}["cheeks"]{.class-1}[ are also like ]{.class-0}["a bed of spices"]{.class-1}[ in that they are pleasant to look upon; the idea is that He has a natural blush in His cheeks.]{.class-0}

"[His lips like lilies, dropping sweet smelling myrrh."]{.class-1}[ She finds His lips sweet like He found her lips back in 4:11. Physically, the verse is speaking of the fact that the Bridegroom's lips are moist. Spiritually, the ]{.class-0}["myrrh"]{.class-1}[ speaks of Christ's suffering for sinners (see comments on 1:13), so you have a picture here of Christ's love for the sinner. Ephesians 5:25 says, ]{.class-0}["Christ\...loved the church, and gave himself for it."]{.class-1}

"[His hands are as gold rings set with beryl"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 14). I'm not sure that I really get this, but I'll give you what I can. A ]{.class-0}["gold ring"]{.class-1}[ on the finger obviously symbolized wealth and a high station in life (James 2:2). In Luke 15:22, the ring was a symbol of sonship, as opposed to being a servant. In Esther 3:10, the King's ring was his ]{.class-0}[signet]{.class-2}[ ring which was used to ascribe his name to law, so it was a symbol of the King's authority.]{.class-0}

[But the verse said ]{.class-0}["as gold rings set with beryl."]{.class-1}[ The only other place you find ]{.class-0}["gold rings"]{.class-1}[ connected with ]{.class-0}["beryl"]{.class-1}[ is in the breastplate of the high priest (Exod. 39:13--16). So not only is the similitude a picture of physical beauty and wealth, and a symbol of sonship and authority, it is another type of Jesus Christ as our ]{.class-0}[High Priest]{.class-2}[ (Heb. 3:1).]{.class-0}

[Beryl is a precious stone found not only in the breastplate of the high priest (Exod. 28:20), but in the foundation stones of the New Jerusalem (Rev. 21:2). The beryl was also part of Lucifer before his fall (Ezek. 28:13). The Hebrew word is ]{.class-0}[tarshish,]{.class-2}[ supposedly named after the city from whence the crystal came (see 2 Chron. 9:21, 20:36; Psa. 48:7, 72:10; Isa. 2:16, 60:9; Ezek. 27:25, 38:13; Jon. 1:3, etc.). All the scholars want to change the word to ]{.class-0}[chrysolite,]{.class-2}[ but Revelation 21:20 clearly shows you that the two gems are not the same.]{.class-0}

[The word ]{.class-0}[beryl]{.class-2}[ comes from a Greek word which means a "bluish-green precious stone colored like the sea." A ]{.class-0}[pure ]{.class-2}[beryl is colorless, but impurities can cause beryls to be sea green (which was the color in the Mediterranean area), gold, pink, aquamarine, darker green, and even red. There is even a beryl called a "heliodor" which has a color like "frozen fire," which would seem to be the color in Ezekiel 1:4--16, 10:9 and Daniel 10:6.]{.class-0}

Although it is just a guess, if you go by the order of the twelve tribes of Israel in Numbers 2, the beryl in the breastplate would stand for the tribe of Dan (see comments on Exod. 28:20 in that Commentary).

"[His belly is as bright ivory overlaid with sapphires."]{.class-1}[ Here is another reference to let you know that Solomon and Jesus Christ were both ]{.class-0}[white]{.class-2}[ as opposed to ]{.class-0}[black]{.class-2}[ (see comments on vs. 10). ]{.class-0}["Bright ivory"]{.class-1}[ is ]{.class-0}[white,]{.class-2}[ not black.]{.class-0}

Ivory speaks of strength (see 7:4), royalty (2 Chron. 9:17), luxury (Amos 6:4), and wealth (Rev. 18:12). In the context, you have the original "six-pack abs" (abdominal muscles).

"[Sapphires"]{.class-1}[ are gems of a sky-blue color; occasionally you have "star" sapphires---blue stones with a white "star" in the middle. The first time it appears, it is associated with ]{.class-0}["God"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["heaven"]{.class-1}[ (Exod. 24:10; see also Ezek. 1:26, 10:1). Like the beryl, you will find it in Lucifer before his fall (Ezek. 28:13), in the breastplate of the high priest (Exod. 28:18, 39:11), and in the foundations of the New Jerusalem (Rev. 21:19). In the context here, it speaks of the Bridegroom's attractiveness (cf. Isa. 54:11; Lam. 4:7).]{.class-0}

"[His legs are as pillars of marble"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 15). It's a picture of ]{.class-0}[strength.]{.class-2}[ The legs are the strongest part of a man's body. That's why Abraham had his servant put his hand under his thigh to swear an oath: he had the servant swear on his ]{.class-0}[strength.]{.class-2}

[If a man's legs give way, the rest of him gives way. The ]{.class-0}["legs"]{.class-1}[ in this verse are like ]{.class-0}["marble"]{.class-1}[; they are not going to give way. Marble is stronger than granite; it's one of the last things in the world to wear out. That's why tombstones are usually made out of marble.]{.class-0}

[When the verse says ]{.class-0}["His legs are as pillars of marble,"]{.class-1}[ it means that the legs can stand, stay standing, and not give way.
