The old songs speak of Christ as a firm foundation, a sure foundation, a rock, an anchor, and a fortress; those songs are right. Nobody could push Him over, and no one ever did, not even the Devil.]{.class-0}

"[Set upon sockets of fine gold"]{.class-1}[: a reference to the ankles and feet. The ]{.class-0}["sockets"]{.class-1}[ of the Tabernacle (Exod. 38:27--30) were made of silver (representing ]{.class-0}[redemption]{.class-2}[) and brass (representing]{.class-0}[ judgment]{.class-2}[). When Daniel and John saw Christ, He had ]{.class-0}["feet like unto fine brass"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 1:15 cf. Dan. 10:6). The sockets of gold here represent Christ's Deity. So you have a picture of Christ's dual nature in this verse: legs of marble (Son of Man), feet of gold (Son of God).]{.class-0}

[Contrast Christ's legs and feet with those of Nebuchadnezzar's image in Daniel 2:33, 40--43. The kingdom of the Antichrist is built on an unsound foundation of iron and clay that is knocked over easily by the ]{.class-0}["stone\...cut out without hands"]{.class-1}[ (Dan. 2:34). That stone is ]{.class-0}["the stone which the builders rejected"]{.class-1}[---Jesus Christ (Matt. 21:42--44).]{.class-0}

"[His countenance is as Lebanon, excellent as the cedars."]{.class-1}[ The appearance of His face is strong. The cedar is a ]{.class-0}[strong]{.class-2}[ tree; in fact, the Hebrew word for cedar means "a firmly rooted and strong tree." The cedar is a ]{.class-0}[straight]{.class-2}[ tree. The cedars of Lebanon run sixty to seventy feet high. They are just like an arrow stuck in the ground. The very tip is about the size of your finger, and the bottom can be as big around as a piano. The Bridegroom's countenance, here, is a straight, strong appearance; back in 2:14, the Bride described His ]{.class-0}["countenance"]{.class-1}[ as ]{.class-0}["comely."]{.class-1}

"[His mouth is most sweet"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 16); again referring not only to the way it looks, but what comes out of it (see 2:4 and comments on 4:11). David said, ]{.class-0}["How sweet are thy words unto my taste! yea, sweeter than honey to my mouth!"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 119:103) Solomon wrote, ]{.class-0}["The wise in heart shall be called prudent: and the sweetness of the lips increaseth learning"]{.class-1}[ (Prov. 16:21); and ]{.class-0}["Pleasant words are as an honeycomb, sweet to the soul"]{.class-1}[ (Prov. 16:24).]{.class-0}

[Finally, having run out of adjectives to describe Jesus Christ, the Bride says, ]{.class-0}["yea, he is altogether lovely."]{.class-1}[ That, of course, is how the Church views her Saviour; that is not how the world views Him or how He appeared when He was here on earth at His First Advent.]{.class-0}

[In describing Jesus Christ as a human being walking around on earth, Isaiah said, ]{.class-0}["he hath no form nor comeliness"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 53:2); although Jesus was a strong man from having been a carpenter, there was nothing particularly attractive about Him. ]{.class-0}["And when we shall see him, there is no beauty that we should desire him."]{.class-1}[ He wasn't exceptionally handsome or good looking; if you had seen Him in Nazareth or Jerusalem or in Galilee, you probably wouldn't have taken notice of Him just by looking at Him. From a human standpoint, He was an ordinary, everyday, average Jew.]{.class-0}

[But to the believer, through the eyes of love, He appears differently. Peter said, ]{.class-0}["Unto you therefore which believe he is precious"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 2:7). To the Christian, the beauty of Jesus Christ is not viewed with his physical eyes, but through the eyes of faith in what He did for him (1 Pet. 1:8--11).]{.class-0}

"[This is my beloved, and this is my friend."]{.class-1}[ That's what the Lord should be to the Christian. That certainly is how the Lord looks at the Christian. Paul talks about ]{.class-0}["his great love wherewith he loved us"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 2:4), and says Christ ]{.class-0}["made us accepted in the beloved"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 1:6). The Christian is ]{.class-0}["beloved of God"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 1:7; Col. 3:12; 2 Thess. 2:13). Jesus was ]{.class-0}["a friend of publicans and sinners"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 7:34). He said to His disciples, ]{.class-0}["I say unto you my friends"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 12:4); and ]{.class-0}["Henceforth I call you not servants\...but I have called you friends"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:15).]{.class-0}

[We sing "What a friend we have in Jesus" and "I love Him, I love Him, because He first loved me." A ]{.class-0}["friend"]{.class-1}[ is someone you can count on when you get in a jam or in a mess, but a ]{.class-0}["beloved"]{.class-1}[ is something stronger than a friend. A ]{.class-0}["beloved"]{.class-1}[ is a closer, more intimate relationship. The Lord ought to be someone you love whether you're in trouble or not.]{.class-0}

[If Jesus Christ is your ]{.class-0}["beloved"]{.class-1}[ and your ]{.class-0}["friend,"]{.class-1}[ you ought to do something for Him (John 14:15, 15:14). You shouldn't be ashamed of Him, and you should "stick your neck out" for Him no matter what people think.]{.class-0}

[Now notice that the final testimony by the Bride concerning the Bridegroom is given to the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem."]{.class-1}[ In type, that's the Church testifying to the Jews about Jesus Christ. That's what Paul wrote about in the book of Romans.]{.class-0}

"[For I am not ashamed of the gospel of Christ: for it is the power of God unto salvation to every one that believeth; to the Jew first, and also to the Greek"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 1:16). Whenever Paul went into a town to preach, he would always go to the synagogue first and preach to the Jews. It wasn't until the Jews rejected his message that he turned to the Gentiles (see Acts 13, 18). In fact, Paul would use the Gentiles turning to Christ to make the Jews jealous so that they would say, "I'm not going to let a Gentile dog get ahead of me; I'm one of God's chosen people, and Jesus Christ is my Messiah," and then they would get saved.]{.class-0}

"[I say then, Have they stumbled]{.class-1}[ \[the Jews\]]{.class-0}[ that they should fall? God forbid: but rather through their fall salvation is come unto the Gentiles, for to provoke them to jealousy\....For I speak to you Gentiles, inasmuch as I am the apostle of the Gentiles, I magnify mine office: If by any means I may provoke to emulation them which are my flesh, and might save some"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 11:11, 13--14).]{.class-0}

That is what seems to be going on, in type, in Song of Solomon 5:8--16.

[Now when it comes to that Jew, some of the brethren, like Texe Marrs, have figured that since the Jews, as a nation, crucified Christ, and since the Antichrist is a Jew, that they, as a people, should be demonized and be blamed for all the problems and corruption that go on in the world. But that Jew is no more or less a sinner than any Gentile (Rom. 11:30). The rule of thumb for the Bible-believing Christian is: ]{.class-0}["As concerning the gospel, they are enemies for your sakes: but as touching the election, they are beloved for the fathers' sakes"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 11:28).]{.class-0}

Those Jews are Christ-rejectors. They believe Mary was a whore and Christ was a bastard (see John 8:41), so they are blasphemers. The Rabbis add to the Old Testament and change it to destroy all prophetic reference to Jesus Christ; they reject the New Testament. The State of Israel forbids Christian missionaries from trying to win Jews to Jesus Christ. Like the rich Jew in Luke 16, they are headed for Hell. BUT THAT DOESN'T CHANGE THE FACT THAT THEY ARE STILL GOD'S CHOSEN PEOPLE.

[God isn't finished with that Jew yet. He brought them back into the land (Isa. 11:11) EVEN THOUGH THEY WERE IN UNBELIEF. And the day will come when ]{.class-0}["the fulness of the Gentiles be come in. And so all Israel shall be saved"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 11:25--26).]{.class-0}

[Until then, a Christian is to ]{.class-0}[love ]{.class-2}[that Jew---whether he feels like it or not. He should ]{.class-0}[support ]{.class-2}[that Jew in his land to avoid the curse of God (Num. 24:9). That doesn't mean that he has to agree with everything every Jewish politician says or does, but it does mean that when it comes to who has a right to the land of "Palestine," the Christian is to side with that Jew because God gave the land to him (Gen. 15:18--21; Exod. 13:5; Deut. 4:38, 6:10, 7:13, 19:8, 20:16; etc.).]{.class-0}

When it comes to individual Jews, the Christian is to take any opportunity the Lord gives him to witness to a Jewish person. Every church should support some missionary to the Jews if it can. If you want to bless a Jew individually, that is the way to do it.

[]{#section-0_1_aeea0e89eed0d381_67e0.xhtml}

CHAPTER 6

6:1 Whither is thy beloved gone, O thou fairest among women? whither is thy beloved turned aside? that we may seek him with thee.

2 My beloved is gone down into his garden, to the beds of spices, to feed in the gardens, and to gather lilies.

3 I am my beloved's, and my beloved is mine: he feedeth among the lilies.

[Verse 1 is spoken by the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ to the Bride. There might be some application to the Tribulation, but I'm not sure about that.]{.class-0}

In type, what you have is a bunch of Jews asking the Church, "Where has your Saviour gone? We want to find him too, so where is He?" That won't match the Tribulation exactly.

[To play it safe, I divide the application where the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ divides the passage. The ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ puts a paragraph mark at 5:9 and then puts the next one at 6:4. I make the passage from 5:9 to 6:3 a reference to the Church Age because that's how the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ divides it by the paragraph marks. It's apparent that in 5:2--8 that that passage is not talking about the Bride of Christ doctrinally because she can't find Christ. And when you get to 6:4, you have the Church perfected in Heaven at the Marriage of the Lamb. In between those two passages, you have the Church witnessing to a bunch of Jews (5:9--6:3), so I make it the Church Age.]{.class-0}

[Now I know all the scholars say that the paragraph marks in a ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ Bible aren't inspired. They say the same thing about the chapters and verses. But ain't it neat how they are all placed? You won't get that kind of phenomena in "the originals."]{.class-0}

[The brethren call me a "heretic" because I teach that the ]{.class-0}[KJV]{.class-2}[ is SUPERIOR to the original Greek and Hebrew manuscripts, but they never discuss the ]{.class-0}[reasons ]{.class-2}[I give for believing that. First of all, you HAVE the ]{.class-0}[KJV,]{.class-2}[ and you DON'T HAVE the "original autographs." How's that for "superiority"? What you ]{.class-0}[have]{.class-2}[ that the Lord gave you is always superior to what you ]{.class-0}[don't have]{.class-2}[ and couldn't get ahold of if you tried.]{.class-0}

But you take these chapter and verse divisions and those paragraph marks. It is perfectly apparent that they were not added randomly or capriciously. The men who put them in the text were obviously "led" to produce such phenomena as you see here in Song of Solomon. The "original Hebrew" won't give you any light on it at all.

[Now, the Jews in verse 1 ask two questions: where has the Bridegroom gone, and where can we find Him. In the Church Age, ]{.class-0}["blindness IN PART is happened to Israel"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 11:25). Although most Jews reject Christ, not ]{.class-0}[all ]{.class-2}[of them do. You have Jews getting saved all throughout the New Testament and the Church Age. Three thousand of them got saved at Pentecost (Acts 2:41), and another 5,000 got saved in Acts 4:4. Saul of Tarsus got saved, and ]{.class-0}["James the Lord's brother"]{.class-1}[ (Gal. 2:19) told Paul, ]{.class-0}["Thou seest, brother, how many thousands of Jews there are which believe"]{.class-1}[ (Acts 21:18--20).]{.class-0}

Felix Mendelssohn, the composer, was a Jewish Christian, as was Benjamin Disraeli, Queen Victoria's Prime Minister. Evangelist Hyman Appelman was a saved Jew. Jacob Gartenhaus was a young Jewish immigrant who got saved in a rescue mission in New York City and started a mission to Jews (International Board of Jewish Missions). So you still have Jews coming to the Church (the Bride of Christ; not the Roman Catholic Whore) to try to find Christ.

[The Apostle Paul wrote: ]{.class-0}["I say then, Hath God cast away his people? God forbid. For I also am an Israelite, of the seed of Abraham, of the tribe of Benjamin. God hath not cast away his people which he foreknew\...Even so then at this present time also there is a remnant according to the election of grace\...What then? Israel hath not obtained that which he seeketh for; but the election hath obtained it, and the rest were blinded"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 11:2, 5, 7).]{.class-0}

If a Jew wants to find Christ in this age, he can. Christians should be busy giving them the Gospel.

"[My beloved is gone down into his garden, to the beds of spices, to feed in the gardens, and to gather lilies"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 2). So the Bride finds her Lover back where she left Him in 4:12--5:1. Figuratively and symbolically, the verse is a reference to the love and communion between a man and his wife.]{.class-0}

If you apply the verse spiritually to a Christian, the lesson is that the only way he can regain fellowship with his Lord is to go back to where he lost it. You have to go to the place where the axe head fell in the water in order to get it back (see 2 Kings 6:5--6).

"[I am my beloved's, and my beloved is mine: he feedeth among the lilies"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 3; see our comments on 2:16). The verse is the description of an ideal marriage: the husband owns the wife, and the wife owns the husband (1 Cor. 7:4). Of course, that is old fashioned, but when the marriage was old fashioned, it didn't have the problems it does today.]{.class-0}

In the Christian's relationship to Christ, you are in Christ (1 Cor. 12:13), and Christ is in you (John 17:23; Col. 1:27). The song says, "I am His and He is mine."

4 Thou art beautiful, O my love, as Tirzah, comely as Jerusalem, terrible as an army with banners.

5 Turn away thine eyes from me, for they have overcome me: thy hair is as a flock of goats that appear from Gilead.

6 Thy teeth are as a flock of sheep which go up from the washing, whereof every one beareth twins, and there is not one barren among them.

7 As a piece of a pomegranate are thy temples within thy locks.

8 There are threescore queens, and fourscore concubines, and virgins without number.

9 My dove, my undefiled is but one; she is the only one of her mother, she is the choice one of her that bare her. The daughters saw her, and blessed her; yea, the queens and the concubines, and they praised her.

[Notice again the placement of the paragraph marks in a ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ Bible. From the paragraph mark in 5:9 to 6:3, you have a picture of the Church Age. From the paragraph at 6:3 to 6:9, you have the Church in Heaven at the Marriage of the Lamb. From the paragraph mark in 6:10 to the paragraph mark at 7:10, you have the Advent and the Millennium. You won't find that phenomenon in "the originals."]{.class-0}

"[Thou art beautiful\...as Tirzah, comely as Jerusalem" ]{.class-1}[(vs. 4). ]{.class-0}["Tizrah"]{.class-1}[ was one of the cities in Canaan taken by Joshua (Josh. 12:24). The city was located in Ephraim. Jeroboam made it the capital of the northern tribes when the kingdom split (1 Kings 14:12, 17). The reason for that choice is obvious from the verse here in Song of Solomon. Tirzah rivaled Jerusalem in its beauty.]{.class-0}

[Jerusalem at the time of Solomon was a beautiful city. First Kings 10:27 says Solomon ]{.class-0}["made silver to be in Jerusalem as stones."]{.class-1}[ Gold was so common there at that time that ]{.class-0}["all king Solomon's drinking vessels were of gold\...it was nothing accounted of in the days of Solomon"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 10:21). The Temple on Mt. Zion was covered with gold (1 Kings 6:22); on a bright sunny day, you could see the sunlight reflecting off it for miles.]{.class-0}

[So when Solomon says his bride is ]{.class-0}["comely as Jerusalem,"]{.class-1}[ he likens her to being covered with gold. As a matter of fact, that is exactly what Psalm 45 says.]{.class-0}

"[The king's daughter is all glorious within: her clothing is of wrought gold"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 45:13).]{.class-0}

[So when the New Jerusalem, ]{.class-0}["the Lamb's wife"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 21:9), comes down from Heaven ]{.class-0}["as a bride adorned for her husband"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 21:2), it is made of ]{.class-0}["pure gold"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 21:18).]{.class-0}

"[Terrible as an army with banners."]{.class-1}[ Notice the two similitudes for the Bride in verse 4. She's likened to a ]{.class-0}[beautiful city]{.class-2}[ and a ]{.class-0}[terrible army.]{.class-2}[ You couldn't imagine a more different contrast than that.]{.class-0}

[As a beautiful city, she is called ]{.class-0}["thou fairest among women"]{.class-1}[ (5:9, 6:1); i.e., the most beautiful of women. She is hauled up to Heaven in the Rapture and decked out in gold and ]{.class-0}["fine linen, clean and white"]{.class-1}[ at ]{.class-0}["the marriage of the Lamb"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 19:7--8); that is the context here in Song 6:8--9.]{.class-0}

[But then before the marriage is hardly over, she's a terrible army mounted on horseback, coming back with her Husband to fight a bloody battle (Rev. 19:14). And if you want to see how ]{.class-0}["terrible"]{.class-1}[ that ]{.class-0}["army"]{.class-1}[ is, look at Joel 2:1--11.]{.class-0}

"[Blow ye the trumpet in Zion, and sound an alarm in my holy mountain: let all the inhabitants of the land tremble: for the day of the LORD cometh]{.class-1}[ \[the Second Advent\]]{.class-0}[\...A day of darkness and of gloominess, a day of clouds and of thick darkness, as the morning spread upon the mountains: ]{.class-1}[\[watch it!\] ]{.class-0}[A GREAT PEOPLE AND A STRONG; there hath not been ever the like, neither shall be any more after it, even to the years of many generations. A fire devoureth before them]{.class-1}[ \[see 2 Thess. 1:7--8\]]{.class-0}[\...The appearance of them is as the appearance of horses ]{.class-1}[\[see Hab. 3:15\]]{.class-0}[; and horsemen ]{.class-1}[\[there's Rev. 19:14\]]{.class-0}[, so shall they run. Like the noise of chariots on the tops of the mountains shall they leap ]{.class-1}[\[see Hab. 3:3--8\]]{.class-0}[, like the noise of a flame of fire that devoureth the stubble, AS A STRONG PEOPLE SET IN BATTLE ARRAY. Before their face the people shall be much pained\...They shall run like mighty men; they shall climb the wall like men of war\...when they fall upon the sword, they shall not be wounded ]{.class-1}[\[you can't kill them because they have a body like Christ's\]]{.class-0}[\...they shall enter in at the windows like a thief ]{.class-1}[\[see John 20:19, 26\]]{.class-0}[. The earth shall quake before them; the heavens shall tremble\...the LORD shall utter his voice before HIS ARMY for his camp is very great\...for the day of the LORD is great and VERY TERRIBLE."]{.class-1}

You will find this "warrior bride" in both Greek and German mythology. In Greece, she is the Amazons; among the Germanic and Norse tribes, she is the Valkyrie, the "sword maidens of Odin." The Valkyrie were women mounted on flying horses (Rev. 19) with armor all over them; you know, a big spear and shield, horns on the helmet, etc. That's stuff in pagan mythology taken from the Bible.

Recently we had some fellow write the Bookstore about something he had read from a book written by an infidel in the Nineteenth Century. This fellow read that the story of Jonah was a copy of the story of Hercules being swallowed by a whale at Joppa. The guy who wrote the letter said the information "disturbed" him.

[Well, the Hercules myth dates to around 440 B.C. Jonah was written around 862 B.C. The Greeks had 400 years to ]{.class-0}[pick up the story of Jonah]{.class-2}[ from Phoenician mariners (Jon. 1:5--16) and pervert it to their own gods.]{.class-0}

[Solomon had a navy traveling all around the Mediterranean in 992 B.C. (see 1 Kings 10:22); he had trade caravans going all over the Middle East (1 Kings 10:15). Wherever those ships and caravans went, they took the writings of Solomon with them (1 Kings 4:32--34), and probably everything else in the Old Testament that was extant at the time (Genesis--2 Samuel and Psalms). So when you run into something in pagan mythology that matches the Bible, ]{.class-0}[it is paganism plagiarizing the Scriptures]{.class-2}[, not the Scriptures copying mythology.]{.class-0}

Verses 5--7 are a repeat of 4:1--3; see our comments on that passage.

[Verses 8--9 are a description of the Marriage of the Lamb as it is found in Psalm 45:9--14. The passage lists three groups:]{.class-0}[ "queens," "concubines,"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["virgins"]{.class-1}[ (called ]{.class-0}["daughters"]{.class-1}[ in vs. 9). These would represent different groups of saints found at the "wedding."]{.class-0}

[In ]{.class-0}["the household of God"]{.class-1}[ mentioned in Ephesians 2:19, there are different groups of ]{.class-0}["saints,"]{.class-1}[ saved in different dispensations, with whom the Church Age are made ]{.class-0}["fellowcitizens."]{.class-1}[ John R. Rice has all the "saints" from Adam onward as "the Church"; he got that by insisting all the groups listed in Hebrews 12:22--24 are the ]{.class-0}["church of the firstborn."]{.class-1}

That comes from the heresy that people in the Old Testament are saved the same way as people in the New Testament. Sometimes you will hear it put this way: "People in the Old Testament were saved by looking forward to the cross while people in the New Testament are saved by looking backwards to the cross."

[That's theological nonsense. ]{.class-0}[No one]{.class-2}[ in the Old Testament was ]{.class-0}[born again, ]{.class-2}[and ]{.class-0}[none]{.class-2}[ of them were ]{.class-0}[baptized by the Holy Spirit]{.class-2}[ into the Body of Christ. ]{.class-0}[None]{.class-2}[ of them were ]{.class-0}[individual sons of God]{.class-2}[ but Adam (Luke 3:38), and that was by ]{.class-0}[creation,]{.class-2}[ not regeneration. "Saints" in the Old Testament weren't eternally secure, and they didn't even go to the same place as a New Testament saint when they died.]{.class-0}

[Old Testament salvation had nothing to do with "looking forward to the cross." The Old Testament prophets didn't even understand what they wrote when they wrote about "the cross" (see 1 Pet. 1:10--12). Old Testament salvation consisted of ]{.class-0}[believing]{.class-2}[ what God said and ]{.class-0}[obeying]{.class-2}[ it (see any example given in Heb. 11)---]{.class-0}[faith and works.]{.class-2}

[In the New Testament, the work was done ]{.class-0}[for you]{.class-2}[ by Christ (Rom. 5:19). The only thing you have to do is ]{.class-0}[trust]{.class-2}[ what Christ did for you (John 6:29; Rom. 4:5).]{.class-0}

[Now when it comes to ]{.class-0}["the household of God,"]{.class-1}[ you not only have the Church, the Bride of Christ, you also have: 1) Old Testament saints before the Law (Job 19:25--27; Matt. 8:11), 2) Old Testament Jewish saints under the Law (Luke 16:16 cf. John 3:29), 3) Old Testament Gentiles under the Law (Rom. 2:6--15), 4) Jewish saints in the Tribulation (Rev. 7:1--8), 5) Gentile saints in the Tribulation (Rev. 7:9--17), 6) Millennial saints (Rev. 20:9). Along with the Church Age saints, those are seven different groups in the family of God.]{.class-0}

[How all of those fit into the groups listed here in verses 8--9, I am not completely sure. What you can say for sure is that the ]{.class-0}["virgins"]{.class-1}[ are the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ (see vs. 8); they would be saved Jews in the Tribulation (Rev. 14:1--4, 7:1--8 cf. Matt. 25:9--10). I take the ]{.class-0}["queens,"]{.class-1}[ which are the ]{.class-0}["kings' daughters"]{.class-1}[ of Psalm 45:9, to be Old Testament Gentiles before the Law, and the ]{.class-0}["concubines,"]{.class-1}[ associated with ]{.class-0}["the daughter of Tyre"]{.class-1}[ in Psalm 45:12, to be Old Testament Gentiles under the Law (see comments on Psa. 45:8--17 in that Commentary). Along with them will be ]{.class-0}["guests"]{.class-1}[ at the Marriage of the Lamb; they would be Tribulation Gentile saints (see Matt. 24:9--10).]{.class-0}

"[My dove, my undefiled]{.class-1}[ \[that's the Bridegroom speaking of His Bride; see 5:2\] ]{.class-0}[is but one; she is the only one of her mother, she is the choice one of her that bare her:]{.class-1}[ (vs. 9). This is Solomon's "O-A-O": his "One-And-Only." We have commented on this verse under 1:2 (which see). The ]{.class-0}["mother,"]{.class-1}[ of course, is the New Jerusalem (Gal. 4:26); she is certainly NOT the Catholic "Mary."]{.class-0}

[Now if you consult Bullinger, Stam, O'Hair, and the Hyperdispensationalists, they will tell you that "the Church is nowhere revealed in the Old Testament." What they actually mean is that no one ever ]{.class-0}[found]{.class-2}[ it in the Old Testament until Paul. But as we said in our comments under 1:2 (which see), every woman married to a ]{.class-0}[type of Christ]{.class-2}[ in the Old Testament is a type of ]{.class-0}[the Church]{.class-2}[. The woman here in this verse is so plainly a type of the Church, that you would have to be blind not to see the connections to 1 Corinthians 12, Ephesians 4, and Ephesians 5.]{.class-0}

[The Song of Solomon has two peculiar things about it that set it apart from the other books of the Bible. First, it, like the book of Esther, never uses the words ]{.class-0}[God]{.class-2}[ or ]{.class-0}[Lord]{.class-2}[ in it, but even unsaved Jewish scholars can see that Solomon is ]{.class-0}[a type]{.class-2}[ of the Lord (see Introduction to the book). Second, the Song of Solomon is the only book of the Old Testament that is not quoted in the New Testament. All the other 38 books of the Old Testament are referred to by the New Testament writers, but not Song of Solomon. But the one book of the Old Testament that has the most information about the Church is the Song of Solomon.]{.class-0}

"[The daughters saw her, and blessed her; yea, the queens and the concubines, and they praised her."]{.class-1}[ This is a reference to Revelation 19:6--7.]{.class-0}

10 Who is she that looketh forth as the morning, fair as the moon, clear as the sun, and terrible as an army with banners?

11 I went down into the garden of nuts to see the fruits of the valley, and to see whether the vine flourished, and the pomegranates budded.

12 Or ever I was aware, my soul made me like the chariots of Amminadib.

13 Return, return, O Shulamite; return, return, that we may look upon thee. What will ye see in the Shulamite? As it were the company of two armies.

[We have already determined that the Bride here in chapter 6 is the ]{.class-0}["one body"]{.class-1}[ of Ephesians 4:4, which is ]{.class-0}["the church"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 1:22--23), the Bride of Christ (Eph. 5 30--32). I say that because here in verse 10 the Bride is given four similitudes: 1) ]{.class-0}["she that looketh forth AS THE MORNING,"]{.class-1}[ 2) ]{.class-0}["fair AS THE MOON,"]{.class-1}[ 3) ]{.class-0}["clear AS THE SUN,"]{.class-1}[ 4) ]{.class-0}["terrible AS AN ARMY with banners."]{.class-1}

[Now, back in verse 8, she was called ]{.class-0}["my undefiled,"]{.class-1}[ so you know she can't be the woman of Revelation 17 because that woman is ]{.class-0}["THE MOTHER OF HARLOTS AND ABOMINATIONS OF THE EARTH"]{.class-1}[ (Rev. 17:5). There's nothing ]{.class-0}["undefiled"]{.class-1}[ about her. But look at Revelation 12:1.]{.class-0}

"[And there appeared a great wonder in heaven: a woman clothed with THE SUN, and THE MOON under her feet, and upon her head a crown of twelve stars."]{.class-1}

[There's ]{.class-0}["a woman"]{.class-1}[ connected with ]{.class-0}["the sun"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["the moon"]{.class-1}[ just like the woman here in verse 10. Now if you consult any postmillennial or amillennial expositor, he will be quick to tell you that the ]{.class-0}["woman"]{.class-1}[ of Revelation 12:1 IS the Church. But that can't be because that woman ]{.class-0}[gives birth to Jesus Christ]{.class-2}[ (see Rev. 12:5). Jesus Christ begat the Church (James 1:18); the Church didn't give birth to Jesus Christ. For that reason, the Catholic Church makes the woman Mary and then says Mary is the "Queen of Heaven" because the woman in Revelation 12:1 has ]{.class-0}["a crown of twelve stars."]{.class-1}[ But in the Bible, the ]{.class-0}["queen of heaven"]{.class-1}[ is a ]{.class-0}[female demon]{.class-2}[ (Jer. 44:17--19).]{.class-0}

So if the woman in Revelation 12 isn't the Church and it isn't Mary, who is she? Look at Genesis 37:9--10.

"[And he ]{.class-1}[\[Joseph\]]{.class-0}[ dreamed yet another dream, and told it his brethren, and said, Behold, I have dreamed a dream more; and, behold, THE SUN and THE MOON and THE ELEVEN STARS made obeisance to me. And he told it to his father, and to his brethren: and his father rebuked him, and said unto him, What is this dream that thou hast dreamed? Shall I AND THY MOTHER AND THY BRETHREN indeed come to bow down ourselves to thee to the earth?"]{.class-1}

[In those two verses, Jacob is ]{.class-0}["the sun,"]{.class-1}[ Jacob's wife is ]{.class-0}["the moon,"]{.class-1}[ and Jacob's twelve sons are the ]{.class-0}["stars"]{.class-1}[ (Joseph himself being the twelfth star). So the woman in Revelation 21:1 is ]{.class-0}[Israel,]{.class-2}[ not the Church or Mary. If that weren't enough, the first time the word ]{.class-0}["armies"]{.class-1}[ shows up in the Bible (Exod. 6:26), it is a reference to Israel.]{.class-0}

[But notice the difference between the woman of Revelation 12:1 and the woman here in Song 6:9--10. The woman in Revelation 12 is ]{.class-0}["CLOTHED WITH the sun,"]{.class-1}[ not ]{.class-0}["CLEAR AS the sun."]{.class-1}[ The woman in Song 6 is ]{.class-0}["FAIR AS the moon"]{.class-1}[; she doesn't have ]{.class-0}["the moon under her feet."]{.class-1}[ The woman here in verse 10 is ]{.class-0}["as an army"]{.class-1}[ SINGULAR, not plural ]{.class-0}["armies"]{.class-1}[ as in Exodus 6:26.]{.class-0}

[The woman here in Song 6 is ]{.class-0}["ONE"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 9), as in the ]{.class-0}["chaste virgin"]{.class-1}[ (]{.class-0}[singular]{.class-2}[) of 2 Corinthians 11:2. She is not the ]{.class-0}[plural]{.class-2}[ ]{.class-0}["virgins"]{.class-1}[ of Song 6:8--9; Matthew 25:1--2; and Revelation 14:4.]{.class-0}

[The Bride of Christ ]{.class-0}["looketh forth as the morning"]{.class-1}[ when ]{.class-0}["the day dawn, and the day star arise in your hearts"]{.class-1}[ (2 Pet. 1:19 cf. Mal. 4:2; 2 Sam. 23:4). So the reference here in verse 10 is a reference to the Church at the Second Advent. When Christ returns at the Second Advent, the Church returns with Him ]{.class-0}["as an army"]{.class-1}[ (see comments on vs. 4). At the Advent, the Church is like ]{.class-0}["the sun"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 13:42) after going through the "night" of the Church Age (Matt. 14:23--25) like ]{.class-0}["the moon"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 5:14 cf. John 8:12).]{.class-0}

[Right now, in the dispensation of the Church Age, we are in ]{.class-0}["the night"]{.class-1}[ (John 9:4--5). In Isaiah 21:11, ]{.class-0}["the watchman"]{.class-1}[ is asked to report on the times and seasons. The question is ]{.class-0}["Watchman, what of the night? Watchman, what of the night?"]{.class-1}[ The ]{.class-0}["watchman"]{.class-1}[ was in ]{.class-0}["the night,"]{.class-1}[ but he was in the last watch of the night (see Matt. 14:25; Mark 13:35) because he says]{.class-0}[ "the morning cometh, and also the night"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 21:12). What you have in Isaiah 21:11--12 is a picture of the ]{.class-0}[Church Age as night,]{.class-2}[ the Rapture of the Church as the morning, followed by the Tribulation as night again. What follows the night of the Tribulation? ]{.class-0}["The Sun of righteousness"]{.class-1}[ arises]{.class-0}[ "with healing in his wings"]{.class-1}[ (Mal. 4:2) at the Second Advent.]{.class-0}

[In the nighttime of the Church Age, the Church is like]{.class-0}[ the moon.]{.class-2}[ On the negative side, I observe that the moon is an ]{.class-0}[earthbound satellite:]{.class-2}[ it can't ever be free of the earth. Like the moon, the Church is bound to this world until her Lord comes to take her away. You may be born again and seated with Christ ]{.class-0}["in heavenly places" ]{.class-1}[(Eph. 2:6), but you are stuck to this earth until the Lord sets you free. Your body lives on this earth, and all too soon it is drawn back into it and buried.]{.class-0}

[The next thing I notice about the moon is that it's a ]{.class-0}[dead planet.]{.class-2}[ Colossians 3:3 says, ]{.class-0}["For ye are dead, and your life is hid with Christ in God."]{.class-1}[ Paul said, ]{.class-0}["I am crucified with Christ"]{.class-1}[ (Gal. 2:2). That means that when a person gets saved, his old nature that is connected to his body of flesh is crucified with Christ]{.class-0}[ "that the body of sin might be destroyed, that henceforth we should not serve sin"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 6:6). So baptism, among other things, is a picture of ]{.class-0}[death]{.class-2}[ (Rom. 6:3--4). When a Christian gets saved, he's walking around in his old body, but the Bible says it's dead: it's a corpse. Paul says, ]{.class-0}["Reckon]{.class-1}[ \[that means to "count it as so"\]]{.class-0}[ ye also yourselves to be dead indeed unto sin."]{.class-1}[ All some Christians do is spend their life running errands for a corpse.]{.class-0}

[On the more positive side, I observe that the moon ]{.class-0}[follows the sun.]{.class-2}[ In Psalm 19:4--5, the Bridegroom (Jesus Christ in type) is likened to the sun. So the nearest thing to true worship is sun worship; in pagan idolatry, the chief god is usually the ]{.class-0}[sun]{.class-2}[ god (]{.class-0}[Ra]{.class-2}[ in Egypt, ]{.class-0}[Baal]{.class-2}[ in the Canaanite religions). So just as the moon follows the sun in the sky, a Christian ought to follow his Saviour.]{.class-0}

[The moon ]{.class-0}[has no light of its own]{.class-2}[. Job 25:5 says, ]{.class-0}["Behold even to the moon, and it shineth not"]{.class-1}[; that's a scientific statement of fact. The moon doesn't shine; ]{.class-0}[it reflects the light of the sun.]{.class-2}[ Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["I am the light of the world"]{.class-1}[ (John 8:12), but He also said, ]{.class-0}["Ye are the light of the world"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 5:14). But the ]{.class-0}["light"]{.class-1}[ the Christian gives to a lost world is not his own; back in John 8:12, Jesus continued and said, ]{.class-0}["he that followeth me shall not walk in darkness, but shall have the light of life."]{.class-1}[ The Christian is to reflect the life of his Saviour.]{.class-0}

But as the light of the moon waxes and wanes, so does the light of the Christian. Sometimes the Body of Christ gives off a bright, shining light, and sometimes it doesn't. The testimony of the Church ought to be strong and powerful so that it guides and moves things in the world like the moon moves the tides. But the sad fact is that the testimony of the Church today is so sorry, so lukewarm, so weak, and so worldly that it has little influence on the community around it.

Evangelists like Billy Sunday and Sam Jones used to go into a town, and when they left, there wouldn't be one theater or one saloon left open. Billy Graham goes into a town, and when he leaves, nothing has changed despite the number of people that walked the aisle in his meetings.

[A few years back here in Pensacola, there was a three-ring circus going on called "The Brownsville Revival." The Assembly of God pastor and the evangelist conducting the meetings (John Kilpatrick and Stephen Hill) were reporting thousands saved (most of them were just Charismatic retreads, some as many as six or seven times). They said so many people were getting saved in Pensacola that the police were bringing criminals and drug dealers to the meetings to get saved so the crime rate went down. The ]{.class-0}[Pensacola News Journal]{.class-2}[ did an investigation of that thing and found out the ]{.class-0}[crime rate went up,]{.class-2}[ the ]{.class-0}[drug rate went up]{.class-2}[, and the ]{.class-0}[prostitution rate went up.]{.class-2}[ Not one bar or liquor store within five miles of the Brownsville Assembly of God was shut down. The whole thing was just a great big show to con a bunch of Charismatic suckers out of millions of dollars (literally) and to cause lost sinners to mock the cause of Christ.]{.class-0}

[Do you know what ]{.class-0}[did ]{.class-2}[shut down some of the bars here in Pensacola? Some of our young men getting out on the streets and preaching and witnessing and passing out tracts. Over the years, we have seen at least ]{.class-0}[three bars]{.class-2}[ shut down like that.]{.class-0}

[While that Brownsville mess was going on, there were people coming out of town to go to it, and they just happened to come into town on a Saturday afternoon when ]{.class-0}[our young men ]{.class-2}[were out street preaching. Those Charismatics were so excited because they thought the Brownsville Revival had spread out on the street. They didn't realize that the students of the Pensacola Bible Institute had been doing that for ]{.class-0}[twenty years]{.class-2}[ before Stephen Hill even showed up here in Pensacola. ]{.class-0}[No one]{.class-2}[ from the Brownsville Revival ]{.class-0}[preached on the street or passed out tracts or witnessed in public.]{.class-2}[ You had the light of one group of Christians ]{.class-0}[waxing]{.class-2}[ on one side of town while the light of another group was ]{.class-0}[waning]{.class-2}[ on the other side of town.]{.class-0}

[All right, another way the Church should be like the moon is that the moon goes ]{.class-0}[against the world.]{.class-2}[ The earth rotates west to east, and the moon travels across the sky in the opposite direction: east to west. The Church should be out of fellowship with the world. Paul said, ]{.class-0}["be not conformed to this world: but be transformed by the renewing of your mind"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 12:2). John wrote, ]{.class-0}["Love not the world, neither the things that are in the world"]{.class-1}[ (1 John 2:15). Any Christian who is a friend of God is an enemy of the world, and any Christian who is ]{.class-0}["a friend of the world is the enemy of God"]{.class-1}[ (James 4:4).]{.class-0}

When the earth gets directly between the moon and the sun, you have a lunar eclipse: the shadow of the earth passes over the moon and puts its light out. When the world gets between the Christian and His Lord, the light of the Christian goes out because the world has blocked the Christian from his source of light.

[Now as we have already said, verse 10 is clearly the Second Advent with no other interpretation allowed, but no Jewish Rabbi or Hebrew scholar could make heads or tails out of the passage because they all have an instinctive, programmed, built-in tendency to ]{.class-0}[omit ]{.class-2}[the Second Coming of Jesus Christ. I thought before moving on to ]{.class-0}["the garden of NUTS"]{.class-1}[ in the next verse, that it would be appropriate to give you a sampling of a typical, rotten piece of exegesis put out by the Scholars' Union. In this case, it was put out by Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown; they had no more idea of how to handle the passage than any other Biblical illiterate in the Alexandrian Cult.]{.class-0}

[According to Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown, ]{.class-0}["the morning"]{.class-1}[ is the Church not coming to the fullness of her light. ]{.class-0}["The sun"]{.class-1}[ isn't Christ at all; it's the light of the ]{.class-0}[Church's justification.]{.class-2}[ They get the cross-reference to Matthew 13:42 for ]{.class-0}["the sun,"]{.class-1}[ but when they got to the ]{.class-0}["army,"]{.class-1}[ they fell all to pieces. Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown applied the term to starry angelic hosts which they leave ]{.class-0}[unidentified.]{.class-2}[ They refer you to Revelation 12:1 for the ]{.class-0}["army,"]{.class-1}[ which is a perfect blank. Finally, when interpreting the whole verse, they say the Church Triumphant (an old-time reference to the saints in Heaven) is the bannered ]{.class-0}["army,"]{.class-1}[ the Adventical Church is likened to ]{.class-0}["the sun,"]{.class-1}[ and the Levitical Church is likened to ]{.class-0}["the moon."]{.class-1}

[That is the mess into which you get with a non-scriptural exegesis based on ]{.class-0}[opinions]{.class-2}[ and ]{.class-0}[preferences.]{.class-2}[ That's the "scholarship" of every scholar in the Nineteenth, Twentieth, and Twenty-first Centuries who attempted to correct the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ text. They're all "birds of a feather"---cuckoos.]{.class-0}

[Verse 11:]{.class-0}[ "I went down into the garden of nuts."]{.class-1}[ There's a good verse for "dynamic equivalence." The Bridegroom is the ]{.class-0}["I"]{.class-1}[ of the verse, and ]{.class-0}["the garden"]{.class-1}[ is the ]{.class-0}["garden"]{.class-1}[ of 4:12 and 5:1 where it refers to the Bride. So Christians are the ]{.class-0}["nuts"]{.class-1}[ in ]{.class-0}["the garden."]{.class-1}[ Speaking facetiously, I can say that's absolutely true; I have known some Christians who were just as nutty as a pecan pie. The world thinks Bible-believing Christians are all nuts (see our comments on 1 Pet. 2:9 in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

[Of course, that is not the real meaning of the passage. What the correct interpretation is, I will have to plead ]{.class-0}["Ich weiss nicht"]{.class-2}[ (I don't know). After going through the Bible over 150 times, I must confess that there are some things I have not gotten and probably never will get. When I get over in Zechariah 1:8 and read about ]{.class-0}["a red horse"]{.class-1}[ standing ]{.class-0}["among the myrtle trees that were in the bottom,"]{.class-1}[ I'm lost, man, I'm lost.]{.class-0}

[The word ]{.class-0}["nuts"]{.class-1}[ only occurs twice in the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ Bible: here and in Genesis 43:11 where they are given as some ]{.class-0}["of the best fruits"]{.class-1}[ in the Promised Land. In that verse, ]{.class-0}["nuts"]{.class-1}[ are distinguished from ]{.class-0}["almonds,"]{.class-1}[ which are nuts as well. Two nut-bearing trees are given by name in Genesis 30:37---the hazelnut and the chestnut trees. According to all the Bible dictionaries, the ]{.class-0}["nuts"]{.class-1}[ in Genesis 43:11 are supposed to be ]{.class-0}[pistachio nuts,]{.class-2}[ and the ]{.class-0}["nuts"]{.class-1}[ here in verse 11 are supposed to be ]{.class-0}[walnuts.]{.class-2}

[What you can gather from Genesis 43:11 and the passage in Song 4:12--14 is that Solomon's ]{.class-0}["garden"]{.class-1}[ contained the very best of the land of Canaan and the most exotic plants from abroad.]{.class-0}

[The rest of verse 11 goes on to say: ]{.class-0}["I went down into the garden of nuts to see the fruits of the valley, and to see whether the vine flourished, and the pomegranates budded."]{.class-1}[ So the idea is that the Bridegroom is going into His garden to check and see if there is any fruit, and of course, He is seeking the fruit of His relationship with the Bride.]{.class-0}

[The two specific fruits He mentions are ]{.class-0}["the vine"]{.class-1}[ (grapes) and ]{.class-0}["the pomegranates."]{.class-1}[ Both are "aggregate fruits"; i.e., several fruits in one. The grapes come in a "cluster," and the pomegranate is filled with things like the parts of a berry. Both are pictures of the Body of Christ bearing ]{.class-0}["the fruit of the Spirit"]{.class-1}[ (Gal. 5:22).]{.class-0}

[Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["I am the vine, ye are the branches: He that abideth in me, and I in him, the same bringeth forth much fruit"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:5). The spiritual application is that every Christian has within him the incorruptible seed of ]{.class-0}["the word of God"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 1:23), and that seed should produce ]{.class-0}["love, joy, peace, longsuffering,"]{.class-1}[ etc., in his life.]{.class-0}

[Not only that, but a Christian should reproduce ]{.class-0}["fruit after his kind"]{.class-1}[ (Gen. 1:11). One of the fruits of a Christian is other Christians (Rom. 1:13). Any Christian ought to be able to lead at least one soul to Christ a year.]{.class-0}

[Verse 12: ]{.class-0}["Or ever I was aware ]{.class-1}[\[meaning "before I was aware of it" or "before I realized it"\]]{.class-0}[, my soul made me like the chariots of Amminadib." "Amminadib" ]{.class-1}[is another spelling of ]{.class-0}[Amminadab.]{.class-2}[ Amminadab was the father of Nahshon, the head of the tribe of Judah in the book of Numbers (Num. 2:3). Amminadab was also the father-in-law of Aaron (Exod. 6:23). So ]{.class-0}["the chariots of Amminadib"]{.class-1}[ were an armored division in the army of Judah.]{.class-0}

[Verse 12 is obviously a reference to the Second Advent of Jesus Christ. For the connection of ]{.class-0}["the chariots"]{.class-1}[ to the Second Coming, see our comments on 3:9. Psalm 68:17 says,]{.class-0}[ "The chariots of God are twenty thousand, even thousands of angels: the Lord is among them."]{.class-1}[ Those are ]{.class-0}["the chariots"]{.class-1}[ at the Second Advent (cf. Jude 14--15; 2 Thess. 1:7--8).]{.class-0}

"[Return, return, O Shulamite"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 13). Some of the commentators will tell you that ]{.class-0}["Shulamite"]{.class-1}[ is another form of ]{.class-0}["Shunammite"]{.class-1}[ and identify ]{.class-0}["the Shulamite"]{.class-1}[ here in verse 13 with ]{.class-0}["Abishag the Shunammite"]{.class-1}[ (1 Kings 1:15). But the "Bride" in Song of Solomon is ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[Abishag (see our comments on 1:5).]{.class-0}

[The word ]{.class-0}["Shulamite"]{.class-1}[ is related to the words ]{.class-0}[shalom]{.class-2}[ and ]{.class-0}[Salem.]{.class-2}[ The meaning is "peaceful." The Hebrew lexicographer Gesenius said the word is a feminine form of ]{.class-0}[Solomon.]{.class-2}[ Be that as it may, ]{.class-0}["the Shulamite"]{.class-1}[ is the female counterpart of Solomon: she is "Mrs. Solomon."]{.class-0}

[Once more, the application is that the Bride of Christ is like her Saviour. He is ]{.class-0}["The Prince of Peace"]{.class-1}[ (Isa. 9:6). Paul said, ]{.class-0}["For he]{.class-1}[ \[i.e., Jesus Christ\]]{.class-0}[ is our peace, who hath made both one ]{.class-1}[\[Jews and Gentiles in one Body\]]{.class-0}[, and hath broken down the middle wall of partition between us"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 2:14). So the Church has the ]{.class-0}["peace"]{.class-1}[ of her Lord.]{.class-0}

[Jesus told His disciples, ]{.class-0}["Peace I leave with you, my peace I give unto you"]{.class-1}[ (John 14:27). God has ]{.class-0}["called us to peace"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 7:15). Christians are commanded to ]{.class-0}["live in peace"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 13:11). Part of ]{.class-0}["the fruit of the Spirit"]{.class-1}[ is ]{.class-0}["peace"]{.class-1}[ (Gal. 5:22). Christians are to have their ]{.class-0}["feet shod with the preparation of the gospel of peace"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 6:15).]{.class-0}

[Now, that ]{.class-0}["peace"]{.class-1}[ is much more than ]{.class-0}[spiritual peace ]{.class-2}[with God or living with other people without fussing and fighting. The context of Song 6:12 is the Second Advent (see vs. 11). So Micah 5:5 says about Christ (see Mic. 5:2), ]{.class-0}["And this man shall be the peace, when the Assyrian]{.class-1}[ \[a reference to the Antichrist---see Isa. 10:5, 24, 14:25, 30:31\]]{.class-0}[ shall come into our land: and when he shall tread in our palaces."]{.class-1}[ When Jesus Christ comes back at the Second Advent, He ends the war the Antichrist began against ]{.class-0}["the saints"]{.class-1}[ and against Israel (Rev. 13:7; Zech. 12:2--3, 14:2). He ends it the same way America ended its war against Japan (Zech. 14:12). He bring peace by the ]{.class-0}[total destruction of His enemies ]{.class-2}[(Psa. 68:21--23).]{.class-0}

[That is the peace ]{.class-0}["the Shulamite"]{.class-1}[ brings. Look at the last part of the verse. ]{.class-0}["What will ye see in the Shulamite? As it were the company of two armies."]{.class-1}[ Those are ]{.class-0}["the armies\...in heaven"]{.class-1}[ which come down with Jesus Christ at the Battle of Armageddon (Rev. 19:14).]{.class-0}

[Now, ]{.class-0}["the Shulamite"]{.class-1}[ is asked to ]{.class-0}["return, return, that we may look upon thee."]{.class-1}[ The speakers in verse 13 are the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem"]{.class-1}[ we encountered in 5:9--6:1.]{.class-0}

[The picture, here, is the Jews in the Tribulation calling for the Church to come back with Christ. They say, ]{.class-0}["return, return, that we may look upon thee."]{.class-1}

Those saved Jews at the end of the Tribulation know the Church has gone up to Heaven, and they know the Church is going to come back with Christ. I don't claim to understand all the details of the Tribulation, but I do know that Jesus makes an appearance to the Jews at the end of the Tribulation at some point before the Advent (see Rev. 14:14--15). Maybe when He makes this appearance, the Jews down on the ground see Christ up in Heaven, and they see the host with Him, but that's an indefinite thing.

What we do know for sure is that, right now, the very creation itself is waiting for the Church to return with her Lord.

"[For the earnest expectation of the creature waiteth for the manifestation of the sons of God\...Because the creature itself also shall be delivered from the bondage of corruption into the glorious liberty of the sons of God"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 8:19, 21).]{.class-0}

"[What will ye see in the Shulamite? As it were the company of two armies."]{.class-1}[ Notice that the ]{.class-0}["armies"]{.class-1}[ of Revelation 19:14 are ]{.class-0}["two armies"]{.class-1}[ (see also Gen. 32:1--2; Judg. 5:10--11, 19--20). Every corrector of the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ from 1700--2010 missed that.]{.class-0}

[One army is the Body of Christ (vs. 10, note the ]{.class-0}[singular]{.class-2}[), and the other army is Old Testament Jewish saints (Ezek. 37:4). The Body of Christ goes up at the Rapture (Rev. 4:1), and the Old Testament Jewish saints are caught up in a post-Tribulation rapture (Psa. 50:4--7; Ezek. 37:1--10; Rev. 11:11--12). So at the beginning of the verse, there are two sets of ]{.class-0}["return, return"]{.class-1}[: that is one call for the ]{.class-0}[Church ]{.class-2}[and another call for ]{.class-0}[Israel]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[Bullinger, just as blind as Stevie Wonder or Ray Charles, devotes a twelve-line paragraph of tiny print---with twenty words on each line---to get you to interpret the passage as ]{.class-0}["the Shulamite"]{.class-1}[ being a ]{.class-0}[beautiful view]{.class-2}[ like Jacob saw at Mahanaim (Gen. 32:1--2). That's what you end up with for suggesting 5,000 changes in the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ text: a perfect blank that you couldn't exposit or apply once you've made the change.]{.class-0}

CHAPTER 7

7:1 How beautiful are thy feet with shoes, O prince's daughter! the joints of thy thighs are like jewels, the work of the hands of a cunning workman.

2 Thy navel is like a round goblet, which wanteth not liquor: thy belly is like an heap of wheat set about with lilies.

3 Thy two breasts are like two young roes that are twins.

4 Thy neck is as a tower of ivory; thine eyes like the fishpools in Heshbon, by the gate of Bathrabbim: thy nose is as the tower of Lebanon which looketh toward Damascus.

5 Thine head upon thee is like Carmel, and the hair of thine head like purple; the king is held in the galleries.

6 How fair and how pleasant art thou, O love, for delights!

7 This thy stature is like to a palm tree, and thy breasts to clusters of grapes.

8 I said, I will go up to the palm tree, I will take hold of the boughs thereof: now also thy breasts shall be as clusters of the vine, and the smell of thy nose like apples;

9 And the roof of thy mouth like the best wine for my beloved, that goeth down sweetly, causing the lips of those that are asleep to speak.

The whole chapter is divided into two parts. Verses 1--9 are the Bridegroom continuing to praise and brag about His Bride; verses 10--13 are the Bride's response. Now we have run into this kind of thing before in chapter 4. The Bridegroom goes into great detail describing the beauty of the Bride. Of course, there are things in those descriptions that you don't preach or expound publicly because they are very intimate. Those passages are meant for private reading.

[There is no part of the Bible that the advocates of "free love," the "new morality," and "situation ethics" (the "buzz words" for ]{.class-0}[fornication]{.class-2}[) love more than the book of Song of Solomon.]{.class-0}

[Now the Bible has ]{.class-0}[everything]{.class-2}[ in it---including sex; it doesn't leave out anything. The difference between the Song of Solomon and ]{.class-0}[Playboy, Penthouse, Hustler,]{.class-2}[ etc., when it comes to sex, is that the Song of Solomon puts sex in its proper place---]{.class-0}[between a married husband and wife.]{.class-2}[ The Song of Solomon has the proper exercise of love between a husband and his wife written out. Because those things are written down where anyone can read them, every sex-obsessed neurotic who has his mind in the sewer likes Song of Solomon more than any other book in the Bible.]{.class-0}

[You can find references and excerpts to the Song of Solomon in nearly every magazine newsstand in the world. Other religions will copy the book (e.g., the Buddhist ]{.class-0}[Karma Sutra]{.class-2}[). Long before I was ever saved, I remember seeing paperback after paperback copies of the Song of Solomon; there's a lot of pornographic literature on it. The reason for all of this is because ]{.class-0}["the natural man receiveth not the things of the Spirit of God"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 2:14), so he takes the book and uses it for carnal purposes.]{.class-0}

Of course, there's nothing wrong or sinful about the description here. In its context, everything is high and holy and proper. But men like to pervert the word of God and rip such passages as this out of their context and give them a dirty meaning.

There are certain passages in the Bible that just aren't meant for public preaching and teaching anyway. I have never preached a message on Ezekiel 23 or Ezekiel 16. Of course, none of the material in those two chapters or here in Song of Solomon can stack up to the stuff being shown these days right in your own living room. You've got stuff on cable television these days that would have taken an act of Congress to be published when I was growing up. But for the sake of decency and sensitivity, there are just some things that don't need to be discussed in a mixed audience of women and children.

[The Bible is like a medical book. There are some parts of a medical book that are for ]{.class-0}[private practice ]{.class-2}[in the office, there are some parts that can be discussed and taught in public, and there are some parts for students. The Bible is the same way. There are some parts that don't need to be brought up before children, there are some parts you wouldn't discuss except behind closed doors, and there are some parts for students studying for the ministry. There are some parts of the Bible that are for private devotion, study, and reading; ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[for public preaching and teaching.]{.class-0}

[John R. Rice said one time that he wanted to live to preach on every verse in the Bible at one time or another. I wouldn't even attempt that. With all due respect to the Lord and the Devil, much of it makes dull reading, not to mention preaching and teaching. I'd like to see a man preach 1 Chronicles 1, 2, or 3 and really put his soul into it, brother. Try preaching on the ]{.class-0}["ouches"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["taches"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["loops"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["fillets"]{.class-1}[ in Exodus 26 some time. I know there's a lot of typology in the gold and silver and other materials; I have written a commentary on the subject. But when it comes to ]{.class-0}["Ten cubits shall be the length of a board, and a cubit and a half shall be the breadth of one board. Two tenons shall there be in one board, set in order one against another\...And thou shalt make forty sockets of silver under the twenty boards, two sockets under one board for his two tenons"]{.class-1}[ (Exod. 26:16--19), that's some rough stuff. So some of the Bible is for private consumption, as we shall see from much of what follows.]{.class-0}

"[How beautiful are thy feet with shoes, O prince's daughter!"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 1). Now that's the Bridegroom bragging about the Bride, and up to this point, with the exception of verses 2--7 in chapter 5, the woman has been the Bride of Christ, and we will certainly make that ]{.class-0}[spiritual application]{.class-2}[ here. But the passage is not without its problems.]{.class-0}

[First, the Bridegroom calls the woman a ]{.class-0}["prince's daughter."]{.class-1}[ Who was the prince that begat her? Well, it could be a reference to Christ. The Bride is called ]{.class-0}["the king's daughter"]{.class-1}[ in Psalm 45:13, and a King in the Bible is sometimes called a Prince (see 1 Kings 1:34, 14:7, 16:2; Ezek. 12:10). Jesus Christ is called a ]{.class-0}["Prince"]{.class-1}[ in Isaiah 9:6; Daniel 9:25; Acts 3:15, 5:31; and Revelation 1:5.]{.class-0}

[But here you have the Bridegroom, a type of Jesus Christ, referring to the woman as a ]{.class-0}["prince's daughter."]{.class-1}[ Well, the woman is not Solomon's daughter. Historically, the "Prince" would be Pharaoh (see comments on 1:5), but ]{.class-0}[doctrinally]{.class-2}[ is something else.]{.class-0}

[Up to this point, the Bridegroom has referred to the woman as ]{.class-0}["my sister, my spouse"]{.class-1}[ (4:9--10, 12, 5:1), not as His ]{.class-0}["daughter."]{.class-1}[ Well, if that's the case, then why would the Bride of Christ pray that Christ was ]{.class-0}[as ]{.class-2}[her brother? Look at 8:1, ]{.class-0}["O that thou wert as my brother."]{.class-1}[ Christ ]{.class-0}[is]{.class-2}[ your brother if you are saved: He is ]{.class-0}["the firstborn among many brethren"]{.class-1}[ (Heb. 2:11).]{.class-0}

[Given that, I have often thought that what follows in chapters 7 and 8 is not the Bride of Christ, but yet another woman. If you entertain the possibility that it might be another woman, do you realize that would give you ]{.class-0}[three different women]{.class-2}[ in the Song of Solomon who are all represented by the one woman in the book? You would have the Bride of Christ in chapters 1--4, a woman representing Tribulation Jews in 5:2--7 (see comments on that passage), and then a third one in chapters 7--8. Now I can't prove that, but boy, when you get comparing Scripture with Scripture, you'll have a hard time making this last one the Bride of Christ.]{.class-0}

[There might even be a ]{.class-0}[fourth woman]{.class-2}[ in the book. Look at 8:8--9, ]{.class-0}["We have a litter sister ]{.class-1}[\[we do?\]]{.class-0}[\...what shall we do for our sister in the day when she shall be spoken for? If she be a wall, we will build upon her a palace of silver: and if she be a door, we will inclose her with boards of cedar."]{.class-1}

[I'm lost; I don't know where I am, man. If she's ]{.class-0}["a wall,"]{.class-1}[ and if she's not ]{.class-0}["a wall,"]{.class-1}[ she's ]{.class-0}["a door"]{.class-1}[? I'm out! I've read through that thing at least 152 times, and I don't get a thing out of it.]{.class-0}

[That just goes to show you that there's a lot of stuff in that Bible that nobody's got worked out yet. I've read all the commentaries on it; J. Peter Lange, Jamieson, Fausset, and Brown, Matthew Henry, Adam Clarke, and the ]{.class-0}[Pulpit Commentary]{.class-2}[ can't give you anything on it. After reading Bullinger on it, you come out just as blind as when you came in. I believe it was Sam Jones who said, "If I understood everything in the Bible, I'd know that someone wrote it who didn't have any more sense than I've got."]{.class-0}

[Now, if you can match those four women to different parts of "the family of God" (see comments on 6:8--9), you would have something. If I had to hazard a guess, I would make one woman the Old Testament saints, another woman the New Testament saints, one of the women the Tribulation saints, and one of those women the Millennial saints: four groups, each one likened to a woman in the Song of Solomon. I don't know if you can do that, but there it is. The Old Testament saints in Israel are likened to a cast-off wife in Hosea 1--2; the New Testament saints are likened to the Bride of Christ, ]{.class-0}["a chaste virgin" "espoused\...to one husband"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 11:2); and the Tribulation saints are likened to virgins (Matt. 25:1--13). It's the Millennial saints that you can't do much with, because there's nothing in the Bible comparing ]{.class-0}[them ]{.class-2}[to a woman.]{.class-0}

[Be that as it may, we are going to take the spiritual application in this passage; it's probably off doctrinally. If we make this woman the Bride of Christ, then the cross-reference to ]{.class-0}["How beautiful are thy feet with shoes"]{.class-1}[ would be Romans 10:15, ]{.class-0}["How beautiful are the feet of them that preach the gospel of peace, and bring glad tidings of good things!"]{.class-1}[ In the Christian's armor, he is to have his ]{.class-0}["feet shod with the preparation of the gospel of peace"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 6:15).]{.class-0}

The spiritual reference is to the Bride of Christ as a witness. The idea is that the Christian ought to be prepared to preach the Gospel. So a Christian should never go any place where he can't preach and witness. Folks ask what's wrong with this or what's wrong with that. Well, that's easy: just stay out of any place where you couldn't witness if you had to.

[Now that solves a lot of problems for a Christian. What's wrong with a dance hall or a pool hall? Not a thing in the world; just make sure you're a ]{.class-0}[good witness]{.class-2}[ when you go. When you're in the middle of a watusi, turn to your partner and ask, "Have you ever been born again?" You say, "I couldn't do that." Then stay away from it.]{.class-0}

[That applies to any kind of company you keep. Don't ever be caught in company where, if you get the opportunity to ]{.class-0}[give a witness]{.class-2}[, you can't stand right up and give it. I wouldn't hang around anybody to whom I couldn't talk about the Bible or the things of Christ. I was out door-knocking one time and came to this house where the fellow told me to leave my Bible and that "Christ stuff" outside. I told him, "I don't go in any place where Jesus Christ isn't welcome. See ya' around, buddy."]{.class-0}

[Be ready ]{.class-0}[to witness]{.class-2}[ and preach the Gospel to anybody, any place, any time the opportunity presents itself. If there's a place where you feel ashamed to present the Gospel, ]{.class-0}[don't go there.]{.class-2}[ If you'd be embarrassed to talk about Jesus Christ to your friends, dump 'em. Have ]{.class-0}["your feet shod with the preparation of the gospel of peace."]{.class-1}

Now, what follows in the rest of verse 1 and verses 2, 3, 4, and 5 is the Bridegroom describing the Bride in the language of love. Americans aren't used to that anymore. I don't know what in the world a woman would think if you told her that her eyes were like "fishpools" and her nose was like a "tower." If you said, "Honey, you've got a nose like the Empire State Building," I don't know what kind of reaction you'd get, but I don't think it would be a good one.

The old joke about this sort of thing is that a guy is trying to woo his ugly girlfriend with a lot of flowery talk and tells her: "Sweetheart, your teeth are like stars---they come out at night; your eyes are like pools---cesspools; your ears are like flowers---cauliflowers; your hands are like petals---bicycle pedals; your hair is like the sea---the Dead Sea."

A teenager was trying to make an impression on this girl one time and said, "My, what beautiful blue lips and red eyes you have." He got his words all mixed up.

Now what you have to remember about this description is that this is an Oriental way of thinking; that is why it doesn't make much sense to the Western mind. If you want to brag about someone, you would do best not to give some Shakespearean sonnet, but just speak what's on your mind and heart.

[A lot of this description matches the material in chapter 4. In 4:15, the Bride says of the Bridegroom, ]{.class-0}["His legs are as pillars of marble, set upon sockets of fine gold."]{.class-1}[ Here he says of her, ]{.class-0}["the joints of thy thighs are like jewels, the work of the hands of a cunning workman"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 1).]{.class-0}

[Of course, it's easy to see what the Christian sees in his Saviour. To the born-again child of God, Jesus Christ is the ]{.class-0}["altogether lovely"]{.class-1}[ one (5:16) because of the ]{.class-0}["great love wherewith he loved us"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 2:4). But it's not so easy to see what the Lord sees in ]{.class-0}[us.]{.class-2}[ The only explanation is that He sees us ]{.class-0}[in Him]{.class-2}[ after He has accomplished His perfect work in us (Eph. 5:25--27).]{.class-0}

[The ]{.class-0}["liquor"]{.class-1}[ of verse 2 is not fermented wine. It is the ]{.class-0}[liquid]{.class-2}[ of a fruit---its ]{.class-0}[juice,]{.class-2}[ like the word ]{.class-0}[pot liquor]{.class-2}[ (see comments on Exod. 22:29 in that Commentary).]{.class-0}

We have already commented on verse 3 and the first part of verse 4 under 4:4--5 (which see).

"[Thine eyes like the fishpools in Heshbon, by the gate of Bathrabbim"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 4). A ]{.class-0}[fishpool]{.class-2}[ is like these goldfish ponds you see in Oriental gardens. The idea is her eyes are deep and tranquil like the pool and beautiful like the ornamental fish in the pond.]{.class-0}

"[Heshbon"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 4) was the capital city of Sihon the Amorite on the east side of Jordan back in Numbers 21 and was originally a Moabite city (Num. 21:26). It became part of the possession of the tribes of Reuben and Gad (Josh. 13:15--17, 21:38--39), and was given to the Levites (the sons of Merari) to dwell in (Josh. 21:34--39).]{.class-0}

[According to the ]{.class-0}[International Standard Bible Encyclopedia,]{.class-2}[ "the tower of Lebanon"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 4) was a watchtower on Mount Hermon from which you could see Damascus. What you can get out of that spiritually or doctrinally, I don't know, but evidently there was something about this woman's ]{.class-0}[nose ]{.class-2}[that reminded Solomon of that tower.]{.class-0}

"[Thine head upon thee is like Carmel"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 5). There are two Carmels in the Bible. One is a town in Judah (Josh 15:55; 1 Sam. 25:2), and the other is a mountain in northwest Palestine where Elijah had the contest with the prophets of Baal (1 Kings 18). It is the mountain that is referred to here. Mount Carmel is a well cultivated area covered with a lot of trees. The idea is that the woman has a beautiful, full head of hair.]{.class-0}

"[The hair of thine head like purple; the king is held in the galleries"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 5). If Solomon had only known that one day teenage girls and young women would be coloring their hair purple, bright green, flaming red, and orange! And it's not just the "punk rockers"; you have professing Christian women doing the same thing. There's an Assembly of God woman on TV (Jan Crouch) who dyes her hair pink, green, and purple. And she's no "spring chicken" either, brother; she's some woman up in her sixties or seventies.]{.class-0}

[Now that's not what Solomon's talking about here. This woman's hair isn't colored purple; it is ]{.class-0}["like purple."]{.class-1}[ What does that mean? Look at the next clause: ]{.class-0}["the KING is held in the galleries."]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}[Purple is the color of royalty.]{.class-2}[ Her hair is like royalty, so much so that it holds a royal monarch captive. The picture here is that of the King watching a performance and being hypnotized or entranced by it. Because the picture is that of an enthralling performance, most of the expositors say that the passage going clear back to 6:13 is the description of an Oriental dance, which I don't particularly buy. ]{.class-0}["The galleries"]{.class-1}[ here are a reference to the tresses of the woman's hair; their beauty "captivated" the King.]{.class-0}

Of course, the typology here is Christ being captivated by the beauty of the Church. Knowing ourselves like we do (if you are honest with yourself), that is hard to imagine. But as I said earlier, Christ is seeing us in our completed state, our glorified and purified state, at the Marriage of the Lamb (Psa. 45:11--13; Rev. 19:7--8).

"[How fair and how pleasant art thou, O love, for delights"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 6). The Lord gets "delight" out of His fellowship with you, and of course, you ought to ]{.class-0}["Delight thyself also in the LORD"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 37:4). The way you ]{.class-0}["delight thyself also in the LORD"]{.class-1}[ is to delight yourself in the ]{.class-0}[word of God]{.class-2}[ (Psa. 1:2, 119:16, 24, 35, 47, 70, 77, 174).]{.class-0}

"[This thy stature is like to a palm tree\...I said, I will go up to the palm tree, I will take hold of the boughs thereof"]{.class-1}[ (vss. 7--8). This is the Bridegroom likening the Bride to a palm tree and going up to her and grabbing ]{.class-0}["the palm tree"]{.class-1}[---He's embracing her. Now the analogy of ]{.class-0}["the palm tree"]{.class-1}[ is very interesting. Men are often likened to trees in the Bible (see Mark 8:24; Dan. 4:20--22; Ezek. 31:3; Psa. 1:3). The psalmist wrote, ]{.class-0}["The righteous shall flourish like the palm tree"]{.class-1}[ (Psa. 92:12).]{.class-0}

[The two trees mentioned in verses 7--8 (the palm and the vine) are connected with the Christian bearing fruit. Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["I am the true vine\...every branch that beareth fruit, he purgeth it, that it may bring forth more fruit"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:1--2). There are three levels of fruit-bearing mentioned in John 15: ]{.class-0}["fruit"]{.class-1}[ (15:2), ]{.class-0}["more fruit,"]{.class-1}[ (15:2), and ]{.class-0}["much fruit"]{.class-1}[ (15:5). Those match the thirty-fold, sixty-fold, and hundred-fold that ]{.class-0}["the good ground"]{.class-1}[ brings forth in the Parable of the Sower (Matt. 13:23). Just by coincidence (of course!), the Palestinian palm tree grows in three sizes: thirty feet, sixty feet, and a hundred feet.]{.class-0}

"[The smell of thy nose like apples"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 8). See our comments on ]{.class-0}["apples"]{.class-1}[ under 2:5.]{.class-0}

For verse 9, see our comments on 4:10 and 5:1.

10 I am my beloved's, and his desire is toward me.

11 Come, my beloved, let us go forth into the field; let us lodge in the villages.

12 Let us get up early to the vineyards; let us see if the vine flourish, whether the tender grape appear, and the pomegranates bud forth: there will I give thee my loves.

13 The mandrakes give a smell, and at our gates are all manner of pleasant fruits, new and old, which I have laid up for thee, O my beloved.

[Verse 10:]{.class-0}[ "I am my beloved's."]{.class-1}[ This is the ]{.class-0}[third time]{.class-2}[ the Bride has said this (see 2:16, 6:3). Jesus said the Christian is in the Father's hand (John 10:29), he is in the Son's hand (John 10:28), and Paul said he is sealed by the Holy Spirit (Eph. 4:30).]{.class-0}

[Continuing in verse 10: ]{.class-0}["and his desire is toward me."]{.class-1}[ The wording is the antithesis of what God tells Eve in Genesis 3:16.]{.class-0}

"[Unto the woman he said, I will greatly multiply thy sorrow and they conception; in sorrow thou shalt bring forth children; AND THY DESIRE SHALL BE TO THY HUSBAND, and he shall rule over thee." ]{.class-1}

The meaning there could have three possible interpretations:

1\) You will desire to rule your husband but will not be able to do it.

2\) You will desire for your husband to rule over you.

3\) You will desire to choose your own husband, not have him picked out for you.

Here, of course, it is not the wife desiring the husband, but the Bridegroom desiring the Bride. The closest interpretation to Genesis 3:16 would be number 3: Christ is desiring to choose the Church as His Bride.

[The significance of this phrase ]{.class-0}["his desire is toward me"]{.class-1}[ is that when you get over to Daniel 11:37, the Bible says the Antichrist will not ]{.class-0}["regard\...the desire of women."]{.class-1}[ That is, Satan's "christ" is a ]{.class-0}[sex pervert.]{.class-2}[ In the Scriptures, the Antichrist is connected with ]{.class-0}[two sexual perversions]{.class-2}[ which were called ]{.class-0}["abomination"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["confusion"]{.class-1}[ in Leviticus 18:22--23; those two perversions are ]{.class-0}[homosexuality]{.class-2}[ (Dan. 11:37) and ]{.class-0}[bestiality]{.class-2}[ (Rev. 17:3). Both practices were connected with ]{.class-0}[Ham]{.class-2}[ (Lev. 18:3). The sodomites were Canaanites descended from Ham (Gen. 10:15--20). The first kingdom mentioned in the Bible (Gen. 10:10) was set up by a Hamite who was a type of the Antichrist (Gen. 10:9), and that kingdom was connected with ]{.class-0}["confusion"]{.class-1}[ (Gen. 11:9). So the Antichrist ends up being a Syrian Jew of ]{.class-0}[Hamitic]{.class-2}[ extraction through Moab (see our work on ]{.class-0}[The Mark of the Beast,]{.class-2}[ 1960).]{.class-0}

"[I am my beloved's, and his desire is toward me."]{.class-1}[ Of all the things Christ desires, He desires the Church more than anything else. Back in 6:9, He said, ]{.class-0}["she is the ONLY ONE of her mother, she is the CHOICE ONE of her that bare her."]{.class-1}[ The Body of Christ is a special object of God's love in a way that no other group is. I realize that's "discrimination," but that's just one of those things.]{.class-0}

[That's illustrated in the twelve apostles. Christ loved all twelve of His disciples (John 13:1), but there were only three who were in His "inner circle" (Peter, James, and John). But of those three, only one them (John) is called]{.class-0}[ "that disciple whom Jesus loved"]{.class-1}[ (John 21:7, 20:2, 13:23).]{.class-0}

[Now, if you are saved and have a Christian spouse and Christian kids, you know the truth of what I am saying. First John 3:14 says, ]{.class-0}["We know that we have passed from death unto life, because we love the brethren."]{.class-1}[ So a Christian loves his brothers and sisters in Christ (or at least he is supposed to). Yet, no Christian woman loves other Christians with the love she has for her own husband or children; that's just one of those facts of life. There's a special love you lavish on your own family that's different from the love you have for other people, even though you don't "have it in" for those other folks. You may love them, but you just don't give them the privileges or fellowship you give your own family.]{.class-0}

[When you apply this principle to the Lord, the Bible says, ]{.class-0}["For God so loved the world, that he gave his only begotten Son, that whosoever believeth in him should not perish, but have everlasting life"]{.class-1}[ (John 3:16). We believe God loved ]{.class-0}[every sinner]{.class-2}[ and showed it at Calvary (Rom. 5:8). ]{.class-0}["God so loved the world"]{.class-1}[---that's the whole mass of unregenerate humanity. God loves everybody in the sense that He sent His Son to die on the cross and save them from their sins and from His wrath on sin. That's absolutely true.]{.class-0}

[But when it comes to those who actually ]{.class-0}[trust Christ as Saviour,]{.class-2}[ His "children" (John 1:12; Rom. 8:14--16), God loves them with a ]{.class-0}[special love]{.class-2}[ and a special care that He ]{.class-0}[doesn't have for a lost man.]{.class-2}[ He gives special privileges of fellowship to His children that no unsaved man has.]{.class-0}

Do you want to see the distinction? Look at John 13:1.

"[Now before the feast of the passover, when Jesus knew that his hour was come that he should depart out of this world unto the Father, having loved his own which were in the world, he loved them unto the end."]{.class-1}

[Christ is about to go to Calvary and show the love the Father had for the world in John 3:16. But in John 13:1, the Lord distinguishes His love for the world from the love He had for His disciples who ]{.class-0}["were in the world."]{.class-1}[ In John 15:19, Jesus says, ]{.class-0}["If ye were of the world, the world would love his own: but because YE ARE NOT OF THE WORLD, but because I have CHOSEN YOU OUT OF THE WORLD, therefore the world hateth you."]{.class-1}

[The modern teaching is that Christ loves everyone the same way---]{.class-0}["unconditionally"]{.class-2}[---so He would never send anyone to Hell. He loved the Roman Emperor Nero the same way He loved the Apostle Paul; He loved Pope Innocent III the same way He loved Martin Luther and John Hus; He loved Napoleon, Hitler, Stalin, and Mao Tse-Tung the same way He loved D. L. Moody, Mordecai Ham, Billy Sunday, and General William Booth. ]{.class-0}[That is a damnable lie.]{.class-2}

[Jesus said, ]{.class-0}["As the Father hath loved me, so have I loved you: continue ye in my love"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:9). Christ loves the believer in the same way God the Father loves the Son. Well, do you think the Father loves Christ the same way ]{.class-0}[He loves the world?]{.class-2}[ Of course not.]{.class-0}

[Listen! Christ didn't even love the world enough to ]{.class-0}[pray]{.class-2}[ for it. He said, ]{.class-0}["I have manifested thy name unto the men which thou gavest me out of the world\...I have given unto them the words thou gavest me; and they have received them\...they have believed that thou didst send me. I pray FOR THEM ]{.class-1}[\[the disciples who received His words and believed on Him\]]{.class-0}[: I PRAY NOT FOR THE WORLD, but for them which thou hast given me; for they are thine"]{.class-1}[ (John 17:6--9).]{.class-0}

[Every Christmas the Pope offers up a prayer and says, "Lord make me an instrument of Thy peace\...pray for world peace." That's not a "Vicar of Christ" praying that;]{.class-0}[ that's a politician.]{.class-2}[ No man who is like Christ would ever pray for "world peace" because Christ said, ]{.class-0}["I pray NOT for the world."]{.class-1}

When a man gets up and says "Let's all pray for world peace," do you know what he means? He means: "that's the one thing I can promote and talk about that won't offend anybody." Everyone will go along with that kind of talk because "who doesn't want peace"?

[Jesus Christ never prayed for world peace,]{.class-2}[ and He never told you to pray for world peace, because He knew there were bigger and better wars coming.
