He said there would be ]{.class-0}["wars and rumours of wars\...nation shall rise against nation, and kingdom against kingdom"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 24:6--7). ]{.class-0}[The three biggest wars are still in the future]{.class-2}[ (Rev. 6:4, 19:11--21, 20:7--9).]{.class-0}

[Given what the Scriptures say, a man would be a fool to pray for "world peace." I mean, why pray for something you ]{.class-0}[know]{.class-2}[ is not going to happen. It would be like a fellow getting down on his knees and praying, "Lord, please give me four arms and six legs." You can have all the faith you want, and "name it and claim it" like some crazy Charismatic nut, ]{.class-0}[but it's never going to happen.]{.class-2}[ Then why pray for "world peace" when God point-blank told you it wasn't going to happen?]{.class-0}

Listen folks, if God brought about "world peace" right now, He'd destroy the Scriptures. If He answered a stupid prayer like that, He'd make a liar out of Himself, and the Bible wouldn't be worth the paper on which it's written. If that were true, you couldn't trust anything God said about Himself, so why pray at all?

[Now what you were told to pray for was this: ]{.class-0}["I exhort therefore that, first of all, supplications, prayers, intercessions, and giving of thanks, be made for all men; For kings, and for all that are in authority; that we may lead a quiet and peaceable life in all godliness and honesty"]{.class-1}[ (1 Tim. 2:1--2).]{.class-0}

[You are told to pray for those in authority so that ]{.class-0}[you,]{.class-2}[ as a ]{.class-0}[Christian,]{.class-2}[ can lead a ]{.class-0}["peaceable life."]{.class-1}[ You are told to pray for people like Obama, Bush, Clinton, Pelosi, Reid, et al., so you can live an honest, godly life and do what God told you to do in peace. That doesn't mean that you pray they will be ]{.class-0}[successful]{.class-2}[ in what they want to do, because nowadays, what the politicians want to do is set up an international Socialist, Soviet Catholic (or Moslem!) State with no Bible, no God, no preaching or witnessing, and no prayer. When that's the case, what you pray for is that the Lord will get them all messed up so they can't do anything.]{.class-0}

When the State of Texas tried to shut down Roloff's homes back in the 70s, I prayed the Lord would foul up those bureaucrats' paperwork, kill the Attorney General who was prosecuting the case (or at least get him out of office somehow), and give those people so many troubles and distractions (both personally and politically) that they wouldn't be able to give any attention to Roloff. Sure, man; why not? I mean, it's either those politicians or damning a bunch of teenage kids trying to get off drugs and get their lives straightened out. I'd pray the same thing for any Christian boys' home or girls' home that's trying to do right and help those kids. Those politicians have already made their own decisions to damn themselves; why pick on a bunch of kids?

[You should pray for the city commissioners and the mayor and the police that the Lord will keep them ]{.class-0}[so busy]{.class-2}[ that they won't have time to interfere ]{.class-0}[with the public proclamation of God's word. ]{.class-2}[When someone tries to shut down your work by getting a "street tax" passed that you can't pay (like some of the dearly beloved brethren tried to do here in Florida a few years back), pray that God will mess up their committees and their bills so they won't be able to carry out their plans.]{.class-0}

[Christ said, ]{.class-0}["Greater love hath no man than this, that a man lay down his life for his friends"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:13). Well, He laid down His life ]{.class-0}["for all"]{.class-1}[ (1 Tim. 2:6), but it doesn't do you any good until you ]{.class-0}[appropriate it ]{.class-2}[for yourself. So He goes on and says, ]{.class-0}["Ye are my friends, if ye do whatsoever I command you"]{.class-1}[ (John 15:14). This world is the enemy of God (James 4:4), and the only way God "loves" it is to get people ]{.class-0}[out]{.class-2}[ of it (Gal. 1:4).]{.class-0}

Now turn to Ephesians 5 and notice the special love Christ has for His Body, the body of all saved people, that He does not have for the world.

[Ephesians 5:25, ]{.class-0}["Husbands, love your wives, even as Christ also loved the church, and gave himself for it."]{.class-1}[ Like we pointed out earlier, Christ died for every sinner; there is no such thing as Calvin's "Limited Atonement." Christ even died for unsaved false teachers and prophets ]{.class-0}[who die and go to Hell]{.class-2}[ (2 Pet. 2:1). But the love of Christ shown on the cross for all sinners is only ]{.class-0}[applied ]{.class-2}[to those who ]{.class-0}[accept ]{.class-2}[that sacrifice. So even though Christ ]{.class-0}["gave himself a ransom for all"]{.class-1}[ (2 Tim. 2:6), the payment is only good for those who receive it ]{.class-0}["by faith"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 5:1).]{.class-0}

[Back to Ephesians 5 (vss. 26--27): ]{.class-0}["That he might sanctify and cleanse it with the washing of water by the word. That he might present it to himself a glorious church, not having spot, or wrinkle, or any such thing; but that it should be holy and without blemish."]{.class-1}

[That's not talking about the unsaved man at all. An unregenerate sinner hits the judgment in the ]{.class-0}["filthy rags"]{.class-1}[ of his own self-righteousness (Isa. 64:6). He is like the Pharisee who came to the Temple and ]{.class-0}["prayed thus with himself, God, I thank thee, that I am not as other men are\...even as this publican"]{.class-1}[ (Luke 18:11); he leaves in the same lost condition he was when he came in. He is like the fellow who comes to the wedding feast without the ]{.class-0}["wedding garment"]{.class-1}[ provided to him by the King: he is ]{.class-0}["cast\...into outer darkness"]{.class-1}[ where ]{.class-0}["there shall be weeping and gnashing of teeth"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 22:12--13).]{.class-0}

[Ephesians 5:28, ]{.class-0}["So ought men to love their wives as their own bodies. He that loveth his wife loveth himself."]{.class-1}[ That's a special kind of love a man has for his wife that he doesn't have for another woman (or anybody else) because the wife is considered to be ]{.class-0}[one body]{.class-2}[ with her husband. Look at Ephesians 5:31, ]{.class-0}["For this cause shall a man leave his father and mother, and shall be joined unto his wife, and they two shall be one flesh."]{.class-1}

[A man ought to love his wife just like he loves his own body because they are ]{.class-0}["one flesh."]{.class-1}[ Generally speaking, most men go to great efforts to take care of themselves. Now they may not be fanatics about it, and they may let their health go to pieces because they love to eat. I mean, some men get overweight and don't take the pride in their personal appearance that their wives would have them do. I know they get pretty careless about that kind of thing, but for the most part a man will pretty well look out for himself. He'll make sure He doesn't break an arm or leg if he can prevent it; he'll try not to get fired at his job; he'll make sure there's food in the ice box; and he'll see to it that he has a comfortable place to sleep at night.]{.class-0}

[Well, the rule is that the man is to take as much care of his wife in that respect as he does ]{.class-0}[himself.]{.class-2}[ Paul wrote, ]{.class-0}["But if any provide not for his own, and especially for those of his own house, he hath denied the faith, and is worse than an infidel"]{.class-1}[ (1 Tim. 5:8).]{.class-0}

[Ephesians 5:29, ]{.class-0}["For no man ever yet hated his own flesh."]{.class-1}[ Now that's a general rule to which there are many exceptions. You take the Apostle Paul; I guess he hated his flesh as much as any man ever could. After all, he said, ]{.class-0}["For I know that in me (that is, in my flesh,) dwelleth no good thing"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 7:18).]{.class-0}

Do you know something? There are times in the Christian life when the flesh will do something that makes you wish the Lord would kill you and take you on home and put you out of your misery. If you have any love for your Saviour, you know that to be so. You become so ashamed over what your flesh has done that the only "out" you can see is to die and go on home to Glory. That is why you have Christian suicides; there are some of God's children who take steps to "help God out" in the matter.

[Of course, unsaved people do that kind of thing all the time. They think death is going to give them some kind of ]{.class-0}[relief ]{.class-2}[from the drugs or the alcohol or the bad marriage or the shame of being caught embezzling funds at work, etc.; but all that happens is they pop the pills or pull the trigger or hang themselves and wake up to find their troubles are a million times ]{.class-0}[worse ]{.class-2}[in Hell.]{.class-0}

[But generally speaking, that kind of thing is not normal; it's not "natural." We call that kind of thinking "abnormal," and when somebody is trying to end his or her life, we say he's ]{.class-0}[sick]{.class-2}[. The reason why is because, by nature, no man naturally has a hatred for his flesh.]{.class-0}

[Of course, you can be talked into such a state by a religious, pagan fanatic. Over there in 1 Kings 18:28, those prophets of Baal were cutting themselves with ]{.class-0}["knives and lancets, till the blood gushed out upon them."]{.class-1}[ They were doing that in an effort to get their god to hear their prayers. Over in the Philippines around Easter, you will see those poor, deluded Roman Catholics going down the street whipping themselves until the blood runs off their backs onto the ground; a few of them will actually allow themselves to be nailed to a cross. You can go over to Italy and Spain and see Catholics crawling up stairs until they have blood on their knees. They do that trying to "do penance" for their sins or to show how holy they are by mortifying their fleshly body. That's the kind of thing Martin Luther did before he was saved to try to get rid of the guilt of his sins.]{.class-0}

[But that is not ]{.class-0}[normal]{.class-2}[, you see; it's the exception. Even the Apostle Paul, for all his trying to get back up to the third heaven (2 Cor. 12:1--5), ate and drank and slept and worked to take care of his needs; he still "nourished" his body and took care of it. That's a general rule with exceptions to it.]{.class-0}

[Ephesians 5:29 is about one of three verses in the Bible that are like that. They are general statements of truth, but none of them are ]{.class-0}[absolute]{.class-2}[. One of them is Hebrews 9:27. ]{.class-0}["And as it is appointed unto men ONCE TO DIE, but after this the judgment."]{.class-1}

[You have a bunch of Fundamentalists who teach that statement is so binding that at the Rapture, the living saints in Christ ]{.class-0}[die ]{.class-2}[when they lose their blood before they go up (1 Cor. 15:50 cf. 1 Thess. 4:17). Of course, that's nonsense. Moses died once (Deut. 34), ]{.class-0}[and he will die again]{.class-2}[ (Rev. 11). Dorcas (Acts 9:36--41) died ]{.class-0}[twice; ]{.class-2}[the widow of Nain's son (Luke 7:11--15) died]{.class-0}[ twice; ]{.class-2}[Eutychus (Acts 20:9--10) died ]{.class-0}[twice;]{.class-2}[ Lazarus (John 11) died ]{.class-0}[twice;]{.class-2}[ Jonah died ]{.class-0}[twice ]{.class-2}[(cf. Jon. 2:2); the widow of Zarephath's son (1 Kings 17:17--24) died ]{.class-0}[twice;]{.class-2}[ the great woman of Shunem's son (2 Kings 4:20--37) died ]{.class-0}[twice;]{.class-2}[ the dead fellow who came back to life when he touched Elisha's bones (2 Kings 13:21) died ]{.class-0}[twice;]{.class-2}[ Jairus' daughter (Mark 5:35--42) died ]{.class-0}[twice;]{.class-2}[ there were all kinds of unnamed people in the Gospels who died ]{.class-0}[twice ]{.class-2}[(see Matt. 10:8; Luke 7:22). You even have a fellow in the Bible who never died ]{.class-0}[and never will die]{.class-2}[ (Enoch---Heb. 11:5); that's a picture of the mortals who ]{.class-0}["put on immortality"]{.class-1}[ at the Rapture without ever seeing death (1 Cor. 15:54). So Hebrews 9:27 is a ]{.class-0}[general rule]{.class-2}[ with some "leeways."]{.class-0}

[Another one is Job 2:4.]{.class-0}[ "Skin for skin, yea, all that a man hath will he give for his life."]{.class-1}[ That's the Devil telling God that all men are so constituted that they'll give up anything in order to stay alive. Is that true? Well, generally, but ]{.class-0}[not exclusively.]{.class-2}

[If there's any doubt in your mind about the ]{.class-0}[general truth]{.class-2}[ of that statement, just study the concentration camp literature of World War II. You had Jewish men helping their wives into the gas chambers because if they didn't, they would take their wives' place. That kind of thing happened over and over again. A lot of them figured that even if they did that, the wife would still die anyway, so what was the good in ]{.class-0}[both ]{.class-2}[of them dying; someone had to ]{.class-0}[stay alive and let the world know what happened.]{.class-2}[ You see how the thing goes?]{.class-0}

[But if you want to see how the Devil lied, just get ]{.class-0}[Foxe's Book of Martyrs.]{.class-2}[ You will read account after account about people who were your brothers and sisters in Christ who loved the Lord so much that their lives didn't mean a thing in the world to them. There was one account of a lady named Constantia Bellione whom a priest tried to get to "renounce the Devil and go to Mass." She told that priest, "I was brought up in a religion by which I was always taught to renounce the Devil; but should I comply with your desire, and go to Mass, I should be sure to meet him there in a variety of shapes."]{.class-0}

[That priest then had slices cut out of her body, and the only thing that woman said to him was: "What horrid and lasting torments will you suffer in Hell, for the trifling and temporary pains which I now endure." That sister gave that Catholic priest a lot more than some nice, little, sweet, daily-Vacation-Bible-School testimony. To shut her up, he had a bunch of musketeers shoot her. One martyr told his tormenters on the way to the stake: "I'd rather be happy with God in death or happy in prison with Jesus Christ and the Holy Spirit than I would be in Hell with ]{.class-0}[you]{.class-2}[."]{.class-0}

[So ]{.class-0}["all that a man hath will he give for his life"]{.class-1}[ is ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[always true. It's a general rule, and the sad fact is that you have professing Christians that will sell the Bible out to make a living: they'll politick, lie, misreport income and attendance, etc., just to keep things going. But that is not always the case. The three Hebrew children told Nebuchadnezzar that God was able to deliver them,]{.class-0}[ "but if not"]{.class-1}[ (Dan. 3:18), they would go ahead and go to the fiery furnace and still not worship the image. Those are men who didn't care much for their lives.]{.class-0}

[Back to Song of Solomon 7:10, ]{.class-0}["I am my beloved's, and his desire is toward me."]{.class-1}[ The woman is saying she has a marriage where the husband prefers her to anybody else and where the husband loves her as much as he loves himself. That's the ideal marriage relationship; that's the way it ought to be. So the woman, here, is describing the perfect marriage.]{.class-0}

[This perfect marriage is also described in Hosea 2:19--20, which doctrinally is a picture of Israel's restoration to God at the end of the Tribulation.]{.class-0}[ "And I will betroth thee]{.class-1}[ \[a betrothal is like an engagement\]]{.class-0}[ unto me for ever."]{.class-1}

[This is the kind of thing you hear in love songs all the time: "I'm going to love you forever until the end of time, when the ages have wasted away, and the stars have turned to dust"---all that kind of stuff, you know. It's a nice sentiment, but it's a bunch of ]{.class-0}[nonsense.]{.class-2}[ Christ said, ]{.class-0}["in the resurrection they neither marry, nor are given in marriage, but are as the angels of God in heaven"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 22:30).]{.class-0}

[When you get to Heaven, you're not going to be divided up into husband and wives and families. ]{.class-0}[That's what the Mormons teach:]{.class-2}[ they believe you'll be married to whatever women you were married to down here on earth (the Mormons are polygamists just like the Moslems), and you'll just keep on producing babies throughout eternity. A Mormon missionary once asked one of our graduates and his wife (the two had a big family of six kids), "Wouldn't you like to be married to each other forever?" The two looked each other and laughed, and in unison said, "No!"]{.class-0}

[There's no man in the world who would want to live to be 150 billion years old with a woman who was 150 billion years old. And the ladies could say the same thing about you, gentlemen; I mean, what woman would want to ]{.class-0}[obey the same man]{.class-2}[ for 150 billion years? So while "I'm going to love you forever" may be a nice sentiment, "till death do us part" is more realistic and more fortunate.]{.class-0}

[But when it comes to the Father's relationship with Israel, and with Christ's permanent relationship with the Church, the "marriage" is ]{.class-0}["for ever."]{.class-1}

[Back in Hosea 2:19, ]{.class-0}["yea, I will betroth thee unto me in righteousness and in judgment."]{.class-1}[ The perfect marriage is based on what is ]{.class-0}[right,]{.class-2}[ not on sentimentality. And generally speaking, if a marriage starts ]{.class-0}[right,]{.class-2}[ it will end ]{.class-0}[right;]{.class-2}[ and if it starts ]{.class-0}[wrong,]{.class-2}[ it will end ]{.class-0}[wrong.]{.class-2}[ That's not an infallible rule, but the exceptions to it certainly prove the rule.]{.class-0}

[Continuing with Hosea 2:19,]{.class-0}[ "And in loving kindness, and in mercies."]{.class-1}[ It's not all ]{.class-0}["judgment"]{.class-1}[ in a marriage. At some point your spouse is going to mess up, and you're going to have to exercise some kindness and mercy in the relationship. I think it was back in the 60s that someone said, "Love is never having to say you're sorry." That's a bunch of bunk. If you really love your spouse, there'll be a lot of times you have to say you're sorry, and there'll be a lot of times you have to forgive him or her.]{.class-0}

[The Apostle Paul wrote,]{.class-0}[ "And be ye kind one to another, tenderhearted, forgiving one another, even as God for Christ's sake hath forgiven you"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 4:32). That's as good advice for a Christian couple as it is for the local church.]{.class-0}

[Hosea 2:20, ]{.class-0}["I will even betroth thee unto me in faithfulness."]{.class-1}[ The marriage vows say, "forsaking all others, keep thee only unto him (or her)." There is no such thing as an "open marriage" in the Bible. When a husband or wife joins his body to someone else besides his spouse, the marriage bond has been broken by adultery (Rom. 7:3).]{.class-0}

"[\...and thou shalt know the LORD"]{.class-1}[ (Hos. 2:20). That's the key to a perfect marriage. It is to be a believing man joined to a believing woman (1 Cor. 7:39 cf. 2 Cor. 6:14), trying to serve God together (1 Pet. 3:7).]{.class-0}

[Now when it comes to the "marriage" relationship between the Christian and His Lord, it is to be a ]{.class-0}[personal]{.class-2}[ one. When you witness, you ask the unsaved person, "Have you received Christ as your ]{.class-0}[personal]{.class-2}[ Saviour?" Salvation is more than knowing ]{.class-0}[about]{.class-2}[ Christ or knowing ]{.class-0}[of]{.class-2}[ Him; it's knowing ]{.class-0}[Him]{.class-2}[ personally by faith. You ]{.class-0}[don't]{.class-2}[ know Him corporately through a religious organization; you ]{.class-0}[don't ]{.class-2}[know Him ritualistically through a sacrament. The Knights of Columbus (a Catholic apologetic organization) put out a pamphlet one time which told a Catholic how to deal with a personal worker. When asked if he had personally received Jesus Christ as his Saviour, the Catholic was to reply, "Yes, I receive Him every Sunday." That's a reference to a Catholic receiving ]{.class-0}[a wafer]{.class-2}[ in the Mass every Sunday morning.]{.class-0}

[Well let me ask you this: if eating a starchy cookie is ]{.class-0}[receiving]{.class-2}[ Christ, what happens the next time you go to the bathroom? Don't you get rid of Him then?]{.class-0}

[You say, "That's crude, Ruckman. How could you even think a thing like that?" ]{.class-0}[No, you're the one who's not thinking.]{.class-2}[ If a piece of bread is the body of Jesus Christ, then when you eat it, you are digesting ]{.class-0}[Jesus Christ]{.class-2}[, and when you go to the bathroom you are getting rid of Christ's ]{.class-0}[literal body.]{.class-2}[ When does it cease to be ]{.class-0}[Christ's body?]{.class-2}

[You see, ]{.class-0}[Catholics ]{.class-2}[don't think. A Catholic is told that the bread and wine are turned into Christ's literal body and blood when the Priest says the magic words of consecration over them. But no magic words of "deconsecration" ever changes them ]{.class-0}[back ]{.class-2}[to bread and wine, ]{.class-0}[so they go through the digestive tract and out the other end.]{.class-2}[ That's why there are actual rules about what to do if "Christ" gets caught on your false teeth or what to do if a rat gets into the "ark" and eats "Christ" or what to do if you vomit up "Christ" when you are sick at the Mass.]{.class-0}

[Catholics don't think the thing through. A "Christ" you can chew up and digest ain't much of a Saviour. There's no ]{.class-0}[personal relationship]{.class-2}[ with a loaf of bread or a jug of "hootch."]{.class-0}

[Now why is our relationship with Christ a ]{.class-0}[personal]{.class-2}[ one? Well, first of all, it's because you ]{.class-0}["are bought with a price"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 6:20). You were a slave knocked down on the block, and Christ paid the price to make you ]{.class-0}[His ]{.class-2}[and set you free from your ]{.class-0}[former master]{.class-2}[ (the Devil). Now you mean to tell me that He could do that for you and there would be no personal relationship between you and Him? I don't think so.]{.class-0}

[When you are out passing out tracts, you get all types of responses. You ask a fellow, "Have you received Jesus Christ as your personal Saviour," and he says, "Well, you've got your religion and I've got mine." You ask another "Are you saved," and he says, "I don't discuss religion and politics." I saw one of our young men give a tract to a Catholic Priest one time, and he took one step and threw it on the ground. Well, those aren't the ways a ]{.class-0}[freed slave]{.class-2}[ would act.]{.class-0}

If you are saved and somebody walks up to you on the street and says "Have you received Christ," you shouldn't have any problem with saying, "Yes, I have," and then telling them how and when you got saved. If somebody hands me a tract, I'll either let him know I'm already saved so they can give it to someone else, or I'll take it and give it to someone else myself if it's a decent tract. I'd never throw it on the ground and walk away.

[Listen, brother, if you don't appreciate the pit from which you were digged, I do. I was on my way to becoming a drunk with a busted-up family and on the verge of committing suicide when the Lord saved me. You don't think that thing between me and Jesus Christ is ]{.class-0}[personal?]{.class-2}

[The next way our relationship with Christ is personal is because it's like a marriage engagement. Just like Abraham sent his servant back to Haran to get a bride for his son Isaac (Gen. 24), God the Father sent the Holy Spirit into the world to call you out of this world to become part of the Bride of Christ. That calling is a ]{.class-0}[personal calling]{.class-2}[, where the Holy Spirit comes to you personally to convict you of sin, righteousness, and judgment (John 16:8--11 cf. Acts 24:25). That's why an unsaved fellow can be in a church of 500 people and listen to a Gospel message and think the preacher is preaching directly at him; the Holy Spirit is taking those words and applying them directly to the heart of that sinner.]{.class-0}

[Now you take you ladies; would you marry some guy who lived twenty miles away who sent you a telegram saying, "I love you and you ought to love me. Here's a questionnaire with twenty things for you to answer. Just fill it out, mail it back to me, and we'll be married on such-and-such a date"? Of course not. You would expect him to come around and ask you out and get to know you. But people are funny when it comes to salvation. They figure if they get baptized, join the church, and subscribe to the Apostles' Creed that means they are "Christians." That isn't ]{.class-0}[salvation;]{.class-2}[ that's knowledge of the fundamentals. Salvation is ]{.class-0}[personally]{.class-2}[ trusting Christ and His blood atonement FOR ]{.class-0}[YOU]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[You can't fall in love and get married without getting ]{.class-0}[personal]{.class-2}[, and you can't get saved without getting ]{.class-0}[personal]{.class-2}[. Back in Genesis 24, the question was put to Rebekah: ]{.class-0}["Wilt thou go with this man?"]{.class-1}[ She had to ]{.class-0}[personally ]{.class-2}[reply]{.class-0}[ "I will go"]{.class-1}[ in order to get married to Isaac (Gen. 24:58). The question is "Will you receive Jesus Christ as your Saviour," and the answer is not Roman Catholic or Campbellite water baptism, the Mass or communion, or the "fundamentals" or some church creed. If your answer is not "Yes, I will receive Him," then anything else is a "No."]{.class-0}

[Verse 11: ]{.class-0}["Come, my beloved, let us go forth into the field; let us lodge in the villages."]{.class-1}[ This is the Bride speaking to the Bridegroom. Notice she says:]{.class-0}[ "let us go forth."]{.class-1}[ She wants to be with him. If you love someone, you want to be with him or her. If you love the Lord, you want to spend time with Him, and the way you do that, of course, is through Bible reading and prayer.]{.class-0}

"[Let us go forth into the field."]{.class-1}[ In the New Testament, ]{.class-0}["the field is the world"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 13:28), so the picture here is the Church inviting her Lord to go with her as she fulfills His command to ]{.class-0}["Go ye into all the world, and preach the gospel to every creature"]{.class-1}[ (Mar. 16:15). If you are going to do that, you are going to have to go where the people are, so her next prayer request is: ]{.class-0}["let us lodge in the villages."]{.class-1}

[From a practical point of view, if you have a good Christian wife, men, then you ought to go out soulwinning ]{.class-0}[with her.]{.class-2}[ The trouble with men is that they get kind of embarrassed or nervous about what the wife might say. And, of course, that may very well happen, but she'll never learn to do it right with you if you don't do it ]{.class-0}[together.]{.class-2}

[Now there is another practical, spiritual application you can make here. ]{.class-0}["The field"]{.class-1}[ is a place of solitude; ]{.class-0}["the villages"]{.class-1}[ are where the crowds are. So if you love somebody, you can be happy with him anywhere. That is applicable to the Christian life as much as it is to marriage. You can be happy anywhere as long as it is ]{.class-0}[with the Lord.]{.class-2}[ It can be at a Rescue Mission in downtown Chicago, in a Servicemen's Center in downtown Philadelphia, street preaching on Wall Street in New York City, starting a church in Montana, or on the mission field in Zambia or Malawi. The testimony of everyone who ever found the will of God and got in it is that they were happier there than anywhere else.]{.class-0}

[I have seen that to be true. I have seen some of the most radiant Christian souls and some of the happiest Christian people in the most unlikely spots. There used to be a Pentecostal preacher in New Orleans (not Bob Harrington but someone else whose name escapes me) who used to go up and down the French Quarter and pass out tracts and preach year in and year out. He was one of the happiest, most cheerful souls you have ever met in your life. Now maybe you couldn't work in a hellhole like that, but that fellow could, because ]{.class-0}[that's where God wanted him.]{.class-2}[ If you love the Lord and you're where He wants you to be, you are just as happy and content in a crowded tenement district in Cincinnatti as you would be on a ranch in Texas or Oklahoma.]{.class-0}

"[Let us get up early to the vineyards; let us see if the vine flourish, whether the tender grape appear, and the pomegranates bud forth: there will I give thee my loves"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 12). Now in verses 10--12, you have a good alliterated sermon outline: there is a ]{.class-0}[personal relationship]{.class-2}[ in verse 10, a ]{.class-0}[prayerful request]{.class-2}[ in verse 11, and a ]{.class-0}[pleasing response]{.class-2}[ in verse 12.]{.class-0}

"[Let us get up early."]{.class-1}[ The spiritual application is that the best time to serve the Lord is early, when you are young. Back in Ecclesiastes 12:1, Solomon said, ]{.class-0}["Remember now thy Creator in the days of thy youth, while the evil days come not, nor the years draw nigh, when thou shalt say, I have no pleasure in them."]{.class-1}[ If you continue to read through that chapter, you'll find that the reason he said that was because the older you get, the more things there are that get in the way and fail and hinder you from doing what God wants you to do. Generally speaking, a younger person can always do more for the Lord than an older person, because as you get older, you have to take care of the wife, you have children and have to take care of them, you have to please the in-laws, your back aches, your eyesight fails, you get hard of hearing, you run out of energy, grandkids come along, etc. So the best time to start serving the Lord is as early in your life as possible.]{.class-0}

"[Let us get up early to the vineyards; let us see if the vine flourish, whether the tender grape appear, and the pomegranates bud forth."]{.class-1}[ The Bride has gone searching for fruit, and she asks her lover to go with her to search the vineyard to see if there is any fruit. We have already commented on the Christian bearing fruit back under verses 7--8. Paul likens the preacher to a ]{.class-0}["husbandman"]{.class-1}[ who tends the vineyard to see that the vines bear fruit (2 Tim. 2:6).]{.class-0}

"[There will I give thee my loves."]{.class-1}[ Outside of the salvation of your own soul (Mark 8:36), real love is the most valuable thing to have, and it's the most valuable thing you can give. Over in Song 8:7, Solomon writes: ]{.class-0}["if a man would give all the substance of his house for love, it would be utterly contemned."]{.class-1}[ In other words, if a man gave away everything he owned to someone, but didn't give his love, it wouldn't be counted of any value by the person receiving it.]{.class-0}

[Paul expresses the same sentiment in 1 Corinthians 13:1--2. ]{.class-0}["Though I speak with the tongues of men and of angels, and have not charity, I am become as sounding brass, or a tinkling symbal. And though I have the gift of prophecy, and understand all mysteries, and all knowledge; and though I have all faith, so that I could remove mountains, and have not charity, I am nothing."]{.class-1}

[In marriage, no woman will take any substitute from her husband for ]{.class-0}[real love,]{.class-2}[ and no man would from his wife either. Even when some spouse acts like he or she does, that is just a show; human nature being what it is, the truth will manifest itself sooner or later.]{.class-0}

[You can't buy ]{.class-0}[love]{.class-2}[. You can buy ]{.class-0}[sex]{.class-2}[, and a spouse may hang around in a loveless marriage for money or possessions; but when it comes to ]{.class-0}[real ]{.class-2}[love, that can't be bought. You can't buy love. You can ]{.class-0}[earn]{.class-2}[ it, but you can't buy it. You can ]{.class-0}[work]{.class-2}[ for it, but you can't buy it.]{.class-0}

[Whatever is substituted for real love in a relationship will eventually fall apart. If the heart isn't in it, you won't be able to keep the thing together. Americans are materialistic in their approach in these matters. They think you can buy a person by offering him (or her) different things: here's a house, here's a car, here's a television, here's a deep freeze, here's wall-to-wall carpeting, here's five rooms full of furniture and two baths. But what good does all that stuff do if there's no love? Without love, you may have a ]{.class-0}[house]{.class-2}[, but it's not a ]{.class-0}[home]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[A lot of parents try to give their kids ]{.class-0}[things]{.class-2}[ instead of love. In the end, all you end up with is a rebellious, spoiled rotten brat. A child can tell when you're not giving him your love. That's why so many parents lose their kids to drugs, alcohol, fornication, etc., in their teenage years: they are trying to fill the void of love left by their parents.]{.class-0}

[If there is love in the home, a family can get by on mighty "slim pickins," but if there's not, no amount of money or things is going to hold the thing together. If there is love in a marriage, it will last, and where love is lost on the part of one or more parties,]{.class-0}[ it won't.]{.class-2}[ When that happens, the only thing that will keep that marriage together is for both parties to learn to love each other again, and if one or both of them are unwilling to do that, the thing is going to split up.]{.class-0}

"[I will give thee my loves."]{.class-1}[ Well, if love is the best thing to have and to give, then the woman is giving her best to her lover.]{.class-0}

[There is a famous sermon illustration that preachers have used for years that took place in India back in the 1800s. A missionary was down by the Ganges River and saw a native woman going down there with two children. In her arms the woman carried a deformed, crippled child with sores, and alongside her walked a happy little girl of about four years old. She walked down to the river, and when she returned, only the deformed child was with her. The missionary asked his interpreter what had happened to the healthy child, and the interpreter told him the woman had ]{.class-0}[drowned the child in the Ganges]{.class-2}[ as a sacrifice to the river. The missionary was enraged and wanted to know why she had drowned the healthy child instead of the deformed one. Through the interpreter the woman told the missionary: ]{.class-0}["I always give my god my best."]{.class-2}

[What a rebuke to a Christian! You have people who are deceived and worship false gods who have a greater devotion to those gods than a Christian has to his Saviour! A lot of these pagans are 100% sold out to their gods; that's a lot more than you can say for a lot of the Lord's people. Those Mohammedans are so devoted to their "prophet" that they will strap a bomb on and blow themselves up in the cause of "Allah." ]{.class-0}[You can't get most Christians to cross the street to pass out a Gospel tract.]{.class-2}

One time the Devil came before God, and the Lord said, "Hey, what do you think about my friend Abraham down there?"

The Devil said, "He's just like all the rest of those sinners."

"[Oh no, he's my friend," the Lord said, "He's]{.class-0}[ 'the Friend of God']{.class-1}[ (James 2:23)."]{.class-0}

"[He's not your friend," said the Devil.]{.class-0}

"[Sure he's my friend. He'll do whatever I tell him to do," said the Lord.]{.class-0}

The Devil said, "I've got friends down there better than Abraham: they're a lot closer to me than Abraham is to you."

"[What do you mean?" asked the Lord.]{.class-0}

"[I've got friends who love me so much that they'll burn their babies in the fire, they'll throw them to the crocodiles, they'll drown them in the river," said the Devil, "You reckon Abraham loves you that much?"]{.class-0}

"[Let's try him out," said God.]{.class-0}

[And you know the story. God asked Abraham to sacrifice the child He had promised Abraham and for whom Abraham had waited for so long. Abraham took the boy and tied him to the altar and raised the knife to kill Isaac, and the Lord stopped him. God wasn't interested in a human sacrifice; He was checking to see what Abraham ]{.class-0}[loved.]{.class-2}

"[I will give thee my loves."]{.class-1}[ If you love the Lord, you will give Him the things you love.]{.class-0}

[Verse 13:]{.class-0}[ "The mandrakes give a smell."]{.class-1}[ This is the ]{.class-0}[mandrageras]{.class-2}[ plant that goes by common names of "love plant," "love flower," or "love apple." It is called that because it is supposed to increase fertility in men and women. Of course, there are all kinds of superstitions connected with these things called "aphrodisiacs." Tomatoes were forbidden by the Puritans for this reason.]{.class-0}

[Mandrakes have dark green leaves and a fruit that looks like an orange tomato. But it's not the fruit that's used because that's poisonous; it's the ]{.class-0}[root]{.class-2}[. The root is like a thick carrot that looks like a man's body, so you get a lot of superstitious folklore connected with that too.]{.class-0}

[Mandrakes are what Reuben found ]{.class-0}["in the field" "in the days of wheat harvest"]{.class-1}[ (Gen. 30:14). Rachel bartered her husband's company with Leah to get them so she could get pregnant, but as it turned out, Leah was the one who got pregnant without them (Gen. 30:15--17).]{.class-0}

[Again, we are on the subject of the Christian bearing fruit (see comments under vss. 7--8), and the specific fruit here is a Christian begetting other Christians. Contrary to the TULIP sniffers (Five-point Calvinists), a Christian does have a part in a sinner's salvation. Paul could say, ]{.class-0}["I have begotten you through the gospel"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 4:15) and ]{.class-0}["I beseech thee for my son Onesimus, whom I have begotten in my bonds"]{.class-1}[ (Phile. 10). A Christian couple may have trouble having a child physically, but there is no excuse for any Christian to be spiritually impotent because we have the ]{.class-0}["incorruptible"]{.class-1}[ seed of ]{.class-0}["the word of God"]{.class-1}[ (1 Pet. 1:23). Paul called the Gospel ]{.class-0}["the power of God unto salvation"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 1:16): it's potent.]{.class-0}

[Back to verse 13:]{.class-0}[ "and at our gates are all manner of pleasant fruits, new and old."]{.class-1}[ And that's probably a reference to the word of God:]{.class-0}[ "Then said he unto them, Therefore every scribe which is instructed unto the kingdom of heaven is like a man that is an householder, which bringeth forth out of his treasure things new and old"]{.class-1}[ (Matt. 13:52).]{.class-0}

"[Which I have laid up for thee, O my beloved."]{.class-1}[ As we close out this chapter, there are three questions every reader should be able to answer in the affirmative, and if you can't, then there are some things you need to get fixed up with the Lord.]{.class-0}

[The first is: "Are you Christ's ]{.class-0}['beloved']{.class-1}[?" Have you come to Him in faith and been ]{.class-0}["made\...accepted in the beloved"]{.class-1}[ (Eph. 1:6). Are you ]{.class-0}["beloved of God"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 1:7) because you are one of ]{.class-0}["the children of the living God"]{.class-1}[ (Rom. 9:24--26)? Are you the ]{.class-0}["beloved of the Lord, because God hath\...chosen you to salvation through sanctification of the Spirit and belief of the truth"]{.class-1}[ (2 Thess. 2:13). Are you His ]{.class-0}[beloved?]{.class-2}

[The second question is: "Is He ]{.class-0}[your ]{.class-2}[beloved?" We gave you the characteristics of how you would treat someone if you really loved him in our comments under 1:7. Do you love the Lord like that?]{.class-0}

A Liberal or a Modernist doesn't love Jesus Christ. If he did, he wouldn't even think of saying Jesus was the illegitimate son of a German soldier or that He just swooned on the cross and was "revived in the coolness of the tomb." He wouldn't call Jesus Christ a liar by saying Darwin was right (cf. Mark 10:5--6). Those are the marks of an enemy of Christ, not someone who loves Him.

[Of course, nowadays, they won't come right out and say those things; they'll couch them in little cutesy questions. One of these new Liberals (now called "emergents") recently said, "Is your faith so weak that it would be shaken if you found out through DNA testing that Jesus had a human father named Larry?" Listen, if Jesus Christ had a human father, then just chuck the Bible, the church, and Christianity, and go do whatever you want to do. If Jesus Christ wasn't virgin born, then the Bible is a lie because it said He ]{.class-0}[was ]{.class-2}[(Isa. 7:14). If Jesus Christ had a human father, then He was ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[God in the flesh (Matt. 1:23). If Jesus Christ was ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[God in human form, then He's stone-cold dead on the market like Mohammed, Buddha, Zoroaster, the Popes, or any other religious fakir (Rom. 1:3--4). If Jesus Christ never rose from the dead, ]{.class-0}["then is our preaching vain, and your faith is also vain\...ye are yet in your sins"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 15:14--17). In other words, you are headed to Hell, and there's nothing that's going to stop you, and you ]{.class-0}["are of all men most miserable"]{.class-1}[ (1 Cor. 15:19).]{.class-0}

[If you love the Lord, you won't believe His ]{.class-0}[enemies]{.class-2}[ when they say things like that, and you will speak up for Him and defend Him when they attack Him like that.]{.class-0}

[I'll tell you something else, if you love His words like you ought (Psa. 119:97), you won't believe a bunch of apostate Conservatives, Fundamentalists, and Evangelicals when they say: "A better translation should be\...," "Unfortunately, the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ has mistranslated the Greek word here\...," "The reading here in the ]{.class-0}[King James Version]{.class-2}[ is wrong\
\...," "The ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ was good enough for Paul, so it's good enough for me; ha!ha!ha!" You aren't going to accept a translation that says Joseph was Christ's father (Luke 2:33) or that gives Satan the title given to Jesus Christ (]{.class-0}["the morning star"]{.class-2}[---Isa. 14:12 in an ]{.class-0}[NIV]{.class-2}[ cf. Rev. 22:16). Those are the words of people who love themselves and their own opinions more than they love what God said in His Book. If you love the Scriptures, you are going to defend them from people like that.]{.class-0}

[Finally, is He ]{.class-0}[real ]{.class-2}[to you? There was a painter once named Vincent Van Gogh. The guy was a no-talent hack who was pumped up by the news media after he died because he was a poor, psychotic tramp who died insane. Van Gogh spent his time in whorehouses and once cut off one of his ears and gave it to a prostitute to prove his "love" for her. When he was about eighteen or nineteen years old, he fell in love with a girl and told her she was more valuable to him than his own life. When she laughed at him, he held his hand over a burning candle until the flesh was bubbling and the woman screamed.]{.class-0}

[Now Van Gogh was a "kook," just as nutty as a pecan pie, but he had the conviction of his feelings: they were real to him. If an unsaved man can have such conviction about his own feelings that he can burn his hand and cut off his ear, why can't a Christian stand up for his Saviour and take a beating? If Jesus Christ is real to you, Christian, you ought to get into the habit of doing some things just to make a ]{.class-0}[fool]{.class-2}[ out of yourself for Him (1 Cor. 4:10). Is Jesus Christ real enough to you that you do some things just for the sake of pleasing Him, with no benefit to yourself at all?]{.class-0}

[]{#section-0_1_6fad2151492bd151_67e1.xhtml}

CHAPTER 8

8:1 O that thou wert as my brother, that sucked the breasts of my mother! when I should find thee without, I would kiss thee; yea, I should not be despised.

2 I would lead thee, and bring thee into my mother's house, who would instruct me: I would cause thee to drink of spiced wine of the juice of my pomegranate.

3 His left hand should be under my head, and his right hand should embrace me.

4 I charge you, O daughters of Jerusalem, that ye stir not up, nor awake my love, until he please.

5 Who is this that cometh up from the wilderness, leaning upon her beloved? I raised thee up under the apple tree: there thy mother brought thee forth: there she brought thee forth that bare thee.

[Now we've come to what I call the most enigmatic chapter in the Bible. There are things in this chapter that nobody has been able to successfully and accurately exposit yet. Of course, there are practical and devotional and spiritual applications that can be made, and we will make them. But when it comes to the actual doctrinal meaning of the passage, there are several places where I am lost, and the only exposition I will be able to make is ]{.class-0}["Ich weiss nicht."]{.class-2}

[The problem in the passage is the ]{.class-0}[identity ]{.class-2}[of the Bride and the Bridegroom. There are two Bridegrooms in the Bible: God the Father is the Bridegroom of Israel, and Jesus Christ is the Bridegroom of the Church. We have commented under 7:1 that there could be a ]{.class-0}[third Bride]{.class-2}[ in the passage before us (vs. 8), but who would be ]{.class-0}[her ]{.class-2}[Bridegroom I have no idea. The logical conclusion you would draw would be the Holy Spirit, but the Bible nowhere speaks of the Holy Spirit "marrying" anyone. God the Father is identified as a Bridegroom in Hosea 2, and Jesus Christ is identified as a Bridegroom Ephesians 5, but you won't find any passage like that on the Holy Ghost. Abraham's servant in Genesis 24 (a picture of the Holy Spirit) goes to get a bride for Isaac (a picture of Christ), not ]{.class-0}[himself]{.class-2}[.]{.class-0}

[Scofield has the chapter outlined as verses 1--4 being the Bride speaking, verses 5--7 being the Bridegroom speaking, verse 8 being the Bride speaking again, verse 9 is the Bridegroom answering her, and the chapter ends with the Bride speaking in verses 10--14. But he gets that outline by getting rid of the ]{.class-0}[King James]{.class-2}[ paragraph marks. The ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ has the paragraph marks at verses 6, 8, and 14; so that is how we'll divide the chapter this time. Most of the chapter is the Bride speaking, but in some verses one can only guess as to the speaker.]{.class-0}

[Verse 1: ]{.class-0}["O that thou wert as my brother."]{.class-1}[ We have already commented on the problem involved here under 7:1. Jesus Christ ]{.class-0}[is]{.class-2}[ the ]{.class-0}["brother"]{.class-1}[ of the Church, so why would she be praying He was ]{.class-0}["as" ]{.class-1}[her brother. So there is a question here as to whether this is the Church, the Bride of Christ.]{.class-0}

"[That sucked the breasts of my mother!"]{.class-1}[ Well, the Church's ]{.class-0}["mother"]{.class-1}[ is the ]{.class-0}[New Jerusalem]{.class-2}[ (Gal 4:26), but Jesus Christ, as God, has no mother (Mary is NOT the "mother of God" as the Roman Catholic Church teaches). So what the Catholics do is make Mary the mother of ]{.class-0}[all]{.class-2}[ the "sons of God," which is a rank heresy. ]{.class-0}[Mary couldn't save herself]{.class-2}[ (Luke 1:47), ]{.class-0}[much less you.]{.class-2}

"[When I should find thee without, I would kiss thee; yea, I should not be despised."]{.class-1}[ It is reminiscent of the Bride being separated from the Bridegroom as she was back in 3:4 and 5:6--7. In fact, compare the first part of verse two to the last part of 3:4.]{.class-0}

"[I would lead thee, and bring thee into my mother's house, who would instruct me"]{.class-1}[ (vs.2).]{.class-0}

"[\...until I had brought him into my mother's house, and into the chamber of her that conceived me"]{.class-1}[ (3:4).]{.class-0}

Look at verse 4 and compare it with 3:5.

"[I charge you, O daughters of Jerusalem, that ye stir not up, nor awake my love, until he please" ]{.class-1}[(vs. 4)]{.class-0}

"[I charge you, O ye daughters of Jerusalem, by the roes, and by the hinds of the field, that ye stir not up, nor awake my love, till he please" ]{.class-1}[(3:5).]{.class-0}

[That's a reference to the Second Advent, so it's not the Church. And since the woman distinquishes herself from the ]{.class-0}["daughters of Jerusalem,"]{.class-1}[ it's not Israel. What you ]{.class-0}[probably ]{.class-2}[have in both passages is a reference to Gentile believers in the Tribulation (see comments on 3:4--5). If you do make the woman the Church, then you have to make a spiritual application (see our comments on 2:7)]{.class-0}

For verse 3, see our comments on 2:6

The first part of verse 5 should be contrasted with 3:6.

"[Who is this that cometh up from the wilderness, leaning upon her beloved?"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 5)]{.class-0}

"[Who is this that cometh out of the wilderness like pillars of smoke\...," ]{.class-1}[etc. (3:6).]{.class-0}

The reference in verse 5 is to the Bride, and the reference in 3:6 is to the Bridegroom, but the setting of both passages is the Second Advent (see also our comments on 6:10).

[Verse 5 continuing: ]{.class-0}["I raised thee up under the apple tree: there thy mother brought thee forth: there she brought thee forth that bare thee."]{.class-1}

[And here is one of the ]{.class-0}["Ich weiss nicht"]{.class-2}[ places in the chapter. If the woman is the Church in this verse as she certainly seems to be (see comments above), then the ]{.class-0}["mother"]{.class-1}[ is the New Jerusalem (see comments on vs. 2). But what ]{.class-0}["the apple tree"]{.class-1}[ would be, I haven't any idea and couldn't even ]{.class-0}[guess]{.class-2}[. In 2:3, the Bride compares the Bridegroom to ]{.class-0}["the apple tree,"]{.class-1}[ and you can see our comments on apples under that verse. I suppose, that being the case, that you could make some spiritual application here to salvation, but that might be stretching things a bit. Of course, that is assuming that it is the Bridegroom speaking in this passage and not the Bride. So as the old Scotsman said when he hit a text he couldn't understand: "We'll bravely face this text and ]{.class-0}[pass on]{.class-2}[ to the next verse."]{.class-0}

6 Set me as a seal upon thine heart, as a seal upon thine arm: for love is strong as death; jealousy is cruel as the grave: the coals thereof are coals of fire, which hath a most vehement flame.

7 Many waters cannot quench love, neither can the floods drown it: if a man would give all the substance of his house for love, it would utterly be contemned.

"[Set me as a seal upon thine heart, as a seal upon thine arm" ]{.class-1}[(vs. 6). The two pictures here are a ]{.class-0}[signet ring]{.class-2}[ used to affix signatures on a document and an ]{.class-0}[arm bracelet]{.class-2}[ used to identify a person's family (like a family crest). You will remember that Judah gave Tamar his ]{.class-0}["signet"]{.class-1}[ and ]{.class-0}["bracelets,"]{.class-1}[ along with his ]{.class-0}["staff,"]{.class-1}[ as a pledge of payment back in Genesis 38:17--18. Of course, this isn't an illicit affair as that was, but the idea is a symbol of commitment in the marriage. Today we do it by ]{.class-0}[exchanging rings.]{.class-2}[ Back in medieval times it was done by both parties wearing garments with long loose sleeves which were tied together upon taking their vows; hence the expression "tying the knot" in reference to getting married.]{.class-0}

[Now I take the speaker here to be the Bride. Notice that she asks the Bridegroom to remember her, to establish or fix her (]{.class-0}["as a seal"]{.class-1}[), in two places: on the ]{.class-0}["heart"]{.class-1}[ and on the ]{.class-0}["arm."]{.class-1}[ The ]{.class-0}[heart ]{.class-2}[is the inward seal; the ]{.class-0}[arm ]{.class-2}[is the outward seal. In a good marriage relationship, a spouse not only wants a visible sign for proof of love, but an inward, invisible commitment of the heart. The ring on the finger is no good without the commitment of the heart.]{.class-0}

"[For love is as strong as death."]{.class-1}[ The idea is that married love lasts until death, so the marriage vows say: "till death do us part" (see our comments under 7:10).]{.class-0}

"[Jealousy is cruel as the grave." ]{.class-1}[Now jealousy is normal in a marriage relationship. If a man loves his wife, he doesn't want some other fellow pawing all over her; if a woman loves her husband, she doesn't want to see him in the arms of another woman. Even the Lord is jealous in His relationship with the believer.]{.class-0}

"[Thou shalt not make unto thee any graven image\...Thou shalt not bow down thyself to them, nor serve them: for I the LORD thy God am a JEALOUS God"]{.class-1}[ (Exod. 20:4--5).]{.class-0}

"[For thou shall worship no other god: for the LORD, whose name is Jealous, is a JEALOUS God"]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-15}[(Exod. 34:19).]{.class-0}

[The Apostle Paul, in writing to the Corinthians, said, ]{.class-0}["For I am JEALOUS over you with godly jealousy: for I have espoused you to one husband, that I may present you as a chaste virgin to Christ"]{.class-1}[ (2 Cor. 11:2).]{.class-0}

[So there is a normal ]{.class-0}["godly jealousy" ]{.class-1}[that expects faithfulness in a marriage. But there is also an undue jealousy based on paranoia. Sometimes it comes because trust has been broken; sometimes it doesn't. That's the kind of ]{.class-0}["jealousy"]{.class-1}[ about which Solomon is writing in this verse.]{.class-0}

[In Proverbs 6:34, he wrote:]{.class-0}[ "For jealousy is the rage of a man: therefore he will not spare in the day of vengeance."]{.class-1}

There is not only jealousy over possible infidelity, there is jealousy based on covetousness. That is, you are jealous of someone because of what they have or who they are, and you want it. In the Bible, that kind of jealousy is called envy.

[Proverbs 27:4 says, ]{.class-0}["Wrath is cruel, and anger is outrageous; but who is able to stand before envy?"]{.class-1}

Envy is what caused Cain to kill Abel. Christ was crucified because of envy (Matt. 27:18).

[Back to verse 6: ]{.class-0}["The coals thereof are coals of fire, which hath a most vehement flame."]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-15}[Now notice the things connected with ]{.class-0}["love"]{.class-1}[ in the passage: ]{.class-0}["death,"]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-0}["jealousy," "cruel," "grave,"]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-15}[and ]{.class-0}["coals of fire."]{.class-1}[ This all flies in the face of the Liberal who always talks about]{.class-0}[ "God is love" ]{.class-1}[(1 John 4:8), the idea being that a "God of love" would never send anyone to Hell.]{.class-0}

[But the ]{.class-0}["vehement flame"]{.class-1}[ is an unquenchable fire (vs. 7 cf. Isa. 34:8--10, 66:24; Mark 9:43--48). Those ]{.class-0}["coals of fire"]{.class-1}[ are not a reference to a fire pan carried on the head, as all the Christian day-school kiddie flannelgraph/flashcard teachers like to tell you (see comments on Rom. 12:20 in that Commentary); they're a reference ]{.class-0}[to Hell and the Lake of Fire]{.class-2}[ (Psa. 140:10).]{.class-0}

[Listen! a "god" who is all love and no ]{.class-0}[hate ]{.class-2}[is a ]{.class-0}[perverted god.]{.class-2}[ God cannot love righteousness and sin at the same time. The teaching of the Liberals (now called "emergents") is that Christ died simply to show His love for you. That's a ]{.class-0}[half-truth,]{.class-2}[ which means it's a ]{.class-0}[whole lie.]{.class-2}[ The God who loved you enough to send His Son to die for you, did that because you were a ]{.class-0}[sinner]{.class-2}[ (Rom 5:8) who was an ]{.class-0}[enemy]{.class-2}[ of God (Rom. 5:10) and was going to ]{.class-0}["perish" ]{.class-1}[(John 3:16) if the Lord didn't do something for you. The same God who has a ]{.class-0}[perfect love]{.class-2}[ that provides a ]{.class-0}[perfect salvation]{.class-2}[, has a ]{.class-0}[perfect jealousy]{.class-2}[ (see above) that leads to ]{.class-0}[perfect vengeance]{.class-2}[ (Deut. 32:35, 41--42; Isa. 61:1--2) because He is ]{.class-0}[perfectly holy]{.class-2}[ (Isa. 57:15--21). For a thorough discussion on the love of God, see our work on ]{.class-0}[God is Love]{.class-2}[ (Bible Baptist Bookstore, 1996).]{.class-0}

[Verse 7: ]{.class-0}["Many waters cannot quench love, neither can the floods drown it." "Waters" ]{.class-1}[and ]{.class-0}["floods"]{.class-1}[ in the Scriptures can stand for two things: multitudes of unsaved people and trouble.]{.class-0}

[Revelation 17:15, ]{.class-0}["And he saith unto me, the waters which thou sawest, where the whore sitteth, are peoples, and multitudes, and nations, and tongues."]{.class-1}

[Psalm 42:7, ]{.class-0}["Deep calleth unto deep at the noise of thy waterspouts: all thy waves and thy billows are gone over me."]{.class-1}

[Psalm 18:4, ]{.class-0}["The sorrows of death compassed me, and the floods of ungodly men made me afraid."]{.class-1}

So real love holds up against people and circumstances; it stands up against them and survives them. Real love survives the opposition of all the people in the world; real love will go through sickness, sorrow, poverty, persecution, adversity, loss, and all kinds of trouble and not waiver.

[The best description of this type of love is found in the New Testament in 1 Corinthians 13, despite the abuse of the passage made by Modernists. Notice in that passage that the word ]{.class-0}["charity" ]{.class-1}[is used for ]{.class-0}[love ]{.class-2}[to distinguish it from other types of "loves," like ]{.class-0}[sex ]{.class-2}[or mere ]{.class-0}[affection]{.class-2}[. Fundamentalists and Conservatives complain about the English not being as exact in its wording as the Greek and then turn right around and change an English word like ]{.class-0}["charity"]{.class-1}[ which is very specific in its meaning. ]{.class-0}["Charity"]{.class-1}[ is not a government handout (which is what the word had degenerated into), but a love which is willing to ]{.class-0}[give ]{.class-2}[and ]{.class-0}[overlook ]{.class-2}[things. So the ]{.class-0}[AV]{.class-2}[ word ]{.class-0}["charity"]{.class-1}[ is a much better word to describe the love a Christian is to have than just the word ]{.class-0}["love" ]{.class-2}[as used in the modern versions.]{.class-0}

[1 Corinthians 3:4, ]{.class-0}["Charity suffereth long"]{.class-1}[: it puts up with the ]{.class-0}["waters" ]{.class-1}[and ]{.class-0}["floods"]{.class-1}[ of adverse circumstances. ]{.class-0}["Charity envieth not"]{.class-1}[; so ]{.class-0}["jealousy" ]{.class-1}[may be ]{.class-0}["cruel as the grave,"]{.class-1}[ but real love doesn't envy. Charity ]{.class-0}["beareth all things\...endureth all things. Charity never faileth" ]{.class-1}[(1 Cor. 13:7--8). No matter what is put on it, real love will overcome when nothing else will, and it will survive.]{.class-0}

[Back to verse 7:]{.class-0}[ "if a man would give all the substance of his house for love, it would utterly be contemned." ]{.class-1}[We have already commented on this part of the verse under 7:12 (which see). Note that the word here is not ]{.class-0}[condemn,]{.class-2}[ which means "to proclaim guilty," but ]{.class-0}[contemn]{.class-2}[, which means "to despise or scorn, to treat as nothing."]{.class-0}

8 We have a little sister, and she hath no breasts: what shall we do for our sister in the day when she shall be spoken for?

9 If she be a wall, we will build upon her a palace of silver: and if she be a door, we will inclose her with boards of cedar.

10 I am a wall, and my breasts like towers: then was I in his eyes as one that found favour.

11 Solomon had a vineyard at Baal-hamon; he let out the vineyard unto keepers; every one for the fruit thereof was to bring a thousand pieces of silver.

12 My vineyard, which is mine, is before me: thou, O Solomon, must have a thousand, and those that keep the fruit thereof two hundred.

13 Thou that dwellest in the gardens, the companions hearken to thy voice: cause me to hear it.

[Scofield says about verse 8: "The reference here is ]{.class-0}[obscure."]{.class-2}[ (Boy, if that ain't the understatement of the year!)]{.class-0}

"[We have a little sister"]{.class-1}[ (vs. 8). ]{.class-0}["We"]{.class-1}[ do? Who's the ]{.class-0}["We"]{.class-1}[? Christ and the Church?]{.class-0}

"[She hath no breasts"]{.class-1}[; i.e., she's young and hasn't developed yet. ]{.class-0}["What shall we do for our sister in the day when she shall be spoken for?"]{.class-1}[ In other words, what are ]{.class-0}["we"]{.class-1}[ (whoever ]{.class-0}[that ]{.class-2}[is) going to do for this girl when it comes time for her to get married? I don't know. I don't know ]{.class-0}["what shall we do"]{.class-1}[ or ]{.class-0}["when she shall be spoken for"]{.class-1}[ or even who ]{.class-0}["she" ]{.class-1}[is! It's like the riddle: "What has six legs, purple spots, and eats people?" Answer:" A six-legged, purple-spotted people-eater." That is, you don't know what the critter is, but there it is.]{.class-0}

[Now, I have already discussed this verse back in our opening remarks in chapter 7. Verses 9--12 are some of those "]{.class-0}[Ich weiss nicht]{.class-2}[" verses. I have no real comment to make on the passage, and, to date, no commentator has any intelligible exegesis on it.]{.class-0}

[The ]{.class-0}["little sister"]{.class-1}[ is obviously not the woman of Song of Solomon, but who she is, I have no idea.]{.class-0}

"[If she be a wall\...I am a wall"]{.class-1}[ (vss. 9--10). What's that? A heavy-set woman? I've got no more idea what that means than if it wasn't even there. Psalm 119:130 says, ]{.class-0}["The entrance of thy words giveth light; it giveth understanding unto the simple." ]{.class-1}[Well, then, I must be really simple because I can't get it.]{.class-0}

[The commentators give you some pious drivel about being "solid" and "steadfast" in resisting the advances of others, and if the girl waits for true love she'll get a large dowry (]{.class-0}["a palace of silver"]{.class-1}[) because silver and cedar are indicative of wealth. Having said that, how do you apply it ]{.class-0}[doctrinally?]{.class-2}[ Answer: ]{.class-0}[you don't]{.class-2}[. They just bluff their way through the passage. Back in 2:9, ]{.class-0}["our wall"]{.class-1}[ had to do with the Rapture and the structure of the universe, but how you could apply that here, I don't know.]{.class-0}

"[If she be a door, we will inclose her with boards of cedar." ]{.class-1}[Well, you don't build a house around a door; you build it on a solid foundation (Matt. 7:24--25; 1Cor. 3:11; Eph. 2:20).]{.class-0}

[Now I assume that the Bride is the one talking in verse 10, but all you can really say is that the woman found favor in her Beloved's eyes because she was beautiful and endowed properly. Who is it? ]{.class-0}[Ich weiss nicht.]{.class-2}

[Verse 11:]{.class-0}[ "Solomon had a vineyard at Baal-hamon." "Baal-hamon" ]{.class-1}[means "lord of a multitude." It has been identified with Hammon in Asher (Josh. 19:28) or with another town near Dothan in Samaria, but the fact is, no one can say for sure where it is.]{.class-0}

[Now Solomon had many vineyards (Eccl. 2:4), and the Bride says as much in verse 12 (]{.class-0}["thou, O Solomon, must have a thousand"]{.class-1}[). The one at ]{.class-0}["Baal-hamon"]{.class-1}[ is singled out by the Bride for some reason. ]{.class-0}

[Of course, with that many vineyards, there was no way Solomon could pay personal attention to it so he leases it out to ]{.class-0}["keepers." ]{.class-1}[Each of them gives Solomon ]{.class-0}["a thousand pieces of silver,"]{.class-1}[ and the reasoning is that for that price they get to try to make a profit on their investment. Of course, as the owner, Solomon could come in at any time and claim the fruit for himself.]{.class-0}

[All the commentators connect the verse to the Parable of the Vineyard in Isaiah 5:1--7 and Matthew 21:38--39. The problem with connecting that parable with the verse here in the Song of Solomon is if you stick with the typology already laid down in the book, Solomon is a picture of the Son, ]{.class-0}[not ]{.class-2}[the Father.]{.class-0}

[In the context before us, verse 11 is contrasted with verse 12: ]{.class-0}["my vineyard, which is mine, is before me."]{.class-1}[ In other words, this woman, unlike Solomon, only had one vineyard which she worked herself.]{.class-0}

[Now there is ]{.class-0}[some ]{.class-2}[spiritual application you can make from this. As we have stated before, every Christian is likened to a ]{.class-0}["husbandman"]{.class-1}[ (2 Tim. 2:6) who is expected to bring forth fruit (cf. John 15:1--5). So the application of the verse is that God has allotted each believer a specific job to do that he, and no one else, is to take care of personally.]{.class-0}

"[My vineyard\...is before me." ]{.class-1}[The idea is that the work is right there in front of you, so get busy. There is no reason for a Christian to be ]{.class-0}["idle" "all the day" ]{.class-1}[(Matt. 20:6).]{.class-0}

[Verse 13: ]{.class-0}["Thou that dwellest in the gardens"---]{.class-1}[and I take that to be a reference to the Bridegroom, Jesus Christ---]{.class-0}["the companions hearken to thy voice." ]{.class-1}[And that looks like a reference to saved people, ]{.class-0}[in type]{.class-2}[. Well, ]{.class-0}[if]{.class-2}[ that's the case, what do you do with what follows?]{.class-0}[ "Cause me to hear it." ]{.class-1}[Is that the Bride as an unsaved person asking God to deal with her? It's rough, man, rough!]{.class-0}

[Now there could be other ways of looking at it, but none of them are without their problems. Back in 4:12, the Bride is likened to ]{.class-0}["a garden"]{.class-1}[ singular, but here you have ]{.class-0}["gardens,"]{.class-1}[ plural. If you run that cross-reference, then Christ dwells in each individual believer in the Church as the Bridegroom dwells in the gardens (cf. Col. 1:27). In the garden of 4:12, Christ has some ]{.class-0}["friends"]{.class-1}[ (5:1) whom He invites to fellowship. So maybe what you have here is the Bride craving fellowship with her Lover.]{.class-0}

14 Make haste, my beloved, and be thou like to a roe or to a young hart upon the mountains of spices.

[Now I saved one last comment on verse 13 for here because verse 13 ends with the Bride begging to hear the Bridegroom's ]{.class-0}["voice," ]{.class-1}[and verse 14 just happens to be a prayer by the Church for the Rapture (cf. 2:8 and comments).]{.class-0}

[Now whatever confusion we may have run into in the rest of the chapter, Song of Solomon ends on a clear note. The book ends where both Testaments end---with a reference ]{.class-0}[to the Second Coming of Jesus Christ.]{.class-2}[ The difference between the two Testaments, in this regard, is that the Old Testament ends with a warning to the Jews to get ready for the Second Advent of their Messiah (Mal. 4:4--6), while the New Testament ends with the Church praying for the return of her Saviour at the Rapture (Rev. 22:20). Song of Solomon ends where the New Testament ends.]{.class-0}

[Look at verse 14: ]{.class-0}["Make HASTE, my beloved." ]{.class-1}[John writes: ]{.class-0}["He which testifieth these things saith, Surely I come QUICKLY. Amen."]{.class-1}

"[Be thou like to a roe or to a young hart upon the mountains of spices."]{.class-1}[ And we have run into this before back in 2:17.]{.class-0}

"[Until the day break, and the shadows flee away, turn, my beloved, and be thou like a roe or a young hart upon the mountains of Bether."]{.class-1}

[The ]{.class-0}["day break" ]{.class-1}[places the verse squarely at the Second Coming (see 2 Pet. 2:19).]{.class-0}

[So although there may be many things in the Song of Solomon that no one, ]{.class-0}[as yet,]{.class-2}[ has the answer to, one thing is clear. The love of a Christian for his Lord should always culminate in a ]{.class-0}["love" ]{.class-1}[for ]{.class-0}["his appearing"]{.class-1}[ ]{.class-15}[(2 Tim 4:8; 1 Pet 1:7--8). There should be no hope dearer to a believer than the ]{.class-0}["blessed hope"]{.class-1}[ (Tit. 2:13). And the prayer of a Christian should never be "wait a little longer, please, Jesus," but "hurry up a little quicker, please, Jesus"!]{.class-0}

"[Even so, come, Lord Jesus."]{.class-1}
